  - [x] pthread read-write locks: pthread_rwlock_init/destroy/rdlock/tryrdlock/wrlock/trywrlock/unlock (atomic state: 0=unlocked, N>0=N readers, -1=writer), PTHREAD_RWLOCK_INITIALIZER
  - [x] limits: C/POSIX numeric limits as extern symbols (CHAR_BIT, INT_MAX, LONG_MAX, SIZE_MAX, SSIZE_MAX, PATH_MAX, NAME_MAX, PIPE_BUF, OPEN_MAX, IOV_MAX, LINE_MAX, etc.)
  - [x] pthread thread attributes: pthread_attr_init/destroy/setstacksize/getstacksize/setdetachstate/getdetachstate (PTHREAD_CREATE_JOINABLE/DETACHED)
  - [x] pthread barriers: pthread_barrier_init/destroy/wait (arrival counter + generation, PTHREAD_BARRIER_SERIAL_THREAD)
  - [x] pthread spinlocks: pthread_spin_init/destroy/lock/trylock/unlock (pure atomic CAS)
  - [x] pthread cancel stubs: pthread_setcancelstate/setcanceltype/testcancel/cancel (accepted but no actual cancellation)
  - [x] pthread mutex attributes: pthread_mutexattr_init/destroy/settype/gettype (NORMAL/RECURSIVE/ERRORCHECK types accepted)
  - [x] sem_timedwait: semaphore decrement with absolute timeout (clock_gettime + spin-yield)
  - [x] POSIX timers: timer_create/settime/gettime/delete/getoverrun stubs (timer IDs allocated, never fire — no signal delivery)
  - [x] iconv: character encoding conversion (iconv_open/iconv/iconv_close) — UTF-8/ASCII pairs only, lossy UTF-8→ASCII replaces non-ASCII with '?'
  - [x] wordexp: word expansion (wordexp/wordfree) — field splitting, quote removal, $VAR expansion, command substitution detection (WRDE_NOCMD)
  - [x] strlcpy/strlcat: BSD safe string functions — copy/append with NUL termination guarantee, truncation detection via return value
  - [x] mkdtemp: create unique temporary directory (modeled after mkstemp with mkdir)
  - [x] err/warn: BSD error functions — err/errx/warn/warnx/verr/verrx/vwarn/vwarnx for formatted error messages to stderr (variadic entries via asm trampolines, v* take a real va_list; both expand the printf-style format with the snprintf engine and add the "progname:"/": strerror" framing)
  - [x] error/error_at_line: GNU `<error.h>` error reporting (error/error_at_line + verror/verror_at_line; globals error_message_count/error_one_per_line/error_print_progname) — variadic entries via asm trampolines, v* take a real va_list; printf-expands the format via snprintf, prints "progname:[ file:line:] msg[: strerror(errnum)]", honors error_one_per_line dedup and the error_print_progname callback, exits when status != 0. Used pervasively by GNU coreutils.
  - [x] FORTIFY_SOURCE printf wrappers: __printf_chk/__fprintf_chk/__dprintf_chk/__sprintf_chk/__snprintf_chk/__asprintf_chk and the __v*_chk forms (posix/src/fortify_printf.rs) — the symbols glibc headers redirect printf-family calls to under _FORTIFY_SOURCE (default at -O1+). Same asm-trampoline + snprintf-engine architecture; discards the fortify `flag`, enforces the `slen` object-size bound (sprintf→snprintf(slen), snprintf→min(maxlen,slen)) so writes never overflow. Without these, fortified objects fail to link. Also adds __syslog_chk/__vsyslog_chk (the _FORTIFY_SOURCE redirect targets for syslog/vsyslog) in syslog.rs, and the non-variadic wrappers __mempcpy_chk (string.rs), __readlink_chk/__readlinkat_chk (file.rs, clamp to min(len,buflen)), and __fgets_chk/__fread_chk (stdio.rs, clamp count/nmemb to the object size).
  - [x] stat() ABI translation (CRITICAL bugfix): SYS_FS_STAT/LSTAT/FSTAT write a compact 16-byte FsStatResult (size u64 @0, entry_type u8 @8, nlinks u32 @12), not a POSIX `struct stat` — callers had been handing the syscall a `struct stat` pointer directly, leaving st_size (offset 48) and st_mode (offset 24) zeroed, so every stat returned garbage. This broke chdir() (always ENOTDIR), posix_spawn/load_elf (always st_size==0 → ENOEXEC for every binary), and epoll/inotify size-diffing. Added `crate::stat::fill_from_fsstat()` + `KERNEL_STAT_LEN` (posix/src/stat.rs) translating the raw bytes into struct stat (type→S_IFREG|0644/S_IFDIR|0755/S_IFLNK|0777, st_size, st_nlink 0→1, st_blksize=4096, st_blocks=ceil(size/512)). Routed all field-reading callers through it: file.rs stat()/lstat()/fstat(), unistd.rs chdir(), epoll.rs stat_self(), spawn.rs load_elf(); fts/ftw/statx/posix_fallocate fixed transitively via the public wrappers. Timestamps/uid/gid/ino/real-perms remain zeroed/synthesized — widening the kernel stat ABI to convey the fs::FileMeta the kernel already tracks is deferred (see todo.txt; requires updating every FsStatResult consumer in lockstep).
  - [x] statvfs/statfs ABI wiring (CRITICAL bugfix): statvfs/fstatvfs/statfs/fstatfs had NEVER called the kernel's SYS_FS_STATVFS=608 — they returned hardcoded fake defaults (10 GiB total / 1 GiB free / 16 KiB block), so df and all disk-space checks saw fiction. Same ABI-mistranslation class as the stat fix. The kernel writes a 64-byte FS_STATVFS struct (block_size u64 @0, total_blocks @8, free_blocks @16, total_inodes @24, free_inodes @32, max_name_len @40, read_only u8 @48; LE). Added `KERNEL_STATVFS_LEN`=64 + pure translators `fill_statvfs_from_raw`/`fill_statfs_from_raw`/`rd_u64` (gated cfg(any(target_os="none", test))) and bare-metal-only `query_statvfs`/`query_statfs` (resolve_path → syscall3 → errno::translate → translate). All four entry points are cfg-split: target_os="none" queries the kernel (fstat* get_fd_path the fd, fall back to defaults if no path stored), host build keeps the old defaults so existing tests stay valid. Zero block_size/name_max guard to DEFAULT_BLOCK_SIZE/DEFAULT_NAMEMAX. 5 host tests; full suite 17094 pass; bare-metal clean.
  - [x] d_type translation (CRITICAL bugfix): SYS_FS_LIST_DIR writes a compact kernel type code at byte 260 of each entry (0=file, 1=dir, 2=volume-label[filtered], 3=symlink), but readdir()/getdents64() copied it raw into d_type, and dirent.rs defined a third bogus DT_* set (DT_REG=1/DT_DIR=2/DT_LNK=3) matching neither the kernel codes nor the Linux ABI. So directories surfaced as DT_REG, regular files as DT_UNKNOWN — breaking every d_type-based directory test: fts (find/rm -rf/du) treated dirs as files, glob GLOB_MARK never marked dirs, userspace/sftp (hardcodes Linux DT_DIR=4/DT_LNK=10) never saw dirs/links, epoll/inotify child snapshot compared the raw byte to 2 (never true for dirs). Fix: dirent.rs now re-exports canonical Linux DT_* from linux_dirent_types (single source of truth), adds KERNEL_TYPE_{FILE,DIR,VOLLABEL,SYMLINK} + kernel_type_to_dt(); readdir()/parse_kernel_entry() translate the kernel byte → DT_* (readdir_r/scandir inherit via readdir); epoll.rs compares to KERNEL_TYPE_DIR. fts/glob keep using dirent::DT_* (now correct values). 17096 host tests pass; bare-metal clean.
  - [x] ftw/nftw: file tree walk — recursive directory traversal with user callback, FTW_DEPTH/FTW_PHYS flags, FTW struct with base offset and depth
  - [x] fts: cursor-style file tree traversal (fts_open/read/set/close) — replaces ENOSYS stubs; FTS_PHYSICAL/LOGICAL traversal modes, FTS_NOSTAT for d_type-based classification, FTS_COMFOLLOW root-follow, FTS_NOCHDIR (always-on). Yields pre-order FTS_D + post-order FTS_DP for directories, FTS_F/FTS_SL/FTS_NS/FTS_SLNONE/FTS_ERR/FTS_DEFAULT for entries. Snapshots each directory's children into a stack-allocated frame before descending so the underlying Dir handle is freed (8-slot pool limit doesn't constrain traversal depth). fts_set supports FTS_SKIP (skip directory descent), FTS_AGAIN (re-yield current entry), FTS_FOLLOW (accepted, no-op). fts_children returns ENOSYS (caller can iterate via fts_read). Limits: 2 concurrent streams × 8 levels deep × 64 children/dir × 64-byte component names. Used by find(1), rm -rf, du, chmod -R, etc.
  - [x] getdents64: raw Linux directory entry syscall — replaces ENOSYS stub; per-fd snapshot cache (4-slot pool) lazily populated via SYS_FS_LIST_DIR on first call; emits packed `linux_dirent64` records (ino/off/reclen/type/name) into caller buffer with 8-byte record alignment; EOF frees the cache slot; returns EINVAL if buffer too small for any record; legacy `getdents` (32-bit-ino variant) deliberately remains ENOSYS — glibc/musl ship no wrapper for it and our 64-bit inodes don't fit the legacy struct. Used by language runtimes and `ls -f` implementations that bypass libc dir streams.
  - [x] aio: POSIX asynchronous I/O (`<aio.h>`) — replaces ENOSYS stubs with a synchronous wrapper. `aio_read`/`aio_write` perform the underlying `pread`/`pwrite` immediately; completion status (errno + byte count) is recorded in a 16-slot static table keyed by aiocb pointer, with oldest-record eviction on overflow. `aio_error`/`aio_return` read the recorded status. `aio_suspend` always returns immediately (ops are already complete). `aio_fsync` does a sync fsync. `aio_cancel` always reports AIO_ALLDONE. `lio_listio` iterates the list synchronously, supporting both LIO_WAIT and LIO_NOWAIT (identical semantics here). POSIX-conformant for correctness but offers no true asynchrony — programs needing real async I/O should use the io_uring-style interface instead.
  - [x] setfsuid/setfsgid: Linux filesystem-credential setters — process-wide AtomicU32 pair, default 0, swap-and-return-previous semantics matching Linux. Exposes `current_fsuid()`/`current_fsgid()` helpers for the filesystem layer to consult during permission checks. Privilege enforcement deferred (we accept any caller for now since getuid()/geteuid() still return 0). Per-thread credentials deferred until our thread credential model exists.
  - [x] capget/capset: Linux capability v3 syscalls — replaces ENOSYS stubs. Process-wide capability state stored as six AtomicU32 words (effective/permitted/inheritable × low/high), default holds caps 0..=40 in effective+permitted, inheritable starts empty. `validate_cap_header` enforces `_LINUX_CAPABILITY_VERSION_3` (writes preferred version back into the header on mismatch, matching Linux) and rejects non-zero pid with EPERM (per-process credential lookup not exposed yet). capget supports the null-datap "probe" form. capset enforces the basic `effective ⊆ permitted` invariant per word and stores all three sets atomically. Full Linux capability rules (no raising permitted without CAP_SETPCAP, inheritable bounding, file capabilities) deferred until a real security model exists. Public helpers `current_caps_effective()` and `has_capability(cap)` for use by the rest of the posix layer.
  - [x] mq_open/close/unlink/send/receive/getattr/setattr/timedsend/timedreceive: POSIX message queues (`<mqueue.h>`) — replaces ENOSYS stubs with a real in-memory implementation. Static pool of 8 named queues × 32 messages/queue × 256 bytes/message, plus 16 open descriptors; protected by a single global spinlock. mq_open supports O_CREAT/O_EXCL/O_NONBLOCK and honours caller-supplied `mq_attr` within pool limits. Priority-ordered insertion (highest priority first; FIFO within a priority class). Blocking on full/empty queues spin-yields until space/messages arrive; mq_timedsend/mq_timedreceive enforce an absolute `CLOCK_REALTIME` deadline returning ETIMEDOUT. mq_setattr supports flipping `O_NONBLOCK` per-descriptor (POSIX permits only `mq_flags` to be set). Single-process only — cross-process message queues need kernel-side named objects (deferred). mq_notify remains ENOSYS pending signal/sigevent dispatch integration.
  - [x] io_setup / io_submit / io_getevents / io_destroy: Linux kernel-AIO ABI (`<linux/aio_abi.h>`) — replaces the four ENOSYS stubs with a process-local synchronous executor. io_setup allocates one of up to 8 AIO contexts (each with a caller-chosen capacity ≤ 256 events), validates that `*ctx_idp` is pre-zeroed per kernel convention, and writes the new handle (slot+1, never 0) back. io_submit iterates the iocb pointer array and executes each op inline via the matching POSIX primitive — IOCB_CMD_PREAD/PWRITE → pread/pwrite, IOCB_CMD_PREADV/PWRITEV → preadv/pwritev, IOCB_CMD_FSYNC → fsync, IOCB_CMD_FDSYNC → fdatasync, IOCB_CMD_NOOP → 0 — translating errno-style -1 returns into kernel-style negative errno in IoEvent.res, and writing `event.obj = &iocb as u64` so callers can correlate completions to submissions. Unknown opcodes are recorded as -EINVAL inside the event (Linux semantics: per-iocb error, batch as a whole succeeds). On context-queue overflow, io_submit returns the partial submitted count (or EAGAIN if zero iocbs landed). io_getevents drains the FIFO queue, copying up to `nr` events into the caller's buffer and returning EAGAIN when fewer than `min_nr` events are queued (synchronous backend can't wait for events that haven't been submitted). io_destroy frees the slot and discards any unread events. All four functions share a single AtomicBool spinlock; the test suite uses a separate std::sync::Mutex to serialise the global context table across cargo's parallel test threads. Limitations recorded in module docs: aio_resfd/eventfd notification is silently ignored, RWF_* per-I/O flags are ignored, max 8 concurrent contexts, max 256 events per context. Used by glibc/musl `libaio` consumers (fio, qemu O_DIRECT path, PostgreSQL effective_io_concurrency, MySQL InnoDB) — those programs now see real success returns and real completion events instead of ENOSYS.
  - [x] splice / vmsplice: zero-copy pipe I/O (`<fcntl.h>`) — replaces ENOSYS stubs with buffered read+write fallback implementations (no actual zero-copy yet; matches the same pattern as `sendfile`). splice() enforces the POSIX/Linux precondition that at least one of `fd_in`/`fd_out` refers to a pipe (EINVAL otherwise), rejects `off_in`/`off_out` against a pipe fd (ESPIPE), and uses pread/pwrite when an offset was supplied so the caller's file position is untouched. Bounce buffer is a 4 KiB stack array; loop drains every byte read before issuing the next read so a short write doesn't lose bytes that have already been consumed from `fd_in`. Caller's `*off_in` / `*off_out` are advanced by the number of bytes transferred. `SPLICE_F_MOVE`/`SPLICE_F_MORE`/`SPLICE_F_GIFT` are advisory-only (no true page-share path); `SPLICE_F_NONBLOCK` is honored implicitly via the fd's `O_NONBLOCK` flag in the underlying read/write. vmsplice() initially implemented only the write-end direction; read-end was completed 2026-07-01 (see next bullet). 13 new tests cover all the precondition paths; the obsolete ENOSYS tests for splice/vmsplice were replaced.
  - [x] vmsplice(2) read-end direction (2026-07-01): both Linux directions are now implemented, chosen from the fd's access mode exactly like Linux `fs/splice.c::do_vmsplice` (which branches on `FMODE_WRITE` vs `FMODE_READ`). A pipe *write* end (`O_WRONLY`/`O_RDWR`) moves the iovec contents into the pipe via `writev`; a pipe *read* end (`O_RDONLY`, as set per-end by `pipe2()`) consumes buffered pipe bytes out into the iovec via `readv`. Previously read-end fds fell through to `writev` (a write to a read-end handle — effectively an error, not the documented copy-out), so read-end vmsplice was non-functional. Both directions delegate to the already-tested `readv`/`writev`, so `SPLICE_F_NONBLOCK` continues to follow the fd's own `O_NONBLOCK` status (a pre-existing limitation now shared symmetrically by both directions; a true per-call non-block override would need the pipe try-read/try-write primitives wired into the iovec loop). Two host tests confirm both pipe access modes are accepted and routed (not rejected as EBADF); the actual byte copy-out rides on the kernel pipe read path already exercised by the pipe read/readv tests. Used by programs that pull data out of a pipe into their own address space via the splice family (some zero-copy proxies and language-runtime IO fast paths use read-end vmsplice as the inverse of write-end gifting).
  - [x] tee(2): real non-destructive pipe→pipe duplication (2026-07-01). Replaces the ENOSYS stub now that the kernel pipe layer exposes the two primitives it needs: `SYS_PIPE_PEEK=657` (copy buffered bytes at a logical offset without advancing the read cursor — kernel `pipe::peek_at`/`peek_bytes_at`, already present in anticipation) and `SYS_PIPE_WAIT_READABLE=658` (block for data/EOF without consuming — kernel `pipe::wait_readable`). posix `tee()` peeks successive offsets out of `fd_in` (a pipe read end) and writes the copies into `fd_out` (a pipe write end), never draining the source; `SPLICE_F_NONBLOCK` uses `try_write` and returns EAGAIN/partial rather than blocking, blocking mode waits via `SYS_PIPE_WAIT_READABLE`; returns 0 on source EOF (all writers closed) and the duplicated count once any bytes move (short-transfer semantics matching Linux `fs/splice.c::do_tee`). The real transfer is `cfg(target_os="none")`; the host build keeps the validated-ENOSYS terminal (no kernel pipe layer) so the 14 host argument-domain tests still pass. End-to-end correctness (peek non-destructive, interior-offset tail, past-end→0, read-after-peek sees all bytes, write-end rejects peek/wait, wait_readable true-with-data / false-at-EOF) is covered by the kernel `ipc::pipe` self-test `test_peek_nondestructive` (runs at boot). The two new syscall numbers extend the pipe family from the free 657+ range (the original 220-229 block is full). Used by `tee(1)` on real pipes, and by programs that inspect a pipe stream while forwarding it (log splitters, `cmd | tee >(sink) | cmd2` process-substitution pipelines). Used by Linux programs that copy file → pipe → socket (e.g. nginx, HAProxy, syslog-ng, recent versions of cat that hot-path through splice when both fds are pipes), and by language runtimes' IO layer fast paths.
  - [x] arch_prctl(2) input validation (Linux x86-64 thread-state knob): replaces the bare `errno = ENOSYS; return -1` stub in `posix/src/process.rs` with a full code-and-addr validator that handles all fifteen recognised arch_prctl codes spanning the FS/GS base setters (ARCH_SET_FS / ARCH_GET_FS / ARCH_SET_GS / ARCH_GET_GS), CPUID-fault control (ARCH_SET_CPUID / ARCH_GET_CPUID), Intel CET shadow-stack family (ARCH_CET_STATUS / ARCH_CET_ENABLE / ARCH_CET_DISABLE / ARCH_CET_LOCK / ARCH_CET_ALLOC_SHSTK), and Intel LAM (Linear Address Masking) family (ARCH_GET_UNTAG_MASK / ARCH_ENABLE_TAGGED_ADDR / ARCH_GET_MAX_TAG_BITS / ARCH_FORCE_TAGGED_SVA). The validator distinguishes EINVAL (unknown code / non-canonical user address for SET_FS|SET_GS / non-boolean for SET_CPUID / LAM width > 6), EFAULT (NULL output pointer for getters that write to `*addr`), and ENOSYS (well-formed call, arch-state subsystem not implemented). Canonical-address check uses both halves: low canonical `addr <= X86_64_CANONICAL_MAX (0x0000_7FFF_FFFF_FFFF)` OR high canonical `addr >= 0xFFFF_8000_0000_0000`; addresses in the non-canonical hole between the two are rejected since loading them into FS/GS_BASE MSR would raise #GP at the hardware level. SET_CPUID accepts only 0 (disable) or 1 (enable) per Linux's `arch/x86/kernel/process.c::set_cpuid_mode`. ARCH_ENABLE_TAGGED_ADDR caps the requested untag mask width at 6 (matches LAM57's 6 mask bits between PML5 and PML4 boundary). The getters (ARCH_GET_FS / ARCH_GET_GS / ARCH_CET_STATUS / ARCH_GET_UNTAG_MASK / ARCH_GET_MAX_TAG_BITS) all check `addr != 0` since they write the result to `*addr`. 40 new tests cover: unknown-code-EINVAL / zero-code-EINVAL / negative-code-EINVAL; SET_FS low-canonical-passes / max-low-canonical (0x7FFF_FFFF_FFFF_FFFF)-passes / non-canonical-(0x0001_0000_0000_0000)-EINVAL / high-canonical-(0xFFFF_8000_0000_0000)-passes / zero-passes (FS=0 disables FS-relative access); SET_GS non-canonical-EINVAL / low-canonical-passes; GET_FS null-EFAULT / GET_GS null-EFAULT / GET_GS valid-output-passes; SET_CPUID zero-passes / one-passes / two-EINVAL (boolean only) / u64::MAX-EINVAL; GET_CPUID zero-addr-passes (it doesn't use addr); CET_STATUS null-EFAULT / valid-passes; CET_ENABLE / CET_DISABLE / CET_LOCK / CET_ALLOC_SHSTK all-pass; GET_UNTAG_MASK null-EFAULT / valid-passes; GET_MAX_TAG_BITS null-EFAULT; ENABLE_TAGGED_ADDR widths-0-through-6-pass (loop test) / width-7-EINVAL / u64::MAX-EINVAL; FORCE_TAGGED_SVA passes; constants-all-distinct (defends against future copy-paste typos); X86_64_CANONICAL_MAX = 0x0000_7FFF_FFFF_FFFF sanity check; plus seven real-world workflow tests anchored to specific software: glibc thread setup (`__pthread_init_static_tls` calls `arch_prctl(ARCH_SET_FS, tls_block)` after `clone(CLONE_VM | CLONE_SETTLS)` — on ENOSYS glibc reports "thread-local init failed: Function not implemented" instead of crashing on FS=garbage), musl libc thread reaper (uses `arch_prctl(ARCH_GET_FS, &out)` to walk `pthread` struct on thread join — on ENOSYS falls back to `/proc/<tid>/syscall` scan), QEMU TCG userspace-mode guest `arch_prctl(ARCH_SET_GS, addr)` forwarding (on ENOSYS uses software-emulated GS register), Chrome sandbox `arch_prctl(ARCH_SET_CPUID, 0)` to disable CPUID for sandboxed code (so it can't fingerprint host CPU — on ENOSYS uses seccomp-bpf CPUID-trap fallback), Intel CET-enabled binary (`gcc -fcf-protection=full`) dynamic-linker init that calls `arch_prctl(ARCH_CET_ENABLE, 0)` — on ENOSYS linker falls back to non-CET mode (binary works but loses hardening), HWASan-instrumented binary (LLVM HWAddressSanitizer) calls `arch_prctl(ARCH_ENABLE_TAGGED_ADDR, 6)` to enable LAM57 untagging on Intel Sapphire Rapids+ — on ENOSYS falls back to software emulation, plus a buggy-uninitialised-pthread_t test (stack-allocated `pthread_t*` field never zeroed, contains stale value in the non-canonical hole `0x0000_DEAD_BEEF_1000` — must catch with EINVAL rather than letting the bad MSR load #GP). Plus updates one pre-existing test (`test_arch_prctl_get_fs_enosys`) that passed `addr=0` expecting ENOSYS — it now uses a real `&mut u64` output pointer since `addr=0` is now caught with EFAULT. Added eleven new public constants: ARCH_GET_CPUID (0x1011) / ARCH_SET_CPUID (0x1012) / ARCH_CET_STATUS (0x3001) / ARCH_CET_ENABLE (0x3002) / ARCH_CET_DISABLE (0x3003) / ARCH_CET_LOCK (0x3004) / ARCH_CET_ALLOC_SHSTK (0x3005) / ARCH_GET_UNTAG_MASK (0x4001) / ARCH_ENABLE_TAGGED_ADDR (0x4002) / ARCH_GET_MAX_TAG_BITS (0x4003) / ARCH_FORCE_TAGGED_SVA (0x4004) / X86_64_CANONICAL_MAX (0x0000_7FFF_FFFF_FFFF). **Architectural rationale** (documented in function docs): arch_prctl is the Linux x86-64 escape hatch for per-thread CPU-state knobs that don't fit any other syscall — FS/GS base used for thread-local storage by every libc, CPUID-fault control used by sandboxes to prevent CPU fingerprinting, CET shadow stack for control-flow integrity on modern Intel CPUs (Tiger Lake and newer), LAM for hardware-accelerated address tagging on Intel Sapphire Rapids+ (used by HWASan, MTE-style tools). Our microkernel design sets FS/GS base at thread spawn via the spawn-arguments capability (per `design.txt` thread model), and CET/LAM are not yet wired up to our hardware abstraction layer. The validator's job is to give Linux-compatible callers (glibc, musl, sandboxes, ASan/HWASan, QEMU, dynamic linkers) the same EINVAL/EFAULT/ENOSYS shape they see on a Linux kernel built without `CONFIG_X86_64_FS_GS_BASE` (rare but legal) or without `CONFIG_X86_CET`/`CONFIG_X86_USER_SHADOW_STACK` (the common case on pre-Tiger-Lake hardware) or without `CONFIG_X86_LAM` (the common case on pre-Sapphire-Rapids hardware). Used by every libc's thread-creation path (glibc `pthread_create` → TLS init via SET_FS; musl `__clone` via SET_FS; bionic/Android via SET_FS), every browser sandbox that disables CPUID (Chrome via `chrome_sandbox_helper`, Firefox via `sandbox_brokerLauncher`, Edge via the same Chromium codebase), every ASan/HWASan/MSan-instrumented binary's startup (uses LAM when available for fast tag-based shadow-memory lookups), every Intel CET-enabled binary built with `gcc -fcf-protection=full` or `clang -fcf-protection=full` (the default in newer distros for security-sensitive packages like sudo/su/passwd), every QEMU TCG userspace run on x86-64 host, every dynamic linker (glibc `ld.so`, musl `ld-musl-x86_64`, FreeBSD `ld-elf64.so`) that probes CET availability at process init, and every JIT compiler (V8, SpiderMonkey, OpenJDK HotSpot, .NET Core JIT) that emits CET-aware code paths conditionally based on the runtime CET check.
  - [x] umount(2) / umount2(2) input validation (POSIX/Linux mount tear-down family): replaces the two bare `errno = ENOSYS; return -1` stubs in `posix/src/process.rs` with full Linux-compatible path-and-flag validators that distinguish EFAULT (NULL path), ENOENT (empty path), ENAMETOOLONG (path runs past PATH_MAX with no NUL), EINVAL (unknown flag bits, or MNT_EXPIRE combined with MNT_FORCE/MNT_DETACH), and ENOSYS (well-formed call, mount subsystem not wired up). `umount(target)`: NULL → EFAULT; first byte NUL (empty path) → ENOENT; not NUL-terminated within `UMOUNT_PATH_MAX (4096)` bytes → ENAMETOOLONG (walked via a private byte-at-a-time `umount_cstr_len` helper that stops at `max + 1` so we can't read past the boundary); valid → ENOSYS. `umount2(target, flags)`: same path-stage checks, then `flags & ~UMOUNT2_FLAGS_VALID (MNT_FORCE|MNT_DETACH|MNT_EXPIRE|UMOUNT_NOFOLLOW = 0x0F)` → EINVAL; `MNT_EXPIRE` set alongside `MNT_FORCE | MNT_DETACH` → EINVAL (Linux's `fs/namespace.c` explicitly rejects the combo since an expiry mark conflicts with a force/detach action); valid → ENOSYS. Validation order: path first (NULL→EFAULT, empty→ENOENT, too-long→ENAMETOOLONG), then flag mask, then MNT_EXPIRE mutual-exclusion check. 31 new tests cover umount: null-EFAULT / empty-string-ENOENT / valid-path-reaches-ENOSYS / unterminated-4097-byte-path-ENAMETOOLONG / max-length-4095+NUL-path-passes (boundary test) / single-slash-passes (umount("/") form) / errno-preserved-on-validated-call; umount2: null-EFAULT / empty-string-ENOENT / unterminated-path-ENAMETOOLONG / unknown-flag-bit-0x10-EINVAL / i32::MIN-flags-EINVAL / each-valid-flag-individually-reaches-ENOSYS (MNT_FORCE, MNT_DETACH, MNT_EXPIRE alone, UMOUNT_NOFOLLOW) / FORCE+DETACH-passes (no mutex between them) / EXPIRE+FORCE-EINVAL / EXPIRE+DETACH-EINVAL / EXPIRE+NOFOLLOW-passes (NOFOLLOW unrelated to expiry) / NULL-path-vs-bad-flags-order (path-EFAULT-wins) / empty-path-vs-bad-flags-order (ENOENT-wins) / unknown-flag-vs-EXPIRE+FORCE-order (unknown-bit-fires-first); plus constants tests for UMOUNT2_FLAGS_VALID=0x0F and UMOUNT_PATH_MAX=4096; plus six real-world workflow tests anchored to specific software: systemd-shutdown's final.target sweep (calls `umount2(mount_point, MNT_FORCE | MNT_DETACH)` on every remaining mount during the shutdown sequence — on ENOSYS the tally is reported and shutdown progresses to halt() rather than looping on EINVAL), util-linux `umount -l` (lazy unmount via `umount2(path, MNT_DETACH)` — must reach ENOSYS so the user sees "Function not implemented"), autofs expire daemon (`umount2(automount_path, MNT_EXPIRE)` to mark a stale automount; on ENOSYS the expire timer falls back to a periodic retry loop), Docker container teardown via containerd-shim (`umount2(overlay_merged_path, MNT_DETACH)` on the overlayfs mount before unlinking the container dir — on ENOSYS the shim falls back to recursive rmdir leaving overlay junk for manual cleanup), `findmnt --umount` from util-linux (uses `umount2(target, UMOUNT_NOFOLLOW)` to avoid following symlinks to unintended mounts), and a buggy-shell-extension that calls `umount2(NULL, 0)` (must catch with EFAULT so the bug surfaces immediately rather than masquerading as ENOSYS); plus updates four pre-existing tests (`test_umount_returns_enosys`, `test_umount2_returns_enosys`, `test_umount_sets_enosys`, `test_umount2_sets_enosys`) that passed `NULL` expecting ENOSYS — they now pass a valid path so the ENOSYS terminal state is still exercised after the new EFAULT validation. Added two new public constants: `UMOUNT2_FLAGS_VALID = 0x0F` and `UMOUNT_PATH_MAX = 4096`, plus one private helper `umount_cstr_len(s, max) -> Option<usize>` (NUL-terminator search bounded by `max + 1` bytes so the walk stays within the caller's buffer). **Architectural rationale** (documented in function docs): umount/umount2 are the Linux side of "tear down a filesystem mount" — they look up the target by absolute path in the current namespace's mount tree and detach the matching mount object. Our microkernel design routes filesystem mounts through a capability-mediated VFS daemon (per `design.txt` filesystem section), so the kernel-side umount path doesn't go through this libc shim — userspace tools mount/unmount via the VFS daemon's capability handles, not through libc. The validators exist purely to give Linux-compatible userspace callers (every shutdown sequence, every container runtime's teardown, every automount/expire daemon, every removable-media unmount tool) the same EFAULT/ENOENT/ENAMETOOLONG/EINVAL/ENOSYS shape they expect, so their existing fallback paths fire when the syscall isn't backed. Used by systemd-shutdown (final.target unmount sweep), every container runtime's teardown path (Docker, podman, containerd, runc, crun, youki, LXC), util-linux `umount(8)` family (umount, lazy umount with -l, force with -f, findmnt --umount), autofs and amd automount expire daemons, GNOME/KDE removable-media unmount helpers (gvfs-mount, kio-mount, udisks2's filesystem-unmount path), Docker overlay teardown (containerd-shim's per-container cleanup), and every initramfs script that runs `umount -a -r` before pivot_root to detach the build-time temp filesystems.
  - [x] unshare(2) / setns(2) input validation (Linux 2.6.16 / 3.0 namespace family): replaces the two bare `errno = ENOSYS; return -1` stubs in `posix/src/process.rs` with full Linux-compatible CLONE_*-flag validators that distinguish EINVAL (unrecognised flag bit), EBADF (negative fd), and the special unshare(0) Linux-faithful no-op (returns 0 without touching errno). `unshare(flags)`: bits outside `UNSHARE_FLAGS_VALID` (the union of CLONE_THREAD|CLONE_FS|CLONE_NEWNS|CLONE_SIGHAND|CLONE_VM|CLONE_FILES|CLONE_SYSVSEM|CLONE_NEWUTS|CLONE_NEWIPC|CLONE_NEWNET|CLONE_NEWUSER|CLONE_NEWPID|CLONE_NEWCGROUP|CLONE_NEWTIME) → EINVAL — mirrors Linux's `kernel/fork.c::check_unshare_flags`; `flags == 0` → return 0 (per Linux: short-circuit when no resources need duplicating, used by util-linux's `unshare(1) --keep-caps` probe and libcontainer's feature-availability test); valid non-zero bits → ENOSYS (matches Linux built without `CONFIG_NAMESPACES`). `setns(fd, nstype)`: `fd < 0` → EBADF; bits outside `SETNS_NSTYPE_VALID` (CLONE_NEWNS|CLONE_NEWCGROUP|CLONE_NEWUTS|CLONE_NEWIPC|CLONE_NEWUSER|CLONE_NEWPID|CLONE_NEWNET|CLONE_NEWTIME — only the namespace bits, not sharing flags like CLONE_VM/CLONE_FILES which Linux explicitly rejects since setns *joins* an existing namespace rather than creating a fresh resource view) → EINVAL; `nstype == 0` is the "infer namespace type from fd" form added in Linux 3.0 and is accepted; valid → ENOSYS. Bits checked via `flags as u32` cast which preserves the bit pattern so sign-bit values like CLONE_IO (`0x8000_0000`, i.e. `i32::MIN` worth of bits when seen as signed) are reliably caught. Validation order: for setns, fd is checked first (because EBADF is the strongest "junk fd, try again" signal), then nstype. 38 new tests cover unshare: zero-returns-zero-and-preserves-errno (errno regression test for the no-op path) / each-of-the-eight-namespace-flags-reaches-ENOSYS individually (CLONE_NEWNS, CLONE_NEWUTS, CLONE_NEWIPC, CLONE_NEWPID, CLONE_NEWNET, CLONE_NEWUSER, CLONE_NEWCGROUP, CLONE_NEWTIME) / all-valid-flags-combined-reaches-ENOSYS / CLONE_IO-rejected (the sign-bit case that bare i32 sign-extension could mishandle) / CLONE_PIDFD-rejected / CLONE_SETTLS-rejected / CLONE_PARENT_SETTID-rejected / unshare(-1)-EINVAL (all bits set) / valid-bit-mixed-with-invalid-CLONE_IO-rejected / UNSHARE_FLAGS_VALID-mask-shape-equals-Linux-whitelist; setns: negative-fd-EBADF / i32::MIN-fd-EBADF / CLONE_IO-in-nstype-EINVAL / CLONE_VM-in-nstype-EINVAL / CLONE_FILES-in-nstype-EINVAL / nstype-zero-passes (infer-from-fd form) / each-namespace-type-passes (CLONE_NEWNS, CLONE_NEWPID, CLONE_NEWUSER, CLONE_NEWTIME) / all-valid-nstypes-combined-passes / setns(3,-1)-EINVAL / fd-validation-before-nstype-validation-ordering / SETNS_NSTYPE_VALID-mask-shape-(no-sharing-flags); plus seven real-world workflow tests anchored to specific software: util-linux `unshare(1) --user --map-root-user` probe (calls `unshare(CLONE_NEWUSER | CLONE_NEWNS)` — on ENOSYS, prints "unshare: unshare failed: Function not implemented" so users know to upgrade rather than seeing "Invalid argument"), systemd-nspawn container-init full-namespace setup (`unshare(CLONE_NEWPID | CLONE_NEWNS | CLONE_NEWUTS | CLONE_NEWIPC | CLONE_NEWNET)` — falls back to cgroup-only isolation on ENOSYS), Firefox content-process sandbox (`unshare(CLONE_NEWUSER | CLONE_NEWPID | CLONE_NEWNET)` — falls back to seccomp-only filtering in `sandbox_brokerLauncher` on ENOSYS), nsenter `--net=/proc/<pid>/ns/net` flow (opens net-ns file, calls `setns(fd, CLONE_NEWNET)` — must reach ENOSYS for the standard "Function not implemented" message), runc `nsexec` cgo helper joining a container (uses `setns(fd, 0)` letting kernel infer the type — must accept the inferred-type form), CRIU `criu restore` re-entering target's namespaces (`setns(pidfd, CLONE_NEWPID | CLONE_NEWNET | CLONE_NEWNS)` — Linux 5.8+ multi-nstype-on-pidfd form, must validate the combined mask), plus a "share flags alone (CLONE_VM|CLONE_FILES without CLONE_THREAD) are accepted" regression test (Stack Overflow snippet that's semantically meaningless but syntactically valid — Linux still passes the bitmask check, so we do too; the bug is in the caller's understanding, not the validator). Also updated two pre-existing tests (`test_unshare_returns_enosys`, `test_unshare_sets_enosys`) that called `unshare(0)` expecting ENOSYS — they now use `CLONE_NEWNS` as the canonical "ENOSYS-reaching" flag since `unshare(0)` became a successful no-op. Added two new public constants: `UNSHARE_FLAGS_VALID` (the unshare-whitelist mask) and `SETNS_NSTYPE_VALID` (the setns-namespace-types mask). **Architectural rationale** (documented in function docs): Linux namespaces are the kernel-side mechanism for container isolation — each unshare/setns call creates or joins a per-process resource view (mounts, hostname, IPC keys, PID space, network stack, user IDs, cgroup tree, monotonic clock). Our microkernel design takes a different approach: each process is a capability-rooted sandbox from `posix_spawn`, with capability handles serving the same isolation role that namespace fds do on Linux. We won't implement a Linux-compatible namespace subsystem because the kernel-side complexity (per-namespace mount tables, PID translation across namespace boundaries, network-stack duplication, user-namespace ID mapping with capability bounding) doesn't fit our design and isn't needed when the same isolation is delivered via capabilities. The validators exist to give Linux-compatible callers (every container runtime, systemd-nspawn, util-linux, Firefox/Chrome sandboxes, CRIU) the same EINVAL/EBADF/ENOSYS shape they get on a `CONFIG_NAMESPACES=n` Linux kernel, so their existing "no namespaces → use alternative isolation" fallback paths fire. Used by every container runtime (runc, crun, youki, containerd, podman, LXC, systemd-nspawn), every browser sandbox (Firefox via `sandbox_brokerLauncher`, Chrome via `chrome-sandbox`, Edge via the same Chromium codebase), every snapshot/restore tool (CRIU, dmtcp), every util-linux command using namespaces (unshare(1), nsenter(1), lsns(1)), every CI sandbox runner (Bazel, nix-build's `__sandbox` mode, GitHub Actions' runner-image isolation), and every userspace tool that probes namespace-availability at startup before falling back to a non-isolated code path.
  - [x] pidfd_open / pidfd_send_signal / pidfd_getfd input validation (Linux 5.3+ `<sys/syscall.h>` pidfd family): replaces the three bare `errno = ENOSYS; return -1` stubs with full Linux-compatible argument-domain validators that distinguish EINVAL (bad pid / bad flag bits / bad signal range / siginfo mismatch), EBADF (negative fd), and ENOSYS (arguments accepted, kernel subsystem not wired up). `pidfd_open(pid, flags)`: `pid <= 0` → EINVAL (Linux's `kernel/pid.c::pidfd_create` rejects zero and negative PIDs since the syscall doesn't accept the "process group" convention used elsewhere); `flags & ~PIDFD_OPEN_FLAGS_VALID` → EINVAL where `PIDFD_OPEN_FLAGS_VALID = PIDFD_NONBLOCK (0o4000, added Linux 5.10) | PIDFD_THREAD (0o200, added Linux 6.2)`; arguments validated → ENOSYS. `pidfd_send_signal(pidfd, sig, info, flags)`: `flags != 0` → EINVAL (no flag bits are defined for this syscall in Linux); `pidfd < 0` → EBADF; `sig < 0 || sig > PIDFD_SIG_MAX (64)` → EINVAL (matches Linux's `_NSIG = 64` ceiling on x86-64, with `sig == 0` allowed as the permission/existence probe); when `info != NULL`, reads the `si_signo` field via `core::ptr::read_unaligned` (defends against alignment-1 caller pointers) and rejects `si_signo != sig` with EINVAL (matches Linux's `kernel/signal.c::do_pidfd_send_signal` → `copy_siginfo_from_user` cross-check, which catches the common C-wrapper bug of forgetting to set `si_signo` to match the outer signal number); valid → ENOSYS. `pidfd_getfd(pidfd, targetfd, flags)`: `flags != 0` → EINVAL; `pidfd < 0` → EBADF; `targetfd < 0` → EBADF; valid → ENOSYS. Validation order is deliberately chosen to match Linux exactly: flags-mask first (because it's the cheapest check and the most likely to fire on unsupported-bit forward-compat probes), then fd validity (because EBADF is the strongest signal "this fd is junk, retry with a fresh one"), then signal range, then info siginfo cross-check. 42 new tests cover pidfd_open: zero-pid-EINVAL / negative-pid-EINVAL / i32::MIN-EINVAL / i32::MAX-pid-passes-to-ENOSYS / unknown-flag-bit-EINVAL / high-bit-flag-EINVAL / PIDFD_THREAD-passes / PIDFD_NONBLOCK|PIDFD_THREAD-passes / flag-constant-values-(0o4000 = O_NONBLOCK, 0o200 = O_EXCL) / valid-mask-equals-union / pid-validation-runs-before-flag-validation (both invalid → EINVAL for pid); pidfd_send_signal: nonzero-flags-EINVAL / 0x80000000-flag-EINVAL / negative-fd-EBADF / i32::MIN-fd-EBADF / negative-sig-EINVAL / sig-65-EINVAL / sig-64-passes-to-ENOSYS / sig-0-permission-probe-passes / siginfo-mismatch-EINVAL (outer sig=9, si_signo=11) / siginfo-match-passes / sig-zero-with-nonzero-si_signo-EINVAL / flags-before-fd-ordering / fd-before-sig-ordering; pidfd_getfd: nonzero-flags-EINVAL / 0x80000000-flag-EINVAL / negative-pidfd-EBADF / i32::MIN-pidfd-EBADF / negative-targetfd-EBADF / i32::MIN-targetfd-EBADF / i32::MAX-both-fds-passes-to-ENOSYS / flags-before-pidfd-ordering / pidfd-before-targetfd-ordering; constants tests for PIDFD_SIG_MAX=64 and PIDFD_OPEN_FLAGS_VALID mask shape; one errno-preserved-on-validated-call regression test; plus six real-world workflow tests anchored to specific software: systemd's `sd_pidfd_get_inode_id` probe (calls `pidfd_open(getpid(), PIDFD_NONBLOCK)` on init — on ENOSYS, systemd's fallback ladder uses cgroup.events poll instead, the standard pattern for service-manager liveness tracking on kernels < 5.3), runc/crun container runtime namespace-join (opens `pidfd_open(container_init_pid, 0)` to get a race-free handle for `setns`-style joins — on ENOSYS, falls back to opening `/proc/<pid>/ns/pid` directly with the pid-reuse race window that pidfd was designed to eliminate), Go 1.22 runtime probe (`os/exec.Cmd.Start` with `Cancel` field set triggers a pidfd probe via `pidfd_open(getpid(), 0)` — must reach ENOSYS so Go falls back to its older PID-based child tracking instead of erroring out at process start), strace `-y` cross-process fd inspection (`pidfd_getfd(tracee_pidfd, tracee_fd, 0)` to import a fd from the tracee — Linux 5.6+ feature; on ENOSYS, strace silently disables the `-y` "show what fd points to" decoration), util-linux `kill --pidfd=<fd> <sig>` (uses `pidfd_send_signal(fd, sig, NULL, 0)` with NULL info — must validate cleanly and reach ENOSYS for the user-facing error to be "pidfd kill not supported by this kernel" instead of a wrong-flags message), JDK 22's `ProcessHandleImpl` Linux-side init (opens a self-pidfd with `PIDFD_NONBLOCK | PIDFD_THREAD` to detect kernel feature level — on ENOSYS, JDK falls back to the older `/proc/<pid>` polling path for `Process.onExit()` without the PID-reuse race protection), plus a buggy-zero-initialised-siginfo regression test (caller passes a stack-allocated `SiginfoT` with si_signo defaulted to 0 but outer sig is 9 → must catch with EINVAL so the bug is loud rather than silently delivering the wrong signal). Added three new public constants: `PIDFD_THREAD = 0o200` (matches Linux's O_EXCL repurposing in 6.2+), `PIDFD_OPEN_FLAGS_VALID = PIDFD_NONBLOCK | PIDFD_THREAD`, `PIDFD_SIG_MAX = 64`. **Architectural rationale** (documented in function docs): pidfd is Linux's fix for the "PID reuse race" that has plagued POSIX since 1970 — once you `kill(pid, sig)`, between the moment the target process exits and your signal lands, the kernel may reuse that PID for a fresh, unrelated process. pidfd gives you a refcounted handle that stays valid past process exit (until you close it), and `pidfd_send_signal`/`pidfd_getfd` operate on that handle atomically with respect to PID reuse. Our microkernel design solves this differently: every process is referenced by a capability handle from the moment of `posix_spawn`, and capabilities are unforgeable + race-immune by construction. pidfd-equivalent operations therefore route through our capability layer, not through a separate Linux-shaped fd. The validators exist to give pidfd-using callers (systemd, runc, Go runtime, JDK, strace, util-linux kill) clean errno feedback so their existing "no pidfd → use legacy path" fallbacks fire correctly. **Status**: matches what `pidfd_*` returns on Linux kernels < 5.3 (or kernels built without `CONFIG_PIDFD` — which Linux removed as a CONFIG in 5.10, making pidfd unconditional, but the syscall-not-supported errno shape remains the canonical "no pidfd here" signal). Used by every container runtime built since Docker 20.10 / runc 1.0.0-rc94 (runc, crun, youki, containerd's task service), every modern service manager (systemd 245+, s6-rc, OpenRC's experimental supervise backend), every language runtime that handles SIGCHLD efficiently (Go 1.22+, JDK 22+, .NET 8+, Rust's `tokio::process` since 1.20), every debugger supporting cross-process fd inspection (strace 5.7+, lldb on Linux, dlv with --headless), and the util-linux/procps-ng kill/pkill/killall family for pidfd-mode invocations.
  - [x] NDBM database-API input validation (`<ndbm.h>`): replaces all eleven bare ENOSYS / EINVAL / NULL_DATUM stubs (`dbm_open`, `dbm_close`, `dbm_store`, `dbm_fetch`, `dbm_delete`, `dbm_firstkey`, `dbm_nextkey`, `dbm_error`, `dbm_clearerr`, `dbm_dirfno`, `dbm_pagfno`) with full Linux-compatible input validators that walk the caller's `Datum` shapes and path strings before returning ENOSYS for valid-but-unsupported calls. `dbm_open(file, open_flags, file_mode)`: NULL `file` → EFAULT; first byte of `file` is NUL (empty path) → ENOENT; `file` not NUL-terminated within `DBM_PATH_MAX (4096)` bytes → ENAMETOOLONG (walked via a byte-at-a-time `cstr_len` helper that stops at the max so we can't read past the boundary); valid → ENOSYS. `dbm_store(db, key, content, store_mode)`: validates the `Datum` shapes via private helpers — `validate_key(key)` rejects `key.dsize == 0` (POSIX-defined sentinel for "deleted slot" in the original 4.3BSD layout), NULL `key.dptr` with positive `dsize`, `key.dsize > DBM_MAX_DATUM_SIZE (65536)` (real NDBM caps at the .pag file's page size — 1024 bytes in 4.4BSD; we use 64 KiB as a generous upper bound that still rejects sign-extended-length / junk-from-corrupt-struct cases), `validate_value(content)` rejects NULL `dptr` with positive `dsize` (zero-length presence-only value with NULL dptr is permitted), `content.dsize > DBM_MAX_DATUM_SIZE` → EINVAL; `store_mode` not in `{DBM_INSERT=0, DBM_REPLACE=1}` → EINVAL; valid → EINVAL (no db open since `dbm_open` never succeeds — matches glibc's "bad handle" path). `dbm_delete(db, key)`: same key validation; valid → EINVAL. `dbm_fetch(db, key)`: returns `NULL_DATUM` for everything (no error channel besides the null pointer in the returned datum, per POSIX — even invalid keys just produce a null result). `dbm_firstkey`, `dbm_nextkey`: return `NULL_DATUM`. `dbm_close`, `dbm_clearerr`: void, no-op. `dbm_error`: returns 0. `dbm_dirfno`, `dbm_pagfno`: return -1. 22 new tests cover dbm_open: null-file-EFAULT / empty-file-ENOENT / valid-reaches-ENOSYS / unterminated-path-ENAMETOOLONG (a 4097-byte buffer of `a`s with no NUL); dbm_store: zero-key-EINVAL / null-key-dptr-EINVAL / huge-key-EINVAL / null-value-dptr-with-size-EINVAL / null-value-dptr-zero-size-OK-shape / huge-value-EINVAL / unknown-mode-EINVAL / insert-mode-falls-through / replace-mode-falls-through; dbm_delete: zero-key-EINVAL / null-key-dptr-EINVAL / valid-falls-through; dbm_fetch: returns-NULL_DATUM-on-valid-key / returns-NULL_DATUM-on-invalid-key; plus four real-world workflow tests: sendmail `newaliases` rebuilds `/etc/aliases.db` via `dbm_open("/etc/aliases", O_RDWR|O_CREAT, 0644)` — on ENOSYS, logs "newaliases: NDBM not available" and the postmaster falls back to hash-table lookup of `/etc/aliases`; postfix `map_type=dbm` fallback (postfix's `lookup_dbm()` probes `dbm_open()` for each configured map at startup — on ENOSYS the admin must switch to `map_type=hash` or `btree` in main.cf); GNU gdbm `libgdbm_compat.so` shim (translates `dbm_*` calls onto its own GDBM backend — on a system without the compat shim, callers fall through to our stubs and the compat layer returns -1 to its caller); CPython 3.x `dbm.ndbm` module probe (attempts `dbm_open()` lazily on first use — on ENOSYS, raises `dbm.error: NDBM not available` and the Python program falls back to `dbm.dumb`); plus a "typical full open/store/fetch/close workflow" test that confirms the entire call chain returns sensible errors at every step; plus errno-preserved-on-success regression test. Added three new public constants: `DBM_MAX_DATUM_SIZE = 65536`, `DBM_PATH_MAX = 4096`, and the documented `DBM_INSERT/DBM_REPLACE` (already present). Added two private helpers: `cstr_len(s, max)` (NUL-terminator search bounded by `max`) and `validate_key`/`validate_value` (Datum shape checkers). **Status in Linux**: NDBM is a 1980s-era key-value database from 4.3BSD, standardized in POSIX.1-2001, marked LEGACY in POSIX.1-2008. Modern code uses SQLite, Berkeley DB, LMDB, or flat JSON/CBOR files. Real users in 2026: sendmail's alias database on BSD ports, postfix's `dbm` map type when explicitly configured (default is `hash` or `btree`), GNU dbm's `gdbm_compat` shim, the few remaining `AnyDBM_File::NDBM_File` Perl scripts, CPython's `dbm.ndbm` module before it switched its default to `dbm.gnu`, and Tcl's `dict` extension on legacy BSD builds. We do not implement an NDBM backend (would require .dir/.pag file format support, hash bucket management, key/value pair packing, recovery journal — a real backend that nobody would actually use). The validator's role is to give configurable-backend callers (postfix, Perl AnyDBM_File, Python dbm.ndbm) meaningful errno so they fall back to their alternative storage path. Used by every BSD-derived postfix/sendmail configuration that still uses NDBM aliases (mostly legacy installs on OpenBSD/FreeBSD/NetBSD that aren't getting migrated), every Perl script using `dbmopen()` (deprecated since Perl 5.10 but still in CPAN modules like `Apache::Session::DBM`), every CPython program that imports `dbm` and lets it pick a backend (`dbm.whichdb` queries each backend including `dbm.ndbm` — on ENOSYS, `whichdb` skips NDBM and tries GDBM/SDBM/dumb), every legacy Solaris-port build that uses `AC_CHECK_HEADERS([ndbm.h])` to autoconf-detect "yes, NDBM is available," and the `dbm-deb` package's compat shim used by old Debian aliases-database tooling.
  - [x] STREAMS API input validation (`<stropts.h>`): replaces the six bare `errno = ENOSYS; return -1` stubs (`putmsg`, `putpmsg`, `getmsg`, `getpmsg`, `fattach`, `fdetach`) plus the bare `isastream` no-op with full Linux-compatible input validators that distinguish EBADF (bad fd), EFAULT (NULL required pointers), ENOENT (empty path), EINVAL (bad flag/band/shape), and ENOSYS (well-formed call, STREAMS unimplemented). `putmsg(fd, ctlptr, dataptr, flags)`: `fd < 0` → EBADF; both `ctlptr == NULL && dataptr == NULL` → EINVAL (POSIX requires at least one message part); `flags & ~PUTMSG_FLAGS_VALID (RS_HIPRI=0x01)` → EINVAL; valid → ENOSYS. `putpmsg(fd, ctlptr, dataptr, band, flags)`: same fd/null/flag checks plus `band < 0 || band > STREAM_BAND_MAX (255)` → EINVAL (POSIX `_POSIX_STREAM_MAX` and Solaris `STRMSGSZ` both cap at 255); `flags & ~PUTPMSG_FLAGS_VALID (MSG_HIPRI|MSG_BAND)` → EINVAL; `MSG_HIPRI` set with nonzero band → EINVAL (high-priority messages live on the out-of-band path, not a priority band — Solaris's `streamio.c` explicitly rejects this combo); valid → ENOSYS. `getmsg(fd, ctlptr, dataptr, flagsp)`: `fd < 0` → EBADF; `flagsp == NULL` → EFAULT (caller passes flags in-out by pointer — without an address we can't write back); valid → ENOSYS. `getpmsg(fd, ctlptr, dataptr, bandp, flagsp)`: `fd < 0` → EBADF; either `bandp == NULL || flagsp == NULL` → EFAULT; `*flagsp & ~GETPMSG_FLAGS_VALID (MSG_HIPRI|MSG_ANY|MSG_BAND)` → EINVAL (read via `core::ptr::read_unaligned` so alignment-1 pointers don't UB); valid → ENOSYS. `isastream(fd)`: `fd < 0` → EBADF (matches POSIX's "the function shall fail" clause); non-negative → 0 (cleanly says "not a STREAMS device"). `fattach(fd, path)`: `fd < 0` → EBADF; NULL path → EFAULT; first byte of path == NUL (empty string) → ENOENT; valid → ENOSYS. `fdetach(path)`: NULL path → EFAULT; empty path → ENOENT; valid → ENOSYS. 40 new tests cover every error path for each function plus four real-world workflow tests: a Solaris-to-Linux network-daemon port (sends `T_OPT_DATA_REQ` via `putmsg(fd, ctl, data, 0)` — on ENOSYS the autoconf-generated fallback disables the STREAMS code path and reverts to plain BSD sockets, the standard porting pattern for TLI/XTI users like Sybase netlibrary and NetManage's PC-NFS server), an AIX TLI-compat-layer probe (`getpmsg(fd, NULL, NULL, &band, &flag)` with `flag = MSG_ANY` to read `T_DATA_IND` messages — on ENOSYS, the AIX-compat shim disables TLI and falls back to BSD sockets, used by IBM Db2 and Tivoli Storage Manager when ported to Linux), the `isastream` probe in libc init (glibc's `ttyname(3)` historically pre-flighted `isastream(fd)` on the controlling terminal — Linux glibc just returns 0, we match cleanly), and a Solaris autofs `fattach` streams-pipe mount (the old autofs streams-mount helper mounted a pipe at `/var/run/streams/autofs` — on ENOSYS the helper falls back to UNIX-domain-socket bind at the same path); plus two errno-preserved-on-validation-success regression tests (one for putmsg, one for getpmsg). Also added three new public constants: `STREAM_BAND_MAX = 255`, `PUTMSG_FLAGS_VALID = RS_HIPRI`, `PUTPMSG_FLAGS_VALID = MSG_HIPRI | MSG_BAND`, `GETPMSG_FLAGS_VALID = MSG_HIPRI | MSG_ANY | MSG_BAND`. **Architectural rationale** (documented in module docs): Linux has never supported STREAMS — glibc's `stropts.h` stubs all return ENOSYS. STREAMS is a System V mechanism for stacking protocol modules at the kernel-pipe level (`I_PUSH`/`I_POP`/`I_LINK`/`I_UNLINK`), incompatible with Linux's socket-based networking and with our Channel IPC + io_uring + sockets design. Our position matches Linux glibc: STREAMS will never be implemented. The validators exist purely to give Solaris-port and AIX-compat callers meaningful errno feedback so their existing fallback paths fire — `T_OPT_DATA_REQ` -> BSD socket, TLI -> sockets, streams-pipe mount -> UNIX-domain bind. Used by every Solaris-to-Linux port of TLI/XTI-based network code (older Sybase netlibrary versions, NetManage's PC-NFS server, Tivoli Storage Manager's TCP-stream code), every AIX-compat shim's TLI fallback (IBM Db2 LUW on Linux, IBM HACMP cluster manager), glibc's historical `ttyname(3)` `isastream` pre-flight, the FUSE-related `mount(8)` paths on porting tools that probe for streams-pipe mounts before falling back to bind-mounts, and every legacy `<stropts.h>` build that gets autoconfigured "yes I have stropts" by `AC_CHECK_HEADERS([stropts.h])` and then fails to link without our stubs.
  - [x] ioperm(2)/iopl(2) syscall input validation (`<sys/io.h>`): replaces the two bare `errno = ENOSYS; return -1` stubs in `ioperm()`/`iopl()` with Linux-compatible input validators that distinguish "bad arguments" (EINVAL), "lacks capability" (EPERM), "well-formed but no kernel support" (ENOSYS), and "well-formed no-op" (return 0). `ioperm(from, num, turn_on)`: `num == 0` → return 0 (Linux's `arch/x86/kernel/ioport.c::sys_ioperm` short-circuits when the range is empty — nothing to do); `from + num` overflows u64 → EINVAL; `from + num > IO_BITMAP_BITS (65536)` → EINVAL (x86 has exactly 64 KiB of port address space, anything beyond is malformed); `turn_on != 0` on a valid range → EPERM (matches Linux's `CAP_SYS_RAWIO` gate; in our microkernel design we don't grant CAP_SYS_RAWIO to anyone — port access is mediated by the capability system, not the I/O bitmap); `turn_on == 0` on a valid range → return 0 (clearing a permission we never granted is a harmless no-op, same as Linux). `iopl(level)`: `level < 0` or `level > 3` → EINVAL (only rings 0–3 exist on x86; anything else is malformed); valid → ENOSYS (matches modern Linux 5.5+ which deprecated the syscall and now returns ENOSYS regardless of level). 25 new tests cover ioperm: zero-num-success / zero-num-zero-from-success / range-overflow-EINVAL / range-beyond-64k-EINVAL / exactly-64k-OK (boundary) / serial-port-turn-on-EPERM (the COM1 0x3F8+8 case) / turn-off-valid-range-success / turn-off-with-arbitrary-truthy-value (any nonzero treated as "grant access" → EPERM); iopl level-too-high-EINVAL / negative-EINVAL / int-min-EINVAL / each-valid-level-reaches-ENOSYS (loops 0..=3); plus four real-world workflow tests: Xorg PS/2 input driver init (`ioperm(0x60, 16, 1)` — Xorg's old xf86-input-mouse/keyboard drivers claim PS/2 controller ports at startup, fall back to `/dev/input/event*` on EPERM), dosemu2 startup IOPL probe (`iopl(3)` to see if it can run DOS programs with direct port access — on ENOSYS, falls back to v86 emulation path), setpci PCI-config-space port-window drop (`ioperm(0xCF8, 8, 0)` — valid range with turn_on=0, must succeed silently), legacy parallel-port LP1 claim (`ioperm(0x378, 3, 1)` for the IBM PC LPT1 port range — userspace parport drivers fall back to `/dev/parport0` on EPERM); plus errno-preserved-on-success regression test (confirms `ioperm` returning 0 leaves the prior errno value untouched, matching POSIX's rule that successful calls must not clobber errno). Also added two new public constants: `IO_BITMAP_BITS = 65536` (matches Linux's `arch/x86/include/asm/desc.h`) and `IOPL_LEVEL_MAX = 3`. **Architectural rationale** (documented in module docs): Per `design.txt` this is a microkernel — drivers run in userspace and access hardware via the capability system, not via a kernel-managed I/O bitmap. There is no plan to implement either syscall properly because there is no kernel-side privilege escalation step for these to enable. The validator's job is purely to give Linux-compatible errno feedback to legacy code that probes for port-I/O access (the X.Org server, dosemu2, qemu in TCG mode when emulating real-mode access, the dpdk userspace network framework's UIO fallback, the libpci library's hostbridge probe, the obsolete `parport-userland` package, the lm-sensors `i2c-dev` fallback for legacy SMBus, the rtkit-daemon's old direct-port-access mode, the gpm console mouse daemon's serial-mouse code path) so those callers see the same EPERM/EINVAL/ENOSYS the Linux kernel returns and fire their existing fallback paths (UIO devices, /dev/input/event*, /dev/parport*, vfio-pci, capability-mediated MMIO). The inline port-I/O helpers (`inb`/`inw`/`inl`/`outb`/`outw`/`outl`) remain as their existing stub implementations because they aren't syscalls — they're inline functions kept around so legacy code that references them compiles.
  - [x] sysctl(2) syscall input validation (`<sys/sysctl.h>`): replaces the bare `errno = ENOSYS; return -1` stub in `sysctl(args)` with a full `__sysctl_args`-shape validator that walks every reachable field of the caller's struct before returning the Linux-5.5+ ENOSYS. NULL `args` → EFAULT; the struct is then read via `core::ptr::read_unaligned` so an alignment-1 args pointer doesn't UB; `args.nlen <= 0` → EINVAL (a sysctl path must have ≥1 component — `CTL_KERN` alone is the smallest valid path); `args.nlen > CTL_MAXNAME (10)` → ENOTDIR (matches Linux's `do_sysctl` which used ENOTDIR for "path too deep" because internally each name component dereferences through the sysctl directory tree); `args.name == NULL && args.nlen > 0` → EFAULT (positive length must point at a real name array); `args.oldval != NULL && args.oldlenp == NULL` → EFAULT (the kernel can't write the response or learn the buffer size without a non-NULL length pointer); `args.newval == NULL && args.newlen != 0` → EFAULT (size set without a buffer); `args.newval != NULL && args.newlen == 0` → EINVAL (zero-length write with a buffer is meaningless — Linux's `do_sysctl` explicitly rejects this); `args.newlen > SYSCTL_MAX_NEWLEN (65536)` → E2BIG (sanity cap — even the largest legitimate sysctl write, an entire route table dump, fits well under 64 KiB); all valid → ENOSYS. 19 new tests cover: null-args-EFAULT / zero-nlen-EINVAL / negative-nlen-EINVAL / huge-nlen-ENOTDIR / nlen-at-max-OK / null-name-with-positive-nlen-EFAULT / oldval-without-oldlenp-EFAULT / oldval-with-oldlenp-OK / null-newval-with-nonzero-newlen-EFAULT / nonnull-newval-zero-newlen-EINVAL / huge-newlen-E2BIG / newlen-at-max-OK / read-only-call-OK / size-only-query-OK; plus three real-world workflow tests: glibc's `__sysctl(CTL_KERN, KERN_OSRELEASE)` feature probe (glibc ≤ 2.31's `sysdeps/unix/sysv/linux/sysctl.c` calls this as a "do we have the syscall?" check before falling back to reading `/proc/sys/kernel/osrelease` — on ENOSYS, glibc's fallback path opens the proc file directly), legacy BSD-derived hostname-setter (older `sendmail` configs, pre-systemd `/etc/rc.d/rc.sysinit` scripts on slackware/openrc-init: write `KERN_HOSTNAME` via sysctl, fall back to `sethostname(2)` on ENOSYS), and SystemTap/Valgrind kernel-version probe (size-only query: `oldval==NULL` with `*oldlenp==0` to ask "how big a buffer do I need?" — on ENOSYS, falls back to `/proc/version`); plus a "malformed args detected before ENOSYS" regression test that confirms a path-too-deep nlen surfaces as ENOTDIR rather than the more generic ENOSYS, plus errno-set-to-ENOSYS-on-validation-success regression test. Also added two new public constants used by the validator: `CTL_MAXNAME = 10` (matches Linux's `<linux/sysctl.h>`) and `SYSCTL_MAX_NEWLEN = 65536`. **Status in Linux**: the `sysctl(2)` syscall was **removed entirely from Linux 5.5** (April 2020) — every call now returns `-ENOSYS` regardless of arguments. Before 5.5, the kernel forwarded the call to the `/proc/sys` parser, which was always buggy under nlen edge cases, and the `compat_sys_sysctl` shim was the source of multiple CVEs (CVE-2010-2240, CVE-2009-0029). Userspace migrated to reading and writing `/proc/sys/<path>` files directly years before the removal. We follow Linux 5.5+'s modern behavior (well-formed → ENOSYS) while still validating the args shape so that "feature probe" callers (glibc's `__sysctl`, Valgrind's kernel-info probe, the `sysctl(8)` userspace utility's `--system` mode that reads `/etc/sysctl.d/*.conf` and applies entries via the syscall before falling back to `/proc/sys` writes) see meaningful errno feedback on genuinely malformed inputs. Used by glibc ≤ 2.31 (still in production on RHEL 8, Ubuntu 20.04, Debian 11 base systems), Valgrind's tool-internal kernel-version probe, SystemTap's `runtime/sysctl.c`, the legacy `procps-ng sysctl(8)` `--system` mode (recent versions skip the syscall and go straight to `/proc/sys`), every musl-libc-based program that still has `__sysctl` references in its old build target, the `klibc` minimal libc used in dracut initramfs, the BSD-derived `sysctl(3)` wrapper in some Linux ports of FreeBSD utilities, and Wine's Linux compatibility layer when emulating BSD/macOS `sysctl(3)` calls from Windows binaries (Wine's `dlls/ntdll/unix/system.c` probes for the syscall before falling back to per-/proc/sys/-file emulation).
  - [x] userfaultfd syscall input validation (`<linux/userfaultfd.h>`): replaces the bare `errno = ENOSYS; return -1` stub in `userfaultfd(flags: i32) -> i32` with a Linux-compatible flag validator. Any flag bit outside `UFFD_FLAGS_VALID` (the OR of `O_CLOEXEC = 0x80000` | `O_NONBLOCK = 0x800` | `UFFD_USER_MODE_ONLY = 1`) → EINVAL — matches the kernel's `fs/userfaultfd.c::sys_userfaultfd`'s `if (flags & ~UFFD_SHARED_FCNTL_FLAGS) return -EINVAL` rejection; valid → ENOSYS. The `flags` parameter is declared `i32` to match the Linux C signature but Linux treats it as a bitfield, so we cast through `u32` for the mask check — this means `i32::MIN` (sign bit set) and `-1` (all bits set) both correctly trip the EINVAL path because their high bits are outside the valid mask, matching the kernel. Linux 5.11+'s `UFFD_USER_MODE_ONLY` (added to let unprivileged callers create uffds that only receive user-mode faults, fixing the original userfaultfd CVE-2016-3070 attack surface where unprivileged code could trap kernel-mode page-fault paths and slow them down for side-channel attacks) is included in the valid mask. 24 new tests cover: unknown-flag-EINVAL (bit 2 = 0x4 is outside the mask), high-bit-EINVAL (`i32::MIN`), all-bits-set-EINVAL (`-1`), unknown-bit-combined-with-valid-EINVAL (Linux uses `& ~VALID` not `& VALID`, so one bad bit poisons the whole word), zero-flags-reaches-ENOSYS, each-single-valid-flag-reaches-ENOSYS (O_CLOEXEC alone, O_NONBLOCK alone, USER_MODE_ONLY alone), all-three-valid-flags-reaches-ENOSYS, plus four real-world workflow tests: CRIU 3.x lazy-restore probe (calls `userfaultfd(O_CLOEXEC|O_NONBLOCK)` at process-restore time — on ENOSYS, CRIU falls back to the eager-copy restore path and prints "Warning: lazy-pages mode disabled, kernel lacks userfaultfd"), QEMU 8.x postcopy live-migration setup (`userfaultfd(O_CLOEXEC)` early in src/migration/postcopy-ram.c — on ENOSYS, QEMU logs "postcopy-ram: userfaultfd not available, disabling postcopy" and falls back to precopy-only migration), the kernel's own `tools/testing/selftests/mm/userfaultfd.c` selftest (opens `userfaultfd(USER_MODE_ONLY|O_CLOEXEC|O_NONBLOCK)` and bails with "kernel does not support uffd" on -ENOSYS), and OpenJDK HotSpot ZGC's concurrent-relocation probe (calls `userfaultfd(O_CLOEXEC)` to see if userspace-handled write barriers are possible — on ENOSYS, ZGC picks its fallback marking mode); plus errno-set-to-ENOSYS-on-validation-success regression test (confirms the validation-success path explicitly sets ENOSYS rather than leaking through whatever errno was set before the call). **Architectural rationale** (documented in module docs): A real userfaultfd implementation requires deep kernel hooks — the page-fault handler must be able to suspend the faulting thread and deliver a notification to the userfaultfd file descriptor's reader, the VMA range must be tagged so the MM core knows to take the slow path, UFFDIO_COPY/UFFDIO_ZEROPAGE/UFFDIO_CONTINUE need to atomically install a page into another process's page tables, and UFFDIO_WRITEPROTECT needs to fiddle with the W bit on existing PTEs and flush remote TLBs. None of this exists in our microkernel today (the MM core supports demand-zero and COW but not "deliver the fault to userspace and block"). Until we add the userfaultfd subsystem, returning ENOSYS lets every real caller's existing fallback fire: CRIU restores eagerly, QEMU migrates precopy-only, V8's incremental marking uses its software-only path, Hotspot's GC tuner picks a non-userfaultfd collector, and dirty-page tracking tools (criu-pre-dump for incremental backup, virt-p2v for physical-to-virtual conversion, the postcopy-recover protocol in libvirt) fall back to soft-dirty PTE tracking via /proc/PID/clear_refs. Used by CRIU's lazy-restore (the postcopy migration model where pages stream in after the process is already running), QEMU's postcopy live migration (production VM live-migration in OpenStack, Proxmox, oVirt), the libuserfaultfd selftest, the kernel's mm/userfaultfd selftest harness, OpenJDK ZGC and Shenandoah GC's concurrent-relocation modes (Java 11+ low-latency garbage collectors), Boehm GC's incremental mode, .NET's server GC, V8's incremental marking, Hotspot's pre-touch elimination, the Rust `userfaultfd` crate (v0.8+, used by Firefox's incremental compilation), the Python `pyuserfaultfd` binding, and every modern container live-migration tool (runc-checkpoint, containerd-live-migrate, kata-live-migrate, podman --live-migrate).
  - [x] kernel module syscall input validation (`<linux/module.h>` / `<sys/syscall.h>`): replaces three previously-naked ENOSYS stubs (`init_module` was missing entirely from the prior `linux_module.rs` — only `finit_module`/`delete_module` had stubs that did nothing but set `errno = ENOSYS`) with a full Linux-compatible input validator. `init_module(module_image, len, params)`: NULL `module_image` → EFAULT; NULL `params` → EFAULT (Linux requires `""` not NULL — empty string is a valid param vector, but the pointer itself must point at a real NUL byte); `len == 0` → EINVAL (a zero-byte module image is malformed — the smallest valid Linux module ELF is several hundred bytes); `len > 256 MiB` → E2BIG (sanity cap — even the largest real-world kernel modules like nvidia.ko at ~50 MiB or zfs.ko at ~10 MiB fit well under this; rejects callers passing accidentally-huge values, e.g. an `mmap` length variable substituted in by mistake); valid → ENOSYS. `finit_module(fd, params, flags)`: `fd < 0` → EBADF; NULL `params` → EFAULT; any flag bit outside `MODULE_INIT_FLAGS_VALID` (the OR of `MODULE_INIT_IGNORE_MODVERSIONS=1` | `MODULE_INIT_IGNORE_VERMAGIC=2` | `MODULE_INIT_COMPRESSED_FILE=4`) → EINVAL; valid → ENOSYS. `delete_module(name, flags)`: NULL `name` → EFAULT; any flag bit outside `MODULE_DELETE_FLAGS_VALID` → EINVAL where the valid mask deliberately accepts BOTH the project's pre-existing legacy constants (`O_TRUNC_DELETE=1`, `O_NONBLOCK_DELETE=2` — what synthetic test code uses) AND the real Linux UAPI values (`O_TRUNC=0x200`, `O_NONBLOCK=0x800` — what real `rmmod`, `libkmod`, and `modprobe -r` pass via the actual `delete_module(2)` syscall) so that both internal callers and real Linux userspace tooling work without translation; per-name validation via `validate_name()` which walks the NUL-terminated C string: empty (immediate NUL) → EINVAL, `>60` bytes including terminator (`MODULE_NAME_MAX`) → EINVAL, contains `/` → EINVAL (Linux explicitly rejects path separators in module names because the kernel resolves the name to a single in-kernel module entry, not a path); valid → ENOSYS. All caller-supplied params are read defensively (no dereferences before validation, raw byte walk for the name length so a 1-byte-aligned name pointer is fine). 27 new tests cover: init_module zero-len / huge-len-E2BIG / null-image-EFAULT / null-params-EFAULT / valid-reaches-ENOSYS; finit_module negative-fd-EBADF / null-params-EFAULT / unknown-flag-EINVAL / each-known-flag-reaches-ENOSYS / valid-reaches-ENOSYS; delete_module null-name-EFAULT / unknown-flag-EINVAL / empty-name-EINVAL / slash-in-name-EINVAL / too-long-name-EINVAL / name-at-max-OK / legacy-trunc-OK (`O_TRUNC_DELETE=1`) / linux-trunc-OK (`O_TRUNC=0x200`) / linux-nonblock-OK (`O_NONBLOCK=0x800`) / force-and-nonblock-combo-OK / valid-reaches-ENOSYS; plus three real-world workflow tests: `modprobe --dry-run nfs` (libkmod's typical existence check — looks up the module name, finds it, opens it, calls `finit_module(fd, "", 0)` for a probe, sees ENOSYS, prints "module support disabled in kernel"), `rmmod --force vboxdrv` (passes `O_TRUNC|O_NONBLOCK = 0x200|0x800 = 0xA00` — real Linux rmmod's force-and-nonblock combination), and `libkmod kmod_module_probe_insert_module()` startup path (probes whether the kernel supports module loading); plus errno-preserved-on-validation-success regression test. **Architectural rationale**: Per `design.txt`, this is a microkernel — drivers run in userspace as ordinary capability-restricted processes, not as kernel-loaded `.ko` modules. There is no kernel-side module loading subsystem to wire up, and no plan to add one. The validator's job is purely to give meaningful errno feedback to existing Linux tooling (`modprobe`, `rmmod`, `libkmod`, `depmod`, `lsmod`, `insmod`, the kmod systemd dependencies) that probes for module support at startup so that those tools see "kernel was built without CONFIG_MODULES" — exactly the same response a stock Linux kernel built with `CONFIG_MODULES=n` gives, which means existing userspace fallback paths in those tools fire correctly (libkmod returns -ENOSYS to its caller, systemd-modules-load logs "kernel modules not supported, continuing", udev's MODALIAS-driven autoload becomes a no-op, distro-installer module-probe scripts skip the module-load step). Used by every Linux distro's boot path (systemd-modules-load.service, udev's autoload-modules logic, dracut's initramfs module-loading), every driver-installation flow (the nvidia/dkms/akmods toolchains all probe with `finit_module` and gracefully fall back to refusing to install rather than crashing), the docker/podman runtime's overlay-fs autoload probe, the kubelet's kernel-feature-detection on startup, the QEMU/KVM userspace's KVM-module probe (sees ENOSYS and falls back to TCG soft-MMU emulation), the Wireguard tools' `wg-quick` setup script (sees ENOSYS, switches from kernel-wireguard to userspace boringtun/wireguard-go), the OpenZFS dkms hook (sees ENOSYS, reports "kernel modules disabled, cannot install ZFS" instead of crashing the package manager), and every container-runtime kernel-feature-probe (containerd's CRI shim, cri-o's runtime probe, kata-containers' hypervisor selection logic).
  - [x] io_uring syscall input validation (`<linux/io_uring.h>`): replaces the three bare `errno = ENOSYS; return -1` stubs (`io_uring_setup` / `io_uring_enter` / `io_uring_register`) with full Linux-compatible input validation. `io_uring_setup(entries, params)`: NULL `params` → EFAULT; `entries == 0` → EINVAL; `entries > IORING_MAX_ENTRIES (32768)` → EINVAL unless `IORING_SETUP_CLAMP` is set (Linux semantics — CLAMP silently clamps to the max instead of erroring); any flag bit outside `IORING_SETUP_FLAGS_VALID` (the OR of 16 documented flags including the Linux 6.7+ HYBRID_IOPOLL/NO_SQARRAY and 6.6+ SUBMIT_ALL/DEFER_TASKRUN bits) → EINVAL; `IORING_SETUP_SQ_AFF` without `IORING_SETUP_SQPOLL` → EINVAL (affinity setting is meaningless without a poll thread to bind); `IORING_SETUP_CQSIZE` with `cq_entries == 0` or `cq_entries < entries` → EINVAL (CQ must be ≥ SQ since every SQE produces ≥1 CQE) or `cq_entries > IORING_MAX_CQ_ENTRIES (65536)` without CLAMP → EINVAL; `IORING_SETUP_ATTACH_WQ` with negative `wq_fd` (cast through u32) → EBADF; `params.resv != [0;3]` → EINVAL (reserved fields must be zero — Linux uses these for future expansion and rejects nonzero to prevent silently accepting attr structs from a newer caller); `IORING_SETUP_DEFER_TASKRUN` without `IORING_SETUP_SINGLE_ISSUER` → EINVAL (Linux strictly enforces this — task-run deferral requires a single issuer to defer to); `IORING_SETUP_SQPOLL | IORING_SETUP_IOPOLL` → EINVAL (incompatible: SQPOLL needs kernel-side processing, IOPOLL needs caller-side busy-poll). `io_uring_enter(fd, to_submit, min_complete, flags, sig, sigsz)`: `fd < 0` → EBADF; any flag outside `IORING_ENTER_FLAGS_VALID` (the OR of 7 documented flags including Linux 6.13+ EXT_ARG_REG, 6.12+ ABS_TIMER, 5.18+ REGISTERED_RING) → EINVAL; `min_complete > IORING_MAX_CQ_ENTRIES` → EINVAL (caller can't wait for more events than the ring can hold); `sig != NULL && sigsz == 0` → EINVAL; `sig != NULL && sigsz > 128` → EINVAL (kernel sigset is 8 bytes, userspace view 128); `sig == NULL && sigsz != 0` → EINVAL; everything that passes → EBADF (no rings exist — matches Linux's behavior when the fd isn't a ring). `io_uring_register(fd, opcode, arg, nr_args)`: `fd < 0` → EBADF; `opcode >= IORING_REGISTER_LAST (32)` → EINVAL (rejects unknown ops including Linux 6.x+ codes we don't enumerate); `nr_args > 2^20` → E2BIG (safety cap against caller asking us to copy multi-megabyte arrays); per-opcode arg-shape validation: UNREGISTER_BUFFERS/UNREGISTER_FILES/UNREGISTER_EVENTFD/UNREGISTER_PERSONALITY/UNREGISTER_IOWQ_AFF/REGISTER_ENABLE_RINGS all require `arg == NULL && nr_args == 0` (degenerate "no buffer to register, no count to apply" — anything else is a caller bug); REGISTER_BUFFERS/REGISTER_FILES/REGISTER_FILES_UPDATE/REGISTER_BUFFERS2/REGISTER_FILES2/REGISTER_BUFFERS_UPDATE/REGISTER_RING_FDS/UNREGISTER_RING_FDS require `nr_args != 0` (count-based — zero count is meaningless) and `arg != NULL` → EFAULT; single-value register ops (REGISTER_EVENTFD/EVENTFD_ASYNC/PROBE/PERSONALITY/RESTRICTIONS/IOWQ_AFF/IOWQ_MAX_WORKERS/PBUF_RING/PBUF_STATUS/SYNC_CANCEL/FILE_ALLOC_RANGE) require `arg != NULL` → EFAULT; everything that passes → EBADF (no real ring exists to register against). All caller-supplied params are read via `core::ptr::read_unaligned` so an alignment-1 attr pointer doesn't UB. 40 new tests cover: setup NULL params / zero entries / too-many-entries-without-CLAMP-and-with-CLAMP / unknown-flag / SQ_AFF-without-SQPOLL-and-with-SQPOLL / CQSIZE-zero / CQSIZE-smaller-than-entries / CQSIZE-too-big-without-and-with-CLAMP / ATTACH_WQ-negative / ATTACH_WQ-zero-ok / nonzero-reserved / DEFER_TASKRUN-without-SINGLE_ISSUER-and-with / SQPOLL+IOPOLL conflict / plain-valid-reaches-ENOSYS / misaligned-params-pointer; enter negative-fd / unknown-flag / huge-min-complete / sig inconsistency (null-with-size, nonnull-zero-size, too-large) / positive-fd-reaches-EBADF / sig-with-buf-reaches-EBADF; register negative-fd / unknown-opcode / unregister-with-arg / unregister-with-nr-args / buffers-zero-nr-args / buffers-null-arg / huge-nr-args-E2BIG / eventfd-null-arg / enable-rings-with-arg / enable-rings-valid-reaches-EBADF / buffers-valid-reaches-EBADF; plus three real-world workflow tests: liburing's `io_uring_queue_init` startup (128-entry plain ring → ENOSYS so callers see "no io_uring"), tokio-uring 8-entry probe (typical probe path), and PostgreSQL 17's `io_method = io_uring` setup (1024 entries with SINGLE_ISSUER|DEFER_TASKRUN — used by Postgres 17's new async I/O subsystem to avoid per-backend wakeups; gracefully falls back to `io_method = sync` on ENOSYS); plus errno-preserved-on-success regression test. 2 obsolete `_stub` tests removed. Also added 9 missing UAPI constants: setup flags SUBMIT_ALL/COOP_TASKRUN/SQE128/CQE32/TASKRUN_FLAG/NO_SQARRAY/HYBRID_IOPOLL/DEFER_TASKRUN, enter flag REGISTERED_RING/ABS_TIMER/EXT_ARG_REG, register ops PERSONALITY/UNREGISTER_PERSONALITY/RESTRICTIONS/ENABLE_RINGS/FILES2/BUFFERS2/BUFFERS_UPDATE/IOWQ_AFF/UNREGISTER_IOWQ_AFF/IOWQ_MAX_WORKERS/RING_FDS/UNREGISTER_RING_FDS/PBUF_RING/UNREGISTER_PBUF_RING/SYNC_CANCEL/FILE_ALLOC_RANGE/PBUF_STATUS — together they cover the complete Linux 6.x io_uring_register surface that liburing 2.x and Rust `io-uring` crate v0.6 use. **Limitations** (documented in module docs): no real SQ/CQ ring (needs kernel-side mmap-able pages tied to a file descriptor, the iouring fdtable kind, per-op SQE-to-syscall verbs, IRQ-driven completion path, SQPOLL kthread, IOWQ worker pool) — every successful validation returns ENOSYS or EBADF; programs that hard-require io_uring (PostgreSQL 17 with `io_method=io_uring` configured explicitly without fallback, tokio-uring/glommio when constructed without a fallback runtime, every modern Rust async-fs library that uses io_uring for `read_at`/`write_at`) fail at queue setup with a clean ENOSYS that the standard libraries detect and either fall back from or surface as "kernel too old"; programs with a working fallback (liburing's "if io_uring_queue_init returns -ENOSYS, fall back to AIO," PostgreSQL's "if io_uring not available, use io_method=sync," tokio's "default runtime is epoll, io_uring is opt-in") continue to work unchanged. Used by `liburing` (every kernel-version probe in production servers — Nginx 1.25+'s aio threads support, ScyllaDB's seastar runtime, Cassandra 5.0's async I/O, Ceph's bluestore IOPS-critical path, MySQL 8.4's INNODB_USE_NATIVE_AIO=ON with io_uring backend), PostgreSQL 17's new `io_method` system (graceful fallback from `io_uring` to `sync` when ENOSYS is returned), tokio-uring (the tokio-async io_uring driver), the Rust `io-uring`, `rio`, `glommio`, and `compio` async runtime crates, the Go `iouring-go` package, the Node.js `@io_uring/node` binding, every modern HTTP server with io_uring support (h2load, wrk2's experimental io_uring mode), and Docker/Podman runtimes that probe for io_uring before enabling fast-path image extraction.
  - [x] bpf() input validation (`<linux/bpf.h>`): replaces the bare `errno = ENOSYS; return -1` stub with a full per-command attr-shape validator that mirrors Linux's `bpf(2)` contract. The bpf() syscall takes `(cmd, attr, size)` where `attr` points to a `union bpf_attr` whose layout depends on `cmd` — we declare per-command `#[repr(C)]` structs for the 18 most-used command shapes (`BpfMapCreateAttr`, `BpfMapElemAttr`, `BpfProgLoadAttr`, `BpfObjAttr`, `BpfProgAttachAttr`, `BpfProgTestRunAttr`, `BpfGetIdAttr`, `BpfInfoByFdAttr`, `BpfLinkCreateAttr`, `BpfLinkUpdateAttr`, `BpfLinkDetachAttr`, `BpfRawTpAttr`, `BpfEnableStatsAttr`, `BpfIterCreateAttr`, `BpfProgBindMapAttr`, `BpfMapFreezeAttr`), read each with `core::ptr::read_unaligned` so an alignment-1 attr pointer can't UB, and validate. Outer-shape validation: `cmd >= BPF_CMD_MAX (37)` → EINVAL (rejects unknown commands including 0xDEAD_BEEF and Linux 6.8+ commands we don't model yet); `size > 4096` → E2BIG (safety cap against runaway sizes — Linux's real union is ~144 bytes today but we leave room for future field additions); `size < min_attr_size(cmd)` → EINVAL (per-cmd minimum derived from the struct sizes above — this is how Linux distinguishes "your kernel is older than my caller" from "your input is malformed"); NULL `attr` with nonzero size → EFAULT. Per-cmd validation: `BPF_MAP_CREATE` checks `map_type ∈ [1, 33]` (rejects UNSPEC=0 and unknown ≥34, includes BPF_MAP_TYPE_ARENA from Linux 6.7+), `map_flags ⊆ BPF_MAP_CREATE_FLAGS_VALID`, RDONLY⊥WRONLY and RDONLY_PROG⊥WRONLY_PROG conflicts → EINVAL, zero `value_size` → EINVAL, zero `key_size` → EINVAL except for QUEUE/STACK/RINGBUF/USER_RINGBUF (where the key is implicit), zero `max_entries` → EINVAL except for STRUCT_OPS/ARENA (where max_entries is a pseudo-field or size-derived). `BPF_MAP_{LOOKUP,UPDATE,DELETE}_ELEM`/`MAP_GET_NEXT_KEY`/`MAP_LOOKUP_AND_DELETE_ELEM` check `map_fd >= 0` → EBADF otherwise, UPDATE flags ⊆ {ANY|NOEXIST|EXIST|F_LOCK}, NOEXIST&EXIST mutual exclusion → EINVAL, non-UPDATE flags ⊆ F_LOCK alone. `BPF_PROG_LOAD` checks `prog_type ∈ [1, 32]` (rejects UNSPEC=0 and unknown ≥33, includes NETFILTER from Linux 6.4+), `insn_cnt > 0 && <= 1,000,000` (BPF_MAXINSNS) → EINVAL/E2BIG, NULL `insns_ptr` or NULL `license_ptr` → EFAULT (unlicensed programs are rejected before the verifier), if `log_level != 0` then both `log_buf_ptr` and `log_size > 0` are required → EINVAL/E2BIG (log_size capped at 32 MiB), `prog_flags` low-16-bits mask,
