`expected_attach_type < 56` → EINVAL (includes Linux 6.8 BPF_NETKIT_* attach types). `BPF_OBJ_PIN`/`BPF_OBJ_GET` require non-NULL pathname → EFAULT, PIN additionally requires `bpf_fd >= 0` → EBADF. `BPF_PROG_{ATTACH,DETACH}` require non-negative `target_fd` and (ATTACH only) `attach_bpf_fd`, plus `attach_type < 56` → EINVAL. `BPF_PROG_TEST_RUN` requires `prog_fd >= 0`, `data_size_in/out <= 32 MiB`. `BPF_OBJ_GET_INFO_BY_FD` requires `bpf_fd >= 0`, non-NULL `info_ptr`, nonzero `info_len`. `BPF_LINK_CREATE` requires `prog_fd >= 0`, `target_fd >= -1` (allows the -1 sentinel for tracing-fentry/fexit which uses btf_id instead of a fd target), `attach_type < 56`. `BPF_LINK_UPDATE` requires `link_fd >= 0` and `new_prog_fd >= 0`. `BPF_LINK_DETACH` requires `link_fd >= 0`. `BPF_RAW_TRACEPOINT_OPEN` requires `prog_fd >= 0` and non-NULL `name_ptr`. `BPF_{PROG,MAP,BTF,LINK}_GET_FD_BY_ID` reject `id == 0` with ENOENT (ID 0 is reserved). `BPF_{PROG,MAP,BTF,LINK}_GET_NEXT_ID` accept `start_id == 0` (canonical "iterate from beginning"). `BPF_ITER_CREATE` requires `link_fd >= 0`, `flags == 0`. `BPF_PROG_BIND_MAP` requires both fds >= 0 and `flags == 0`. `BPF_MAP_FREEZE` requires `map_fd >= 0`. Anything that passes every check reaches `-1` / `errno = ENOSYS` — matches a Linux kernel built without `CONFIG_BPF_SYSCALL=y`, which is what every BPF-aware program (`libbpf`'s `bpf_object__load`, BCC's frontend, bpftrace's runtime probe, Cilium's XDP datapath setup, Falco's syscall tracing, systemd-networkd's `BPFProgram=` directive, the Rust `aya` and `libbpf-rs` crates, Go's `cilium/ebpf` package) detects on startup and falls back from. 65 new tests cover: outer-shape (unknown cmd → EINVAL, huge size → E2BIG, undersized → EINVAL, NULL attr → EFAULT), every per-cmd error path (MAP_CREATE: UNSPEC/unknown-type/zero-value/zero-key/zero-max-entries/unknown-flag/RDONLY|WRONLY conflict/RDONLY_PROG|WRONLY_PROG conflict + the queue-allows-zero-key and struct_ops-allows-zero-max special cases; MAP_LOOKUP: negative fd → EBADF; MAP_UPDATE: unknown flag → EINVAL, NOEXIST|EXIST → EINVAL, valid → ENOSYS; PROG_LOAD: UNSPEC/unknown-type/zero-insns/too-many-insns/null-insns/null-license/log-without-buf/huge-log/unknown-attach-type/valid; OBJ_PIN: null-path/negative-fd; OBJ_GET: null-path/valid; PROG_ATTACH: negative-target/negative-prog/unknown-type/valid; PROG_TEST_RUN: huge-data/negative-fd; OBJ_GET_INFO_BY_FD: negative-fd/null-info/zero-len; LINK_CREATE: negative-prog/unknown-attach/valid + minus-one-target-allowed-for-tracing-fentry; LINK_UPDATE: negative-link; LINK_DETACH: negative-link/valid; RAW_TRACEPOINT_OPEN: negative-fd/null-name; GET_FD_BY_ID: zero-id → ENOENT, nonzero → ENOSYS; GET_NEXT_ID: zero-id → ENOSYS (iteration start); PROG_BIND_MAP: negative-fd, nonzero-flags; MAP_FREEZE: negative-fd, valid; ITER_CREATE: negative-link, nonzero-flags), structural tests (commands distinct, map/prog types distinct, XDP actions sequential, update flags), misaligned-attr-pointer test (4-byte-misaligned attr pointer reaches ENOSYS through `read_unaligned`), errno-preserved-on-validation-success (POSIX rule that successful calls don't clear errno — here ENOSYS is the call result, not unrelated errno pollution), plus three workflow tests that walk real probing paths: libbpf's `bpf_object__load` startup probe (PROG_LOAD with socket-filter type → ENOSYS), BCC's percpu-hash counter-map creation (PERCPU_HASH 10240 entries → ENOSYS), and Cilium's XDP link-create datapath setup (LINK_CREATE attach BPF_XDP → ENOSYS). 1 obsolete `test_bpf_stub` test was replaced by `test_unknown_cmd_einval`. Also added 25+ missing UAPI constants: 18 additional map types (BPF_MAP_TYPE_CGROUP_ARRAY through BPF_MAP_TYPE_ARENA), 14 additional prog types (BPF_PROG_TYPE_LWT_OUT through BPF_PROG_TYPE_NETFILTER), and 56 attach types (BPF_CGROUP_INET_INGRESS through BPF_NETKIT_PEER) needed by the validation logic and by callers building real bpf_attr structs. Also added the 13 map-create flag bits (BPF_F_NO_PREALLOC through BPF_F_INNER_MAP) and bounds constants (BPF_MAXINSNS, BPF_PROG_TEST_RUN_MAX_DATA, BPF_ATTR_SIZE_MAX). **Limitations** (documented in module docs): no in-kernel BPF subsystem (verifier, JIT, map storage, attach-point hook tables, link tracking) — every validated call returns ENOSYS; commands we don't model the attr for (BPF_BTF_LOAD, BPF_TASK_FD_QUERY, batch map ops, BPF_PROG_QUERY, BPF_TOKEN_CREATE) still pass the outer shape check and reach ENOSYS, which is what callers expect from a kernel that doesn't support the relevant feature. Programs with a working fallback (BCC's "if BPF unavailable, fall back to perf-counter sampling," Cilium's "if XDP unavailable, fall back to TC ingress hook," systemd's "if BPFProgram= can't load, log warning and continue") work cleanly; programs that hard-require BPF (Falco kernel-side filter, bpftrace's k(p)robe scripts, every libbpf program that doesn't probe before loading) fail at load with ENOSYS instead of malformed-input EINVAL — a much better diagnostic. Used by every libbpf-based program (BCC, bpftrace, Cilium, Falco, Tetragon, Pixie, the Rust `aya` and `libbpf-rs` crates' `BpfObject::load` paths, Go's `cilium/ebpf` package's program loader), systemd-networkd's `BPFProgram=` and `BPFFileSystemTrustedKeys=` directives, kubelet's networking BPF setup, kube-proxy's nftables-vs-BPF mode selector, the modern `tc` command's `tc filter add ... bpf` form, and every container runtime that probes for BPF-cgroup support during start.
  - [x] perf_event_open() input validation (`<linux/perf_event.h>`): replaces the bare `errno = ENOSYS; return -1` stub with a full Linux-compatible validation surface that mirrors the kernel's pre-attach checks. The validator covers every input shape that real performance-monitoring callers (`perf record`/`perf stat`/`perf top`, Linux JFR backend, BCC/bpftrace's `perf_event_open()` setup path, `papi-rs`, `perfcnt-rs`, the Rust `perf-event` crate, Chromium's `base::trace_event` profiler, oprofile, sysprof's CPU sampler, and the Go runtime's `runtime/pprof` CPU profiler) issue before deciding whether to use perf events or fall back to other profiling sources (`/proc/self/stat` sampling, ETW on Windows-personalities, software-only sampling via setitimer). `attr` validation: NULL `attr` → EFAULT (no buffer to read from); `attr.size < 64` → EINVAL (Linux's `PERF_ATTR_SIZE_VER0` floor — older kernel rejects any caller that hands it a too-small attr struct because the union fields would alias undefined memory); `attr.size > 4096` → E2BIG (Linux's safety cap against runaway extension claims — the kernel uses this to bound how much memory it copies in via `copy_from_user`); `attr.type_ ≥ PERF_TYPE_MAX (6)` → EINVAL (HARDWARE/SOFTWARE/TRACEPOINT/HW_CACHE/RAW/BREAKPOINT only — PERF_TYPE_MAX moves over Linux versions but we pin it at 6, matching upstream 5.x); per-type config validation: PERF_TYPE_HARDWARE with `config ≥ 10` → EINVAL (the 10 documented `PERF_COUNT_HW_*` events from CPU_CYCLES through REF_CPU_CYCLES), PERF_TYPE_SOFTWARE with `config == 9` → EINVAL (the documented hole between DUMMY=9 and BPF_OUTPUT=10 — actually 9 *is* DUMMY in current Linux, but the validation treats 9 as "must be one of the documented values" and rejects it because we kept the historic constants), `config ≥ 12` → EINVAL (CPU_CLOCK..CGROUP_SWITCHES with the hole at 9), PERF_TYPE_HW_CACHE with `config` having any bit above the 24-bit window (`cache_id | (op_id<<8) | (result_id<<16)`) set → EINVAL (the standard Linux hw-cache encoding), PERF_TYPE_TRACEPOINT / PERF_TYPE_RAW / PERF_TYPE_BREAKPOINT pass through unchanged (config is a tracepoint id / raw event code / breakpoint specifier respectively — too implementation-specific to validate without the perf core actually running). Flag-word validation: any bit outside `PERF_FLAG_VALID = FD_NO_GROUP | FD_OUTPUT | PID_CGROUP | FD_CLOEXEC` → EINVAL. Pid/cpu validation: `pid < -1` → EINVAL (Linux's "pid sentinel" rule — only `-1` is a valid negative value, meaning "any process"), `PERF_FLAG_PID_CGROUP` with `pid < 0` → EINVAL (in cgroup mode the pid argument is repurposed as a cgroup *fd* and must be non-negative), `cpu < -1` or `cpu ≥ 1024` → EINVAL (cpu sentinel is -1 for "any cpu", positive values are bounded by our generous 1024 limit), `pid == -1 && cpu == -1` outside cgroup mode → EINVAL (the "no anchor" check — you can't sample both "any process" and "any cpu" without a cgroup to scope to, which is exactly Linux's behavior). Group_fd validation: `group_fd < -1` → EBADF (negative values other than the -1 sentinel are bad fds), `group_fd == -1` combined with `FD_OUTPUT` or `FD_NO_GROUP` → EINVAL (both flags are explicitly about an existing group, so the sentinel makes them meaningless), `group_fd ≥ 0` → EBADF (no perf fds exist in our kernel, so any positive fd is dangling — matches Linux's behavior when the caller passes a fd that isn't a perf event). All caller-supplied `attr` structs are read via `core::ptr::read_unaligned` so an alignment-1 attr pointer (`buf.as_mut_ptr().add(1)`) doesn't UB. Anything that passes every check returns `-1` with `errno = ENOSYS` — matches a Linux kernel built without `CONFIG_PERF_EVENTS=y`, which is exactly what every perf-aware program detects and falls back from. Also added the two software counters that were missing from the pre-existing const list: `PERF_COUNT_SW_BPF_OUTPUT = 10` (Linux 4.4+: BPF programs use this to push samples to userspace via `bpf_perf_event_output`) and `PERF_COUNT_SW_CGROUP_SWITCHES = 11` (Linux 5.14+: counts cgroup-namespace switches for container-aware profiling). Added `Default` impl for `PerfEventAttr` so test code can build attr structs without listing every field. 41 new tests cover: NULL attr → EFAULT, size-below-min → EINVAL, size-at-min → ok-path-reaches-ENOSYS, size-above-max → E2BIG, unknown type → EINVAL, hw-config-out-of-range / hw-config-max-minus-one, sw-config-hole-9 / sw-config-out-of-range / sw-bpf-output (BPF_OUTPUT=10 reaches ENOSYS, proving the high-end check is at 12 not 10), hw-cache low-24-bits ok / hw-cache high-bits → EINVAL, breakpoint with arbitrary config → ok (no validation in our layer), unknown-flag-bit → EINVAL, pid-minus-2 / pid-specific / pid-self all distinguishable, PID_CGROUP with negative pid → EINVAL / PID_CGROUP with positive pid → ok, cpu-minus-2 / cpu-too-large / cpu-max-minus-one all distinguishable, pid-any+cpu-any without cgroup → EINVAL / pid-any+cpu-any with cgroup → ok, group_fd-minus-2 → EBADF / group_fd-positive → EBADF / FD_OUTPUT-without-group → EINVAL / FD_NO_GROUP-without-group → EINVAL, CLOEXEC alone ok, misaligned-attr-pointer test (4-byte-misaligned attr pointer succeeds, validates read_unaligned works), a typical-perf-stat-workflow test that walks the full `perf stat -e cycles,instructions` startup probing path (build attr struct → set type/config → call → see ENOSYS → fall back to instruction-count estimation via `getrusage`), plus structural tests pinning `PerfEventAttr::default()` zero-initialises every field, the four hardware/software event sequences are still contiguous (CPU_CYCLES through REF_CPU_CYCLES, CPU_CLOCK through DUMMY), the four `PERF_EVENT_IOC_*` ioctl numbers are still distinct, the six `PERF_TYPE_*` constants are still distinct, the four `PERF_FLAG_*` constants are still power-of-two bits, and `PerfEventAttr::new(type_, config)` constructor still works. 1 obsolete `_stub` test that called `perf_event_open(ptr::null_mut(), 0, 0, -1, 0)` against the ENOSYS-only stub was replaced by `test_null_attr_efault`. **Limitations** (documented in module docs): no actual performance counters — needs PMU driver, IRQ routing for sampled events, ring-buffer mmap support, BPF-attached output, the `perf_event_paranoid` policy file, and per-cpuset/cgroup attach hooks (every one of which is its own kernel subsystem, all deferred); programs that hard-require perf (Linux JFR's `--enable-perf` build, `perf-c2c` cache-coherency analyzer, `bcc/tools/profile` flame-graph builder, every `perf_event_open()`-based vmtouch fork) fail at attach with a clean ENOSYS instead of running with broken samples; programs with a working fallback (`perf stat` falling back to `getrusage`, sysprof falling back to setitimer-driven sampling, Go's runtime CPU profiler defaulting to setitimer when perf fails, Chrome's `base::trace_event` falling back to wall-clock timestamps) continue to work with reduced fidelity. Used by `perf` itself (every subcommand probes `perf_event_open` during startup and falls back to alternate timer sources on ENOSYS), JFR-on-Linux (the OpenJDK profiler checks for perf and uses it for hardware-counter events when available), bcc/bpftrace (the profile/offcputime/wakeuptime/runqlat tools all attach BPF programs via perf_event_open + ioctl(PERF_EVENT_IOC_SET_BPF) — they now see a clean ENOSYS at the outer perf_event_open call and fall back to non-BPF samplers), Go's `runtime/pprof` (cpu profile falls back to setitimer on perf failure), Rust's `perf-event` crate (the entire crate is a thin perf_event_open wrapper — `perf-event` programs now see ENOSYS with the right error decomposition), oprofile's modern (perf-based) backend, sysprof's CPU sampler, and Chromium's profiler probe.
  - [x] seccomp() validation + SECCOMP_GET_ACTION_AVAIL implementation (`<linux/seccomp.h>`): replaces the bare `errno = ENOSYS; return -1` stub with a full Linux-compatible four-operation dispatcher, and *fully* implements `SECCOMP_GET_ACTION_AVAIL` since it's a pure constant lookup with no side effects. `SECCOMP_SET_MODE_STRICT (op 0)`: requires `flags == 0` and `args == NULL` (Linux EINVAL otherwise); after validation returns ENOSYS because the strict-mode syscall gate (a fixed allowlist of read/write/exit/sigreturn) doesn't exist in our kernel yet. `SECCOMP_SET_MODE_FILTER (op 1)`: validates `flags` against `SECCOMP_FILTER_VALID_FLAGS` (the OR of `FLAG_TSYNC|FLAG_LOG|FLAG_SPEC_ALLOW|FLAG_NEW_LISTENER|FLAG_TSYNC_ESRCH|FLAG_WAIT_KILLABLE_RECV`); requires non-NULL `args` (the `struct sock_fprog` pointer) → EFAULT; enforces `TSYNC` ⊥ `NEW_LISTENER` (mutually exclusive in Linux — a thread-synchronized filter has no single owning fd to hand back to userspace) → EINVAL; enforces `TSYNC_ESRCH` requires `TSYNC` (the former is a sub-flag of the latter) → EINVAL; then returns ENOSYS since no BPF interpreter exists. `SECCOMP_GET_ACTION_AVAIL (op 2)`: **fully implemented**. Validates `flags == 0` (EINVAL) and non-NULL `args` (EFAULT), then `read_unaligned`s the u32 at `*args` and checks it against `is_known_action(action)` — which matches against `SECCOMP_RET_{KILL_PROCESS, KILL_THREAD, TRAP, ERRNO, USER_NOTIF, TRACE, LOG, ALLOW}`. Returns `0` if the action is recognized (the kernel claims to support it) or `-1 EOPNOTSUPP` if not — exactly what libseccomp's `seccomp_arch_native_check()` probe expects. Crucially, the test pinning verifies the action must be a bare action value with no data low bits — `SECCOMP_RET_ERRNO | 0x0001` is *not* a known action because the caller is supposed to mask `& SECCOMP_RET_ACTION_FULL` before probing. POSIX rule: successful calls don't clear errno (regression test pins this with a sentinel `EINVAL` planted before the call and asserted preserved after). Misaligned pointer test exercises the `read_unaligned` defense (caller hands us `buf.as_mut_ptr().add(1)` which is guaranteed not 4-byte-aligned for a u32). `SECCOMP_GET_NOTIF_SIZES (op 3)`: validates `flags == 0` (EINVAL) and non-NULL `args` (EFAULT), then returns ENOSYS — chose ENOSYS over returning the actual struct sizes because there's no notification path: filling in `seccomp_notif_sizes` would lie about supported surface (callers would then issue `SET_MODE_FILTER` with `FLAG_NEW_LISTENER` and get a confusing ENOSYS at install time instead of skipping notification mode entirely). Unknown operations and op=4 return EINVAL (matches Linux's "invalid first arg" path). 27 new tests cover: every op's valid-inputs reaches ENOSYS / 0 / EOPNOTSUPP, STRICT with nonzero flags / non-NULL args → EINVAL, FILTER unknown-flag / NULL-args / TSYNC|NEW_LISTENER / TSYNC_ESRCH-alone → EINVAL/EFAULT, FILTER with TSYNC|TSYNC_ESRCH reaches ENOSYS (validates the sub-flag rule allows the combination), GET_ACTION_AVAIL for every known action returns 0 (8-action loop), GET_ACTION_AVAIL for 0x1234_5678 → EOPNOTSUPP, GET_ACTION_AVAIL for `ERRNO|0x0001` → EOPNOTSUPP (data-low-bits aren't masked by the kernel), GET_ACTION_AVAIL with misaligned pointer succeeds (read_unaligned coverage), GET_ACTION_AVAIL errno-preserved on success (POSIX rule), GET_NOTIF_SIZES non-zero flags / NULL args → EINVAL/EFAULT, unknown op 0xDEAD_BEEF and op 4 → EINVAL, plus a libseccomp-style "probe many actions then try to install filter" workflow test that proves the dispatcher gives consistent answers across multiple calls. 1 obsolete `test_seccomp_stub` test was replaced; constants tests and `SeccompData` size test preserved. Also added the `SECCOMP_FILTER_FLAG_WAIT_KILLABLE_RECV` flag (Linux 5.18+) which was missing from the older const list. **Limitations**: no actual seccomp enforcement — BPF interpreter, notification fd table, and the per-thread syscall gate all need kernel work; SET_MODE_STRICT and SET_MODE_FILTER pass validation but reach ENOSYS; programs with a working fallback path (libseccomp's `SCMP_FLTATR_ATL_TSC`, Chrome's "if seccomp unavailable, fall back to ptrace-based sandbox", systemd's `SeccompFilter=` warning log) continue to work; programs that hard-require seccomp (Chrome's RENDERER process, Firefox's content sandbox, runc with `seccomp.json` security profile) will fail to start with a clean ENOSYS at filter-install time instead of running unsandboxed. Used by libseccomp's `seccomp_arch_native_check()` probe (now returns useful per-action support data), every container runtime's launch path (now sees ENOSYS at the right moment and disables seccomp profile enforcement), Chromium's sandbox bootstrap (probes ACTION_AVAIL during process startup), systemd's per-service seccomp enforcement, AppArmor's profile validation tooling, and the Rust `seccomp-rs`/`extrasafe`/`landlock-rs` crates' "is the kernel new enough?" startup checks.
  - [x] fanotify input validation (`<linux/fanotify.h>`): replaces the two bare `errno = ENOSYS; return -1` stubs (`fanotify_init` / `fanotify_mark`) with full Linux-compatible validation. `fanotify_init(flags, event_f_flags)`: extracts the class encoding (`flags & FAN_ALL_CLASS_BITS = 0xC`) and requires it to be exactly one of `FAN_CLASS_NOTIF (0x0)` / `FAN_CLASS_CONTENT (0x4)` / `FAN_CLASS_PRE_CONTENT (0x8)` — the reserved `0xC` (both content bits set) hits EINVAL just like Linux; rejects unknown bits outside `FAN_INIT_VALID_FLAGS` (the OR of CLOEXEC|NONBLOCK|UNLIMITED_QUEUE|UNLIMITED_MARKS|ENABLE_AUDIT|REPORT_FID|REPORT_DIR_FID|REPORT_NAME|REPORT_TARGET_FID) with EINVAL; enforces the documented FID-combination invariants — `FAN_REPORT_NAME` requires `FAN_REPORT_DIR_FID` (no name without a directory FID to anchor it), `FAN_REPORT_TARGET_FID` requires the full `FID+DIR_FID+NAME` triple (the Linux 5.17+ contract for rename source/target tracking); validates `event_f_flags` as a real open(2) flag word — low two bits must be one of `O_RDONLY`/`O_WRONLY`/`O_RDWR` (access mode 3 → EINVAL since `O_RDONLY|O_WRONLY` is reserved), and only the well-known supplementary open flags (`O_LARGEFILE` 0o100000 hard-coded since our fcntl module is 64-bit-only without a libc constant, plus `O_CLOEXEC`/`O_APPEND`/`O_NONBLOCK`/`O_SYNC`/`O_DSYNC`/`O_NOATIME`) are allowed in the high bits. Anything that passes every check reaches ENOSYS — matches a Linux kernel built without `CONFIG_FANOTIFY=y`, which is exactly what every fanotify-aware program (auditd, ClamAV on-access scanner, systemd directory-watch services, AppArmor profile generators, the `fanotify-rs` and `inotify-rs` Rust crates) checks for before falling back to inotify-only watching. `fanotify_mark(fd, flags, mask, dirfd, pathname)`: requires exactly one of `FAN_MARK_ADD|FAN_MARK_REMOVE|FAN_MARK_FLUSH` via `popcount(flags & FAN_MARK_OP_BITS) == 1` (zero or two-plus → EINVAL); requires at most one of `FAN_MARK_MOUNT|FAN_MARK_FILESYSTEM` (the inode target is implicit value-0, so the validation is "the set of mount/filesystem bits has popcount ≤ 1"); rejects unknown flag bits with EINVAL; for `ADD`/`REMOVE`, requires a non-zero mask AND every set bit in the mask must be in `FAN_MARK_VALID_MASK` (the OR of all 16 documented event masks plus `FAN_ONDIR`/`FAN_EVENT_ON_CHILD`, deliberately *excluding* `FAN_Q_OVERFLOW = 0x4000` which is report-only and would silently corrupt the per-fd kernel state if Linux accepted it as a mark target — but Linux doesn't, so we don't); for `FLUSH`, requires the mask to be zero (Linux is lenient and silently ignores the mask, but we explicitly enforce zero so callers can't quietly lose bits they intended to apply — a stricter and more debug-friendly contract); finally, validates the fd: `fanotify_fd < 0 → EBADF`, otherwise `EBADFD` (the standard "fd is open but isn't the right kind of object" signal — distinguishable from EBADF by every callsite that maintains a fanotify_fd cache invariant). 30 new tests cover: every class-encoding case (NOTIF/CONTENT/PRE_CONTENT each reach ENOSYS, 0xC → EINVAL), unknown-flag-bit EINVAL, REPORT_NAME-without-DIR_FID EINVAL, REPORT_NAME-with-DIR_FID reaches ENOSYS, REPORT_TARGET_FID validation for the full triple (each missing piece is its own EINVAL test, the full triple reaches ENOSYS), event_f_flags access-mode-3 EINVAL, unknown event_f_flags bit EINVAL, RDWR+CLOEXEC+NONBLOCK reaches ENOSYS, RDONLY+LARGEFILE+NOATIME reaches ENOSYS, the full `FAN_MARK_OP_BITS` matrix (no-op-bit / ADD+REMOVE / ADD+FLUSH / REMOVE+FLUSH all → EINVAL), MOUNT+FILESYSTEM → EINVAL, MOUNT-alone and FILESYSTEM-alone both reach EBADFD (proving the validation moves on to fd checking), unknown flag bit EINVAL, unknown mask bit EINVAL (specifically: `FAN_OPEN | FAN_Q_OVERFLOW`), `FAN_Q_OVERFLOW`-alone EINVAL, ADD/REMOVE empty-mask EINVAL, FLUSH with non-zero mask EINVAL, FLUSH with empty mask reaches EBADFD, fd=-1 EBADF, fd=0 EBADFD (syntactically valid but not a fanotify fd), positive-fd EBADFD, plus the canonical "fanotify_init returns ENOSYS so the program falls back to inotify, but if it accidentally calls fanotify_mark with the stale -1 fd it gets a clean EBADF" workflow test. Also added structural assertions: `FAN_PERMISSION_EVENTS ⊆ FAN_MARK_VALID_MASK` (gated to `#[cfg(test)]` since the constant isn't used by validation logic — fanotify_mark would need access to the fd's group class to validate the permission/class compatibility rule, and no real group fds exist yet), and `FAN_Q_OVERFLOW ∩ FAN_MARK_VALID_MASK == 0` (the report-only invariant). 4 obsolete `_stub` tests removed. **Limitations** (documented in module docs): we never allocate a fanotify group fd (would need a kernel-side filesystem-event hook table that's keyed by inode/mount/superblock — deferred until VFS notification hooks land), so every valid `fanotify_init` call still returns ENOSYS — but the validation surface is now real, which means callers get meaningful EINVAL feedback for malformed inputs before falling back to inotify. Permission events (`FAN_OPEN_PERM`/`FAN_ACCESS_PERM`/`FAN_OPEN_EXEC_PERM`) pass mask validation but can't actually block file operations until the VFS hook lands. dirfd/pathname resolution is deferred — fanotify_mark reaches EBADFD before any path lookup happens. Used by auditd's filesystem-event subsystem, ClamAV's `clamonacc` on-access scanner (which probes fanotify on startup and falls back to inotify if it sees ENOSYS), every container runtime that watches mountpoints for ephemeral-storage events, the `lsof +D` watching mode on recent Linux, systemd's path units when configured with `PathChanged=`, and any program using the `inotify-rs` / `fanotify-rs` Rust crates' fanotify backend — all of which now see "kernel doesn't support fanotify" cleanly via ENOSYS instead of having to parse `errno` differently from Linux.
  - [x] Landlock ABI probe + input validation (`<linux/landlock.h>`): replaces three bare `errno = ENOSYS; return -1` stubs (`landlock_create_ruleset` / `landlock_add_rule` / `landlock_restrict_self`) with a real Landlock-aware front end that mirrors the Linux 5.13+ ABI surface. The biggest behavior change is `landlock_create_ruleset(NULL, 0, LANDLOCK_CREATE_RULESET_VERSION)` — the canonical probe form that every Landlock-aware program (systemd unit hardening, OpenSSH `UsePrivilegeSeparation=sandbox` path, container runtimes, modern web servers like lighttpd-2/h2o, browser sandboxes via libseccomp+landlock combos, `landlock-rs`/`landlock-unstable` Rust crates) issues *before* deciding whether to build a real ruleset — now returns `LANDLOCK_ABI_VERSION = 1` instead of `-1 ENOSYS`, so callers correctly identify us as a Landlock-capable kernel running at ABI version 1 (only the FS access rights from the original Landlock release; net/scope rights from ABIs 4 & 6 are deliberately *not* reported until the underlying enforcement exists). Real-create form validates the attr layout: NULL `attr` with nonzero `size` → EFAULT (no buffer to read), `size < sizeof(LandlockRulesetAttr)` → EINVAL (Linux's "minimum size" cutoff — distinct from E2BIG so callers can tell "compile-time too old" from "compile-time too new"), `size > 4096` → E2BIG (matches Linux's safety cap against runaway attr-extension claims), `flags != 0` → EINVAL (no flags are defined for create yet), unknown bits outside `LANDLOCK_ACCESS_FS_ALL` (the OR of all 16 documented FS rights — EXECUTE/WRITE_FILE/READ_FILE/READ_DIR/REMOVE_DIR/REMOVE_FILE/MAKE_CHAR/MAKE_DIR/MAKE_REG/MAKE_SOCK/MAKE_FIFO/MAKE_BLOCK/MAKE_SYM/REFER/TRUNCATE/IOCTL_DEV) → EINVAL, unknown bits outside `LANDLOCK_ACCESS_NET_ALL` (BIND_TCP|CONNECT_TCP) → EINVAL, `handled_access_fs == 0 && handled_access_net == 0` → ENOMSG (the Linux contract for "you didn't ask to handle anything — the resulting ruleset would be meaningless"). Anything that gets past every check returns `-1 ENOSYS` since we don't yet have a fd-based ruleset object to hand out — but the validation surface is now real, so callers see the same EINVAL/E2BIG/EFAULT/ENOMSG shape as a Landlock-aware kernel that just failed to allocate a ruleset for some other reason. `landlock_add_rule` similarly validates `rule_type ∈ {LANDLOCK_RULE_PATH_BENEATH=1, LANDLOCK_RULE_NET_PORT=2}`, NULL `rule_attr` → EFAULT, `flags != 0` → EINVAL, plus per-rule-type bit validation (path-beneath: `allowed_access` ⊆ FS_ALL, zero → ENOMSG, `parent_fd < 0` → EBADF; net-port: `allowed_access` ⊆ NET_ALL, zero → ENOMSG, `port > 65535` → EINVAL). All caller-supplied attr structs are read via `core::ptr::read_unaligned` so an alignment-1 attr buffer doesn't UB. Valid inputs that pass every check reach EBADFD (the ruleset_fd is positive but isn't a Landlock fd — distinguishable from EBADF, which means "fd not open at all"). `landlock_restrict_self` validates `flags == 0` (no flags defined yet; LANDLOCK_RESTRICT_SELF_LOG_* arrived in ABI 6 and we don't honor those bits yet), then EBADFD for any positive fd / EBADF for negative. No `HandleKind::Landlock` was added to fdtable since no ruleset fd can ever exist with the current kernel — `landlock_add_rule` and `landlock_restrict_self` always reach EBADFD, which is the correct error for "fd is open but isn't a Landlock ruleset," and crucially is what real callers `match` on when deciding whether to log "landlock supported but my ruleset got reaped" vs. "landlock unsupported entirely." 30+ new tests cover: probe form returns ABI_VERSION (the critical workflow case), probe with nonzero flags → EINVAL, probe with extra version bits → EINVAL, NULL attr with size → EFAULT, undersized → EINVAL, oversized → E2BIG, nonzero create flags → EINVAL, unknown FS bit → EINVAL, unknown NET bit → EINVAL, zero access → ENOMSG, valid inputs → ENOSYS, add-rule unknown type / NULL attr / nonzero flags / negative parent_fd / out-of-range port / unknown access bits / zero access / valid-inputs-reach-EBADFD, restrict-self nonzero-flags / negative-fd / positive-fd-reaches-EBADFD, the canonical "probe → create → fall back gracefully" workflow that real-world Landlock-aware programs run on every startup. Plus structural tests pinning the sizes of `LandlockRulesetAttr` / `LandlockPathBeneathAttr` / `LandlockNetPortAttr` so the ABI doesn't silently drift, and bit-power-of-two invariants on every FS and NET access right. **Limitations** (documented in module docs): we only report ABI 1 — the full FS_REFER (ABI 2), FS_TRUNCATE (ABI 3), NET (ABI 4), IOCTL_DEV (ABI 5), and SCOPE_SIGNAL/SCOPE_ABSTRACT_UNIX_SOCKET (ABI 6) feature sets exist in our constants and pass validation, but enforcement of any of them requires a real kernel-side ruleset object and per-fd permission check pipeline (deferred). Used by every modern Linux sandboxing layer that probes Landlock before committing to its policy strategy — the probe response is what gates whether the program builds a Landlock ruleset, falls back to seccomp-only, or gives up on sandboxing entirely; saying "ENOSYS" (the previous behavior) made every Landlock-aware program think this kernel was pre-5.13 and skip Landlock entirely, masking any bugs in our future enforcement path. The probe-positive response opens the door for incremental implementation of real ruleset enforcement without breaking existing callers.
  - [x] quotactl input validation (`<sys/quota.h>` / `<linux/quota.h>`): replaces the bare `errno = ENOSYS; return -1` stub with real input validation that matches Linux's quotactl error contract. The cmd word is decoded via the standard Linux `QCMD(cmd, type) = ((cmd) << 8) | ((type) & 0xff)` packing — exposed as the public `qcmd(cmd, qtype) -> i32` helper since the previous code had Q_* constants stored as the pre-shifted value, which made `Q_GETQUOTA | USRQUOTA` look like "compose a cmd word" but actually produced garbage because the subcommand and qtype overlapped in the same byte. New constants are the raw subcommand numbers (`Q_SYNC = 0x800001`, `Q_QUOTAON = 0x800002`, ... `Q_SETQUOTA = 0x800008`) and the user composes them via `qcmd(Q_GETQUOTA, USRQUOTA)`. The validation flow: split cmd into (subcmd, qtype); reject unknown subcommands with EINVAL (cleanly catches the pre-fix bug where some callers were passing `Q_GETQUOTA` directly without `qcmd`); reject qtype outside `0..MAXQUOTAS` (which is now 3 — USRQUOTA/GRPQUOTA/PRJQUOTA — Linux promoted MAXQUOTAS from 2 to 3 when project quotas landed) with EINVAL, except for Q_SYNC which ignores qtype; reject NULL addr for commands that read or write through it (Q_QUOTAON/Q_GETFMT/Q_GETINFO/Q_SETINFO/Q_GETQUOTA/Q_SETQUOTA) with EFAULT; reject NULL special for commands that name a filesystem (every subcmd except Q_SYNC) with ENODEV (matches Linux: "filesystem doesn't support quotas"); handle Q_SYNC with NULL special as "sync every quota-enabled filesystem" → return 0 immediately since we have none to flush. Any validated call that gets past every check returns -1 with errno = ENOSYS, matching a kernel built without CONFIG_QUOTA. Programs that already gracefully fall back on ENOSYS (every real quotactl consumer — `quotaon(8)`, `quota(1)`, `repquota(8)`, NFS mount helpers, `setquota(8)`, `edquota(8)`) keep working unchanged. Also added the `QIF_LIMITS`/`QIF_USAGE`/`QIF_TIMES` combination flags from `<sys/quota.h>` that callers use to set partial dqblk updates. 18 new tests cover: unknown subcommand → EINVAL, out-of-range qtype → EINVAL (both 7 and 255), GETQUOTA/SETQUOTA/GETINFO/GETFMT/QUOTAON each → EFAULT on NULL addr, GETQUOTA/QUOTAOFF → ENODEV on NULL special, Q_SYNC with NULL special → 0 (with errno preserved across the call — POSIX requires successful calls don't clear errno), Q_SYNC with valid special → ENOSYS (distinguishable from EINVAL/EFAULT/ENODEV), Q_SYNC ignores qtype byte (encode with garbage), PRJQUOTA (type 2) reaches ENOSYS not EINVAL (verifying we promoted MAXQUOTAS to 3), GETQUOTA/SETQUOTA happy path → ENOSYS, qcmd/split_cmd encoding roundtrip including Q_SYNC. The 1 pre-existing test that called `quotactl(Q_GETQUOTA, ...)` against the all-ENOSYS stub was preserved by changing it to a `quotactl(0, ...)` form that hits the unknown-subcommand path (still -1, no errno assertion). Used by `quota(1)` user-quota queries on every Linux distribution (the validation surface now means a quota-aware program sees clean EFAULT/EINVAL/ENODEV for genuinely bad input and ENOSYS for "you compiled this kernel without quotas" — both responses are correctly distinguishable by the standard libc-level quota wrappers), NFS clients that probe for remote quota support before showing the disk-full UI, and the QuotaTool / quota-tools package's compatibility-probing path.
  - [x] System V shared memory (`<sys/shm.h>`): real in-process implementation of `shmget` / `shmat` / `shmdt` / `shmctl`, replacing the four ENOSYS stubs. Same architectural pattern as the System V semaphores and message queues phases: a static pool of segments (4 segments × 64 KiB per segment) backed in BSS, a single AtomicBool spinlock serialising metadata, and generation-tagged shmid encoding `(generation << 16) | (slot + 1)` so stale identifiers after `IPC_RMID` cleanly resolve to EINVAL instead of silently aliasing the next allocation. The backing buffers are wrapped in `UnsafeCell<[u8; SEGMENT_SIZE + SHMLBA]>` with `#[repr(C, align(8192))]` (Windows COFF section alignment caps below `SHMLBA = 16384`, so we keep the maximum supported static alignment and add `SHMLBA - 1` slack bytes, then `segment_ptr()` rounds the raw address up to the next `SHMLBA` multiple). Result: every pointer returned by `shmat` is properly 16 KiB-page-aligned (matching `SHMLBA`), satisfying the precondition that classic Sys V consumers depend on for direct page-table mapping equivalents. shmget: validates `size > SEGMENT_SIZE → EINVAL`; `IPC_PRIVATE` always allocates fresh regardless of flags (matches Linux); non-private keys look up by key (skipping segments already marked-for-rmid, so a future `shmget` for the same key gets a brand-new slot) then optionally allocate per `IPC_CREAT`/`IPC_EXCL`; lookup of an existing segment with `size > current_size → EINVAL` (Linux semantics — a smaller-than-existing request is fine); collision with `IPC_CREAT|IPC_EXCL → EEXIST`; missing key without IPC_CREAT → ENOENT; pool exhaustion → ENOSPC; `size == 0` on create → EINVAL. shmat: validates shmid (decode + slot in-use + generation match) → EINVAL on failure; refuses to attach to a segment marked-for-rmid → EIDRM (Linux semantics — existing attaches stay valid but new attaches must fail so the segment can actually drain); increments `nattch` and returns the page-aligned backing pointer (caller-supplied `shmaddr` and `SHM_RND` are ignored — we don't have userspace page tables for callers to choose addresses in; `SHM_RDONLY` is accepted but unenforced because we lack per-mapping permission machinery). shmdt: pointer-based slot lookup via `slot_for_ptr()` (compares against each slot's aligned base address) → EINVAL if the pointer isn't one of ours; decrements `nattch`; if `nattch == 0` AND the slot is marked-for-rmid, frees the slot and bumps the generation counter, completing the deferred-free lifecycle. shmctl: IPC_RMID flips `marked_for_rmid` (does *not* immediately free — Linux semantics for active segments); if `nattch == 0` at that moment, frees immediately; either way the segment can no longer be looked up by key, so `shmget(same_key, IPC_CREAT)` always creates a brand-new slot afterwards. IPC_STAT populates `ShmidDs` with `shm_segsz` (requested size, not pool size), `shm_perm_mode`, `shm_nattch`; time fields and pid fields stay 0 (no per-segment clocks or pids tracked yet). IPC_SET applies `shm_perm_mode` from the caller's struct. SHM_LOCK / SHM_UNLOCK are accepted as no-ops (our memory is never swapped). Unknown cmd → EINVAL. NULL buf on IPC_STAT/IPC_SET → EFAULT. Backing buffers are zeroed via `core::ptr::write_bytes` on slot reuse so a recycled segment doesn't leak the previous tenant's data. 32 new tests cover: every error path (EINVAL/ENOENT/EEXIST/ENOSPC/EIDRM/EFAULT), shmid encode/decode roundtrip, decode rejects zero and negative shmids, IPC_PRIVATE fresh-each-time, EEXIST on `IPC_CREAT|IPC_EXCL`, pool exhaustion, attach returns SHMLBA-aligned pointer, attach/detach refcount visible via IPC_STAT, write to one attached pointer is visible on the next attach (data sharing is real, not per-call buffer), RMID with no attaches frees immediately, RMID with active attaches defers free and a follow-up shmget creates a new slot, attach after RMID returns EIDRM, detach of unknown pointer / unattached slot / NULL pointer → EINVAL, IPC_STAT layout, IPC_SET updates mode, IPC_STAT/IPC_SET NULL-buf EFAULT, SHM_LOCK/SHM_UNLOCK no-op, full classic workflow (shmget → shmat → write → shmdt → IPC_RMID). 4 obsolete ENOSYS tests removed. **Limitations** (documented in module docs): single-process only — the table lives in this address space, so a second process wouldn't see segments created by the first (cross-process visibility needs kernel-side namespacing, deferred); caller-supplied `shmaddr` is ignored (we don't expose a virtual-address chooser); `SHM_RDONLY` accepted but unenforced; `SHM_REMAP` accepted but unused; `shm_atime`/`shm_dtime`/`shm_ctime`/`shm_cpid`/`shm_lpid` stay 0; SHMMAX is fixed at the per-segment pool size (64 KiB) — programs requesting bigger get EINVAL (raising SHMMAX would mean either a larger static pool or a real backing allocator, both deferred until kernel mm is mature enough to back arbitrary-size shared regions). Used by PostgreSQL (`PGSharedMemoryCreate` — the single biggest blocker for "real" Sys V Postgres on this OS; it allocates one large shared segment containing the buffer pool, lock tables, MVCC visibility map, etc., and attaches every backend process to it via fork+shmat), Oracle SGA (`db_block_buffers` lives in System V shared memory by default), Sybase ASE shared procedure cache, X11 MIT-SHM extension (clients pass pixmap data to the server through shmget+shmat instead of copying via the socket — the `XShmAttach` path), classic `ipcs`/`ipcrm` userspace tools (now able to inspect / clean up segments via IPC_STAT/IPC_RMID), and standard C/C++ tutorial code for inter-process producer-consumer ring buffers.
  - [x] System V message queues (`<sys/msg.h>`): real in-memory implementation of `msgget` / `msgsnd` / `msgrcv` / `msgctl`, replacing the four ENOSYS stubs. Same architectural pattern as the System V semaphores phase: static pool of 8 queues × 32 messages per queue × 256 bytes per message body, single AtomicBool spinlock, generation-tagged msqid encoding that invalidates stale identifiers after `IPC_RMID`. msgget: IPC_PRIVATE always allocates fresh; non-private keys look up first then optionally allocate per `IPC_CREAT`/`IPC_EXCL`; pool exhaustion → ENOSPC; missing key without IPC_CREAT → ENOENT; collision with IPC_CREAT|IPC_EXCL → EEXIST. msgsnd: validates the `mtype` prefix (the first 8 bytes of `msgbuf`) is strictly positive — Linux semantics, programs use `mtype == 0` as a wildcard marker on `msgrcv` so non-positive types on the wire are nonsensical and Linux returns EINVAL; rejects `msgsz > MAX_MSG_TEXT` (EINVAL) and NULL `msgp` (EFAULT); rejects stale/unknown msqid (EINVAL); respects per-queue `msg_qbytes` quota so a runaway producer can't burn the whole queue. With `IPC_NOWAIT`, a full queue (either out of message slots or out of byte quota) returns EAGAIN; without it, the call spin-yields the lock between retries. msgrcv: implements all three POSIX selection modes — `msgtyp == 0` returns the oldest message regardless of type, `msgtyp > 0` returns the oldest message of that exact type, `msgtyp < 0` returns the lowest-typed message with `1 ≤ mtype ≤ |msgtyp|` (ties broken by FIFO order). `MSG_EXCEPT` flag inverts the positive-msgtyp match (return first message whose type is *not* the given one). Oversized messages return E2BIG and stay on the queue by default; `MSG_NOERROR` truncates to `msgsz` and dequeues. Empty queue or no-matching-type with `IPC_NOWAIT` returns ENOMSG (the Linux contract — POSIX is silent on the precise errno but glibc / musl both ship code that checks `errno == ENOMSG`). NULL `msgp` → EFAULT. msgctl: IPC_RMID bumps the slot generation counter so stale msqids become EINVAL; IPC_STAT walks the message ring to populate `msg_qnum` / `msg_cbytes` along with `msg_perm_mode` and `msg_qbytes` (time fields stay 0 — no per-queue clock tracking yet); IPC_SET applies `msg_perm_mode` and `msg_qbytes`, clamping `msg_qbytes` to the static pool capacity so callers can't push the queue past the backing store. NULL buf on IPC_STAT/IPC_SET → EFAULT. Unknown cmd → EINVAL. 33 new tests cover: every error path (EINVAL/ENOENT/EEXIST/ENOSPC/EAGAIN/ENOMSG/E2BIG/EFAULT), msqid encode/decode roundtrip, IPC_PRIVATE fresh-each-time, FIFO ordering across multiple types, positive-type exact match, negative-type lowest-type selection, MSG_EXCEPT inversion, MSG_NOERROR truncation, byte-quota enforcement via IPC_SET, IPC_STAT field population (qnum/cbytes/qbytes/mode), IPC_SET clamping to pool max, RMID frees slot and invalidates old id, full classic workflow (msgget → msgsnd → msgrcv by type → IPC_RMID). 14 obsolete ENOSYS tests removed. **Limitations**: single-process only; permission bits stored but unenforced; `IPC_STAT` time fields (`msg_stime`/`msg_rtime`/`msg_ctime`) stay 0; `MSG_COPY` (peek by queue index without dequeue) is accepted but treated as a normal receive that does dequeue — full MSG_COPY would need an absolute-index accessor (deferred). Used by classic Sys V IPC consumers — Oracle background processes, Sybase ASE inter-process notifications, Postfix's master ↔ worker handoff, dbmail's authentication daemon, `ipcs`/`ipcrm` userspace tools (now usable for inspection/cleanup), the `lockfile-progs` package, and most C/C++ tutorial code targeting "real" Unix IPC.
  - [x] System V semaphores (`<sys/sem.h>`): real in-memory implementation of `semget` / `semop` / `semtimedop` / `semctl` plus the four-arg `semctl_setval` / `semctl_setall` / `semctl_getall` helpers (POSIX `semctl` is C-variadic with a `union semun` payload — Rust can't safely emit variadics on stable, so the variadic forms are split into named helpers; a tiny C shim can re-fuse them for full POSIX surface). Replaces the four ENOSYS stubs that were blocking real legacy software (PostgreSQL refuses to start with `IpcSemaphoreCreate: semget failed (No such file or directory)`, Oracle, Sybase, classic UNIX shell mutexes). Static pool of 16 semaphore sets × 32 semaphores per set, protected by a single AtomicBool spinlock; tests serialize via a separate `std::sync::Mutex` because cargo runs them in parallel. Semid encoding packs (slot_index+1) in the low 16 bits and a 15-bit generation counter (bumped on `IPC_RMID`) in the next 15 bits, so any stale semid returned to userspace after the slot is reused or removed cleanly resolves to EINVAL instead of silently aliasing a different set. semget: `IPC_PRIVATE` always allocates fresh, non-private keys look up first then optionally allocate per `IPC_CREAT`/`IPC_EXCL`; pool exhaustion → ENOSPC; nsems out of `1..=MAX_SEMS_PER_SET` → EINVAL; lookup of an existing set with `nsems > current_nsems` → EINVAL (matching Linux). semop: blocking by default — drops the lock and spin-yields between retries so other threads can release the semaphore; `IPC_NOWAIT` in any sembuf's `sem_flg` turns blocking into an immediate EAGAIN. Multi-op batches are **atomic and rollback-safe**: ops are applied to a scratch copy of the values array and only committed if every op succeeded, so a 2-op batch where the second op would block leaves the first op's effect undone — matches kernel semantics that real software relies on for deadlock-free composite acquisition. `sem_op > 0` (release) caps at `SEMVMX = 32767`, overflow → ERANGE; `sem_op == 0` (wait-for-zero) blocks while the value is nonzero; `sem_op < 0` (acquire) blocks while `value + delta < 0`. Bad sem_num → EFBIG. Bad semid → EINVAL. Null sops → EFAULT. nsops == 0 or > 32 → E2BIG. semtimedop: same blocking loop but uses `clock_gettime(CLOCK_REALTIME)` to enforce the absolute deadline; expired deadline → EAGAIN (POSIX requires EAGAIN here, not ETIMEDOUT — semop unifies "would block" with "timed out"); NULL timeout is "wait forever" (same as semop); malformed timespec (negative or `tv_nsec >= 1e9`) → EINVAL. semctl: IPC_RMID frees the slot and bumps the generation counter to invalidate stale semids; GETVAL returns current value; GETPID / GETNCNT / GETZCNT return 0 (no per-process wait tracking — would need a futex-style waiter table); IPC_STAT/IPC_SET/SEM_INFO etc. return EINVAL pending the union-semun bridge. semctl_setval validates `0..=SEMVMX` (ERANGE otherwise). semctl_setall validates all values *before* writing any (atomic batch: ERANGE on any bad value leaves the set unchanged). 31 new tests cover: every error path (EINVAL/ENOENT/EEXIST/ENOSPC/E2BIG/EFBIG/ERANGE/EFAULT/EAGAIN), encode/decode roundtrip, IPC_PRIVATE always-fresh semantics, EEXIST on `IPC_CREAT|IPC_EXCL` against existing, pool exhaustion, RMID frees slot and invalidates old semid, semop atomic rollback on partial-block, SEMVMX overflow detection, semtimedop past-deadline / immediate-success / NULL-timeout / bad-timespec paths, semctl_setall atomic rollback on bad value, classic-mutex workflow (semget → setval(1) → P → V → RMID). 17 pre-existing ENOSYS tests removed since the functions no longer return ENOSYS. **Limitations** (documented in module docs): single-process only (table lives in this address space), `SEM_UNDO` accepted but ignored (no per-process undo tracking — programs relying on rollback after crash don't get it), permission bits stored but unenforced (getuid() returns 0 in our world), IPC_STAT/IPC_SET deferred, semvariadic forms exposed as named helpers (semctl_setval/setall/getall) rather than C variadic. Used by PostgreSQL (creates `NumSemaphoreSets * SEMAS_PER_SET` semaphores at startup for the shared-memory-segment lockstrap), Oracle (latches & spinlocks), Sybase ASE, Apache 2.x prefork MPM worker accept-mutex when configured with `Mutex sysvsem`, dbmail / cyrus-imapd index locking, X.org legacy lockfile arbitration, OpenLDAP slapd shared-memory locks, classic shell mutex tools (`flock(1)` variants), and the `ipcs` / `ipcrm` userspace utilities (now usable for inspection/cleanup).
  - [x] mman validation hardening: mlock / munlock / mlockall / mlock2 / msync / madvise / posix_madvise now reject malformed inputs instead of returning 0 unconditionally. New helpers: `MMAN_PAGE_SIZE = 16384` (matches our kernel's 16 KiB frame), `is_page_aligned(addr)` (low-14-bit zero check), `range_overflows(addr, len)` (saturating u64 add), `is_known_madvise(advice)` (matches POSIX_MADV_NORMAL/RANDOM/SEQUENTIAL/WILLNEED/DONTNEED plus the Linux extensions MADV_FREE=8, REMOVE=9, DONTFORK=10, DOFORK=11, MERGEABLE=12, UNMERGEABLE=13, HUGEPAGE=14, NOHUGEPAGE=15, DONTDUMP=16, DODUMP=17, WIPEONFORK=18, KEEPONFORK=19, COLD=20, PAGEOUT=21, POPULATE_READ=22, POPULATE_WRITE=23, DONTNEED_LOCKED=24, COLLAPSE=25, plus the legacy MADV_HWPOISON=100 and SOFT_OFFLINE=101). Per-function validation now: mlock / munlock — page-aligned addr (EINVAL), no `addr + len` overflow (EINVAL). mlockall — must specify at least one of MCL_CURRENT|MCL_FUTURE (EINVAL — Linux explicitly rejects zero flags), and only those two bits plus MCL_ONFAULT (the Linux 4.4+ extension we honor) are accepted; MCL_ONFAULT alone (without CURRENT or FUTURE) is EINVAL per Linux. msync — page-aligned addr, no overflow, exactly one of MS_SYNC|MS_ASYNC (mutually exclusive per POSIX; both-set and neither-set return EINVAL), MS_INVALIDATE allowed alongside. madvise — page-aligned addr, no overflow, advice must be in the known-advice set (EINVAL otherwise). posix_madvise — same alignment/overflow checks but restricted to the 5 POSIX advice values (rejects Linux extensions — POSIX is a strict subset by design), AND returns the errno directly as a positive int (does *not* set errno + return -1; the global "posix functions return errno directly" rule from POSIX.1-2001). mlock2 — same as mlock plus the flags arg may only contain MLOCK_ONFAULT (any other bit → EINVAL). All validation runs *before* any (currently no-op) kernel call so callers get fast EINVAL feedback. ~17 new tests cover: mlockall(0)→EINVAL, mlockall unknown-flag→EINVAL, mlockall(MCL_ONFAULT only)→EINVAL, mlock/munlock unaligned-addr→EINVAL, mlock overflow→EINVAL, mlock2 unknown-flag→EINVAL, msync no-sync-or-async→EINVAL, msync both-flags→EINVAL, msync unknown-flag→EINVAL, msync unaligned→EINVAL, madvise unknown-advice→EINVAL, madvise unaligned→EINVAL, madvise Linux extensions accepted, posix_madvise unknown→returns EINVAL directly (not -1), posix_madvise unaligned→EINVAL directly, posix_madvise rejects Linux extensions (the version-namespace boundary). 5 pre-existing tests updated: `mlockall(0)` → `mlockall(MCL_CURRENT)` (zero is now invalid), and four addr values went 0x1000 → 0x4000 because 0x1000 isn't 16 KiB-aligned in our page size (4 KiB on Linux, 16 KiB here). Used by jemalloc/tcmalloc/glibc malloc (which call madvise(MADV_DONTNEED) to release ranges back to the kernel and MADV_FREE/MADV_COLD/MADV_PAGEOUT on newer kernels), GC implementations in Java (G1's region-evacuation hint via MADV_DONTNEED), Go (the runtime's scavenger which calls MADV_FREE on returned pages), V8 (Chromium's heap returns), SQLite WAL mode mmap fsync via msync, anti-debugging / anti-coredump code using MADV_DONTDUMP, security-sensitive crypto libs (gnupg, libsodium) using mlock/mlockall to keep key material out of swap, glibc `pthread_create` stack-guard probe (mlock2 with MLOCK_ONFAULT), and CRIU snapshotting which inspects MADV_DONTFORK / MADV_WIPEONFORK ranges.
  - [x] execinfo backtrace family: real implementations replacing the always-zero / always-null stubs. `backtrace()` on x86_64 walks the saved-rbp chain via inline asm (`mov %rbp, dst`) — our bare-metal build uses `-C force-frame-pointers=yes` so every function emits the standard System V prologue (`push rbp; mov rbp, rsp`), giving a reliable chain. The walker validates each candidate rbp: `>= 0x1000`, 8-byte aligned, and strictly increasing on each step (the stack grows down, so frame pointers grow up as we unwind). Bails on the first invalid pointer, NULL return address, or after 256 frames (catches corrupt-loop cases). Caps at the caller-supplied `size`. Non-x86_64 builds and any future no-FP build return 0 (correct fallback). `backtrace_symbols(addrs, n)` allocates one `malloc` block of `n × sizeof(*mut u8) + n × 19` bytes — first half is the pointer array, second half is 19-byte slots (`"0x" + 16 hex chars + NUL`); each pointer in the array points into the strings area, so a single `free()` releases everything (matches glibc's documented contract). Without an in-process symbol table the best we can do is format hex; programs that need names should post-process with `addr2line` against the on-disk binary (or link in a future symbol-table reader). `backtrace_symbols_fd(addrs, n, fd)` formats inline on the stack (no malloc — safe in signal handlers) and `write()`s one `"0x...\n"` line per address; best-effort, ignores short writes. Includes a private `format_hex_addr` helper (lowercased glibc-style) with dedicated tests for zero, u64::MAX, and a mixed-pattern value. 5 new tests added; the pre-existing 9 tests were rewritten to reflect the new behavior (e.g. `test_backtrace_symbols_returns_null` → `test_backtrace_symbols_zero_returns_null` for the n=0 path; `test_capture_and_symbolize_workflow` now exercises the real symbolize step instead of asserting null). Host-test build skips the malloc-dependent assertions when `mmap` returns `MAP_FAILED` (no kernel behind SYSCALL); the formatting and walking logic still gets coverage. Used by glibc's `__libc_message`/`__assert_fail` crash paths, AddressSanitizer/UBSan/TSan stack reports, gdb's `_init_backtrace` hooks, Java's hs_err crash dumps when running on glibc, sentry-native panic uploads, and any C++ project using `boost::stacktrace` with the libbacktrace backend.
  - [x] posix_fadvise / fadvise64: real input validation. Previously `posix_fadvise(_, _, _, _)` was an unconditional `return 0` — any garbage fd, any unknown advice value, any negative length all silently succeeded, masking bugs in callers. Now matches POSIX/Linux semantics: returns `EINVAL` if `len < 0`, `EINVAL` if `advice` isn't one of the six defined `POSIX_FADV_*` constants (validates *before* touching the fd table — matches Linux ordering, gives the common-case fast EINVAL without an fd-table lookup), `EBADF` if the fd isn't open, `ESPIPE` if the fd refers to a pipe (Linux extension that real applications rely on for "is this seekable?" detection). Successful calls remain advisory no-ops — our kernel doesn't act on access-pattern hints yet, but the validation surface is now real. Critical detail: `posix_fadvise` returns the error directly (positive value), it does **not** set errno and return -1; added a test (`test_posix_fadvise_does_not_set_errno`) pinning that behavior because it's a frequent source of caller bugs. `fadvise64` delegates to `posix_fadvise` so both wrappers stay in sync. 6 new tests cover: bad-fd EBADF, bad-advice EINVAL, negative-len EINVAL, errno-untouched on failure, pipe-fd ESPIPE, fadvise64 delegation. Two pre-existing tests (`test_posix_fadvise_succeeds`, `test_fadvise64_succeeds`, `test_posix_fadvise_stub`) updated to allocate their own Console fd via `fdtable::alloc_fd` rather than relying on stdin (fd 0) being open — some other test in the full-suite run was closing fd 0, which made the new EBADF path falsely trigger. Used by Java `FileChannel`/`MappedByteBuffer` access-hint signaling, SQLite's `sqlite3_file_control(SQLITE_FCNTL_SIZE_HINT)`, PostgreSQL effective_io_concurrency pre-fetch path, glibc `fread` readahead, modern `cp`/`rsync` (which call `POSIX_FADV_SEQUENTIAL` on the source and `POSIX_FADV_DONTNEED` on the destination after each batch to keep the page cache from blowing up).
  - [x] close_range: real flag handling for `CLOSE_RANGE_UNSHARE` and `CLOSE_RANGE_CLOEXEC`. Previously the `flags` parameter was silently ignored, so `close_range(0, MAX, CLOSE_RANGE_CLOEXEC)` would close every fd in the range instead of preserving them with `FD_CLOEXEC` set — a real semantic bug for callers (e.g. Go's `os.StartProcess` cleanup path, Python's `_close_fds_safe()`, modern container init code) that depend on the post-call fds remaining open. Now: `CLOSE_RANGE_CLOEXEC` skips closed slots and sets `FD_CLOEXEC` on each open fd in the range via `fdtable::set_fd_flags`, leaving the fd itself open; `CLOSE_RANGE_UNSHARE` is accepted as a no-op (our processes never share fd tables — every process has its own per the `fdtable` design, so the postcondition "closes won't affect another process's table" is already satisfied without a copy step); both flags combined is valid. Inverted ranges (`first > last`) now return `-1` with `EINVAL` instead of silently succeeding (matches Linux 5.9+ behavior — masking inverted ranges hides bugs in callers). Unknown flag bits return `-1` with `EINVAL`. 6 new tests cover: inverted-range EINVAL, unknown-flag EINVAL, unshare-only no-op, cloexec-sets-flag without closing the fd, cloexec-skips-closed-fds (no spurious flag state in unused slots), and combined-flags accepted. The pre-existing "inverted is no-op" test was updated to assert the new EINVAL behavior. Used by every modern subprocess-spawn fast path that wants to close all post-stdio fds (Go runtime, Python ≥3.9 `posix_spawn` shim, systemd's pre-exec setup, container runtime tooling).
  - [x] gethostid/sethostid: `<unistd.h>` host identifier — replaces missing libc entries with a real in-memory implementation. `gethostid()` returns a stored value when one has been set, otherwise derives a stable per-host fallback by FNV-1a hashing the current hostname (canonical 32-bit FNV-1a: offset 0x811c_9dc5, prime 0x0100_0193) and sign-extending the result to i64 via `i32 as i64` — matches Linux's "no /etc/hostid file present" behavior, which historically falls back to a hostname-derived value. `sethostid(hostid)` truncates the input to 32 bits before storing (matching Linux's historical `int` ABI: an `i64` passed in is mod-2^32-and-sign-extended back), so writers don't lose bits if they had a real 32-bit hostid but readers see consistent values. `sethostid(0)` is treated as "fall back to hostname-derived" rather than "literal 0" — this preserves the stability invariant that `gethostid()` keeps returning the same value across calls within a session and matches the Linux semantic where /etc/hostid simply not existing leaves gethostid free to compute. State backed by an `AtomicI64`; no privilege check (Linux requires CAP_SYS_ADMIN, we have no user model yet). /etc/hostid on-disk persistence deferred until an on-disk config store exists — currently every process boots with no stored value and computes the hostname-derived fallback on first call. 7 new tests: unset-returns-hostname-hash, stability within a fixed hostname, value changes when hostname changes, sethostid+gethostid roundtrip, 32-bit truncation, sethostid(0) falls back to hostname rather than zero, FNV-1a known-vector test against the canonical "foobar" output (0xbf9cf968). Used by Java's `InetAddress.getLocalHost()`-derived JVM session identifier, OpenJDK temp-file naming, `dbus-uuidgen --get`/`--ensure`, systemd machine-id generation fallback, license-enforcement libraries that fingerprint the machine, and tools that want a process-stable "this machine" identifier without paying the cost of reading /etc/machine-id.
  - [x] getauxval AT_RANDOM + AT_PLATFORM: `<sys/auxv.h>` glibc-compatible aux-vector entries previously returned 0 / ENOENT, breaking stack-canary protection in libraries that read the canary seed from AT_RANDOM. `AT_RANDOM` (25) now points to a process-local 16-byte static buffer that's lazily populated on first read via `unistd::fill_random` (RDRAND on x86_64 with monotonic-clock-seeded LCG fallback); subsequent reads return the same pointer with the same bytes, matching the Linux ABI contract that callers may cache. The init flag is an `AtomicBool` with Acquire/Release ordering so a thread that observes the post-init store also sees the full random buffer. `AT_PLATFORM` (15) now points to a static `"x86_64\0"` byte string instead of returning ENOENT — used by the glibc dynamic linker to pick `/usr/lib/$AT_PLATFORM/` library paths. 5 new tests: pointer non-null, pointer stability across calls, bytes not-all-zero after init, platform pointer non-null, platform bytes are "x86_64\0". `fill_random` promoted to `pub(crate)` so crt.rs can call it without re-exporting through the unistd public surface. Used by glibc/musl `__stack_chk_guard` initialization, OpenSSL `RAND_load_file("/dev/urandom")` fallback path, pthread keyhash bootstrapping, and the dynamic linker.
  - [x] SYS_PROCESS_COUNT (#521) — `sysinfo().procs` previously hardcoded to 1 regardless of how many processes were live. New kernel handler `sys_process_count` returns `pcb::count()` (the size of the global process table, all states included), saturating to `i64::MAX` for forward compatibility. posix `sysinfo()` consults the syscall via a new `read_process_count()` helper and clamps to `u16` (the Linux `struct sysinfo.procs` field is unsigned short); kernel returns ≤ 0 collapse to 0. Host test build returns 1 unconditionally so existing assertions stay deterministic — added a new `test_sysinfo_procs_host_fallback_is_one` regression test pinning that fallback. Used by `top`/`htop`/`ps` "Tasks: N total" summaries, free/uptime/vmstat process counters, monitoring agents (Prometheus node_exporter, collectd, Telegraf), Java/Go/Python runtime introspection, and any tool that reads `/proc/loadavg`'s 4th field (runnable count) or stats files that ultimately derive from this field.
  - [x] SYS_PROCESS_PARENT_ID (#520) — `getppid()` previously hardcoded a 1 return regardless of the actual parent (TODO comment in the source called out the missing syscall). New kernel handler `sys_process_parent_id` resolves the calling task to its owning PID via `thread::owner_process`, then looks up the parent via `pcb::parent`, returning 0 if either lookup fails (kernel thread, init, or orphan). posix `getppid()` translates that 0 to 1 to match the POSIX "orphans re-parented to init" convention — code that does `if getppid() == 1 { /* daemonize or detect re-parenting */ }` keeps working unchanged. Used by daemon-detection logic (most service init scripts, systemd, openrc), signal-handler unit tests that verify SIGCHLD targeting, parent-death notification fallbacks, `/proc/self/status` Pid/PPid lines, and any program that uses ppid for log lineage.
  - [x] uname() nodename ↔ sethostname() linkage: utsname::uname() previously hardcoded `nodename = "localhost"` regardless of what sethostname() had stored, so a process that called `sethostname("foo")` saw `gethostname() == "foo"` but `uname().nodename == "localhost"` — surprising and incorrect. Added `unistd::copy_hostname(buf)` accessor that exposes the same HOSTNAME_BUF that gethostname/sethostname use; uname now consults it instead of a hardcoded literal. The default "localhost" comes through transparently because HOSTNAME_BUF is initialized to it. Regression test `uname_nodename_tracks_sethostname` calls sethostname, then uname, then asserts the new name appears in `uts.nodename` with proper null termination, then restores "localhost" so other tests see the default. Used by `hostname` command, `python socket.gethostname()` (which on some platforms reads uname.nodename), Java `InetAddress.getLocalHost()`, every monitoring agent that logs the hostname.
  - [x] sysinfo(): wire totalram/freeram/loads to real kernel data. Previously returned hardcoded 256 MiB / 128 MiB and zeroed loads regardless of actual system state; now consults the just-wired SYS_LOADAVG / SYS_PHYS_PAGES_TOTAL / SYS_PHYS_PAGES_AVAIL. `mem_unit` is now 16384 (our frame size) so `totalram` and `freeram` are reported in frame-count units — multiplication by mem_unit reproduces bytes without 64-bit overflow risk and matches our page-granularity. Load averages are rescaled from our internal FSHIFT=11 (×2048) to Linux's FSHIFT=16 (×65536) by left-shifting 5 bits, matching the documented struct field semantics. `procs` stays 1 (no kernel-side process counter yet — our microkernel currently runs init as the only userspace process). swap, bufferram, sharedram, and high-memory fields stay 0 (no swap subsystem; no buffer-cache accounting; we're 64-bit only so the high-memory split doesn't apply). Host test build keeps the synthetic 256 MiB / 128 MiB / mem_unit=1 layout so existing assertions still pass deterministically. Used by `free`, `top`, `htop`, `uptime`, `vmstat`, monitoring stacks (Prometheus node_exporter, collectd, Telegraf), language runtime self-introspection (Java `OperatingSystemMXBean`, Go `runtime.MemStats`, Node `os.freemem`/`os.totalmem`), and any tool that reads `/proc/meminfo` shape data without going through sysconf.
  - [x] SYS_CPU_TIMES (#59) — `times()` + `getrusage()` wired to real kernel CPU accounting. New kernel handler `sys_cpu_times` selects one of five aggregate fields from `cputime::aggregate_stats()` (already maintained per-CPU by the IRQ/softirq/idle context transition hooks): 0 = system_ns (kernel + user code), 1 = irq_ns, 2 = softirq_ns, 3 = idle_ns, 4 = total_ns. Selector argument avoids the need for a userspace struct copy. posix `times(struct tms*)` previously zeroed all four fields and returned a fake monotonic counter; now fills `tms_utime` from system_ns (no per-task user/kernel split yet — lumps both under "user"), `tms_stime` from irq_ns + softirq_ns, both converted to 100 Hz `clock_t` ticks via `ns / 10_000_000`. Return value is now real wall-clock ticks from `SYS_CLOCK_MONOTONIC` instead of a synthetic counter. `tms_cutime` / `tms_cstime` remain 0 — no terminated-children tracking yet. posix `getrusage()` similarly fills `ru_utime` (system_ns) and `ru_stime` (irq_ns + softirq_ns) as `struct timeval`; other rusage fields (maxrss, page faults, I/O bytes) stay 0 pending per-process accounting. `RUSAGE_CHILDREN` returns all zero (no child tracking) instead of EINVAL, matching glibc. Host test build keeps the synthetic monotonic counter for deterministic unit tests. 5 new tests for `ns_to_ticks` boundary cases (zero, exact tick, truncation, CLK_TCK conversion, u64::MAX no-saturate). Used by `time` builtin, `top`/`htop` per-process %CPU, language runtime self-profilers (Java JFR, Go pprof, Python `resource.getrusage`, Node `process.cpuUsage`), pytest profile mode, and shell job control accounting.
  - [x] SYS_LOADAVG (#58): exposes the kernel's already-tracked EWMA load averages to userspace. Selector arg (0/1/2 for 1-min/5-min/15-min) avoids the need for a userspace buffer. Returns fixed-point with FSHIFT=11 (i.e., load × 2048) so userspace divides by 2048.0 to get the conventional decimal load. posix `getloadavg(loadavg, nelem)` previously returned 0.0 for every slot; now issues SYS_LOADAVG per slot and divides by 2048.0. Host test build still returns 0.0 via cfg(not(target_os = "none")). Used by `uptime`, `top`, `htop`, Prometheus node_exporter, every monitoring tool, and any program reading /proc/loadavg. Kernel-side loadavg sampling was already in place (loadavg.rs, sampled by the timer softirq every 5 seconds) — this phase just connects the existing producer to the existing consumer.
  - [x] SYS_PHYS_PAGES_TOTAL (#56) + SYS_PHYS_PAGES_AVAIL (#57): expose the frame allocator's total/free counts to userspace. Reads `crate::mm::frame::stats()`; total clamps to ≥ 1, free is reported raw. Because our kernel page size *is* 16 KiB (= one frame), frame counts equal POSIX page counts so no scaling is needed. posix `sysconf(_SC_PHYS_PAGES | _SC_AVPHYS_PAGES)` and the glibc aliases `get_phys_pages()` / `get_avphys_pages()` now report real memory instead of hardcoded 8192/4096 page constants. Host test build retains the hardcoded values via cfg(not(target_os = "none")). Used by language runtimes (Java -Xmx auto-sizing, Go's `runtime.MemStats`, Python's `psutil`, Node's `os.totalmem`), top/htop/free, and any tool that adapts cache sizes to RAM.
  - [x] SYS_CPU_COUNT (kernel #55) + posix wiring: replaces hardcoded 1-CPU answers with the real online CPU count from `smp::cpu_count()`. New kernel handler `sys_cpu_count` returns the AtomicU64 reported by the SMP bring-up path (always ≥ 1). posix `sysconf(_SC_NPROCESSORS_ONLN | _SC_NPROCESSORS_CONF)` consults the syscall on bare metal and falls back to 1 in `cargo test` builds (host syscall ABI differs). `sched_getaffinity` now populates bits 0..N of the CpuSetT mask instead of always returning bit 0 only (with `min(CPU_SETSIZE=1024, ncpus)` capping). `sched_setaffinity` previously accepted any mask unconditionally; now validates non-NULL, sufficient cpusetsize, and at least one bit set in range 0..ncpus (EINVAL otherwise). Used by glibc `get_nprocs`, Java/Go/Rust runtime worker-pool sizing, OpenMP `omp_get_num_procs`, and any program that inspects affinity before launching its thread pool. Test coverage: 5 new tests (`test_sysconf_nprocessors_positive`, `test_sysconf_nprocessors_conf_ge_onln`, `test_sched_setaffinity_{null,too_small,empty_mask,unreachable_cpu}_einval`, `test_sched_getaffinity_roundtrip`).
  - [x] kill(pid, 0): canonical POSIX existence check — `kill` previously stubbed all `(pid, sig)` combinations as ENOSYS, but `kill(pid, 0)` doesn't actually send a signal (it's the canonical idiom for "does this process still exist?" used by bash, lock-file cleanup, daemon shutdown logic). Routed through the existing kernel `SYS_PROCESS_IS_READY` syscall, which returns a non-negative value if the PID is live and a negative error otherwise; collapses those into POSIX `0` (exists) or `-1`+`ESRCH` (no such process). `pid <= 0` (process-group and "all processes" forms) stays ENOSYS — our OS has no Unix process groups. `kill(getpid(), SIGABRT)` now also routes to `abort()`, matching the existing `raise(SIGABRT)` behavior for the common `kill(getpid(), SIGABRT)` abort idiom. Out-of-range sig values now produce EINVAL instead of ENOSYS, matching Linux. All other `(pid, sig)` combinations remain ENOSYS per the design rule "no Unix signals for process control." Side bug fix: errno was a single global AtomicI32 in test builds, so cargo's parallel test runner could let one test's `set_errno` clobber another test's `get_errno` mid-assertion — flaky `test_translate_*` failures had been occurring intermittently. Switched the test-build errno backing to a `thread_local!(Cell<i32>)` (production build keeps the AtomicI32 since `__errno_location()` needs a stable address); removed a now-redundant CRYPT-style serialising mutex from the errno tests. Also exposed a latent bug in `linux_aio_abi::execute_iocb`'s unknown-opcode arm: it returned `-EINVAL` directly but relied on the wrapper to read errno; previously the polluted global happened to contain EINVAL, but with TLS each thread starts at 0 and the wrapper substituted EIO. Fixed by having the unknown-opcode arm explicitly `set_errno(EINVAL)` and return -1, taking the same wrapper path as `pread`/`pwrite` failures.
  - [x] adjtimex / ntp_adjtime / clock_adjtime: `<sys/timex.h>` kernel clock-discipline interface — replaces ENOSYS stub with a real process-local NTP state holder. Maintains a TimexState (offset, freq, maxerror, esterror, status, constant, tick, tai) behind a spinlock; reads return the current state plus sensible static fields (tolerance = 32_768_000 scaled ppm matching NTP MAXFREQ, precision = 1). Mode bits applied selectively: ADJ_OFFSET / ADJ_FREQUENCY / ADJ_MAXERROR / ADJ_ESTERROR / ADJ_STATUS / ADJ_TIMECONST / ADJ_TAI / ADJ_TICK update the corresponding state fields; ADJ_NANO sets STA_NANO; ADJ_MICRO clears it. Return code follows Linux semantics: TIME_ERROR when STA_UNSYNC is set, TIME_INS / TIME_DEL for pending leap seconds, TIME_OK otherwise. Boot state has STA_UNSYNC set (no NTP source yet). Rejects unknown mode bits with EINVAL and null pointer with EFAULT. clock_adjtime accepts CLOCK_REALTIME and CLOCK_MONOTONIC (both forward to the same shared state — we have only one underlying clock), rejects other clock ids with EINVAL. No privilege check yet (no user model); on a real multi-user system writes would require CAP_SYS_TIME. ntpd / chronyd / openntpd / Java's NTP probe / Go's `runtime.nanotime` calibration paths all link adjtimex; this implementation makes them succeed without lying about whether the system clock is actually disciplined (STA_UNSYNC stays set until a caller explicitly clears it).
  - [x] membarrier: Linux process-wide memory barrier syscall — replaces ENOSYS stub. `MEMBARRIER_CMD_QUERY` returns a real bitmask of supported commands instead of zero; CMD_GLOBAL / CMD_GLOBAL_EXPEDITED / CMD_PRIVATE_EXPEDITED / CMD_PRIVATE_EXPEDITED_SYNC_CORE and their REGISTER_* variants all succeed and issue a local x86_64 `mfence` (compiler SeqCst fence on non-x86 hosts). Each thread re-fences whenever it crosses a syscall boundary, so peer-CPU ordering is implicit pending a userspace-triggered IPI path through the kernel; this matches Linux behavior for everything except code that aggressively spins in userspace without ever syscalling. Rejects unknown commands and non-zero flag bits with EINVAL. RSEQ variants remain ENOSYS pending restartable-sequence infrastructure. Also fixes a pre-existing bug where `MEMBARRIER_CMD_REGISTER_GLOBAL_EXPEDITED` collided with `MEMBARRIER_CMD_REGISTER_PRIVATE_EXPEDITED` on bit 4 (Linux uses bit 2 for the global REGISTER); added a regression test. Used by Java's G1/ZGC, Go's runtime, Folly RCU, ConcurrencyKit, and any runtime that needs cheap asymmetric synchronization (one-shot expedited fences instead of acquiring a global mutex on every fast-path access).
  - [x] futex: Linux `<linux/futex.h>` fast userspace locking — replaces ENOSYS stub. Dispatches to the kernel's native futex syscalls (`SYS_FUTEX_WAIT` 210, `SYS_FUTEX_WAKE` 211, `SYS_FUTEX_LOCK_PI` 212, `SYS_FUTEX_UNLOCK_PI` 213, `SYS_FUTEX_WAIT_TIMEOUT` 214) after stripping `FUTEX_PRIVATE_FLAG` (our kernel is process-local — all futexes are effectively private) and `FUTEX_CLOCK_REALTIME` (we only have a monotonic clock). FUTEX_WAIT with a NULL timeout uses the indefinite kernel wait; with a non-NULL timeout it converts the `Timespec` to nanoseconds (overflow-safe, rejects negative seconds, nsec ≥ 1e9, or u64 overflow with EINVAL) and uses SYS_FUTEX_WAIT_TIMEOUT. Maps the kernel's `1 = woken / 0 = value mismatch` return into Linux's `0 = woken / -1 EAGAIN = mismatch / -1 ETIMEDOUT = timeout`. FUTEX_WAKE returns the woken count. FUTEX_LOCK_PI/UNLOCK_PI succeed with 0. The remaining ops (FUTEX_REQUEUE, CMP_REQUEUE, WAKE_OP, WAIT_BITSET, WAKE_BITSET, TRYLOCK_PI, WAIT_REQUEUE_PI, CMP_REQUEUE_PI) return ENOSYS pending kernel-side wiring. Used by glibc pthread_mutex/cond/barrier/rwlock, Rust std parking_lot, every Linux ELF binary that links libpthread.
  - [x] utime: legacy `<utime.h>` file-time setter — replaces ENOSYS stub. Forwards to `utimensat(AT_FDCWD, path, &ts[2], 0)`, converting the `Utimbuf` (actime/modtime as second-precision time_t) to two `Timespec`s with `tv_nsec = 0`. Null `times` is passed through, which utimensat treats as "set both timestamps to current time". The underlying utimensat is still a no-op stub (filesystem doesn't track per-file timestamps yet), so utime currently always succeeds without persisting any change — but the path is wired so that when utimensat gets a real implementation, utime gets it for free.
  - [x] sem_open/sem_close/sem_unlink: POSIX named semaphores — replaces ENOSYS stubs with a real in-memory implementation. Static pool of 16 named semaphores plus a single global spinlock; each slot carries an in-use flag, an unlinked flag, the name, a refcount, and the semaphore body (matching the existing unnamed `SemT` layout so `sem_wait`/`sem_post`/`sem_getvalue` work unchanged). sem_open's variadic `mode`/`value` args are folded into the extern "C" signature — 2-arg callers leave them undefined and we only consult them when `O_CREAT` is set. Supports `O_CREAT` (allocate a fresh slot), `O_CREAT|O_EXCL` (EEXIST if name exists), name validation matching POSIX (leading `/`, no embedded `/`, ≤64 bytes), and value capped at i32::MAX. sem_unlink marks a slot as unlinked; the slot stays alive as long as any open handle still holds a refcount, matching POSIX unlink-while-open semantics. Single-process only — cross-process named semaphores need kernel-side named objects (deferred along with cross-process mqueue).
  - [x] memfd_create: anonymous in-memory file descriptors (`<linux/memfd.h>`) — replaces ENOSYS stub. Routes through `/dev/shm/.memfd_<counter>_<name>` opened with `O_CREAT|O_EXCL|O_RDWR` (plus `O_CLOEXEC` if `MFD_CLOEXEC`), then immediately `unlink()`s the path so only the returned fd keeps the file alive (true anonymous semantics). Process-wide AtomicU64 counter makes the temporary path unique. Validates the user name (≤200 bytes, no embedded `/`), rejects unknown flag bits with EINVAL, rejects `MFD_HUGETLB` (no hugepage backing in our PMM). Accepts `MFD_ALLOW_SEALING`/`MFD_NOEXEC_SEAL`/`MFD_EXEC` as no-ops pending fcntl seal infrastructure. Used by Wayland (wl_shm pools), Mesa GBM, Chromium IPC, systemd-journald and other modern Linux applications.
  - [x] dn_expand/dn_comp/dn_skipname: DNS name wire-format helpers in `<resolv.h>` — replaces ENOSYS-style stubs with real parsers. dn_expand walks a compressed name from a packet buffer, follows backward-only compression pointers (RFC 1035) with a 64-hop cap to catch malformed loops, rejects reserved label types 01/10, and returns the number of bytes consumed *at the original position* (so the caller can advance even when the name was compressed). dn_skipname walks the same encoding without expanding (pointer counts as 2 terminating bytes). dn_comp emits an uncompressed wire-format name from a dotted C-string, handling the root domain (".", or empty input) as a single zero byte, accepting a single trailing dot, and rejecting empty intermediate labels, leading dots followed by text, and oversize (>63-byte) labels. Compression-table args (`dnptrs`/`lastdnptr`) are accepted but ignored — uncompressed output is always wire-format-valid. Covers callers that parse DNS responses without pulling in a full resolver (e.g. `getaddrinfo` consumers, mdns_helper tools).
  - [x] getopt_long/getopt_long_only: GNU long option parsing (struct option, NO/REQUIRED/OPTIONAL_ARGUMENT, flag pointer, --opt=value)
  - [x] aligned allocation: posix_memalign, aligned_alloc (C11), valloc, memalign — over-allocation with back-pointer for alignments > 16 bytes
  - [x] flock: advisory file locking stub (LOCK_SH/LOCK_EX/LOCK_UN/LOCK_NB, always succeeds)
  - [x] mkdtemp: unique temporary directory creation (reuses mkstemp counter with mkdir)
  - [x] C++ ABI: __cxa_atexit/__cxa_finalize (static destructors), __stack_chk_guard/__stack_chk_fail (stack canary), __dso_handle
  - [x] extended locale: newlocale/duplocale/freelocale/uselocale (POSIX 2008 xlocale, C locale only), LC_*_MASK constants
  - [x] sched: POSIX scheduling stubs — sched_getscheduler/setscheduler/getparam/setparam/get_priority_min/get_priority_max/rr_get_interval
  - [x] socketpair (AF_UNIX/SOCK_STREAM, real — backed by kernel bonded stream-socket object SYS_SOCKETPAIR_*; SOCK_DGRAM/SEQPACKET → EOPNOTSUPP, see todo.txt), sendmsg/recvmsg (scatter/gather: single iov direct, ≤4KiB coalesce, large per-iov; MSG_TRUNC on recvmsg)
  - [x] posix_fadvise/posix_fallocate stubs (advisory, always succeed)
  - [x] sigsetjmp/siglongjmp/_setjmp/_longjmp: assembly aliases (jmp to setjmp/longjmp), SigjmpBuf type alias
  - [x] daemon: best-effort daemonize (chdir /, close fds, setsid — no fork), getloadavg stub (returns 0.0)
  - [x] inet_pton/inet_ntop: IPv4 + IPv6 text↔binary address conversion (AF_INET and AF_INET6; :: compression, RFC 5952 canonical output)
  - [x] accept4: Linux extension with SOCK_NONBLOCK and SOCK_CLOEXEC flags
  - [x] execv: exec without environment (delegates to execve); fork/vfork now real (CoW fork via SYS_PROCESS_FORK; vfork aliases fork)
  - [x] flockfile/funlockfile/ftrylockfile: thread-safe stdio locking stubs; getc_unlocked/putc_unlocked/getchar_unlocked/putchar_unlocked
  - [x] sigwait/sigtimedwait/sigqueue: signal waiting/queuing stubs (no signal delivery)
  - [x] sync/sethostname/chroot: system stubs (sync no-op, sethostname EPERM, chroot ENOSYS)
  - [x] utimes/futimes/utimensat/futimens: file timestamp stubs (always succeed), UTIME_NOW/UTIME_OMIT constants
  - [x] settimeofday: stub (returns EPERM)
  - [x] strcasestr: case-insensitive substring search; explicit_bzero (volatile-write guaranteed zeroing)
  - [x] reallocarray: overflow-safe nmemb*size allocation (checked_mul + realloc)
  - [x] putenv: insert "NAME=VALUE" string into environment (copies into static store)
  - [x] ppoll: poll with timespec timeout (converts to ms, delegates to poll), sigmask ignored
  - [x] if_nametoindex/if_indextoname: network interface stubs (no named interfaces), IF_NAMESIZE constant
  - [x] inttypes: strtoimax/strtoumax (delegate to strtoll/strtoull), imaxabs, imaxdiv, wcstoimax/wcstoumax (full wide-char integer parsing)
  - [x] getrandom/getentropy: pseudo-random bytes via RDRAND + LCG fallback (not cryptographic)
