  - [x] dup3: dup2 with flags (O_CLOEXEC accepted but not enforced), EINVAL when oldfd==newfd
  - [x] fdatasync/syncfs: stubs (writes are synchronous), sendfile (userspace read+write loop)
  - [x] clock_settime (stub EPERM), clock_nanosleep (relative + absolute time, TIMER_ABSTIME)
  - [x] posix_madvise: POSIX_MADV_* constants + stub (returns 0); memfd_create stub (ENOSYS)
  - [x] ffs/ffsl/ffsll: find first set bit (trailing_zeros + 1)
  - [x] timegm: inverse of gmtime (identical to mktime — we're always UTC)
  - [x] INET_ADDRSTRLEN/INET6_ADDRSTRLEN/INADDR_BROADCAST/INADDR_NONE constants
  - [x] sched_getaffinity/sched_setaffinity: CPU affinity stubs (single-CPU mask), CpuSetT struct
  - [x] mkostemp: mkstemp with additional open flags (flags accepted, not enforced)
  - [x] posix_spawn_file_actions: init/destroy/addclose/adddup2/addopen with storage (16 actions max, paths stored inline); posix_spawnattr: init/destroy/setflags/getflags/setpgroup/getpgroup with storage (kernel fd inheritance now available via SYS_PROCESS_SPAWN_EX — posix layer can apply actions)
  - [x] scandir: filter + sort, malloc'd array of malloc'd Dirent*, insertion sort, full OOM rollback
  - [x] setsockopt/getsockopt: SO_REUSEADDR, SO_KEEPALIVE, TCP_NODELAY, SO_RCVBUF/SO_SNDBUF, SO_BROADCAST, SO_LINGER, SO_REUSEPORT, SO_RCVTIMEO, SO_SNDTIMEO stored per-socket; values returned consistently by getsockopt
  - [x] pseudo-terminal stubs: posix_openpt (ENOSYS), grantpt/unlockpt (succeed), ptsname/ptsname_r (null/ENOSYS)
  - [x] dladdr: symbol lookup stub (returns 0=failure), DlInfo struct
  - [x] mqueue: POSIX message queue stubs (mq_open/close/unlink/send/receive/getattr/setattr — all ENOSYS)
  - [x] getpagesize: returns 16384 (16 KiB pages), _SC_PAGE_SIZE alias
  - [x] strchrnul: GNU extension — strchr that returns null-terminator instead of null
  - [x] clearenv: clear all environment variables; secure_getenv (identical to getenv — no privilege escalation)
  - [x] __ctype_b_loc/__ctype_tolower_loc/__ctype_toupper_loc: glibc ctype lookup tables (384-entry compile-time arrays)
  - [x] program_invocation_name/program_invocation_short_name/__progname/__progname_full: program name globals
  - [x] dirent additions: rewinddir, seekdir/telldir, dirfd (-1 stub), alphasort comparator
  - [x] waitid: extended wait (P_PID/P_ALL/P_PGID, delegates to waitpid)
  - [x] copy_file_range: cross-file copy (userspace read+write loop), offset tracking
  - [x] epoll stubs: epoll_create/create1/ctl/wait/pwait (all ENOSYS), EpollEvent struct, EPOLLIN/OUT/ERR/HUP/ET constants
  - [x] strftime/strptime expansion: 22 additional format specifiers (%C/%y/%e/%w/%u/%U/%W/%I/%k/%l/%P/%D/%F/%T/%R/%r/%x/%X/%z/%Z/%s + ISO 8601 %V/%G/%g), strptime month/weekday name parsing (%b/%B/%a/%A case-insensitive)
  - [x] system(): posix_spawnp("sh", "-c", command) + waitpid (was ENOSYS stub), NULL→stat /bin/sh check
  - [x] tmpnam: /tmp/tmp_NNNNNN name generation with monotonic counter, L_TMPNAM=20 (was null stub)
  - [x] fcntl advisory locking: F_GETLK/F_SETLK/F_SETLKW commands, struct Flock (l_type/l_whence/l_start/l_len/l_pid), F_RDLCK/F_WRLCK/F_UNLCK constants; stubs (no kernel lock enforcement — F_GETLK returns F_UNLCK, F_SETLK/F_SETLKW always succeed)
  - [x] signal additions: sigaltstack (stack_t struct, SS_ONSTACK/SS_DISABLE/MINSIGSTKSZ/SIGSTKSZ constants, validates stack size), siginterrupt (stub — no SA_RESTART behavior to toggle)
  - [x] setgroups: stub succeeding silently (single-user OS)
  - [x] terminal control: cfmakeraw (raw mode for TUI apps), cfsetspeed, tcsendbreak/tcdrain/tcflow/tcflush stubs; BRKINT/INPCK/ISTRIP/IXON/PARENB constants
  - [x] string additions: memmem (byte sequence search), mempcpy (copy returning end pointer), rawmemchr (unbounded memchr)
  - [x] strtold: long double conversion (delegates to strtod — Rust lacks 80-bit float)
  - [x] stdio buffering: real FILE structs with 1 KiB buffers, line-buffered stdout (flush on '\n'), unbuffered stderr, fully-buffered fopen'd files; read-ahead for input; printf/fprintf routed through buffer; feof/ferror real status; fseek/ftell account for buffered data; stdout auto-flush before stdin reads; 16-slot static FILE pool for fopen'd files
  - [x] sysconf expansion: 13 additional _SC_* constants (CLK_TCK, ARG_MAX, CHILD_MAX, NGROUPS_MAX, VERSION, HOST_NAME_MAX, LOGIN_NAME_MAX, LINE_MAX, THREADS, THREAD_STACK_MIN, PHYS_PAGES, AVPHYS_PAGES, IOV_MAX) with reasonable values
  - [x] strverscmp: proper version-aware string comparison (was incorrect strcmp alias); numeric segments compared by value ("file9" < "file10"), glibc-compatible leading-zero handling (fractional vs integer); 8 unit tests
  - [x] wctype/iswctype: generic character class dispatch by name (12 POSIX classes); wctrans/towctrans: generic transformation dispatch ("tolower"/"toupper"); used by regex engines, grep, sed
  - [x] dprintf: formatted output to raw fd (assembly trampoline + Rust impl); used for error logging and protocol output to non-stdio fds
  - [x] tmpfile: fixed to return FILE* via fdopen() (was incorrectly returning raw fd cast to pointer)
  - [x] wcstoimax/wcstoumax: full wide-char integer parsing (was stub returning 0); whitespace skip, sign, base auto-detect, 0x prefix, endptr
  - [x] wcstol/wcstoul/wcstoll/wcstoull/wcstod/wcstof: wide string → number conversion in wchar.rs; shared helpers (wc_space, wc_digit, wc_skip_ws, wc_detect_base)
  - [x] scanf %[...] scanset: character class matching with negation (%[^...]), ranges (%[a-z]), leading-] inclusion; 256-bit bitmap for O(1) membership testing
  - [x] UDP connect: stores default peer in SocketMeta (userspace only); send()/sendto(NULL) use stored peer; recv() works on connected UDP sockets
  - [x] Socket option tracking: SO_RCVBUF, SO_SNDBUF, SO_BROADCAST, SO_LINGER stored in SocketMeta and returned by getsockopt (was hardcoded defaults)
  - [x] mkostemp: flags (O_CLOEXEC, O_APPEND) now ORed into open() call (was silently ignored)
  - [x] Terminal fd validation: tcsendbreak/tcdrain/tcflow/tcflush validate fd is a terminal (EBADF/ENOTTY) and validate argument ranges (EINVAL)
  - [x] Mutable hostname: gethostname/sethostname use static buffer (default "localhost"); _SC_HOST_NAME_MAX returns 255 (matching buffer size)
  - [x] Process group tracking: PGID, SID, foreground PGRP stored in static variables with lazy init; setpgid/setsid/tcsetpgrp store values; getpgrp/getsid/tcgetpgrp return stored state consistently (was always returning PID)
  - [x] gethostbyaddr: reverse DNS lookup via SYS_DNS_REVERSE_RESOLVE, returns Hostent with PTR-resolved hostname
  - [x] h_errno/herror/hstrerror: legacy DNS error reporting (HOST_NOT_FOUND, TRY_AGAIN, NO_RECOVERY, NO_DATA)
  - [x] getifaddrs/freeifaddrs: interface address enumeration (eth0 + lo with IFF_UP/LOOPBACK/MULTICAST/BROADCAST flags)
  - [x] getpeername kernel fallback: queries SYS_TCP_PEER_ADDR when cached metadata unavailable (dup'd fds)
  - [x] getifaddrs real IP: queries SYS_NET_IF_INFO to populate eth0 address and netmask (was INADDR_ANY)
  - [x] getservbyname/getservbyport: built-in service database (27 entries: http, https, ssh, ftp, smtp, dns, mysql, postgresql, redis, etc.)
  - [x] getprotobyname/getprotobynumber: built-in protocol database (11 entries: ip, icmp, tcp, udp, gre, esp, ah, sctp, etc.)
  - [x] poll/select kernel-queried readiness: check_readiness() queries SYS_TCP_POLL_STATUS/SYS_TCP_LISTENER_READY/SYS_UDP_RX_READY for actual socket state (was always-ready)
  - [x] recv MSG_PEEK/MSG_DONTWAIT: flags passed through to kernel; O_NONBLOCK on fd auto-adds MSG_DONTWAIT
  - [x] shutdown half-close: delegates to SYS_TCP_SHUTDOWN for proper SHUT_RD/SHUT_WR/SHUT_RDWR semantics
  - [x] Error translation fix: translate_net_error() aligned to actual KernelError enum values
- [-] Translate POSIX calls to native syscalls
- [x] /proc, /sys equivalents (for programs that need them)
  - [x] procfs mounted at /proc: 10K+ lines, 70+ root files (version, uptime, meminfo, cpuinfo, stat, vmstat, buddyinfo, net, etc.) + per-PID directories (status, cmdline, stat, maps, caps)
  - [x] sysfs mounted at /sys: kernel info, hostname (r/w), sysctl params (r/w), PCI devices, fs cache stats; `/sys/devices/system/cpu/{online,present,possible,kernel_max}` CPU-count tree added (2026-06-13) — the authoritative path glibc `get_nprocs()`/`get_nprocs_conf()`, lscpu, nproc, hwloc, and OpenMP/TBB consult before the `/proc/cpuinfo` fallback; ranges use Linux `0`/`0-N` formatting (clamped to ≥1 CPU), online from `smp::cpu_count()`, present/possible from `acpi::processor_count()`, kernel_max from `priority_rr::MAX_CPUS-1`; read-only, self-tested. Per-CPU topology subtree `/sys/devices/system/cpu/cpuN/topology/{physical_package_id,core_id,core_siblings[_list],thread_siblings[_list]}` added (2026-06-13) — the dirs hwloc/lscpu read to reconstruct socket/core/thread layout; sourced from real `cputopo` detection (`get_cpu`/`cpus_in_package`/`thread_siblings`) with the honest single-thread-core-in-package-0 fallback when topology is undetected, masks as 8-hex-digit words and lists in Linux `0-2,4` range form; cache/ subtree deliberately omitted (no honest per-CPU cache share-maps available yet); read-only, self-tested. Per-CPU `cpuN/online` toggle added (2026-06-13) — hwloc/lscpu read it to skip offline CPUs; cpu0 omits it (boot CPU can't be offlined), cpu1+ read "1"/"0" from `smp::cpu_count()`, read-only (no runtime hot-plug model). Per-CPU `cpuN/cache/indexI/` subtree added (2026-06-13, TD23) — `level`/`type`/`size`/`coherency_line_size`/`ways_of_associativity`/`number_of_sets` sourced directly from `cpu::cache_topology()` (CPUID-derived), plus `shared_cpu_map`/`shared_cpu_list` from real topology (`cache_shared_cpus()`, never overclaiming); present only when geometry is detected (absent under QEMU's default model rather than fabricated); read-only, self-tested. This is the honest data source that replaced lscpu's removed fabricated cache defaults
- [x] POSIX signals → translate to native IPC messages — implemented via the kernel signal shim (kernel/src/proc/signal.rs + posix/src/signal.rs). kill()/raise() no longer pretend to be Unix signals: cross-process kill() routes through SYS_SIGNAL_SEND, the kernel holds per-process pending/blocked/trampoline state and delivers asynchronously at syscall-return by redirecting to a userspace trampoline (SEH-style), and the target's own disposition table decides terminate/ignore/handle. This is the native-mechanism translation the design calls for (process control via the kernel's own signal channel, not real Unix signals). See POSIX section "Full signal delivery via kernel signal shim" for the full description.

### 2.6 Init / service manager
- [x] PID 1 init process
  - [x] Minimal userspace init binary (ring 3, SYSCALL-based I/O, embedded in kernel ELF)
  - [x] Interactive shell: console read/write, echo command, help, exit
  - [x] Filesystem shell commands: ls, cat, write, stat, mkdir, rmdir, rm
  - [x] System info commands: pid, uptime
  - [x] Userspace pointer validation on all syscall handlers
  - [x] Service spawn/management (init reads ELF from VFS, spawns child, waits for exit)
- [x] Dependency-based parallel service startup
- [x] Socket activation
  - [x] SocketActivationEntry: name, spawn_path, status, pre_queue
  - [x] register_socket_activation/unregister_socket_activation API
  - [x] connect() integrates with activation: queues connection + triggers spawn for idle services
  - [x] register() transfers pre-queued connections to service's pending queue
  - [x] Activation lifecycle: Idle → Starting → Running, Failed with reset
  - [x] mark_activation_failed/reset_activation for supervisor integration
  - [x] Kshell `sockact`/`sa` command (list/add/remove/reset)
  - [x] Self-test: register activation, connect triggers spawn, register transfers queue, channel works
- [x] Automatic crash restart with backoff
- [x] Resource limits per service (cgroup-equivalent)
  - [x] Per-service ResourceLimits configuration registry (64 entries)
  - [x] set_service_limits/get_service_limits/remove_service_limits API
  - [x] 4 predefined profiles: Daemon (16M/10%), NetworkService (64M/25%), SystemService (256M/50%), Sandboxed (8M/5%)
  - [x] apply_profile() for quick configuration with presets
  - [x] Kshell `slimit`/`sl` command (list/show/set/profile/remove)
  - [x] Self-test: set/get, update, remove, profiles, list
- [x] JSON-lines structured logging (text-based, not binary)
- [x] "Service ready" notification API
- [x] Startup app list (simple serial list, separate from service manager)
  - [x] Disk-idle heuristic for "app is loaded, start next one" (2-3 sec timeout via blkdev::is_idle_for)
  - [x] Explicit readiness notification API
- [x] Login manager / display manager (init/login):
  - [x] User accounts: uid, username, display name, password hash (SHA-256+salt), avatar, admin flag
  - [x] YAML user database (/etc/users.yaml), default root + guest accounts
  - [x] Login UI: avatar circles, password field, power menu, clock, error messages
  - [x] Authentication with 5-failure lockout (5 min), auto-login, guest login
  - [x] Session management: environment setup (HOME/USER/SHELL/PATH/XDG), session tracking
  - [x] Lock screen: owner-only unlock, idle timeout, 30s dim warning, Super+L
  - [x] Accessibility: high contrast, large text, on-screen keyboard, screen reader
- [x] Cron daemon (time-based task scheduler) — Rust userspace binary
  - [x] Standard crontab syntax (min/hour/day/month/weekday with *, ranges, steps, lists)
  - [x] Special time strings (@reboot, @hourly, @daily, @weekly, @monthly, @yearly)
  - [x] Daemon mode with per-minute wake, automatic crontab reload
  - [x] Per-user crontabs (/var/spool/cron/) and system cron.d directory
  - [x] Execution logging, next-execution preview, status reporting
  - [x] CLI: add/remove/list entries, run-pending, log viewer
- [x] Syslog daemon (JSON-lines log aggregation) — Rust userspace binary
  - [x] JSON-lines structured log format (ts, level, service, msg, extras)
  - [x] Log rotation (5 MiB per file, 10 rotated files max)
  - [x] Query/filter by level, service, message content, time range
  - [x] Tail and live-follow modes
  - [x] Log statistics with level and service breakdowns
  - [x] Clean/prune old entries by age

### 2.7 Shell and basic userspace tools
- [-] Port **Oils (OSH)** — a bash-*superset* shell — for POSIX compatibility (replaces bash; this is the "A" initiative in the large-initiative ordering above, NOT bash itself). See roadmap-detailed.md §2.7. **In progress:** Rust reimplementation of the OSH language in-tree (`userspace/oils`, binary `osh`) — no C++→slateos cross-toolchain exists, so a faithful `oils-for-unix` cross-compile is blocked; see design-decisions.md §72 and open-questions.md Q26. MVP done: lexer + recursive-descent parser + tree-walking interpreter that forks/execs real externals via `std::process::Command`; pipelines, redirections, `&&`/`||`/`;`/`&`, if/while/until/for, functions, brace-groups/subshells, `$var`/`${…}`/`$(( ))`/`$( )`/backtick expansion, IFS field splitting, and ~20 builtins (`cd pwd echo printf export unset set shift getopts mapfile/readarray command builtin read test [ eval source . type exit return break continue : true false`). Grow phase since MVP: case statements, here-docs/here-strings, richer parameter expansion (`#`/`##`/`%`/`%%` trim, `:offset:len` substring, `/`/`//`/`/#`/`/%` replace), `[[ … ]]` conditional expressions (string/glob/numeric comparisons, file/string unary tests, `!`/`&&`/`||`/grouping, and `=~` POSIX-ERE regex match with `BASH_REMATCH` capture extraction — matched by an in-tree linear-time Pike-VM engine that is ReDoS-safe; RHS matching is quote-aware — quoted spans of the pattern match literally while unquoted spans are regex, per bash), `(( … ))` arithmetic commands, command-line pathname (glob) expansion (`*`/`?`/`[…]`, quoting-aware, leading-dot rule, unmatched-stays-literal), and indexed arrays (`a=(x y z)`, `a[i]=v`, `a+=(w)`/`a+=str`, `${a[i]}`/`${a[@]}`/`${a[*]}`, `${#a[@]}`/`${#a[i]}`, `unset a[i]`; `"${a[@]}"` preserves one field per element, unquoted `${a[@]}` field-splits), compound-command redirections (`while read …; done < file`, `for … done > out`, `{ …; } >> log`, pipeline-into-`while read`; body `read`s consume successive lines via a shared input cursor, captured stdout written to the target file, and compound *stderr* redirection — `{ …; } 2> err`/`2>>`, `for … done 2>&1`, `>&2` inside a group — honored via a per-shell `stderr_stack` that every fd-2 write (diagnostics, builtin `>&2`, external child stderr) consults; `2>&1` into a captured stdout folds stderr in after the body, see known-issues TD-OILS3), and associative arrays (`declare -A m`/`typeset`/`local`, `m[key]=v`, `m=([k]=v …)`, `${m[key]}`/`${m[@]}`/`${m[*]}`, `${!m[@]}` keys, `${#m[@]}`, `unset m[key]`; insertion-ordered, string subscripts; keyed/sparse indexed literals `a=([2]=x y)` and `${!a[@]}` indices too), and **concurrent, streaming pipelines** (all-external pipelines wire real OS pipes between child processes; any pipeline with a builtin/function/compound stage uses the *threaded* path — each stage runs in its own subshell on its own thread connected by real OS pipes, so data streams as produced and each stage is a subshell per bash semantics; downstream early-exit propagates upstream — an in-process producer stops via the `pipe_broken` SIGPIPE-analogue and an external producer on the OS broken-pipe signal, e.g. `yes | head`, on targets that deliver it), plus **pipefail + `${PIPESTATUS[@]}`** (both pipeline paths record every stage's exit code in `PIPESTATUS`, in order — including a one-element array for a bare command — and `set -o pipefail`/`set +o pipefail` folds `$?` to the rightmost non-zero stage), and the combined **`declare -A m=([k]=v)` one-liner** (array-literal operands to a declaration builtin are parsed as `decl_arrays` and applied with the declared kind; works for `declare -a a=(x y)`/flagless `declare a=(x y)` too). Negative array subscripts (`${a[-1]}` = last, scalar = one-element array), arithmetic subscripts inside `(( … ))`/`$(( … ))` (`(( a[i]+1 ))`, `a[-1]`), and subscripts combined with a parameter operator (`${a[i]:-def}`, `${a[i]#pat}`, `${a[i]:off:len}`, `${a[i]/pat/repl}`, `${a[i]:=v}` with element write-back; associative keys too — only `[@]`/`[*]`+operator bulk transforms are rejected) are also implemented. Indexed arrays are **sparse** (an ordered `index → value` map): `a=([5]=x)` stores one element, `${#a[@]}` counts only assigned elements, `${!a[@]}` lists only assigned indices, `unset a[i]` leaves a gap, and a negative subscript counts from `highest_index+1` — all bash-correct. Per-stage redirects compose with the inter-stage pipe (`a | b > f`, `a | b 2>err` route to the threaded path and merge the stage's `RedirPlan` with the pipe endpoints — verified by Windows tests). The `=~` regex engine (`ere.rs`) is an in-tree POSIX-ERE Pike-VM/Thompson-NFA implementation with capture groups (linear-time, ReDoS-safe); the lexer reads the `=~` RHS as one regex word so metacharacters (`(`, `)`, `|`, `<`, `>`) stay literal while parameter expansion still applies; the RHS is quote-aware (quoted spans matched literally via `regex_pattern_from_rhs`, unquoted spans are regex). Associative subscripts inside `(( … ))`/`$(( … ))` (`m[foo]`, `m[$k]`) are read by string key (not arith-evaluated), while indexed subscripts stay arithmetic — via `VarLookup::is_assoc`/`get_assoc`. The arithmetic evaluator also supports the ternary `?:` (right-associative) and comma operators (`$(( cond ? a : b ))`, `$(( e1, e2 ))`), plus the full **mutation set**: assignment `= += -= *= /= %= <<= >>= &= |= ^=` (right-associative, chained `a = b = c`), pre/post increment/decrement (`++x`/`x++`/`--x`/`x--`), and exponentiation `**` — including on array/associative elements (`(( a[i] += 1 ))`, `(( m[key]++ ))`). Numeric literals accept the full bash syntax: `0x`/`0X` hex, leading-zero octal (`017` = 15), and `base#num` arbitrary bases 2–64 (`2#1010`, `16#ff`, `64#_` = 63; digits above 9 are lowercase then uppercase letters then `@`/`_`, with letter cases interchangeable for bases ≤ 36). `arith.rs` is a two-phase AST evaluator (parse with immutable `&dyn VarLookup`, evaluate with mutable `&mut dyn VarLookup` via `set`/`set_index`/`set_assoc`), so `&&`/`||` short-circuit and `?:` is branch-lazy (side effects fire only on the taken path). The **C-style `for (( init; cond; update )); do …; done`** loop is implemented (`ForArithClause`; empty condition ⇒ always-true; `update` runs after each iteration including after `continue`; `break`/`continue` levels propagate). **Case-modification parameter expansion** `${v^}`/`${v^^}` (upper) and `${v,}`/`${v,,}` (lower) is implemented (doubled = every character, single = first character only; an optional glob pattern like `${v^^[aeiou]}` selects which characters convert; works on array elements). **Indirect expansion `${!ref}`** (reads the variable named by `ref`, including array-element referents `ref=a[0]`/`ref=m[k]`) and **prefix name-matching `${!prefix*}`/`${!prefix@}`** (sorted names of all set variables — scalars, indexed and associative arrays — beginning with `prefix`; quoted `@` form yields one field per name) are implemented. **ANSI-C quoting `$'…'`** processes backslash escapes (`\n \t \r \a \b \e \f \v \\ \' \" \?`, octal `\nnn`, hex `\xHH`, unicode `\uHHHH`/`\UHHHHHHHH`, control `\cx`; unknown escapes keep the backslash) and yields a literal (no expansion/splitting); `$"…"` is treated as a plain double-quoted string (no message catalogs). The **`getopts optstring name [args]`** builtin is implemented: POSIX-style single-option-per-call parsing with `OPTIND`/`OPTARG`, bundled short flags (`-abc`), options-with-arguments (`-b val` or `-bval`), `--` end-of-options, silent error mode (leading `:` → unknown sets `name=?`+`OPTARG`, missing arg sets `name=:`+`OPTARG`) vs. verbose mode (diagnostics to stderr), and external-`OPTIND=1` reset detection (a per-shell `getopts_col` cursor tracks bundling). **`mapfile`/`readarray [-t] [-d delim] [-n count] [-s skip] [-O origin] [array]`** reads its whole input (here-doc/here-string, `< file`, pipeline stream, or stdin) into an indexed array (default `MAPFILE`): each element keeps its trailing delimiter unless `-t`, `-d` sets an alternate delimiter, `-n` caps the count, `-s` skips leading lines, `-O` sets the starting index. **`printf` now recycles its format string** until all arguments are consumed (`printf '%s\n' a b c` → three lines), matching bash, and emits the format exactly once when it has no argument-consuming conversion. `printf` also supports **`-v var`** (assign the formatted result to a shell variable instead of writing to stdout) and a full conversion/format-spec set: `%s %b` (interpret backslash escapes) `%q` (shell-quote) `%c` (first char) `%d %i %u %x %X %o` (integers, with `0x`/`'c` input forms) `%f %F %e %E %g %G` (floats), plus flags (`- + space # 0`), numeric field width, and precision (`%5d`, `%-5s`, `%05d`, `%.2f`, `%.2s`) — with **dynamic `*` width/precision** taken from an argument (`printf '%*d' 5 42`, `printf '%.*f' 2 3.14159`, `printf '%*.*f' 8 2 3.14159`; a negative `*` width left-justifies, a negative `.*` precision is ignored) — and the **`%(FORMAT)T` strftime time conversion** (consumes one epoch-seconds argument — missing/negative ⇒ now — and renders it in UTC via an in-tree `civil_from_days`/`format_strftime`, supporting `%Y %C %y %m %d %e %H %I %M %S %p %P %A %a %B %b %h %j %u %w %s %n %t %F %T %R %D %%`; local-timezone offset is not yet applied — see known-issues TD-OILS9). **Brace expansion** (`brace.rs`) runs first (textually, before parameter/other expansion) on command words and `for`-loop lists: comma lists (`a{b,c,d}e`), numeric sequences (`{1..5}`, `{5..1}`, `{1..9..2}`), zero-padded sequences (`{01..10}`), character sequences (`{a..e}`, `{Z..A}`), cross-products/nesting (`{a,b}{1,2}`, `{a,{b,c}}`), and empty alternatives (`{,x}`); invalid braces (`{}`, `{abc}`) and quoted braces stay literal, and alternatives may contain parameter refs (`{$v,b}`) which expand after the brace pass. **`${var@op}` parameter transformations**: `@Q` (quote the value for safe reuse — safe words unquoted, control chars via `$'…'`, else single-quoted), `@U`/`@u`/`@L` (upper-all/upper-first/lower-all), `@E` (expand ANSI-C backslash escapes), `@a` (attribute flags: `a` indexed / `A` associative), `@A` (a re-inputtable assignment/`declare` statement recreating the variable — a plain scalar renders as the short `name=value` form via `shell_quote`, while an attributed scalar, array, or associative array renders as a full `declare` command via `format_declare_def`), the key-aware **`@k`/`@K`** (`${a[@]@k}` interleaves each subscript and value as separate words `0 x 1 y`; `${a[@]@K}` yields one field with double-quoted values `0 "x" 1 "y"`; both work over indexed/associative arrays and the positional parameters, keyed from 1, via a `bulk_keyvalue` helper), and **`@P`** (expand the value as a prompt string, interpreting the bash prompt escapes `\u \h \H \w \W \s \j \l \d \D{fmt} \t \T \@ \A \a \e \n \r \v \V \! \# \$ \\ \nnn` and `\[`/`\]`; time escapes render in UTC, `\h`/`\H` read `$HOSTNAME`, `\u` reads `$USER`/`$LOGNAME`, `\w`/`\W` use the live cwd with `$HOME`→`~`; via a `prompt_expand` helper). **Dynamic special variables** `$RANDOM` (15-bit LCG, reseeded by `RANDOM=n`), `$SECONDS` (elapsed seconds since shell start, rebased by `SECONDS=n`), `$EPOCHSECONDS`, `$EPOCHREALTIME` (`secs.micros`), and `$BASHPID` are implemented (computed on read via `Cell`-backed state, so they bypass `vars`). The **`command [-v|-V] [-p] name`** builtin runs `name` bypassing shell functions (builtin if it is one, else external) or describes it (`-v` terse name/path, `-V` verbose) with a `$PATH` search, and **`builtin name`** forces builtin lookup even when a same-named function exists. **Shell options `set -e`/`-u`/`-x`** (and `+e`/`+u`/`+x` to disable, `set -o errexit|nounset|xtrace|pipefail` long forms, and clustered `set -eux`) are implemented: **errexit** (`-e`) exits the shell when a command fails, with the correct POSIX exemptions — conditions of `if`/`while`/`until`, non-final `&&`/`||` operands, and negated (`!`) commands are ignored (tracked by an `errexit_suppress` counter and per-and-or "final element executed" logic); **nounset** (`-u`) makes referencing an unset variable (bare `$x`/`${x}`/`${#x}`, but not `${x:-def}` or special params like `$@`/`$#`/`$?`) an error that aborts the shell; **xtrace** (`-x`) prints each expanded simple command (prefixed `+ `) to stderr before running it. (Along the way the `while`/`until`/`for` loops now yield the POSIX exit status — the last body execution, or 0 when the body never runs — instead of leaking the failed loop-condition's status, which errexit made observable.) **Function-local variables** (`local`) now have real dynamic scoping instead of aliasing `declare`: each function call pushes a local frame, `local name[=val]` snapshots the name's full prior state (scalar/indexed/associative/export flag) and shadows it, and the frame is restored on return (including for names that were unset before, and for `local a=(…)` array locals); `local` outside a function is an error. `declare`/`typeset` remain global. The **`read`** builtin now supports **`-r`** (raw — no backslash escaping), **`-a array`** (split the line into an indexed array), **`-p prompt`** (write a prompt to stderr), **`-s`** (silent, no-op for non-tty input), and proper **`$IFS`-aware field splitting**: IFS-whitespace runs collapse and are trimmed while non-whitespace IFS characters each delimit a field, the final named variable receives the raw remainder (internal spacing preserved), and — without `-r` — a backslash escapes the next character (also preventing a split on it), plus **`-d delim`** (read up to an alternate delimiter; `-d ''` ⇒ NUL), **`-n N`** (stop after N characters *or* the delimiter, whichever comes first), and **`-N N`** (read exactly N characters, ignoring the delimiter). `-d`/`-n`/`-N` use a byte-level, UTF-8-aware `read_record` helper dispatched over the same `StdinSrc`/`RedirPlan` sources as `read_line`, and set the exit status correctly (0 on delimiter/count reached, 1 on a short read at EOF). (`read -t`/`-u` are parsed/consumed but not yet honored — they need timer/fd-table support — see known-issues TD-OILS6.) **Case fallthrough terminators** `;&` (fall through and run the next arm's body unconditionally) and `;;&` (resume pattern testing at the following arms) are implemented alongside the normal `;;` break, so bash-style `case x in a) …;& b) …;; c) …;;& esac` control flow works. The **`select name [in words]; do body; done`** menu loop is implemented: it brace-expands the word list (or iterates `"$@"` when `in` is omitted), prints the numbered menu to stderr (again after a blank line), writes the `PS3` prompt (default `#? `), reads a line from stdin, stores the raw line in `REPLY`, sets `name` to the chosen word (empty on an out-of-range/non-numeric entry), runs the body until EOF or `break`, and yields the last body execution's status; `select` is now a reserved keyword. **`readonly name[=value] …`** (and **`declare -r`**) mark variables read-only: a subsequent assignment (`x=2`), `unset`, or value-bearing `declare` is rejected with status 1 and the diagnostic `osh: NAME: readonly variable`, leaving the value intact (enforced by a per-shell `readonly` set consulted in `apply_assignment`/`builtin_unset`/`builtin_declare`); `readonly -p` (or no operands) lists the readonly variables in re-inputtable form, and `-a`/`-A` select the array kind. Read-only enforcement now also covers the **`read` builtin** (a readonly scalar/array target — `read x`, field `read a b`, or `read -a arr` — is rejected with status 1 and no mutation; earlier fields in a multi-name read are still assigned before the readonly field aborts, matching bash) and **temporary `NAME=val cmd` env prefixes** (`readonly x; x=1 cmd` errors `osh: x: readonly variable`, does not run the command, and yields status 1 — guarded before dispatch so no function/builtin/external path mutates the variable). TD-OILS7 fully resolved. The **`let arg …`** builtin evaluates each argument as an arithmetic expression (with assignment/increment side effects, reusing the `(( … ))` evaluator) and sets the exit status from the last result (0 non-zero, 1 zero; no args → error). The **`-v` set-test** — `[ -v name ]`, `test -v name`, and `[[ -v name ]]` — reports whether a variable is set: a plain scalar/array/associative name, an explicit indexed/keyed element (`a[2]`, `m[key]`), or `a[@]`/`a[*]` (any element), plus special/positional parameters that resolve to a value; an empty-but-set variable counts as set. **`declare -p [names]`** prints variable definitions in re-inputtable form (`declare -- x="5"`, `declare -a a=([0]="x" [1]="y")`, `declare -A m=([k]="v")`), combining the readonly/exported/integer attribute flags (`-r`/`-x`/`-i`) and array-kind flags into one group, double-quoting/escaping the value (`"`, `\`, `$`, backtick); with no names it lists every set variable sorted by name, and an unset name is an error (status 1). The **`shopt [-s|-u|-q] [optname …]`** builtin toggles/queries shell options (`-s` set, `-u` unset, `-q` quiet-query, no flag ⇒ list/query rendering `on`/`off`); unknown option names are a status-1 error. `nullglob` (an unmatched glob produces no word at all rather than the literal pattern) and `dotglob` (pathname expansion includes dotfiles — but never `.`/`..`) are honored in glob expansion (`glob_or_literal`/`glob_expand_field` take the two flags, read from a per-shell `shopt` map inherited by subshell clones); **`nocasematch`** is honored in `case` and `[[ == ]]`/`[[ != ]]` matching (both the glob and the fully-quoted-literal comparison fold case via `glob_match_ci`, which lowercases pattern and text — including class ranges), and **`nocaseglob`** is honored in pathname expansion (`glob_expand_field` matches an ASCII-lowercased copy of the pattern against ASCII-lowercased filenames, still returning the original names); **`nocasematch`** is also honored in `[[ str =~ regex ]]` matching — the ERE engine (`ere.rs`) takes a case-insensitive flag (`Regex::new_flags(pattern, ci)`) that folds literal-char and character-class comparisons via `char_eq`/`ClassData::matches_ci` (the positive set is folded *before* negation, so `[^a-z]` under `nocasematch` correctly excludes `A`). **`extglob`** is honored everywhere glob patterns are matched — pathname expansion, `case`, `[[ == ]]`/`[[ != ]]`, and parameter-expansion pattern operators (`${v#pat}`/`${v%pat}`/`${v/pat/repl}`/`${v^pat}`) — supporting all five extended operators `?(list)` (zero/one), `*(list)` (zero+), `+(list)` (one+), `@(list)` (exactly one), and `!(list)` (negation), with `|`-separated and arbitrarily-nested alternatives. This unified a previously-duplicated pair of glob matchers into a single recursive `PatTok` engine (`compile_glob`/`match_glob_toks`), and the lexer now consumes an unquoted `X(…)` group into one word token (parens/pipes/whitespace literal inside, `$`/quotes still expanded) so extglob patterns parse — the extglob *decision* is deferred to match time (`compile_glob` only treats the group specially when the option is set; otherwise it matches literally). One superset caveat: because parsing is shopt-independent, `!(cmd)` written with no space is now a pattern word rather than a negated subshell — use `! (cmd)` for the latter (see known-issues TD-OILS8). The **`declare -i`/`+i` integer attribute** is implemented (a per-shell `integer_attr` set inherited by subshell clones): a name marked `-i` has its assignments evaluated as arithmetic before storing (`declare -i x; x=5+3` stores `8`, a non-numeric value stores `0`), `+=` performs numeric addition rather than string append (`z=10; z+=5` → `15`), the initializer on the declaration itself is evaluated (`declare -i y=2*3` → `6`), and integer indexed/associative array elements are evaluated too (`declare -ia a; a[0]=3+4` → `7`); `+i` removes the attribute so assignments become plain strings again. The **`declare -l`/`-u` case attributes** (with per-shell `lower_attr`/`upper_attr` sets, also inherited by subshell clones) fold assigned values to lower/upper case before storing (`declare -l x; x=HeLLo` → `hello`; `declare -u y=abc` → `ABC`; array elements folded too); they are mutually exclusive (the last flag seen wins, including within a cluster like `-ul`), `+l`/`+u` clear them, and `unset` drops all attributes. All three attributes (`-i`/`-l`/`-u`) appear in `declare -p` output. **`globstar`** is honored in pathname expansion: a `**` path component matches across directory levels — as an intermediate component (`a/**/b`) it stands for the base directory plus every descendant directory (zero-or-more levels), and as the final component (`a/**`) it stands for every descendant file *and* directory; dotfiles are skipped unless `dotglob`, and symlinked directories are not recursed into (matching bash ≥ 4.3, which also prevents symlink-loop infinite recursion). With `globstar` off, `**` degrades to an ordinary single-level `*`. Other known options (`failglob`, etc.) are stored and reported faithfully but not yet behavior-affecting. The **directory stack** builtins **`pushd`/`popd`/`dirs`** are implemented (a per-shell `dir_stack: Vec<String>` inherited by subshell clones, holding the saved directories *below* the current one — the current directory is the conceptual top and is the live process cwd, not stored): `pushd DIR` changes to `DIR` and pushes the old cwd, `pushd` (no arg) swaps the top two, `pushd +N`/`-N` rotates the stack so the N-th entry (from the left / right) becomes current; `popd` pops the saved top and changes to it, `popd +N`/`-N` deletes the N-th entry (deleting the current entry falls back to a plain pop); `dirs` prints the stack (tilde-contracting `$HOME` → `~`), with `-c` clear, `-l` long (un-contracted) paths, `-p` one-per-line, `-v` numbered one-per-line, and `+N`/`-N` to print a single entry. **`cd -`** changes to `$OLDPWD` (echoing the new directory), and every directory change (`cd`, `pushd`, `popd`) maintains `$PWD`/`$OLDPWD` via a shared `change_dir` helper. The **`time` reserved word** (`time [-p] pipeline`) is implemented: it is recognized only at pipeline start (so `time` stays a usable plain word elsewhere, e.g. in a `for … in` list, and a bare `time` with no following command is an ordinary command), precedes an optional `!` negation, and after the pipeline runs it prints a timing report to stderr — bash's default `\nreal\tNmS.SSSs\nuser…\nsys…` form, or the POSIX `-p` form (`real S.SS` three lines, no leading newline). Real (wall-clock) time is measured exactly via `Instant`; user/sys CPU are reported as zero pending per-child CPU accounting (see known-issues TD-OILS10). The pipeline's stdout and exit status are unaffected. The **`trap`** builtin (`trap [-lp] [[action] sigspec ...]`) records signal/pseudo-signal handlers in a per-shell `traps` map (not cloned into subshells except ignored `''` traps, matching bash's reset-to-default): `trap 'cmd' SIG …` sets, `trap - SIG` resets, `trap '' SIG` ignores, `trap`/`trap -p [SIG …]` prints the current traps in re-inputtable `trap -- 'action' SIG` form (signal-number sorted), and `trap -l` lists the known signal names. Signal specs normalize case-insensitively with/without a `SIG` prefix and accept numbers (`0` = `EXIT`); the pseudo-signals `EXIT`/`ERR`/`DEBUG`/`RETURN` are accepted. All **synchronous** traps are fired: **`EXIT`** (once, when the top-level shell exits via the `exit` builtin, end of script, or interactive EOF — preserving the pending exit status), **`ERR`** (on a failing command outside an exempt context — the same rule as `errexit`, but independent of `set -e`), **`DEBUG`** (before each simple command), and **`RETURN`** (on function return, in the function's scope); a reentrancy guard stops a handler's own commands from re-triggering the same trap. Only **async** signal handlers (`INT`/Ctrl-C, `TERM`, `HUP`, …) are stored/printed but not yet delivered — that needs kernel signal/exception support (see known-issues TD-OILS11). The **file-comparison test operators** `-nt` (newer-than), `-ot` (older-than), and `-ef` (same file) are implemented in both `test`/`[` and `[[ … ]]` (shared `file_cmp` helper): `-nt`/`-ot` compare modification times with bash's existence rule (`a -nt b` is also true when `a` exists and `b` does not), and `-ef` compares canonicalized paths as a portable stand-in for a device+inode match (distinct-name hard links are not detected — see known-issues TD-OILS12). The **`type [-t|-p|-P|-a|-f] name …`** builtin now classifies commands fully: it recognizes shell keywords (`if`/`while`/`case`/`select`/`{`/`[[`/… → "shell keyword"), functions, builtins, and external files found via a `$PATH` search (`find_all_in_path` returns every match). `-t` prints one type word (`keyword`/`function`/`builtin`/`file`, precedence in that order; status 1 if unknown), `-p` prints the path only when the name resolves to a file, `-P` forces a `$PATH` search and prints the path, `-a` lists every location in precedence order (function line, builtin line, then each file path), and `-f` skips function lookup; flags may be clustered (`-ap`). **Background-job tracking with `jobs`/`wait`** is implemented: a `&` command is recorded in a per-shell job table (job number = lowest unused, bash-style, so numbering restarts at 1 once the table drains; the spawned `Child` handle is retained and `$!` set to its pid). **`jobs [-l|-p]`** polls the table without blocking (`try_wait`) and prints each job as `[n]  Running/Done  cmdline` (`-l` adds the pid column, `-p` prints pids only), then drops any jobs it reported as Done. **`wait [pid|%job ...]`** blocks until the named jobs finish and yields the last waited job's exit status; with no operand it waits for every job. **`wait -n [ids…]`** returns as soon as the *next* job in the candidate set (the named ids, or all jobs when none are named) terminates — polling the live child handles — and returns 127 when there are no candidate jobs, and **`wait -p VAR`** stores the returned job's pid in `VAR`. The **`disown [-h] [-ar] [jobspec …]`** builtin removes jobs from the table (so `jobs`/`wait` no longer track them): `-h` keeps the job but marks it no-SIGHUP (advisory, pending signal delivery), `-a` selects all jobs, `-r` only running (not-yet-finished) jobs, and with no jobspec the current (last) job is used. Jobs are not inherited by subshell clones. The POSIX **`times`** builtin prints the shell's and its children's accumulated user/system CPU times (two `user sys` lines in bash's `%dm%d.%03ds` form); both are currently `0m0.000s` pending per-process CPU accounting (see known-issues TD-OILS10). The **`enable [-a] [-n] [name …]`** builtin enables/disables shell builtins: `enable -n NAME` disables a builtin so command resolution falls through to a same-named external (checked at every resolution site — plain dispatch, `command`, `&` background, and `type`/`command -v` classification — via a `builtin_enabled` helper backed by a per-shell `disabled_builtins` set inherited by subshell clones), `enable NAME` re-enables it, and the listing forms (`enable`, `enable -n`, `enable -a`) print builtins in re-inputtable `enable NAME` / `enable -n NAME` form; `builtin NAME` still force-runs a disabled builtin. The builtin name set is now a single `BUILTIN_NAMES` source of truth. **`declare -F`/`-f`** operate on functions: bare `declare -F` lists every function as `declare -f NAME` (sorted), `declare -F name` prints each name that is a function (status 1 if any is absent), and `declare -f name` reports the correct existence status (0 iff the name is a function) so `declare -f fn >/dev/null` works — function *body* printing awaits an AST source pretty-printer (see known-issues TD-OILS18/TD-OILS16). The **`exec [command [args]]`** builtin replaces the shell with `command` (run with the current environment/redirections, after which the shell exits with the command's status — a following command never runs; a missing command exits 127); `exec` with no command is a no-op that keeps running (redirection-only `exec > file` rebinding of the shell's own fds is not yet supported — see known-issues TD-OILS14). A true in-place `execve` that preserves the pid awaits kernel support. **`cd` now honors `CDPATH` and the `-L`/`-P` flags**: a bare relative target (not `/`-, `./`-, or `../`-anchored) is searched under each colon-separated `CDPATH` entry and, when found through a non-`.` entry, the destination path is echoed (bash); `-P` reports/stores the canonical (symlink-resolved) `$PWD`, `-L` (default) keeps the logical path. The **`umask [-S] [-p] [mode]`** builtin gets/sets the per-shell file-creation mask: no operand prints the mask (octal `0NNN`, or symbolic `u=rwx,g=rx,o=rx` with `-S`, or a re-inputtable `umask …` command with `-p`), and a `mode` operand sets it from an octal number or a symbolic clause list (`u=rwx,g=rx,o=`, `go-r`, `a=`, `+`/`-`/`=` operators). The mask is inherited by subshell clones; applying it to created-file permissions is gated on the target file-mode model (see known-issues TD-OILS15). The **`-o optname` shell-option test operator** — `[ -o NAME ]`, `test -o NAME`, and `[[ -o NAME ]]` — reports whether a `set -o` option (`errexit`/`nounset`/`xtrace`/`pipefail`) is currently enabled (unknown option names report disabled, matching bash). Bare **`set -o`** now lists the modelled options as `name  on/off` columns and **`set +o`** lists them as re-inputtable `set -o NAME`/`set +o NAME` lines (only the options the shell actually models — errexit/nounset/pipefail/xtrace — are listed, alphabetically, so reported state is always truthful). Bare **`set`** (no operands) now lists every shell variable in sorted, re-inputtable `name=value` / `name=([i]="v" …)` form (function definitions are not yet included — see known-issues TD-OILS16). Two further behavior-affecting options are modelled: **`set -f`/`-o noglob`** disables pathname (glob) expansion so patterns stay literal (wired into the glob-expansion entry point), and **`set -a`/`-o allexport`** auto-exports every subsequently-assigned variable (wired into `apply_assignment`); both appear in the `set -o` listing and are readable via `[ -o NAME ]`. A third such option, **`set -C`/`-o noclobber`**, is modelled with its **`>|` clobber-override redirection operator** (new lexer `Op::GreatPipe`, `RedirectOp::Clobber`): under noclobber a plain `>` refuses to truncate an existing regular file (status 1, `NAME: cannot overwrite existing file`, wired into `resolve_redirects`), while `>|` and `>>` always proceed; `set +C` clears it, and it appears in the `set -o` listing / `[ -o noclobber ]` test. The **`hash [-lr] [-p pathname] [-dt] [name …]`** builtin manages a remembered command-path table that is now *actually consulted during execution*: external command resolution routes through a `resolve_external` helper that reuses a cached full path (bumping its hit count) or runs a fresh `$PATH` search and remembers the result (falling back to the bare name so the OS can still locate it). `hash` prints the `hits`/`command` table, `-r` forgets all, `-d` forgets named entries, `-t` prints the remembered path(s), `-p pathname name` remembers without searching, `-l` lists re-inputtable `builtin hash -p …` lines, and bare `name`s force a fresh search; the table is inherited by subshell clones, and **`type`** now reports a remembered command as `NAME is hashed (path)` (and `type -p` prints the remembered path when a live PATH search comes up empty). **`unset`** now honors the **`-v`** (variables only) and **`-f`** (functions only) flags, and without a flag unsets a set variable in preference to a same-named function (bash precedence) instead of removing both. **Array/positional slicing** `${a[@]:off:len}` / `${a[*]:off:len}` / `${@:off:len}` / `${*:off:len}` is implemented: it selects a contiguous run of elements by position (0-based over the set values; for `@`/`*` the list is `$0` then the positional parameters, matching bash), a negative offset counts from the end, a negative length trims that many from the end, and an absent length runs to the end; the quoted `"${a[@]:o:l}"` form preserves one field per element (via a new `WordPart::ArraySlice` and `slice_elements` helper). **Bulk (element-wise) array transforms** `${a[@]#pat}`/`##`/`%`/`%%` (prefix/suffix trim), `${a[@]/pat/repl}`/`//`/`/#`/`/%` (substitution), `${a[@]^}`/`^^`/`,`/`,,` (case), and `${a[@]@Q}`/`@U`/`@u`/`@L`/`@E` (transform) now apply the scalar operator to *every* element of an array (or every positional parameter, `${@#pat}`/`${*/x/y}`/`${@^^}`); the `[*]`/`$*` form is accepted too, the quoted `"${a[@]#pat}"` form yields one field per transformed element, and only the *default* operators (`:-`/`:=`/…) remain rejected on `[@]`/`[*]`. Implemented via a new `WordPart::ArrayBulk`/`BulkOp` AST pair, a shared `parse_bulk_op`/`parse_replace_pieces` parser, and `bulk_elements`/`apply_bulk_op`/`transform_value` interp helpers. **Namerefs** (`declare -n ref=target` / `local -n`) are implemented: a nameref variable holds the *name* of another variable, and reads/writes of the nameref transparently redirect to the target — scalar `$ref`/`ref=v`, array elements `${ref[i]}`/`ref[i]=v`, whole-array `${ref[@]}`/`${#ref[@]}`, and the canonical pass-an-array-by-reference-to-a-function pattern (`declare -n out=$1; out=(…)`). A `resolve_ref_name` helper follows nameref chains with a cycle guard and is applied at the read/write chokepoints (`param_value`, `param_elem_value`, `assign_elem`, `array_elements`, `array_keys`, `expand_array_ref`, and `apply_assignment` — which rewrites the name and recurses); `declare -n`/`+n` set/clear the attribute (shown as `-n` in `declare -p`), `unset -n ref` drops the nameref while plain `unset ref` removes the target (bash semantics). `${!ref}` on a nameref yields the target *name* (bash special case), and namerefs to an array element (`declare -n ref=arr[0]`) resolve for both read (`$ref`) and write (`ref=v`) — TD-OILS17 fully resolved. **Local attribute scoping** is now correct: the per-call `VarSnapshot` captures and restores each name's `-i`/`-l`/`-u`/`-n`/readonly attributes alongside its value, and `declare_local` clears `-i`/`-l`/`-u`/`-n` when a bare `local x` shadows a global (matching bash, which does not inherit a global's attributes; readonly is left intact so a readonly global is not silently shadowed) — so a `local -n`/`local -i` inside a function no longer leaks its attribute out on return. The **`FUNCNAME` array** reflects the function call stack (bash: `FUNCNAME[0]` is the currently-executing function, then each caller, then `main` at the bottom; unset outside any function) — backed by an `fn_stack` pushed/popped in `call_function` and materialised into `arrays["FUNCNAME"]` by `refresh_funcname`, so `$FUNCNAME`, `${FUNCNAME[@]}`, and `${#FUNCNAME[@]}` all read through the normal array paths; a subshell inherits the enclosing function context. The unary file-test operators **`-L`/`-h`** (path is a symbolic link, via `symlink_metadata` so a broken link still tests true) and **`-t fd`** (descriptor 0/1/2 is a terminal, via `IsTerminal`) are implemented in both `test`/`[` and `[[ … ]]`. Fixed a latent `test`/`[` 3-argument bug where a leading `!` negation (`[ ! -f X ]`) was misparsed as a binary operator; the 3-arg path now follows POSIX order (binary primary first, then `!` negation, then `( expr )` grouping). The **`alias`/`unalias`** builtins are implemented with a real bash-style pre-parse alias-expansion pass (`lexer::expand_aliases`, run over the token stream by `parser::parse_with_aliases` before parsing): `alias name=value` defines, bare `alias`/`alias -p` lists every alias in re-inputtable `alias NAME='VALUE'` form (single-quoted value, sorted via a `BTreeMap`), `alias name` prints one alias (status 1 if undefined), and `unalias name …`/`unalias -a` removes. Expansion only fires on a single unquoted-literal word in **command position** (start of a simple command — after `;`/`&`/`|`/`&&`/`||`/`(`/newline or a command-introducing reserved word like `then`/`do`/`{`/`!`), the alias value's own first word is re-checked (guarded against self-recursion so `alias ls='ls -l'` terminates), and a value ending in a blank makes the *next* word alias-eligible too (bash's trailing-blank rule, enabling `alias sudo='sudo '`). Aliases are inherited by subshell clones. One fidelity gap: because a whole `run_source` input is parsed at once, an alias defined earlier in the *same* script/`-c` string is not seen by later commands in that input (interactive per-line REPL use is unaffected); command-substitution bodies are also not alias-expanded — see known-issues TD-OILS19. **`declare`/`typeset` now honor bash's function-scope rule**: inside a function they create *locals* by default (exactly like `local`, snapshotting/restoring the prior binding on return), and **`declare -g`** opts back out to global scope even inside a function (the array one-liner `declare -g -a a=(…)` honors it too); at global scope `-g` is a harmless no-op. The **`command_not_found_handle`** hook is honored: when a bare command name resolves nowhere on `$PATH` and a function of that name is defined, it is invoked with the command word as `$1` and its arguments as `$2`… (its exit status becomes `$?`) instead of reporting "command not found"; a slash-containing path bypasses the hook (bash semantics), and the cheap function-existence check is done before any extra `$PATH` scan so the common case is unaffected. The **`fg`/`bg`** job-control builtins are implemented for a shell without terminal job control: **`fg [jobspec]`** foregrounds a background job — it prints the job's command line to stdout (bash behavior) and blocks until the job finishes, returning its exit status; with no jobspec the current (most recently backgrounded) job is used, and an empty table or unknown spec is a status-1 error. **`bg [jobspec …]`** reports each targeted job in bash's `[id] cmd &` form and returns 0 (backgrounded jobs already run here — there is no SIGTSTP/SIGCONT, so `bg` is a spec-resolving reporting form); no jobspec targets the current job, and an empty table or unknown spec is a status-1 error. Resuming a *stopped* job and controlling-tty transfer await kernel signal/job-control support (see known-issues TD-OILS13). A faithful **AST source pretty-printer** (`unparse.rs`) reconstructs re-parseable shell source from a parsed `Program`/`FunctionDef` — covering every compound command, all `WordPart` expansion variants, assignments, redirections, and `[[ … ]]`/`(( … ))`, round-trip-stability tested — so **`declare -f NAME`** and bare `declare -f` now print each function's reconstructed body, **`type NAME`** prints the "is a function" line followed by the source, and **bare `set`** lists function definitions after the variables (closing TD-OILS16 and TD-OILS18; here-docs are re-emitted as equivalent here-strings). **`$LINENO`** reports the 1-based source line of the currently-executing item: the parser counts the top-level newline tokens it consumes and stamps the running line number onto each parsed `Item`, the interpreter sets `self.current_line` before running each item, and `param_value` returns it on read (blank/comment lines advance the counter; semicolon-joined commands share a line). Lines inside multi-line quotes/substitutions/here-doc bodies are undercounted because their interior newlines are absorbed by the lexer (see known-issues TD-OILS20). The **`BASH_SOURCE`/`BASH_LINENO` call-stack arrays** and the **`caller [expr]`** builtin are implemented on top of the call stack: a per-shell `call_line_stack` captures the source line at each function call site (kept in lockstep with `fn_stack`), so `refresh_funcname` now materialises all three parallel arrays — `FUNCNAME[i]` (function), `BASH_LINENO[i]` (line where `FUNCNAME[i]` was called, `0` for the bottom `main` frame), and `BASH_SOURCE[i]` (source file, `$0`) — and clears them outside any function. `caller` prints "LINE SOURCE" for the current call site; `caller N` prints "LINE FUNCNAME SOURCE" for frame N (0 = current function), returning 1 outside a function or when N is out of range/non-numeric. Per-function definition source isn't tracked, so `BASH_SOURCE`/`caller` always report `$0` even for functions loaded via `source` (see known-issues TD-OILS21). The **`$_` special variable** tracks the last argument of the most recent simple command (set after each command's argv is expanded, read by the following command; a single-word command leaves `$_` as that word); the startup form where `$_` is the shell/script pathname is not modelled. The **`$BASH_COMMAND` special variable** holds the command currently executing — the *unexpanded* reconstructed source text of the running simple command (via `unparse::simple_src`, so `echo $BASH_COMMAND` prints `echo $BASH_COMMAND` and `x=1 echo hi` records the prefix/redirections too), stored in `vars` (visible to `set`/`declare -p`) and updated at the top of every simple command *except* while a trap handler runs — so a `DEBUG`/`ERR` trap still sees the command that triggered it (bash). Granularity is simple-command-level (compound commands are not separately recorded). The **`$-` special variable** reports the currently-enabled single-letter option flags: the modelled toggles `a` (allexport), `e` (errexit), `f` (noglob), `u` (nounset), `x` (xtrace), `C` (noclobber), plus `h` (hashall) and `B` (brace expansion) which are always on here — emitted in bash's fixed flag-table order regardless of the order they were set (`set -xu` ⇒ `huxB`); `-o`-only options without a letter (e.g. `pipefail`) are excluded, matching bash. The **`help [-dms] [pattern …]`** builtin displays information about shell builtins from an in-tree synopsis table (name, usage line, one-line description) kept in sync with `BUILTIN_NAMES`: with no pattern it lists every builtin's usage synopsis sorted; each pattern is matched against builtin names as a shell glob (a bare name is an exact topic); `-s` prints only the usage synopsis, `-d` only the short description, `-m` renders the default long form, and the default prints the usage line followed by an indented description; a pattern matching nothing writes `no help topics match` to stderr and returns 1. The **combined-output redirections `&>file`/`&>>file`** (and the equivalent `>&file` form with a non-numeric target) send both stdout and stderr to the file (truncate / append), equivalent to `>file 2>&1`: new lexer ops `AmpGreat`/`AmpDGreat`, `RedirectOp::WriteBoth`/`AppendBoth`, and a parser rule that keeps a numeric `>&N`/`>&-` as an fd duplication while treating `>&filename` as a both-streams redirect. When stdout and stderr target the same file the compound path now appends the buffered stdout after the stderr already written (fixing a latent truncation where flushing the stdout capture would clobber stderr) — both streams survive, in stderr-then-stdout order (interleaving is not preserved by the capture model). **Tilde expansion** now covers `~+` (→ `$PWD`), `~-` (→ `$OLDPWD`), and the directory-stack forms `~N`/`~+N` (Nth entry from the left, 0 = current dir) and `~-N` (Nth from the right), each keeping any trailing `/path` remainder; a `~` alone still expands to `$HOME`, `~/path` keeps the remainder, and an unresolvable `~user` prefix (no user database on this target) is left literal, matching bash's "no expansion if lookup fails" rule. In an **assignment RHS**, a tilde-prefix that follows an unquoted `:` (or begins the value) is also expanded (`PATH=~/a:~/b`, `x=$PATH:~/bin`), while a quoted tilde stays literal. This now extends to **declaration-builtin operands** (`export X=~/foo`, `declare Y=~/a:~/b`, `typeset`, `local L=~/lib`, `readonly R=~/r`): the command word is recognised syntactically as a declaration builtin and each `NAME=value`/`NAME+=value`/`NAME[idx]=value` operand is expanded in assignment context — tilde-expanded, and neither word-split nor glob-expanded (so `export S=$v` keeps embedded spaces). Along the way the **`NAME+=value` append form** on the declaration builtins `declare`/`typeset`/`local`, `export`, and `readonly` (previously mis-parsed as a variable literally named `NAME+`, silently dropping the append) now correctly appends to the current value (numeric add under `-i`). The **redirection-only `exec` form** now persistently rebinds the shell's ambient fd 1 / fd 2: `exec > file`/`>> file`/`2> file`/`2>> file`/`> file 2>&1`/`1>&2` store a per-shell `exec_stdout`/`exec_stderr` target (truncated once for `>`, then append), which every ambient-fd write consults — builtins via `write_bytes`, `>&2` diagnostics via `emit_stderr`, and external children via `run_external` — so all subsequent commands (and inherited subshells) route to the file. The **input** form `exec < file` (and `exec << EOF`) likewise rebinds the ambient fd 0: the source is read once into a per-shell `exec_stdin` cursor that every base fd-0 read consults (the `read` builtins, `read_all_bytes`/`mapfile`, and an external inheriting fd 0), so successive `read`s consume successive lines; a subshell inherits a snapshot of the remaining bytes. **Named input descriptors** are also modelled: `exec 3< file` (or `exec 3<< EOF` / `3<<< str`) opens a user-space fd ≥ 3 in a per-shell `open_fds` table (the file slurped once into a position-tracking cursor, errors surfaced at redirection time), `exec 3<&-` closes it, and **`read -u N`** consumes successive records from that descriptor independently of fd 0 (a bad/unopened fd is a status-1 `read: N: bad file descriptor`); a subshell inherits an independent-offset snapshot of each open fd. **Named write descriptors** complete the story: `exec 3> file`/`3>> file` opens a user-space write fd ≥ 3 in a per-shell `open_write_fds` table (a shared `Arc<File>`, truncate-once for `>`), `echo … >&3` routes a builtin's stdout there (via a `write_to_fd` helper) and `cmd >&3`/`cmd 2>&3` routes an external child's fd 1/fd 2 there (via `RedirPlan.stdout_to_fd`/`stderr_to_fd`), successive writes accumulate on the shared handle, `exec 3>&-` closes it, and a subshell shares the same handle (bash fd inheritance); an unopened write fd is a status-1 `N: Bad file descriptor`. This also fixed a latent bug where a per-command `N> file` (N ≥ 3) fell into the stdout arm and wrongly redirected fd 1 (now fd ≥ 3 output redirects route to `extra_fds`, a documented no-op on non-`exec` commands). **Scoped per-command extra-fd redirects** also work: a compound command carrying a fd ≥ 3 redirect (`while read -u 3 line; do …; done 3< file`, `{ …; } 4> log`, `… 3<&-`) installs the descriptor into the shell's fd table for the body's duration only — `exec_redirected` saves each touched fd's prior binding (by ownership) and restores it (removing the scoped fd) when the body finishes — so `read -u 3` inside the loop reads the file while fd 0 stays free, and fd 3 is gone afterward. **Builtin stderr redirects** also work now: a simple-command builtin honors its own fd-2 redirect — `read … 2> file`/`2>> file` (a builtin diagnostic lands in the file), `echo … 2>&3`/`read … 2>&3` (routes builtin stderr to a user-space write descriptor via a scoped `StderrTarget::WriteFd`), and `… 2>&1` (folds builtin stderr into fd 1's live sink — captured stdout, pipeline stage, or terminal) — installed as a scoped `StderrTarget` for the builtin's duration in `run_builtin` (the `exec` builtin is exempt, since it sets the persistent `exec_stderr` itself). **Function-invocation redirects** also work: a function call carrying its own redirects (`myfunc > file`, `myfunc 2> err`, `myfunc < in`, and compound-scoped fd ≥ 3 forms) runs the whole function body inside a redirect scope — `exec_simple` routes the call through a shared `exec_with_redirects` helper (extracted from `exec_redirected`) when the plan `needs_scope`, so the body's stdout/stderr/stdin and any diagnostics honor the redirect; without redirects the call dispatches directly to avoid scope-setup overhead. Still deferred: duplicating a write-fd *onto* a standard fd (`exec 3>&1`) — see known-issues TD-OILS14. Only a true pid-preserving `execve` remains (gated on kernel support — see known-issues TD-OILS14). **Process substitution** `<(cmd)`/`>(cmd)` is implemented via a temp-file model (the host has no `/dev/fd` or named pipes): the lexer reads an unquoted `<(`/`>(` as a `Seg::ProcSub` word (concatenation-friendly), the parser lowers it to `WordPart::ProcSub`, and at expansion `<(cmd)` runs the body *now* capturing its stdout into a temp file whose path is substituted (`diff <(sort a) <(sort b)`, `read x < <(cmd)`, `. <(cmd)`), while `>(cmd)` creates an empty temp file, substitutes its path, and defers the body until after the enclosing command — running it with the file's contents as stdin (`echo … > >(cmd)`); both temp files are cleaned up by an `exec_simple` wrapper (drained from a per-command mark on `procsub_in_temps`/`procsub_out_jobs`), and a subshell manages its own. Not streaming — an infinite producer like `<(tail -f)` would block at expansion — a documented limitation (known-issues TD-OILS22). **Colon vs. colon-less parameter expansion** is now distinguished: the parser records whether a `${var-word}`/`${var=word}`/`${var+word}`/`${var?word}` operator carried a leading `:` (new `colon: bool` on `WordPart::ParamOp`), and `expand_param_op` selects the "active" predicate accordingly — the colon forms (`:-`/`:=`/`:+`/`:?`) treat an empty-but-set value the same as unset (active only when set *and* non-empty), while the colon-less forms treat an empty-but-set value as set (active whenever the variable is set), so `x=; echo ${x-D}` now prints empty and `x=; echo ${x+A}` prints `A`, both matching bash (previously both were wrongly treated as the colon form). **Indirect expansion to a whole-array referent** now works: `${!ref}` where `ref` resolves to `name[@]`/`name[*]` expands like `${name[@]}`/`${name[*]}` (previously it fed `@`/`*` into the arithmetic subscript evaluator and errored) — the unquoted form space-joins/field-splits the elements and the quoted `"${!ref}"` form preserves one field per element (via `indirect_array_elems` in the annotated per-element path). 400 host tests pass; builds clean for x86_64-slateos; clippy-clean. Remaining gap: the `-r`/`-x` file-permission tests are approximated, gated on the slateos permission model (TD-OILS1).

The default feature set (including os, network, mimalloc) builds cleanly — not just os-minimal.  See todo.txt "Roadmap §2.7" entry for the gnu→msvc finding and the two upstream-grade fixes committed inside the nushell tree: (1) scripts/build.rs skip-on-missing rc.exe and (2) nu-cmd-extra/build.rs from_reader→from_str portability fix)

  - [x] budibase-cli: Budibase — Michael Drury + Joe Johnston 2019 Belfast, GPL-3.0 open-source with first-class built-in BudibaseDB (CouchDB-backed), $7M Series A 2022 Concentric + Frontline (budibase)
  - [x] tooljet-cli: ToolJet — Navaneeth Pandiyaraj 2021 Bengaluru YC W22, MIT-licensed (most permissive in the segment) Retool-alternative low-code internal-tools platform (tooljet)
  - [x] softr-cli: Softr — Mariam Hakobyan + Artur Mkrtchyan 2019 Berlin (ex-Lufthansa engineers), no-code client portals + member sites on top of Airtable + Google Sheets, $15M Series A FirstMark 2022 (softr)
  - [x] glide-cli: Glide — David Siegel + Antonio Garcia Aprea 2018 SF, mobile-first no-code apps from Google Sheets (2019 viral demo) pivoted to business apps + Glide AI, Benchmark-led Series A 2020 + Series B 2021 (glide)
  - [x] noloco-cli: Noloco — Darragh Mc Kay + Simon Kerr 2020 Dublin (ex-Intercom + ex-Pointy), no-code client portals + internal tools on Airtable + Sheets + Postgres + HubSpot, ~$5M seed + Series A (noloco)
- [x] Personality binaries batch 330 — design + whiteboarding + visual collaboration (8 utilities):
  - [x] miro-cli: Miro — Andrey Khusid + Oleg Shardin 2011 Perm Russia (rebranded 2019), infinite-canvas collaborative whiteboard market leader, $400M Series C 2022 at $17.5B ICONIQ-led, relocated post-2022 (miro)
  - [x] framer-cli: Framer — Koen Bok + Jorn van Dijk 2014 Amsterdam (ex-Sofa/ex-Facebook), designer-first publish-to-real-web site builder pivot 2022, $27M Series C 2023 Atomico + AlleyCorp (framer)
  - [x] penpot-cli: Penpot — Kaleidos 2020 Madrid, MPL-2.0 open-source SVG-native Figma alternative, $8M Series A late 2023 Decibel + Athletica, Mozilla + GitLab + EU public-sector customers (penpot)
  - [x] invision-cli: InVision — Clark Valberg + Ben Nadel 2011 NYC, dominant 2014-2018 prototype platform peaked at $2B+ valuation, sunset 31 Dec 2024 after losing to Figma, Freehand spun to Miro 2024 (invision)
  - [x] marvel-cli: Marvel — Murat Mutlu + Brendan Moore 2013 London, lightweight UK-based design + prototype platform, ~$8M Series A 2017 Connect Ventures, strong UK education funnel — survivor brand (marvel)
  - [x] zeplin-cli: Zeplin — Pelin Kenez + Berk Cebi 2014 SF/Istanbul, original design-to-developer handoff category leader pivoted upmarket to design-systems + Connected Components, $13M Series B 2018 (zeplin)
  - [x] whimsical-cli: Whimsical — Steve Schoeffel + Kaspars Dancis 2017 Toronto + Riga (both ex-Wave), bootstrapped + profitable opinionated visual-collab platform for flowcharts + wireframes + mind maps + boards (whimsical)
  - [x] excalidraw-cli: Excalidraw — Christopher Chedeau (vjeux) + maintainers Jan 2020 hobby project, MIT open-source hand-drawn-style whiteboard built on Rough.js, 80k+ GitHub stars, Excalidraw+ to Notion 2024 (excalidraw)
- [x] Terminal emulator (basic, serial/framebuffer):
  - [x] VT100/xterm ANSI escape sequence support (cursor movement, scroll regions, insert/delete lines/chars, SGR attributes, 256-color, truecolor, DEC private modes, alt screen buffer, DSR cursor report)
  - [x] Persistent searchable history (Ctrl+R reverse incremental search, history save/load to tmpfs, `history` command with list/search/clear, 512-entry ring buffer, shadow copy for command access), tab completion (command name prefix + filesystem path completion)
  - [x] Unicode support (UTF-8 multi-byte accumulation, procedural box drawing/block element/geometric/arrow/symbol glyph generation, East Asian width detection, comprehensive self-tests)
  - [x] Configurable colors (6 built-in schemes: default/solarized-dark/monokai/dracula/gruvbox/light, custom FG/BG via hex RGB, runtime palette swap, SGR uses scheme defaults, `color` kshell command)
  - [x] tmux-like session detach/reattach (termsession module: 10 sessions, per-session screen/scrollback/history/CWD/env, Ctrl+B quick-switch, tsession command)
  - [x] Find in backscroll (Ctrl+F interactive search with Ctrl+N/P navigation, 1000-line scrollback ring buffer, `scrollback` command with search/list/screen dump, per-cell screen text buffer for capture)

### 2.8 I/O scheduler
- [x] BFQ-style I/O scheduler:
  - [x] Realtime priority (audio/video)
  - [x] Best-effort with priority levels
  - [x] Idle priority (background indexing, backup, dedup)
  - [x] Per-process queues with elevator (C-SCAN) sector ordering
  - [x] Budget-based fairness with two-pass rotation
  - [x] Adjacent request merging
  - [x] Capability-gated realtime I/O priority

---

## Phase 3: Graphics and GUI

_Depends on: Phase 2 (drivers, filesystem, basic userspace). Goal: boot to a graphical desktop._

### 3.1 GPU drivers
- [ ] Port AMDGPU driver (open source, well-documented — first priority)
- [ ] Port Intel i915/xe driver (integrated graphics — covers most laptops)
- [ ] NVIDIA: defer until open-source driver matures, or use Linux compat layer later

### 3.2 Graphics stack
- [x] DRM/KMS equivalent (kernel mode setting, GPU memory management)
  - [x] DRM core: object model (DrmObjectId, device registry, per-device object tables)
  - [x] Connector, CRTC, Plane, Encoder abstractions
  - [x] PixelFormat enum (XRGB8888, ARGB8888, XBGR8888, ABGR8888, RGB565)
  - [x] DrmMode (resolution + timing, mode name formatting)
  - [x] GEM buffer objects (system-RAM backed, frame allocator, zeroed on alloc)
  - [x] Framebuffer objects (GEM-backed, format metadata)
  - [x] Atomic modesetting data structures (AtomicState, CrtcState, PlaneState, ConnectorState)
  - [x] Property system (typed enum for CRTC/plane/connector properties)
  - [x] LimineBackend: bootloader framebuffer (enumerate, gem_create/destroy/mmap, page_flip, flush_region)
  - [x] VirtioGpuBackend: paravirtualized GPU (enumerate, gem_create/destroy/mmap, page_flip via virtio-gpu driver)
  - [x] Enum dispatch for hot-path performance (no dyn Trait overhead)
  - [x] Self-tests (6 tests: device registration, enumeration, GEM lifecycle, FB lifecycle, display size, format utils)
  - [x] Migrate compositor from direct fb.rs to DRM API (double-buffered page flip)
  - [x] DRM syscalls (1000-1099 range) for userspace GPU access
  - [x] EDID parsing for real hardware mode detection
  - [x] Hotplug detection framework
  - [x] Atomic modesetting check + commit (atomic_check validates objects/modes/bindings, atomic_commit applies state, test_only dry-run mode)
  - [x] Cursor plane support (per-CRTC cursor state, cursor_set/cursor_move, GEM-backed cursor image, hot spot)
  - [x] Display query syscalls (connector status, mode enumeration, CRTC info)
  - [x] Cursor syscalls (SYS_DRM_CURSOR_SET, SYS_DRM_CURSOR_MOVE)
  - [x] Atomic commit syscall (SYS_DRM_ATOMIC_COMMIT with serialized state buffer)
- [-] Vulkan loader and basic GPU command submission
  - [x] virtio-gpu DRM driver-specific uAPI ABI layer (`kernel/src/drm/virtgpu_uapi.rs`): byte-exact `virtgpu_drm.h` struct mirrors + `DRM_IOCTL_VIRTGPU_*` numbers + `VIRTGPU_PARAM_*`/capset/blob/context-param constants + GETPARAM policy + exhaustive self-test. Pure ABI (no device state/unsafe), mirroring the DRM/KMS `uapi.rs` shim. Foundation for routing render-node ioctls (GETPARAM/GET_CAPS/RESOURCE_CREATE/CONTEXT_INIT/EXECBUFFER/TRANSFER_*/WAIT/MAP) into the virtio-gpu driver's 3D/virgl path.
  - [x] Boot test attaches `-device virtio-gpu-pci` so the virtio-gpu 2D device bring-up path is exercised on real hardware (DRM device 1 = virtio-gpu, promoted to primary; live pixel write/read + flush_rect self-test).
  - [x] `/dev/dri/card0` + `renderD128` bound to the primary GPU device (`drm::primary_device`), so a libdrm/Mesa client's render node targets the GPU rather than the fallback dumb framebuffer.
  - [~] **Acceleration payoff gated on Q18** (open-questions.md): real 3D/virgl needs a virgl-capable test env (`virtio-gpu-gl` + host GL/display + virglrenderer — the headless CI is 2D-only) **and** the Mesa port (§4583, a large external C port needing operator go-ahead). Next kernel-side step (render-ioctl dispatch with honest no-3D reporting) is option B in Q18, available on request.
- [ ] OpenGL via Mesa (port Mesa's Vulkan and OpenGL drivers)
- [ ] 2D drawing library: Vello (Rust-native, GPU compute shaders) + HarfBuzz via FFI for complex text shaping

### 3.3 Compositor
- [-] Wayland-inspired compositor (userspace):
  - [x] Window management (create/destroy/move/resize/minimize/maximize/focus/Z-ordering)
  - [x] Compositing pipeline: double-buffered framebuffer, alpha blending, damage tracking
  - [x] Render engine: execute guitk RenderCommands (rect fill/stroke, text, lines, clip/translate)
  - [x] Bitmap font rendering (monospace, A-Z/a-z/0-9/punctuation)
  - [x] Font rendering library (gui/font): built-in 8x16 monospace, text layout with word wrap, glyph rendering to ARGB
  - [x] Window client library (gui/window): WindowBuilder, EventLoop, 16 event types, CursorShape, compositor protocol
  - [x] Input routing: hit testing, keyboard→focused, mouse→under-cursor
  - [x] Window decorations: title bar with buttons, borders, shadow
  - [x] Drag operations: window move (title bar), resize (8 edges/corners)
  - [x] Cursor shape management (arrow, resize variants, text, hand, wait)
  - [x] Multi-monitor display management with virtual bounds
  - [x] Compositor protocol: request/response/notification enums (ready for IPC)
  - [x] Frame timing for VSync-aware scheduling
  - [ ] GPU acceleration (currently software rasterizer)
  - [x] DMA-BUF buffer sharing between apps and compositor (gui/compositor/src/buffer.rs: SharedBuffer + BufferFormat{Argb8888,Xrgb8888}; zero-copy wl_buffer/dma-buf-style surface path alongside the render-tree path. SharedBuffer::import validates client geometry against a hostile trust boundary — caps dimensions to the framebuffer pixel limit, requires stride >= width*bpp, rejects strides/sizes that overflow or mappings shorter than the declared rows, all with checked arithmetic and bounds-checked reads (no panic/index) — and normalizes the source (stride padding + format) into densely-packed ARGB8888. Compositor::attach_buffer/detach_buffer attach an imported buffer to a Window (new Window.buffer field); render_window blits attached buffers via blit_buffer (top-left aligned, clipped to the buffer×client overlap, alpha-blended through Framebuffer::blend_pixel honoring per-pixel alpha and window opacity, offscreen coords skipped) instead of replaying RenderCommands. wl_buffer.release-style protocol: SharedBuffer.mark_released/take_release + Compositor::take_released_buffer_handles drains composited buffers' handles exactly once so the IPC layer can notify clients to reuse shared memory. 15 tests (10 buffer-module unit tests covering import/validation/format/release + 5 compositor integration tests covering blit-into-framebuffer, bad-geometry rejection leaving the render-tree path, window-not-found, detach-reverts, release notification). IPC note: real SlateOS shm handles not yet wired into the still-stubbed compositor IPC — import currently takes the mapped bytes directly; when channel IPC lands only the byte source changes (a mapping of the pages named by handle), validation/blit/release stay identical.)
  - [x] Fullscreen bypass (direct scanout for games) (gui/compositor/src/main.rs: true fullscreen window state (Window.fullscreen + fs_restore_rect, distinct from maximize) via Compositor::set_fullscreen/is_fullscreen + a SetFullscreen protocol request; fullscreen windows drop all decorations and cover the whole display. New Scanout enum {Composited, Direct(WindowId)} + a per-frame scanout field. direct_scanout_window() detects eligibility — topmost visible window is fullscreen, fully opaque, covers the entire framebuffer, has an attached shared buffer whose dimensions exactly match the display, and nothing visible sits above it; a smaller/larger buffer is rejected so the screen can't go stale. When eligible, compose_frame takes a zero-copy fast path: no framebuffer clear, no per-pixel blit, no occluded windows drawn, no buffer swap — it just flags the buffer released (wl_buffer.release), bumps FrameStats.bypass_frames, and returns. present_pixels() then returns the client buffer's pixels directly (true direct scanout), with is_scanout_bypassed()/scanout() accessors; front_buffer() documented as the composited (possibly stale during bypass) surface. 6 new tests: fullscreen geometry+restore, bypass-presents-buffer (verifies pixels come from the client buffer + bypass_frames + release), and no-bypass for buffer-smaller-than-display / not-fullscreen / translucent. clippy-clean on the slateos target; 50 compositor tests green.)
  - [x] Native remote desktop streaming (gui/remote: guiremote crate — compact binary wire format for guitk RenderCommand frames; encoder + streaming-friendly decoder with try_decode_frame returning None on partial input; bounds-checked + size-capped against hostile senders; round-trips all 10 RenderCommand variants including text with optional max-width and FontWeightHint; 19 tests covering full round-trip, per-variant, back-to-back streaming, every error path, multi-byte UTF-8, frame-size sanity). Multi-window scene protocol layered on the codec (gui/remote/src/scene.rs): SCEN-magic delta frames carry per-window geometry (id/x/y/w/h/opacity) + an optional embedded ORDR sub-frame of commands; SceneSession tracks an FNV-1a fingerprint of each window's last-sent command bytes and suppresses re-sending unchanged content (geometry-only deltas), reports removed windows, and reset() forces a full resend on viewer reconnect. apply_scene_frame reconstructs the viewer's window→RenderTree map from deltas; decode is bounds-checked + window-count-capped (TooManyWindows). The compositor (gui/compositor/src/main.rs) drives a per-viewer SceneSession via capture_stream_frame and encodes with encode_scene_frame over the still-stubbed IPC. 7 scene unit tests + a tests/scene_session.rs end-to-end integration test (server↔viewer reconstruction across new/unchanged/changed/moved/removed windows + reconnect, plus corrupt/truncated-transport rejection); 26 guiremote + 54 compositor tests green.)
  - [ ] Video-encoded capture fallback (H.264/VP9 for games/video)

### 3.5 GUI toolkit / widget API
- [x] Layout engine (Flexbox/Grid-based, not CSS — native implementation)

  - [x] BoxShadow, opacity, overflow (visible/hidden/scroll)

  - [x] Buttons (text), labels
