  - [x] Grid view (grid.rs: virtual-scrolled grid, icon+label cells, multi-select, rubber-band, type-ahead, drag)
  - [x] Modal and non-modal dialogs, alert popups (modal.rs: ModalOverlay, AlertDialog, InputDialog, ProgressDialog, NonModalDialog)
- [x] Render tree abstraction (backend-agnostic drawing primitives)
  - [x] RenderCommand enum: FillRect, StrokeRect, Text, Image, Line, BoxShadow

  - [x] RenderTree with command list and viewport
- [x] Additional widgets: Separator, ProgressBar, Slider, Image, Container
- [x] Text views (textview.rs):
  - [x] SimpleTextView: plain text + full ANSI SGR parser (4/8/24-bit color), selection, search, max lines
  - [x] RichTextView: headings, lists, code blocks, links, word wrap, inline images (placeholder)
  - [x] Scroll-to-bottom / stay-at-bottom when new text added (auto-scroll on append)
- [x] Advanced features:
  - [x] Clipboard (multi-format: text, HTML, image, structured data, history)
    - [x] System clipboard service with 7 formats (PlainText/RichText/Html/ImagePng/ImageBmp/FilePaths/Custom)
    - [x] History (50 entries), pinning, search, format conversion (HTML→text, RTF→text)
    - [x] Sensitive mode (auto-clear 30s, excluded from history), change subscriptions
  - [x] Drag-and-drop (OLE-style multi-format data transfer)
    - [x] DataObject with multi-format storage, DataFormat enum (7 standard + Custom)
    - [x] DragDropManager state machine (Idle→Dragging→OverTarget)
    - [x] Drop target registration, hit testing, format compatibility, effect negotiation
    - [x] Drag threshold, cancel support, DragEvent lifecycle events
  - [x] File picker / save dialog (reuses file explorer component)
    - [x] Open/Save/SelectFolder modes with builder API
    - [x] Directory navigation (back/forward/up), quick-access sidebar
    - [x] Sortable file list, extension filters, auto-extension append
    - [x] Keyboard navigation, dark theme rendering
  - [x] Notification system (gui/notifications daemon)
    - [x] Toast notifications (top-right, max 4, auto-dismiss by priority)
    - [x] Notification center (grouped by app, clear all, read/unread)
    - [x] Do Not Disturb (manual + scheduled, critical bypass)
    - [x] Per-app settings, progress bars, action buttons
  - [x] DPI/scaling awareness, automatic image scaling (scaling.rs: LogicalPixel/PhysicalPixel, ScaleContext, per-monitor, image scale helpers)
  - [x] Enable/disable controls with optional reason tooltip (disabled.rs: groups, conditional enable, form validation)
  - [x] SVG rendering support (svg.rs: path commands, shapes, transforms, scanline AA rasterizer, Bézier flattening)
  - [x] Context menu extension API (context_ext.rs: capability-gated, lazy-loading, 200ms timeout, glob matching)
- [x] Credential manager service (gui/credentials):
  - [x] Central credential storage (6 types: Password/Token/Certificate/SshKey/ApiKey/Custom)
  - [x] XOR stream cipher encryption with SHA-256-derived session key
  - [x] Master password, auto-lock (5 min idle), rate-limited unlock (3 fails = 30s lockout)
  - [x] URL matching for autofill (exact > parent domain > wildcard, path prefix)
  - [x] Password generator with strength estimation
  - [x] Store/retrieve/update/delete/list/search API
  - [x] User identity verification with debounce (IdentityVerifier: 4 sensitivity levels, per-level debounce, lockout, classify_operation)

### 3.6 Audio
- [x] Audio driver framework
  - [x] Intel HDA controller driver: PCI detection (14 device IDs + class fallback), MMIO BAR0, controller reset, CORB/RIRB command ring setup (256 entries), codec discovery via STATESTS, codec topology probe (AFG walk, DAC/pin node identification), output stream configuration (BDL, 48kHz/16-bit/stereo format), amp unmute, start/stop playback, 440 Hz test tone generator, kshell `audio`/`hda` command
  - [x] PC speaker driver (PIT channel 2): tone(freq)/off()/beep(freq, dur) API, startup chime, self-test
  - [x] Virtio-sound driver: PCI probe (legacy 0x1058 + modern 0x1059), legacy I/O transport, 4 virtqueues (control/event/TX/RX), PCM stream info query, set_params/prepare/start/stop/release lifecycle, 440 Hz test tone playback (48kHz/S16/stereo), kshell `audio` integration with fallback chain (virtio→HDA→pcspk)
  - [x] AC97 legacy audio driver: Intel ICH family (8 device IDs), dual-BAR PIO (NAM mixer + NABM bus master), cold reset, codec config, BDL ring buffer DMA playback, variable rate audio
- [x] Audio mixing (per-app volume control)
  - [x] Software mixer: 8 concurrent streams, per-stream volume/mute, master volume/mute, 48kHz/S16/stereo, 32-bit intermediate summing with i16 clamping, ring buffers (16KB/stream), kshell `mixer` command
- [x] System notification sounds
  - [x] 7 event types (Error/Warning/Success/Notification/Critical/BootComplete/Shutdown), procedural PCM generation (sweeps, fades, multi-tone sequences), mixer integration with PC speaker fallback, separate notification volume
- [x] Sound history (which apps played/are playing sound)
  - [x] Circular log (64 entries): stream name, open/close TSC timestamps, bytes played, volume, duration; is_playing()/active_count() real-time queries, recent(n) history API, stats()

### 3.7 File type associations
- [x] Extension → default app mapping (fs::associations registry with MIME→app priority system, extension override, kshell `assoc` command)
- [x] MIME type detection (fs::mime: ~40 magic signatures, ~100 extensions, from_bytes/from_extension/detect/category API, kshell `mime` command)
- [x] Per-app icons per extension (associations.rs: per-type icon_id, app icons in UI)
- [x] Easily discoverable UI to change associations (associations.rs: settings page with search, categories, expand-to-change)
- [x] Fallback to previous app when handler is uninstalled (handle_uninstall with 3-deep history)
- [x] File extensions: .nx (executable), .dso (shared library), .slib (static library) — defined in filetypes.rs with magic bytes

## Phase 4: Applications

_Depends on: Phase 3 (GUI toolkit and desktop shell). Goal: usable daily-driver desktop._

### 4.1 Core applications
- [x] File explorer:
  - [x] Navigation with back/forward history, breadcrumb address bar
  - [x] Detail view with columns (name, size, modified, type)
  - [x] File type detection (18+ extensions), icon assignment
  - [x] View modes (Details/List/Icons), sort by name/size/date/type
  - [x] Toolbar, sidebar with quick-access locations, status bar
  - [x] Path bar with autocomplete (pathbar.rs: breadcrumb + edit mode, Tab completion, overflow, validation)
  - [x] Thumbnails (thumbs.rs: LRU cache, BMP/PNG/GIF/JPEG parsing, downscale, text preview, folder preview, batch queue)
  - [x] Custom columns per file type, app-extensible columns (columns.rs: 5 providers, auto-detect, sort/resize/reorder)
  - [x] Drop zones for drag-and-drop (dropzone.rs: hit-testing, operation selection, nested prevention, feedback)
  - [x] Atomic copy/move/delete with undo, resume on interruption (fileops.rs: journal, recycle bin, conflict policies, progress)
- [x] Text editor:
  - [x] Multi-tab document editing with tab bar
  - [x] Cursor movement, selection, clipboard (cut/copy/paste)
  - [x] Undo/redo stack (insert/delete char, insert/delete line)
  - [x] Find & replace (find all, next/prev match, replace current/all)
  - [x] Language detection (12 languages from extension)
  - [x] Line numbers (gutter), scroll support, status bar
  - [x] Dark theme (Catppuccin Mocha)
  - [x] Syntax highlighting (highlight.rs: 8 languages, 19 token types, multi-line state, Catppuccin theme)
  - [x] Advanced structural editing (syntree.rs: scope-aware syntactic tree across 12 languages with brace/paren/bracket nodes, string + line/block comment awareness, depth-first outline, fold ranges, and expand-selection primitive — pure-Rust alternative to upstream tree-sitter, swappable behind same API when the C library becomes available in the SlateOS toolchain)
- [x] Process explorer:
  - [x] Sortable process table (PID, name, status, CPU%, memory, threads, priority, user)

- [x] Photo/video viewer:
  - [x] Image format detection (BMP/PNG/JPEG/GIF magic bytes, header parsing for dimensions)

  - [x] Audio format detection (WAV/MP3/FLAC/OGG header parsing, metadata extraction)

### 4.2 Package manager — Python/fastpy candidate
- [x] Content-addressed immutable store (Nix model) — SHA-256 CAS with Git-style prefix dirs
- [x] Atomic updates and rollback (generation pointer swap) — append-only generation history
- [x] Show requested capabilities before install (Android-style) — manifest capabilities field
- [x] Dependency resolution with version constraints (>=, <=, ^, ==, *)
- [x] CLI: install, remove, upgrade, update, list, search, info, rollback, generations, gc, verify, files, which
- [x] Shared dynamic linking within a generation (fast security patches)
  - [x] Reverse dependency query (rdeps): find all packages depending on a library
  - [x] Library listing (libs): enumerate all installed .dso/.so shared libraries
  - [x] Library-aware upgrade (upgrade-lib): upgrade library, report affected dependents, single-generation atomic switch
  - [x] Shared library path detection (is_shared_lib_path) for .dso/.so files
- [x] File-level deduplication via hardlinks within the store (deploy_hardlink CAS→filesystem, DeployStats tracking, nlink-based dedup reporting, fallback to copy for cross-device)
- [x] Binary packages (preferred) with source build option (PKG1 binary archive format is the native distribution format; source builds not yet implemented)
- [x] Network repository fetching:
  - [x] HTTP/1.1 client library (net/httpclient): URL parser, request builder, chunked transfer, cookies, redirects, base64
  - [x] DNS resolver library (net/dns): RFC 1035, compression pointers, cache, A/AAAA/CNAME/MX/PTR, hosts file
  - [x] `fetch` coreutil (wget/curl-like CLI): URL parsing, redirect following, progress display
  - [x] Wire httpclient into package manager for repository index + package download (fetch_url + http_roundtrip + TcpStream, hash verification, CAS storage)
- [x] Repository model:
  - [x] Official curated repository (default "stable" repo at priority 100 in /etc/pkg.conf)
  - [x] Third-party repository support (pkg repo add/remove/enable/disable, priority-ordered fetching, per-repo cached indices)
  - [x] Direct .pkg installation from anywhere (PKG1 binary format with manifest + file blobs, parse_pkg_archive/create_pkg_archive, cmd_install_local for local file install, cmd_pack for creating archives, auto-detection of .pkg paths in install args)

### 4.3 Port Chromium
_This is the biggest single porting effort. Unlocks browser, web apps, and VS Code._
- [ ] Port Chromium (~35M lines C++) — requires functional POSIX layer, GPU, audio, networking
- [ ] System web app framework (Chromium as shared system component, not per-app Electron)
- [ ] Port VS Code (runs on Chromium + Node.js)
- [ ] Port Thunderbird (email client)

### 4.4 Development tools
- [ ] gcc, cmake, make, pkg-config (via POSIX layer)
- [ ] Rust toolchain (for kernel recompilation)
- [ ] CPython (latest, for ecosystem compatibility and fastpy bootstrapping)
- [ ] fastpy compiler (Python AOT compiler — first-class language for OS userspace components)
- [x] Custom Rust target for the OS — `toolchain/x86_64-slateos.json` defines a custom target spec (linux/musl ABI shape, code-model=large, panic=abort, +sse/+sse2, gnu-lld linker). All userspace tools (~280 binaries) build against this target via `-Zbuild-std=core,alloc,std,panic_abort` and the pre-built sysroot. The "yslateos" name in this roadmap entry was a working-name slip; the actual target is named `x86_64-slateos`. See CLAUDE.md "Build Environment Notes / Rust toolchains" section for usage.
- [x] Port Rust std library to native syscalls — std runs against the custom target above. The `posix` crate is built as a `staticlib` and installed at `toolchain/sysroot/lib/libc.a`, providing libc-shaped wrappers (open/read/write/mmap/clock_gettime/etc.) that translate Linux/musl-style calls into SlateOS native syscalls (SYS_FS_OPEN, SYS_TCP_CONNECT, SYS_CLOCK_REALTIME, etc.). `toolchain/stubs/` fills in the handful of symbols std references that posix doesn't yet implement; `libunwind.a` provides unwinding support. The full sysroot (libc.a + libstubs.a + libunwind.a) is built by `toolchain/build-sysroot.ps1` and every userspace crate links against it, so `std::fs`, `std::net`, `std::time`, `std::process`, etc. all transparently dispatch through the native SlateOS syscall ABI. This is the "port via libc-compatible shim" approach (the same way std is "ported" to musl on Linux) rather than a fork of std itself — equivalent and far less maintenance burden.

### 4.5 Remote desktop
- [ ] Port FreeRDP (working remote desktop early)
- [x] Native compositor-level streaming (efficient draw-command forwarding) — the multi-window **scene protocol** lives in the shared `guiremote` crate (`gui/remote/src/scene.rs`), layered on that crate's existing single-window `RenderCommand` wire codec (`encode_frame`/`decode_frame`, `ORDR` magic) rather than a compositor-local duplicate. `SCEN`-magic frames forward each window's vector `RenderCommand`s instead of pixels, so a remote viewer replays the scene through its own rasterizer (orders of magnitude smaller than a raster for typical flat-shaded desktops). `SceneFrame`/`SceneWindow` carry per-window geometry+opacity in bottom→top z-order plus removed-window ids; `encode_scene_frame`/`decode_scene_frame` embed an `ORDR` sub-frame per present window and round-trip every `RenderCommand` variant (bounds-checked decoder rejects truncation, bad magic, unsupported version, oversized/`TooManyWindows` counts). `SceneSession` does delta suppression via an FNV-1a fingerprint of each window's command blob — unchanged windows send geometry-only (`commands: None`), and `apply_scene_frame` reconstructs the full scene viewer-side by carrying forward prior commands for delta windows. The compositor depends on `guiremote`; `Compositor::capture_stream_frame` walks the z-stack and emits a `SceneFrame` from the live visible window set, exposed over IPC via `StreamStart`/`StreamCapture`/`StreamStop`. 7 scene unit tests (frame round-trip, malformed-input rejection, version/magic checks, delta suppression, content-change resend, removed-window reporting, apply carry-forward, reset) on top of guiremote's 19 codec tests, plus 2 compositor IPC/forwarding tests. NOTE: DMA-BUF/buffer-backed windows have no vector commands, so they stream as empty command lists — pixel forwarding for those is the video-encoded capture fallback's job (next item).
- [ ] Video-encoded capture fallback for fullscreen games/video
- [x] DynDNS setup helper in settings (remote.rs: 5 DynDNS providers, remote desktop config, firewall integration)

### 4.6 System snapshots
- [x] Package snapshots (manifest of active store paths — essentially free)
  - [x] Snapshot export: serialize current generation as portable text manifest (name, version, explicit/dep, manifest hash)
  - [x] Snapshot diff: compare current installed state against a saved snapshot (added/removed/changed)
  - [x] Snapshot apply: install/remove/upgrade packages to match a snapshot (with dry-run support)
  - [x] Parse/serialize round-trip format with version header and comment metadata
- [x] Mutable data snapshots (snapshots.rs: CoW block store, 64 KiB blocks, content-addressed dedup)
- [x] Snapshot tree (branch like VMs, select what to include — parent/child with ASCII visualization)
- [x] Rollback any OS update, permanently disable it or retry later (RollbackManager, pre-update snapshots)

### 4.7 Service discovery / RPC
- [x] D-Bus-like named service registry (binary protocol, not XML)
  - [x] Named service registration with typed interface descriptions
  - [x] TypeDesc system: 14 types (primitives, String, Bytes, Array, Map, Struct, Optional, Handle)
  - [x] Name ownership queue with transfer on disconnect
  - [x] Message routing: MethodCall, MethodReturn, Error, Signal
  - [x] Binary wire serialization with natural alignment
  - [x] Signal subscriptions with match rules (sender/interface/member filter)
  - [x] Service activation on first request (configurable timeout)
  - [x] Bus policy: allow/deny rules per sender/destination/interface
  - [x] Per-connection rate limiting (messages/sec)
  - [x] Connection lifecycle: Hello handshake, unique names (:1.N), disconnect cleanup
  - [x] Name watching: subscribe to acquired/lost notifications
  - [x] Introspection: query interfaces/methods a service exposes
- [x] Standard event loop integration API ("give me the waitable handle")
  - [x] EventLoop struct wrapping kernel completion ports (SYS_CP_CREATE/WAIT/TRY_WAIT)
  - [x] Register channels, timers, pipes, eventfds, process exits with user_data tags
  - [x] Blocking wait and non-blocking poll for multiplexed events
  - [x] Manual notification (wake waiter from another thread)
  - [x] Timer integration (one-shot and periodic kernel timers)
- [x] Client library (libservicebus) for easy integration
  - [x] Connection: connect to named service, send/recv messages, call+wait-for-reply
  - [x] ServiceHost: register a service, accept incoming connections
  - [x] Message: structured wire format (type/member/payload/serial) with serialization
  - [x] BusError: typed errors matching kernel error codes
  - [x] Blocking, non-blocking, and timeout variants for all operations
  - [x] Unit tests for message round-trip, error mapping, duration helpers

## Phase 5: Advanced Features and Ecosystem

_Depends on: Phase 4 (working daily-driver desktop). Goal: competitive OS._

### 5.1 Linux compatibility layer
- [-] Linux syscall translation layer (like FreeBSD's Linuxulator) — broad Linux syscall dispatch already in place (kernel/src/syscall/linux.rs); System V (Linux) initial-process-stack construction added (2026-06-12): new kernel/src/proc/linux_stack.rs builds the argc/argv[]/envp[]/auxv[] stack a Linux `_start` expects (16-byte-aligned %rsp at argc; AT_RANDOM/AT_PAGESZ=4096/AT_PHDR/AT_PHENT/AT_PHNUM/AT_ENTRY/AT_EXECFN/AT_CLKTCK/identity auxv), wired into the AbiMode::Linux branch of spawn_process + exec only (native setup_user_stack untouched, per design-decision #4). Exhaustive boot self_test on the byte layout + an end-to-end test (Linux-tagged ELF that reads argc from [rsp] and exit(argc), verified zombie exit code == argc). The built auxv is now persisted into Linux-ABI PCB state (pcb::linux_saved_auxv, cloned across fork, cleared on exec→native) at spawn/exec time and served back from prctl(PR_GET_AUXV) and /proc/<pid>/auxv (gen_pid_auxv); native processes correctly have no auxv (empty file / 16-byte AT_NULL terminator) per design-decision #4 (2026-06-12). Dynamic-linker (ld.so) load path added (2026-06-12): elf::ElfFile::interp_path() extracts the PT_INTERP path; elf::load_segments_with_bias() maps PT_LOAD at a runtime base; spawn::load_interpreter() reads the interpreter from the VFS, loads it at an ASLR-randomised base drawn from the LINUX_INTERP_BASE=0x0000_7000_0000_0000 window (28 bits of entropy in 16 KiB-page units via apply_aslr_base + rng::next_bounded; interpreter ASLR DONE 2026-06-14, design-decision #20), enters at base+interp.e_entry, and passes Some(base) to the SysV stack builder so ld.so receives AT_BASE (AT_ENTRY stays the executable's e_entry). The PIE main-executable load base is likewise ASLR-randomised from LINUX_PIE_BASE=0x0000_5555_5555_4000 under the same 28-bit policy via choose_exec_load_bias (computed once per spawn/exec, threaded through load_segments_with_bias + the biased entry + AT_ENTRY/AT_PHDR auxv), with a ≥1 TiB headroom invariant below the interpreter window asserted by test_pie_aslr_window — **known-issues.md TD9 fully RESOLVED 2026-06-14**. Defensive fallback (non-UTF-8 path / missing / unreadable / unparseable / unloadable interpreter → enter executable directly) keeps static + native binaries unaffected. Boot self-tests cover interp_path (dynamic/static/empty) and load_interpreter fallbacks (static-ELF + absent-interpreter Ok(None)); end-to-end interpreter EXECUTION deferred until a real glibc/musl ld.so is on disk. **File-backed `mmap` implemented (2026-06-13)** — the #1 blocker for running prebuilt Linux binaries: `ld.so`'s `_dl_map_segments` reserves a load span with a file-backed `MAP_PRIVATE` mmap then overlays each PT_LOAD segment with `MAP_FIXED`, which previously returned ENOSYS. New `linux_file_mmap` (kernel/src/syscall/linux.rs) serves regular-file + memfd maps with an **eager private-copy** model: each 16 KiB frame is `alloc_frame_zeroed`'d, the file bytes are `read_at`-copied in (tail past EOF stays zero, matching Linux page-tail zero-fill), the frame is mapped at prot-derived permissions, and a `VmaKind::Fixed` VMA is registered (so `/proc/<pid>/maps` reflects it and the fault resolver treats a fault there as a bug). `MAP_FIXED` correctly *replaces* an existing mapping via two new helpers — `unmap_user_range` (unmap + refcount-aware free of the old frames) and `pcb::remove_vma_range` (Linux `__split_vma`-style VMA surgery: drops fully-covered VMAs, truncates edge overlaps, splits strict supersets) — which is exactly what ld.so relies on for its segment overlays. Full rollback (unmap+free mapped frames, refund RLIMIT_AS) on any mid-map failure. Writable `MAP_SHARED` returns ENOSYS (no writeback — known-issues.md TD22); read-only `MAP_SHARED` is served as a private copy. VFS-dependent boot self-test `self_test_file_mmap` (throwaway process via pcb::create) verifies a 2-frame file map's content byte-by-byte through a page-table walk, the tail zero-fill, and the MAP_FIXED overlay + VMA split. **MAP_FIXED RLIMIT_AS net-accounting fix (2026-06-13):** the overlay path now charges only the *net* address-space delta — `linux_vma_overlap_bytes` sums the existing-VMA intersection of the target range and that prior charge is subtracted (or released when the new span is smaller), so ld.so reserving a span then overlaying each segment with MAP_FIXED no longer ~2x over-counts; the self-test asserts RLIMIT_AS == length_aligned after the map and unchanged after the single-frame overlay. **Ring-3 end-to-end test added (2026-06-13):** `proc::spawn::self_test_linux_file_mmap` spawns a real Linux-ABI process (hand-assembled `elf::build_linux_mmap_test_elf`) that itself issues `open(2)`+`mmap(2)`, reads a byte from the *second* 16 KiB frame of the mapping, and `exit`s with it — proving the whole syscall path (fd install via open's `require_cap_type(File,READ)` gate, `mmap` dispatch with a live `caller_pid`, ring-3 readability, multi-frame file content delivery) works, not just the kernel-context helper. **Real `brk`/`sbrk` heap implemented (2026-06-14)** — `sys_brk` (kernel/src/syscall/linux.rs) was a no-op stub that echoed the requested break while mapping nothing (a latent ring-3 SIGSEGV for any glibc program whose malloc used the brk fast path). Now a real per-process demand-paged heap: new `brk_start`/`brk_current` PCB fields (inherited across fork as a CoW heap, recomputed from the new image's page-aligned `elf::image_end` on exec for Linux images / cleared for native), a single `VmaKind::Brk` VMA labelled `[heap]` in /proc/maps that faults zero-filled like Anonymous, grow that charges RLIMIT_AS for the full added virtual span up-front (committed-by-default) and enforces RLIMIT_DATA, shrink that unmaps+frees faulted frames and refunds the charge, an image-dependent ceiling (`USER_MMAP_BASE` for low ET_EXEC, `LINUX_INTERP_BASE` for high PIE) plus a VMA-overlap guard, and Linux's return-the-unchanged-break-on-any-failure contract (so glibc's `__sbrk` falls back to mmap). Tests: pure `self_test_brk_logic` (brk_round_up boundary/overflow + brk_ceiling ET_EXEC/PIE) and ring-3 `proc::spawn::self_test_linux_brk` (real process queries break, grows 32 KiB, writes/reads the second heap frame, exits 0x6D). The heap floor is ASLR'd via `spawn::choose_brk_start` (Linux `arch_randomize_brk`, 13 bits of entropy / 128 MiB max gap at 16 KiB pages, matching Linux's position count per design-decisions #20/#21; covered by `test_brk_aslr_gap`). **`madvise(MADV_DONTNEED)` reclaim implemented (2026-06-14)** — `sys_madvise` previously accepted MADV_DONTNEED/MADV_FREE/MADV_DONTNEED_LOCKED but never freed anything (documented limitation pending VMA tracking), so long-running glibc/jemalloc/tcmalloc processes that `madvise(MADV_DONTNEED)` freed arenas grew RSS unbounded. Now that the brk/mmap VMA layer exists, those hints free the resident frames backing anonymous-class pages (Anonymous/Stack/Brk VMAs) in the range via `madvise_reclaim` (reuses `unmap_user_range`: refcount-aware free + per-page TLB invalidation; VMA + RLIMIT_AS reservation preserved so the mapping stays valid and a later access zero-fills via the fault resolver — exactly Linux's anonymous DONTNEED contract; only whole 16 KiB frames fully inside the 4 KiB-ABI request are dropped; file-backed/fixed maps keep the lenient no-op). Tested by boot self-test `self_test_madvise_dontneed` (faults 2 anon frames, stamps a sentinel, reclaims, asserts PTEs cleared + VMA persists + re-fault reads zero). A coverage audit confirmed **every defined Linux syscall number is dispatched** (the flat `dispatch_linux` match + the frame-aware `dispatch_linux_with_frame` for fork/vfork/clone); remaining `ENOSYS` returns are deliberate (io_uring/AIO/fanotify with proper validation gates). **Path Z END-TO-END ACHIEVED (2026-06-15):** a real prebuilt **dynamically-linked glibc** binary (`/bin/hello`) now runs the *complete* startup — ring-3 `ld.so` maps `libc.so.6`, applies relocations, sets up TLS, and `__libc_start_main → main → exit_group(42)` — driven from boot by `proc::spawn::self_test_linux_real_glibc` (verdict: `REAL glibc dynamic execution (ring 3: ld.so mapped libc.so.6, relocated, set up TLS, __libc_start_main → main → exit(42)): OK`; three BOOT_OK cycles). The real-glibc **output** path is proven too (2026-06-15): `proc::spawn::self_test_linux_real_glibc_stdio` runs a second prebuilt binary (`/bin/stdio`, `printf("…%d\n", 1234)`) with its fd 1 redirected from the console to a capture file (via new `pcb::linux_fd_install_at`), drives glibc's full-buffered stdio → exit-time `write(2)` flush, and asserts the captured 26 bytes match exactly — the gate for any glibc program that produces output. The real-glibc **argv/env/stdin/heap** paths are proven too (2026-06-15): `proc::spawn::self_test_linux_real_glibc_full` runs a third prebuilt binary (`/bin/full`) that sums `argv[]` lengths, reads `getenv("SLATE_TAG")`, `fgets()`-es a line from a redirected fd 0, and runs 64 rounds of mixed small (brk-arena) + large (>128 KiB, mmap-backed) `malloc`/`free` touching every page; with fd 0 fed a known input file and fd 1 redirected to a capture file, the test asserts the exact deterministic output line and `exit(11)` — proving the kernel-built argv vector, envp delivery, the glibc *input* path (`fstat(0)` buffering + `read(2)`), and the brk+mmap heap under genuine glibc allocator pressure. The final blocker was **16 KiB-frame vs. 4 KiB-ABI mismatch**: standard x86-64 glibc links with `max-page-size=0x1000`, so `ld.so` overlays adjacent library segments with *different* permissions (R-- rodata, RW- data) that share one 16 KiB physical frame and uses 4 KiB-aligned `MAP_FIXED`/`mprotect` (e.g. RELRO `mprotect(0x…203000, 0x4000, PROT_READ)`). Resolved by making the memory subsystem **4 KiB-sub-frame-granular** while keeping the 16 KiB frame as the allocation/RSS/rmap/reclaim unit: (1) per-subpage demand faulting — `pcb::resolve_subpaged_fault` resolves each 4 KiB subpage of a straddling frame with its own PTE permissions/file-backing via `map_4k_if_absent`, plus `change_flags_4k`/`is_hw_page_aligned` page-table primitives; (2) 4 KiB-granular anonymous `MAP_FIXED` (`linux_anon_mmap_fixed` + a `sys_mmap` fixed-dispatch path, fixing the bss zero-fill overlay); (3) 4 KiB-granular `mprotect` (`mprotect_validate_args`/`sys_mprotect` now gate + step on `HW_PAGE_SIZE` and flip a single PTE via `change_flags_4k`, fixing RELRO); (4) per-subpage ELF segment loading (two-pass `elf.rs` loader maps each 16 KiB frame with the union of its overlapping segments' permissions via `map_frame_subpages`, preserving W^X). **`mprotect` is now VMA-aware (2026-06-15, known-issues TD27 FIXED):** `sys_mprotect` calls `pcb::protect_vma_range`, which performs per-subpage VMA surgery (`vma_subrange` splits VMAs at 4 KiB boundaries and recomputes WRITABLE/NO_EXECUTE, adjusting FileBacked `file_offset`s) so the VMA flag set tracks the live permission — a RELRO page reclaimed under memory pressure and re-faulted now restores the *read-only* permission the `mprotect` established, not the old writable VMA permission. Coverage is validated Linux-style *before* any mutation: `vma_coverage_gaps` plus a present-PTE check accepts the eagerly-mapped (VMA-less but PTE-present) PIE/RELRO segments while still returning ENOMEM on a genuine hole. **Path Z Part 4 — real glibc pthread (clone3 + CLONE_SETTLS TLS + futex) ACHIEVED (2026-06-15):** `proc::spawn::self_test_linux_real_glibc_pthread` runs a fourth prebuilt binary (`/bin/pthread`) that spawns 4 worker threads via `pthread_create` (glibc `clone3` with `CLONE_VM|FS|FILES|SIGHAND|THREAD|SETTLS|PARENT_SETTID|CHILD_CLEARTID`, each thread's stack demand-paged through the VMA fault resolver after glibc's pre-touch `mprotect`), runs 40000 `pthread_mutex` ops across them (uncontended CAS fast path + contended `futex_wait`/`futex_wake`), and `pthread_join`s all four (each join blocks on the child-tid futex zeroed-and-woken by CLONE_CHILD_CLEARTID on thread exit) — asserting the deterministic `SLATE_GLIBC_PTHREAD_OK counter=40000 joinsum=10\n` output and `exit(13)`. The final blocker was the **futex-wait Linux-ABI return-value convention**: Slate's native futex handlers return `Ok(1)` for blocked-and-woken / `Ok(0)` for value-mismatch, but Linux `FUTEX_WAIT*` must return `0` on wake / `-EAGAIN` on mismatch / `-ETIMEDOUT` on timeout, and glibc calls `futex_fatal_error()` (aborting) on any other value. Fixed by `linux_from_futex_wait` (maps native `1→0`, `0→-EAGAIN`, negative errors via `linux_from_native`), applied to FUTEX_WAIT / FUTEX_WAIT_BITSET / futex2_wait / waitv. **Path Z Part 5 — real glibc signals (byte-exact Linux `rt_sigframe`) ACHIEVED (2026-06-15):** unmodified glibc binaries can now install `SA_SIGINFO` handlers and return from them. Signal delivery for `AbiMode::Linux` processes branches (in `handlers.rs::deliver_pending_signal` → new `deliver_linux_signal`) away from the native SEH-style `SignalContext` trampoline into `linux::build_linux_rt_frame`, which constructs a byte-exact Linux `struct rt_sigframe` (256B `sigcontext_64` + 304B `ucontext` + 128B `siginfo`, in `kernel/src/proc/linux_sigframe.rs`) on the user stack with Linux's `align_sigframe` rule (`sp = round_down(sp - size, 16) - 8`, so the ucontext is 16-aligned), enters the handler with `rdi=signo, rsi=&siginfo, rdx=&ucontext, rsp=&pretcode, rip=sa_handler`, and wires `pretcode = sa_restorer` so the handler's `ret` jumps to glibc's `__restore_rt` (`mov $15,%rax; syscall` → `rt_sigreturn`). `linux_rt_sigreturn` (rewritten) restores all GPRs/rip/rsp from the user ucontext's `uc_mcontext`, **sanitizes the attacker-controlled RFLAGS** (keeps only `SIGRETURN_RFLAGS_USER_MASK=0x0024_0DD5`, force-sets `SIGRETURN_RFLAGS_FORCED=0x202` = IF+reserved bit, dropping IOPL/NT/VM), and restores the saved signal mask. Per-signal Linux disposition (`linux_disposition` → Handler/Ignore/Default over the per-process `LinuxSigaction` table) honours `SA_NODEFER`/`SA_RESETHAND`/`sa_mask` blocking semantics; Default falls through to terminate/stop/ignore/continue. Proven in ring 3 by `proc::spawn::self_test_linux_real_glibc_signal` (a fifth prebuilt binary `/bin/signal` installs an `SA_SIGINFO` SIGUSR1 handler, `raise()`s it, reads the delivered `siginfo`, resumes via `rt_sigreturn`, asserts `si_code == SI_TKILL` and `si_pid == getpid()`, prints `SLATE_GLIBC_SIGNAL_OK signo=10 code=-6 self=1` and `exit(17)` — captured bytes asserted exactly). **Sender-faithful `siginfo` (2026-06-15, known-issues TD29 RESOLVED):** `SignalState` (`kernel/src/proc/signal.rs`) now carries a per-signal `Option<SigInfo>` array co-located under the pending-bitmap lock, recorded on the clear→set transition (Linux standard-signal first-wins coalescing) and taken at delivery, so the `siginfo` handed to an `SA_SIGINFO` handler reports the correct sender class — `kill(2)`→`SI_USER`+sender pid/uid, `tkill`/`tgkill` (`raise`/`pthread_kill`)→`SI_TKILL`+sender pid, timer expiry (SIGALRM)→`SI_KERNEL`. Threaded through the post funnel (`kill_common`/`sys_signal_send_with_code`→`classify_post_info`→`set_pending_info`) and consumed by `build_linux_rt_frame`; covered by the `siginfo record/deliver/coalesce` unit self-test (13 signal tests). **Path Z Part 5b — synchronous fault → Linux signal with faithful `si_addr`/`si_code` (2026-06-16):** a CPU fault taken by an `AbiMode::Linux` process with an installed handler is now delivered as a real Linux signal carrying a fault-specific `siginfo`. The delicate `rt_sigframe`-building logic is extracted into a shared emitter `emit_linux_rt_frame(pid, sig, act, regs: &LinuxTrapRegs, siginfo) -> Option<RtFrameEntry>` (`kernel/src/syscall/linux.rs`) that takes a neutral register snapshot, so it is reused by both the async syscall-return path (`build_linux_rt_frame`, snapshot from the `SyscallFrame`) and the synchronous fault path (`try_deliver_linux_fault_signal`, `kernel/src/idt.rs`, snapshot read out of the `InterruptStackFrame` + `SavedRegisters` via `read_volatile` raw-pointer discipline — never forming an `&mut` from the ISR frame). `linux_fault_mapping` classifies the trap vector → `(signo, si_code)` (`#DE`→`SIGFPE`/`FPE_INTDIV`, `#OF`→`SIGFPE`/`FPE_INTOVF`, `#UD`→`SIGILL`/`ILL_ILLOPN`, `#MF`/`#XM`→`SIGFPE`/`FPE_FLTINV`, `#AC`→`SIGBUS`/`BUS_ADRALN`, `#BR`/`#NP`/`#SS`/`#GP`→`SIGSEGV`/`SI_KERNEL`; `si_addr` = faulting RIP for these). `#PF` is handled in `handle_page_fault`, which sets `si_addr = CR2` and `si_code = SEGV_ACCERR` (present bit set → protection) or `SEGV_MAPERR` (not mapped). The emitter does **not** re-arm on a frame-build failure — the fault caller terminates instead (resuming would immediately re-fault). Native processes keep the SEH-style `SignalContext` trampoline (design-decision #4). Proven in ring 3 by `proc::spawn::self_test_linux_real_glibc_fault` (a sixth prebuilt binary `/bin/fault` stores to an unmapped `0xDEAD000`, taking a real `#PF` that enters an unmodified glibc `SA_SIGINFO` SIGSEGV handler reading `si_signo==11`/`si_code==SEGV_MAPERR(1)`/`si_addr==0xdead000` and `siglongjmp`ing out, printing `SLATE_GLIBC_FAULT_OK signo=11 code=1 addr=0xdead000` and `exit(19)` — captured 52 bytes asserted exactly, boot test PASSED). **Path Z Part 5c — `SI_QUEUE` `si_value` payload (2026-06-16):** `rt_sigqueueinfo(2)`, `rt_tgsigqueueinfo(2)` and `pidfd_send_signal(2)` now read the user-supplied `siginfo` (`read_user_siginfo_payload`, SMAP-safe `copy_from_user`), carry `si_code` + the 8-byte `si_value` union onto the pending signal, and stamp them into the delivered `siginfo_t` at the ABI offset (struct +24) via the new `LinuxSiginfo::queue(...)` builder (`build_linux_rt_frame` branches to it when `si_code == SI_QUEUE`). The kill funnel was refactored into shared `kill_common_value` / `tgkill_common_value` / `sys_signal_send_with_info(args, si_code, value)` cores so all gate ordering (EFAULT → forging-EPERM → ESRCH-before-EINVAL → authority) is reused and only the final post stamps the payload; Linux's `do_rt_sigqueueinfo` forging gate (`(si_code >= 0 || si_code == SI_TKILL) && caller != target → EPERM`) is enforced on all three queued-signal entry points, with the recorded `si_pid`/`si_uid` always the *real caller* (unforgeable). Proven in ring 3 by `proc::spawn::self_test_linux_real_glibc_sigqueue` (a seventh prebuilt binary `/bin/sigqueue` `sigqueue(getpid(), SIGUSR1, {.sival_int=0x12345678})`s itself; the `SA_SIGINFO` handler reads `si_code==SI_QUEUE(-1)`, `si_value.sival_int==0x12345678`, `si_pid==getpid()`, printing `SLATE_GLIBC_SIGQUEUE_OK signo=10 code=-1 value=0x12345678 self=1` and `exit(23)` — captured 65 bytes asserted exactly, boot test PASSED) plus in-kernel forging-gate (EPERM) and SI_QUEUE-bypass (ESRCH-before-EINVAL) assertions. **Path Z Part 6 — real glibc `fork()`+`execl()`+`waitpid()` of a real glibc child ACHIEVED (2026-06-16):** an unmodified glibc binary can now `fork()` (glibc's `arch_fork` issues `clone(SIGCHLD|CLONE_CHILD_SETTID|CLONE_CHILD_CLEARTID, stack=0, ptid=0, ctid=&THREAD_SELF->tid, tls=0)`), have the child `execl()` a *different* real glibc binary (re-running `ld.so`/`libc.so.6` startup in the CoW child image), and reap it via `waitpid()`→`wait4`. The blocker was the Linux `clone()` fork-equivalent path (`linux_clone_inner`, `kernel/src/syscall/linux.rs`) rejecting glibc's fork with `-ENOSYS` because its reject mask lumped the TID-notification bits (`CLONE_CHILD_SETTID`/`CLONE_CHILD_CLEARTID`/`CLONE_PARENT_SETTID`) in with the genuinely-unsupported partial-resource-share bits. Fixed by narrowing the fork-path reject mask to `FORK_REJECTED_SHARE_BITS` (CLONE_VM/FS/FILES/SIGHAND/THREAD/SYSVSEM/SETTLS only) and **honouring the TID-notification bits across a CoW fork**: `fork::ForkCloneTid` threads the bits into `fork::fork_process_clone`, which writes `CLONE_PARENT_SETTID` (child's task-id → parent's `ptid`, in the parent's still-active address space), registers `CLONE_CHILD_CLEARTID` (`register_clear_child_tid(child_task_id, ctid)` so the child-tid futex is zeroed-and-woken on the child's exit — glibc's own `fork()` relies on this internally), and defers `CLONE_CHILD_SETTID` to a child-context write inside `fork_child_trampoline` (the new `ForkChildImage` carries the `settid_ptr`) — the write *must* run in the child's CoW address space, since doing it from the parent would trip copy-on-write and the value would never reach the child. The forked child's `execve` keeps the same task-id, so glibc startup's `set_tid_address(&new_tcb.tid)` re-registers the clear-child-tid slot at a valid address in the new image (no execve-clear needed). Proven in ring 3 by `proc::spawn::self_test_linux_real_glibc_forkexec` (an eighth prebuilt binary `/bin/forkexec` `fork()`s, the child `execl("/bin/hello")` — the silent real-glibc binary that exits 42 — and the parent `waitpid()`s and prints `SLATE_GLIBC_FORKEXEC_OK childexit=42` returning 27; captured 37 bytes asserted exactly, boot test PASSED). This is the foundation for a real shell. **Path Z Part 7 — real glibc `pipe()`+`fork()`+`dup2()`+`execl()`+`read()`-to-EOF+`waitpid()` (the `cmd1 | cmd2` shell primitive) ACHIEVED (2026-06-16):** two new prebuilt glibc binaries — `/bin/emit` (writes `"SLATE_PIPE_BODY\n"` to fd 1) and `/bin/pipe` (`pipe(2)`→`fork(2)`; the child `dup2`s the write end onto fd 1, closes the raw ends, and `execl`s `/bin/emit`; the parent closes the write end, `read`s the pipe to EOF, `waitpid`s the child, and `printf`s what it read) — prove the full pipeline plumbing a shell builds: (a) pipe-fd inheritance across the CoW fork, (b) `dup2` redirection, (c) open fds surviving `execve` into a fresh glibc image, and (d) pipe EOF arriving once every write end (parent's + the exec'd child's) is closed. **Two latent kernel correctness bugs were found and fixed in the process: (1) fd-bearing resources were closed at *reap* (`destroy`) instead of at *exit* (zombie), causing a pipe deadlock** — a parent blocked in `read()` waiting for EOF could never get it, because EOF requires the child's inherited pipe write end to close, but that close only happened when the parent reaped the child, and the parent couldn't reach `waitpid()` until EOF (classic deadlock). Fixed by `pcb::exit_close_fds(pid)`, called from `thread::on_thread_exit` at the zombie transition, which closes every `ipc_handle` + unclaimed initial fd the moment the process exits — matching Linux's `exit_files()` in `do_exit` (a process's open file descriptions close when it *exits*, not when its parent reaps it). `destroy_process_resources` still runs the same teardown for the force-kill / never-zombied path (the slices are empty by then on the normal path), so no double-close and no leak. **(2) `on_thread_exit_hook` dereferenced user pointers (PI-futex owner walk, robust-list, `clear_child_tid`) unconditionally, panicking with a page fault when the cleanup ran cross-address-space** — e.g. a boot self-test reaping a glibc process from task 0's (boot) address space. Fixed with an AS-active guard: the user-memory operations now run only when the active CR3 equals the dying task's process PML4 (`page_table::active_pml4_phys() == pcb::get_pml4(owner_process(task_id))`); the in-kernel map removals (`ROBUST_LIST`/`RSEQ`/`CLEAR_CHILD_TID`) always run. (See known-issues.md F16, F17.) Proven in ring 3 by `proc::spawn::self_test_linux_real_glibc_pipe` (captured 46 bytes `SLATE_GLIBC_PIPE_OK n=16 body=SLATE_PIPE_BODY\n` == expected, `exit(29)`, boot test PASSED). **Path Z Part 8 — real glibc program-driven `cmd > file` output redirection ACHIEVED (2026-06-16):** a ninth prebuilt glibc binary (`/bin/redir`) performs its *own* shell-style output redirection entirely from ring 3 — `open("/redir-out.txt", O_WRONLY|O_CREAT|O_TRUNC, 0644)`, `dup2(fd, 1)` (redirecting stdout onto the just-opened file), `close(fd)`, then `printf("SLATE_GLIBC_REDIR_OK marker=%d\n", 4242)` whose glibc full-buffered stdio flushes to the program's own file at exit. This proves the redirection direction a shell builds for `> file` (vs Part 7's `dup2` onto a *pipe*): (a) ring-3 `open(2)` with `O_CREAT|O_TRUNC` creating a fresh file through `translate_open_flags`→VFS, (b) `dup2(2)` of a self-`open()`ed **File** handle onto fd 1 — exercising the displaced-console-fd close path (the original fd-1 console handle's refcount is correctly dropped when overwritten via `sys_dup2_impl`→`close_handle`→`sys_fs_close`→`deregister_ipc_handle`), and (c) glibc's exit-time stdio flush landing in the redirected file. `proc::spawn::self_test_linux_real_glibc_redir` spawns `/bin/redir` with **no fd injection** (the program opens its own file), polls for the zombie, reads `/redir-out.txt` back via `Vfs::read_file`, and asserts `exit(31)` and the captured 33 bytes (`SLATE_GLIBC_REDIR_OK marker=4242\n`) match exactly (boot test PASSED). **Path Z Part 9 — real glibc program-driven `cmd < file` input redirection ACHIEVED (2026-06-16):** the mirror image of Part 8 — a tenth prebuilt glibc binary (`/bin/redirin`) performs its *own* shell-style *input* redirection from ring 3 — `open("/redir-in.txt", O_RDONLY)`, `dup2(fd, 0)` (redirecting stdin from the just-opened file), `close(fd)`, then `fgets(buf, …, stdin)` reading a line through glibc's buffered input path. This proves the redirection direction a shell builds for `< file`: (a) ring-3 `open(2)` with `O_RDONLY` resolving an existing file through the VFS gated on `File READ`, (b) `dup2(2)` of a self-`open()`ed read-only **File** handle onto fd 0 — exercising the displaced-console-stdin close path, and (c) glibc's *input* path (`fstat(0)` to size the buffer + `read(2)` + `fgets`) reading from a regular file rather than the console. `proc::spawn::self_test_linux_real_glibc_redirin` pre-creates `/redir-in.txt` with a known 33-byte line, spawns `/bin/redirin` with **no fd injection** and only a `File READ` cap (exactly the authority an `O_RDONLY` open needs), polls for the zombie, and asserts `exit(37)` — the program returns 37 *only* if the line it read via the redirected stdin byte-exactly matches its compiled-in literal (`strcmp`), so a correct exit code is a byte-exact proof the right bytes flowed in (2=open failed, 3=dup2 failed, 4=fgets EOF, 5=content mismatch). Boot test PASSED (`glibc fgets read 33 bytes from the program's own file == expected, exit 37`). **Path Z Part 10 — a real unmodified prebuilt POSIX shell (`dash`) runs ACHIEVED (2026-06-16):** the culmination of Parts 6–9 — instead of a bespoke test binary issuing the syscalls directly, an *unmodified* `/bin/dash` (stock Ubuntu glibc-dynamic shell, staged onto the rootfs; links only against the already-present `libc.so.6` + `ld-linux` + kernel `linux-vdso`) interprets a command and drives the shell primitives itself. `proc::spawn::self_test_linux_real_glibc_shell_redir` spawns `dash -c 'echo SLATE_DASH_REDIR_OK marker=4242 > /dash-out.txt'` with **no fd injection** (only a `File READ|WRITE` cap), polls for the zombie, reads `/dash-out.txt` back via `Vfs::read_file`, and asserts `exit(0)` and the exact 32 bytes (`SLATE_DASH_REDIR_OK marker=4242\n`). This proves the full real-shell stack: ld.so loads dash + libc and runs dash's startup, dash's lexer/parser handles the command line + the `>` redirection token, dash `open(2)`s the target and `dup2`s it over fd 1 (saving/restoring fd 1 around the builtin via `dup`/`dup2`/`close`), runs its `echo` builtin, flushes, and exits 0. `echo` is a dash *builtin*, so this first shell test isolates "the real shell runs + parses a command + does its own redirection" from external `fork`/`exec` (already proven by Parts 6/7); the next escalation is `dash -c '/bin/emit > file'` (the shell forking + exec'ing a real external glibc binary). Boot test PASSED. **Path Z Part 11 — a real `dash` shell forks + exec's an external glibc binary with redirection ACHIEVED (2026-06-16):** the full shell-orchestration proof. Part 10's command (`echo`) was a dash *builtin* (no fork); here `proc::spawn::self_test_linux_real_glibc_shell_exec` spawns `dash -c '/bin/emit > /dash-exec-out.txt'`, so dash must drive the complete external-command pipeline itself: parse `cmd > file`, `fork(2)`, the child `open(2)`s the redirect target + `dup2`s it over fd 1 then `execve(2)`s the *external* real-glibc `/bin/emit` (which `write(2)`s its 16-byte payload to fd 1 — now the file — and exits 0), and the parent dash `wait4(2)`s the child and exits with its status. With **no fd injection** (only a `File READ|WRITE` cap), the test reads `/dash-exec-out.txt` back and asserts `exit(0)` and the exact 16 bytes (`SLATE_PIPE_BODY\n`). Every piece (CoW fork, child-side redirect, exec into a fresh glibc image, reap) was proven individually in Parts 6–9; here a real unmodified shell orchestrates all of them. This is the foundation for an interactive shell session. Boot test PASSED (`read back 16 bytes == expected, exit 0`). **Path Z Part 12 — a real `dash` shell runs a two-stage *pipeline* `cmd1 | cmd2 > file` ACHIEVED (2026-06-16):** the multi-process pipeline proof. `proc::spawn::self_test_linux_real_glibc_shell_pipe` spawns `dash -c '/bin/emit | /bin/countbytes > /dash-pipe-out.txt'`, so dash must build the whole pipeline itself: `pipe(2)`, `fork(2)` the upstream `/bin/emit` (writes its 16-byte payload to the pipe via the inherited write end), `fork(2)` the downstream `/bin/countbytes` (an eleventh new prebuilt glibc binary that `read(2)`s stdin to EOF and `printf`s `n=<count>\n`) with stdin `dup2`'d from the pipe read end and stdout `dup2`'d onto the redirect file, close all raw pipe ends in the parent, and `wait4(2)` both children. With **no fd injection** (only a `File READ|WRITE` cap), the test reads `/dash-pipe-out.txt` back and asserts `exit(0)` and the exact 5 bytes `n=16\n`. **A latent kernel CoW correctness bug was found and fixed (known-issues.md F18):** a per-16 KiB-frame refcount vs per-4 KiB-PTE CoW-resolution granularity mismatch double-freed a still-shared frame, crashing the *parent* dash with a #GP at glibc `wait4`'s errno store (`mov %eax,%fs:(%rdx)`) — but only on the `wait4` error path, which is why the single-fork Part 11 never hit it. The ELF loader packs a read-only segment tail and a writable segment head into one 16 KiB frame; a forked child resolving the writable CoW sub-PTE decremented the frame's refcount once *while still mapping it via the read-only sub-PTE*, then double-decremented it at exec teardown (which freed per group keyed on only the base PTE), driving a parent-shared frame to refcount 0 → reuse → `.got` errno-slot corruption → garbage `%rdx` → #GP. Fixed by making CoW refcounting consistent across `cow::resolve_cow_fault`, `cow::clone_frame_group`, and `page_table::clear_user_address_space` on one invariant — *each address space holds exactly one refcount on each **distinct** 16 KiB frame its group's sub-PTEs reference*: resolve drops the old frame's reference only when no sub-PTE of the group still points into it; clone increments once per distinct frame among present siblings; teardown inspects all four sub-PTEs and frees each distinct frame once. Boot test PASSED (`read back 5 bytes [110, 61, 49, 54, 10] == expected, exit 0`). **Path Z Part 13 — a real `dash` shell runs a `for` LOOP that fork+exec's an external glibc binary every iteration ACHIEVED (2026-06-16):** the shell *iteration* proof and a direct F18 regression guard. `proc::spawn::self_test_linux_real_glibc_shell_loop` spawns `dash -c 'for i in a b c; do /bin/emit; done > /dash-loop-out.txt'`, so dash parses a `for` compound command, opens the redirect target *once*, then on each of three iterations forks a CoW clone of itself, exec's `/bin/emit` into the child (tearing down the CoW image), and `wait4`s it before the next iteration — running the fork→exec→reap cycle three times back-to-back in one long-lived parent. This is exactly the path that surfaced the F18 CoW-refcount double-free, so a regression would corrupt the shell's image and crash it mid-loop (short/garbled output or non-zero exit). With only a `File READ|WRITE` cap (no fd injection), the test reads `/dash-loop-out.txt` back and asserts `exit(0)` and the exact 48 bytes = three concatenated copies of `/bin/emit`'s 16-byte `SLATE_PIPE_BODY\n` payload. Boot test PASSED. **Path Z Part 14 — a real `dash` shell reads and runs a multi-command SCRIPT from stdin (no `-c`) ACHIEVED (2026-06-16):** Parts 10–13 drove dash via `-c '<one line>'` (a single command string parsed once); this spawns `/bin/dash` with **no arguments** and fd 0 redirected from a script file, so dash detects a non-interactive stdin and runs its *main read-eval loop* — read a line from fd 0, parse, execute, repeat until EOF, then exit 0. `proc::spawn::self_test_linux_real_glibc_shell_script_stdin` injects fd 0 (a 48-byte script `"/bin/emit\n/bin/emit\necho SLATE_DASH_SCRIPT_DONE\n"`, opened read-only) and fd 1 (a capture file) via `pcb::linux_fd_install_at`, with only a `File READ|WRITE` cap, and asserts `exit(0)` and the exact 55 bytes `SLATE_PIPE_BODY\nSLATE_PIPE_BODY\nSLATE_DASH_SCRIPT_DONE\n` — proving dash's top-level driver loop (vs. the one-shot `-c` string), two sequential external `fork`+`exec`+`wait4` commands inheriting the advanced script-fd offset harmlessly, a builtin, and EOF-driven clean termination. Boot test PASSED (`captured 55 bytes == expected, EOF→exit 0`). **Path Z Part 15 — a real `dash` shell performs filesystem GLOBBING (`echo /globdir/*`) end-to-end ACHIEVED (2026-06-16):** `proc::spawn::self_test_linux_real_glibc_shell_glob` creates `/globdir/{a,b,c}.txt`, spawns `dash -c 'echo /globdir/* > /glob-out.txt'`, and asserts `exit(0)` and the exact 45 bytes `/globdir/a.txt /globdir/b.txt /globdir/c.txt\n` — proving dash's pathname-expansion path: `open("/globdir/", O_RDONLY|O_NONBLOCK|O_CLOEXEC|O_DIRECTORY)` → `fstat`/`statx` (st_blksize sizes the dirent buffer) → `getdents64` → match each entry against `*` → sort → `echo` the joined matches (POSIX no-match leaves the pattern literal, so a correct 45-byte result is a byte-exact proof the directory read worked). **A latent kernel correctness bug was found and fixed (known-issues.md B-DP1):** `mm::user::validate_user_range` rejected committed-but-not-yet-faulted-in **demand-paged** user buffers — it returned `InvalidAddress` for any page `translate()` reported not-present, so glibc's freshly-allocated 32 KiB `getdents64` dirent buffer (only its first page faulted in) failed `validate_user_write`, `readdir` returned NULL, and dash's glob matched nothing (emitting the literal `/globdir/*`). Fixed by faulting committed demand-paged pages in *during* validation via the new `try_fault_in_user_page` → `pcb::try_resolve_fault` (mirrors Linux's `get_user_pages()`); a genuinely unmapped/permission-violating address still fails. Also `fstat`/`statx` on a directory fd now report `S_IFDIR | 0o755` with a 16 KiB `st_blksize` (was `S_IFREG`). Boot test PASSED (`read back 45 bytes == expected, exit 0`). Path Z Part 16 — real dash command substitution (2026-06-16): `dash -c 'echo [$(/bin/emit)] > /cmdsub-out.txt'` now runs end-to-end in ring 3. dash creates a pipe, forks a subshell whose stdout is redirected to the pipe write end, execs `/bin/emit` (a prebuilt glibc binary that writes `SLATE_PIPE_BODY
` to fd 1), then dash itself reads the pipe to EOF, strips the trailing newline, and splices the captured text into the `echo` command line. Exercises pipe2 + dup2 + fork-with-shared-pipe + waitpid reaping of the substituted child + dash read-to-EOF on the pipe read end. Self-test `self_test_linux_real_glibc_shell_cmdsub` (kernel/src/proc/spawn.rs) stages ld.so/libc/dash/emit into rootfs.ext4, runs with File READ|WRITE caps, and verifies `/cmdsub-out.txt` == `[SLATE_PIPE_BODY]
` (18 bytes) with exit 0. Boot test PASSED (`read back 18 bytes == expected, exit 0`). Path Z Part 17 — real dash conditional / variable expansion / `[` test builtin (2026-06-16): `dash -c 'x=hello; if [ "$x" = hello ]; then echo EQ; else echo NE; fi > /cond-out.txt'` now runs end-to-end in ring 3. Exercises dash variable assignment, `$x` parameter expansion, the `[`/`test` builtin string comparison, `if`/`then`/`else`/`fi` compound-command evaluation driven by the test exit status, and a redirection applied to the whole compound command — all internal to dash, stressing its parser + word-expansion machinery on our Linux ABI rather than fork/exec. Self-test `self_test_linux_real_glibc_shell_cond` (kernel/src/proc/spawn.rs) stages ld.so/libc/dash, runs with File READ|WRITE caps, and verifies `/cond-out.txt` == `EQ
` (3 bytes) with exit 0. Boot test PASSED (`read back 3 bytes == expected, exit 0`). Path Z Part 18 — real dash arithmetic expansion `$(( ))` (2026-06-16): `dash -c 'x=3; y=4; echo $((x * y + 2)) > /arith-out.txt'` now runs end-to-end in ring 3. Exercises dash arithmetic evaluator: variable lookup inside the arithmetic context (no `$` needed there), `*` binding tighter than `+` per C precedence, and substitution of the decimal result into the echo word list — a distinct code path from parameter expansion and the test builtin, purely internal to dash. Self-test `self_test_linux_real_glibc_shell_arith` (kernel/src/proc/spawn.rs) stages ld.so/libc/dash, runs with File READ|WRITE caps, and verifies `/arith-out.txt` == `14
` (3 bytes) with exit 0. Boot test PASSED (`read back 3 bytes (==14) == expected, exit 0`). Path Z Part 19 — real dash here-document `<<EOF` (2026-06-16): `dash -c 'read a <<EOF
HELLO
EOF
echo "$a" > /hd-out.txt'` now runs end-to-end in ring 3. dash materialises the heredoc body, plumbs it onto fd 0 via a pipe (forks a writer that pushes the body and dups the read end to stdin), the `read` builtin consumes one line into `$a`, and `echo` writes it back. Unlike the cond/arith parts this is NOT purely internal — it drives the kernel pipe create + blocking read/write + fd dup path entirely from the shell. Self-test `self_test_linux_real_glibc_shell_heredoc` (kernel/src/proc/spawn.rs) stages ld.so/libc/dash, runs with File READ|WRITE caps, and verifies `/hd-out.txt` == `HELLO
` (6 bytes) with exit 0. Passed first try — heredoc pipe plumbing already correct. Boot test PASSED (`read back 6 bytes == expected, exit 0`).  Path Z Part 20 — real dash background job + `wait` builtin (2026-06-16): `dash -c '/bin/emit > /bg-out.txt & wait'` now runs end-to-end in ring 3. dash forks /bin/emit as an asynchronous job (redirecting its stdout to the file), returns to the prompt, then the `wait` builtin blocks until the child is reaped. This exercised the real dash job-control path: dash arms a SIGCHLD handler, calls `waitpid(WNOHANG)`, and `rt_sigsuspend`s until SIGCHLD wakes it (the synchronous pipe/loop/cmdsub parts use blocking waitpid and never needed SIGCHLD). Two kernel gaps were fixed to make this work, both proper fixes: (1) SIGCHLD is now posted to the parent process when a child becomes a zombie (`proc/thread.rs` `on_thread_exit`) — via the Linux-ABI disposition path for Linux parents (`set_pending_info`, delivered through `deliver_linux_signal`→`linux_disposition`) and `classify_post` for native parents; and (2) `sys_rt_sigsuspend` is no longer a stub returning EINTR immediately (which livelocked dash into a busy-spin that starved the boot thread) but a real park loop modeled on `sys_pause`: it installs the temporary mask, blocks on the signalfd wait-queue until a signal deliverable under that mask arrives, and restores the original mask correctly via a Linux saved_sigmask/TIF_RESTORE_SIGMASK mechanism (`emit_linux_rt_frame` writes the saved pre-suspend mask into `uc_sigmask` so `rt_sigreturn` restores it; the no-handler tail of `deliver_linux_signal` restores it directly). Self-test reads back 16 bytes == expected, exit 0. Path Z Part 21 — real dash pipeline with shell-builtin downstream stage (2026-06-16): `dash -c '/bin/emit | while read l; do echo "<$l>"; done > /pipe2-out.txt'` now runs end-to-end in ring 3. This is distinct from the Part-N `/bin/emit | /bin/countbytes` pipe test: here the downstream stage of the pipeline is a dash shell builtin (`while read` loop) rather than an execve'd external binary, so dash keeps the read end of the kernel pipe in its own process and drives the loop in-shell — exercising the pipe()/dup2 plumbing where the consumer is the shell itself, line-buffered `read` of piped bytes, variable expansion in the loop body, and stdout redirection of the whole compound command to a file. Passed first try — no kernel changes needed (the Part 20 SIGCHLD/rt_sigsuspend fixes plus the existing pipe/read/dup2 paths already covered it). Self-test reads back 18 bytes (`<SLATE_PIPE_BODY>\n`) == expected, exit 0. Path Z Part 22 — real dash changes working directory and reads it back (2026-06-16): `dash -c 'cd /cwdtest && pwd -P > /cwd-out.txt'` now runs end-to-end in ring 3. This is the first Path Z test to change the working directory at all, so it is the first end-to-end exercise of the per-process cwd stored in the PCB: dash's `chdir("/cwdtest")` updates it and `pwd -P` (the physical flag, which forces a real `getcwd()` syscall rather than printing the logical `$PWD` dash tracks internally) reads the exact same canonical path back. This validates the chdir/getcwd round-trip and the getcwd ABI buffer-sizing / NUL-termination contract that glibc's getcwd wrapper depends on. Passed first try — no kernel changes needed. Self-test reads back 9 bytes (`/cwdtest\n`) == expected, exit 0. Path Z Part 23 — real dash relative-path open after cd (cwd resolution fix) (2026-06-16): `dash -c 'cd /reltest && echo RELOK > relfile.txt'` now correctly creates `/reltest/relfile.txt` (cwd-relative), not `/relfile.txt` (root). This both exercises and regression-tests a REAL bug fix (B-CWD1): the Linux ABI's relative path resolution previously ignored the per-process cwd — `open_common` forwarded the raw userspace path to the VFS and `resolve_at_path` returned `AT_FDCWD` paths verbatim, and `Vfs::normalize_path` treats `rel` identically to `/rel`, so a relative `open`/`*at` after `chdir` resolved against the filesystem root instead of the working directory — breaking standard Unix semantics for any program using relative paths after cd. The fix resolves relative paths against `pcb::get_cwd(caller)` at the Linux ABI boundary using the existing `canonicalize_path` helper: `open_common` canonicalises then opens via a new kernel-string `handlers::fs_open_kernel_path`, and `resolve_at_path` canonicalises its AT_FDCWD/absolute result. Kernel context and the native ABI are unchanged (cwd falls back to `/`). Self-test asserts the file landed cwd-relative and NOT at root, reads back 6 bytes == expected, exit 0. Path Z Part 24 — path-based stat now does real VFS lookups (stat-stub fix) (2026-06-16): the Linux-ABI stat/lstat/newfstatat/statx syscalls all unconditionally returned ENOENT for path lookups (stale no-file skeleton-FS assumption), so any program that stat'd a path before opening it — e.g. dash's `[ -f FILE ]` test predicate, `ls`, configure probes — saw every file as missing even though the VFS now holds real files. Fix: stat_path_common (shared by stat follow / lstat no-follow) and the non-empty-path branches of newfstatat/statx now canonicalise the path against the caller's cwd and call Vfs::metadata (follow) / Vfs::lmetadata (no-follow) via the new stat_meta_for_path + fill_stat_from_meta / fill_statx_from_meta helpers, which map EntryType→S_IF* bits (default perms 0o755/0o777/0o644 when the FS reports none) and backfill 0 timestamps with the current realtime clock. Statbuf pointer gates are deferred until after a successful lookup, matching Linux's getname/filename_lookup-before-cp_new_stat ordering. Kernel context (caller_pid().is_none()) still returns ENOENT, preserving the batch-488 syscall-fidelity self-tests. Self-test: `dash -c '[ -f /bin/dash ] && echo HASFILE > /stat-out.txt'` — the redirect only fires if the path stat reports a regular file; asserts exit 0 and 8 bytes == expected. Path Z Part 25 — directory stat mode bits (`[ -d ]`/`[ ! -f ]`/`[ -e ]`) (2026-06-16): complements Part 24's regular-file stat by exercising the *directory* metadata path of the stat-stub fix. fill_stat_from_meta must report S_IFDIR for a directory so dash's `[ -d ]` is true and `[ -f ]` is false, and the VFS lookup must succeed so `[ -e ]` is true. Self-test: `dash -c 'if [ -d /bin ] && [ ! -f /bin ] && [ -e /bin ]; then echo DIROK > /dirstat-out.txt; fi'` — the redirect fires only when all three predicates hold; asserts exit 0 and 6 bytes == expected. Passed first run with no kernel change (the Part 24 stat fix already handles directory EntryType correctly), confirming the fix covers both file and directory metadata. Path Z Part 26 — append redirect `>>` honours O_APPEND (2026-06-16): first self-test of the append write path (distinct from the truncating `>` of Part 10). Self-test: `dash -c 'echo first > /append-out.txt; echo second >> /append-out.txt'` — the `>>` open carries O_WRONLY|O_CREAT|O_APPEND and the kernel must position the second write at EOF; asserts the file is exactly `first\nsecond\n` (13 bytes), exit 0. Passed first run with no kernel change — O_APPEND is already translated and the write path positions appends at end-of-file correctly. Path Z Part 27 — symlink()/readlink() syscalls now do real VFS work (symlink/readlink stub fix) (2026-06-16): the Linux-ABI symlink/symlinkat syscalls were stale stubs returning EROFS and readlink/readlinkat returned EINVAL unconditionally, even though the VFS is fully writable and supports symlinks — so no ring-3 program could create or resolve a symlink. Fix: sys_symlink/sys_symlinkat share a new symlink_common back-end that stores the target verbatim (a symlink may dangle / be relative, so the target is NOT resolved or canonicalised) while resolving the linkpath against the caller's cwd/newdirfd via resolve_at_path, requires a File-WRITE capability (require_fs_write), and calls Vfs::symlink; sys_readlink/sys_readlinkat share a new do_readlink_copy back-end that calls Vfs::readlink and copies min(target_len, bufsiz) bytes with NO trailing NUL, returning the byte count (Linux do_readlinkat contract), validating the user buffer only after the dentry is confirmed to be a symlink (NotFound→ENOENT, InvalidArgument→EINVAL/"not a symlink"). Kernel context (caller_pid().is_none()) preserves the prior EROFS/EINVAL terminals the batch-478/487 syscall-fidelity self-tests assert; only ring-3 callers do real VFS work. Self-test: a hand-built raw-syscall Linux-ABI ELF (build_linux_symlink_readlink_test_elf) calls symlink("Z", "/sl-rl-link") then readlink("/sl-rl-link", buf, 64) from ring 3 and asserts the call returned exactly 1 byte == 'Z'; self-diagnosing exit sentinels 0xB1/0xB3/0xB4. The harness pre-removes the link path (no EEXIST) and, after the process exits 0, independently confirms kernel-side via Vfs::readlink that the created link resolves to "Z". (Raw ELF rather than dash because dash has no `ln` builtin and cannot invoke symlink(2)/readlink(2) directly.) Path Z Part 28 — link()/linkat() syscalls now create real hard links (link stub fix) (2026-06-16): the Linux-ABI link/linkat syscalls were stale stubs returning EROFS after their argument gates, even though the VFS supports hard links (Vfs::link). Fix: sys_link/sys_linkat share a new link_common back-end that resolves both the existing (oldpath) and new (newpath) names against the caller's cwd/dirfds via resolve_at_path, requires a File-WRITE capability (require_fs_write), and calls Vfs::link (which follows symlinks in oldpath and rejects cross-mount links). Kernel context (caller_pid().is_none()) preserves the EROFS terminal the batch-481 syscall-fidelity self-test asserts. Fidelity note: plain link(2) should NOT follow a symlink oldpath and linkat follows only with AT_SYMLINK_FOLLOW, but Vfs::link always follows — so the rare symlink-as-oldpath case links the target instead (documented in known-issues B-SYM1). Self-test: a hand-built raw-syscall Linux-ABI ELF (build_linux_link_test_elf) calls link("/mnt/lnk-src", "/mnt/lnk-dst") then open("/mnt/lnk-dst", O_RDONLY)+read one byte from ring 3 and asserts it is 'L' (the byte the harness pre-wrote to /mnt/lnk-src); self-diagnosing exit sentinels 0xC1/0xC2/0xC3/0xC4. After the process exits 0, the harness independently confirms kernel-side via Vfs::read_file that /mnt/lnk-dst reads back "L". The test runs on the ext4 mount at /mnt (not the memfs root): memfs stores file data inline in by-value tree nodes and cannot share an inode between two names, so it correctly reports unsupported — Linux likewise returns EPERM for FSes without hard-link support; ext4 implements real hard links. memfs hard-link support would need an inode-table refactor and is deferred (documented in known-issues B-SYM1). Path Z Part 29 — utimensat()/utimes()/utime() now apply file timestamps (timestamp-stub fix) (2026-06-16): the Linux-ABI utimensat/utimes/utime family were stale stubs returning EROFS after their Linux-faithful input-shape gate ladders (batch 489), even though Vfs::set_times is implemented by memfs/ext4/fat — so no ring-3 program could update a file's atime/mtime (touch, make target stamping, tar -x mtime restore, configure probes). Fix: for ring-3 callers each handler resolves the target (resolve_at_path against the caller's cwd/dirfd; utimensat with a NULL pathname resolves the open file behind dirfd via handle_path), translates the parsed timespec/timeval/utimbuf into ns-since-epoch (UTIME_NOW→clock_realtime, UTIME_OMIT/NULL-field→leave-unchanged, otherwise sec*1e9[+sub-second]), requires a File-WRITE capability, and calls Vfs::set_times. Kernel context (caller_pid().is_none()) preserves the EROFS terminal the batch-489 syscall-fidelity self-tests assert. Fidelity gaps (minor, documented in known-issues B-UTIME1): Vfs::set_times always follows symlinks so utimensat's AT_SYMLINK_NOFOLLOW is a no-op, and the Timestamp=u64 VFS API overloads 0 as the leave-unchanged sentinel so setting a field to exactly the Unix epoch / a pre-epoch instant is treated as leave-unchanged. Self-test: a hand-built raw-syscall Linux-ABI ELF (build_linux_utimensat_test_elf) calls utimensat(AT_FDCWD, "/utimensat-test", {atime=1.6e9 s, mtime=1.5e9 s}, 0) from ring 3 (self-diagnosing exit sentinel 0xD1); the harness stages the file on the memfs root (memfs implements set_times, unlike hard links) and, after the process exits 0, independently asserts the kernel-side Vfs::metadata reports accessed_ns==1.6e18 and modified_ns==1.5e18 exactly. Path Z Part 30 — chmod()/fchmod()/fchmodat()/chown()/lchown()/fchown()/fchownat() now mutate file metadata (chmod/chown stub fix) (2026-06-16): the entire Linux-ABI chmod/chown family were stale stubs returning EROFS after their (batch-483/484) input-shape gates, even though the VFS tracks Unix mode bits and uid/gid and implements Vfs::set_permissions / Vfs::set_owner across memfs/ext4/fat — so no ring-3 program could chmod +x, install -m, or restore perms/owner from a tar. Fix: for ring-3 callers each handler resolves the target (resolve_at_path for path variants against the caller's cwd/dirfd; handle_path on the open file for the fchmod/fchown fd variants and the fchownat(AT_EMPTY_PATH) form), requires a File-WRITE capability, and calls Vfs::set_permissions (mode masked to 0o7777 via a shared chmod_apply) or Vfs::set_owner (uid/gid narrowed to 32 bits via a shared chown_apply; the (uid_t)-1/(gid_t)-1 leave-unchanged sentinels are honoured by Vfs::set_owner). Kernel context (caller_pid().is_none()) preserves the EROFS terminal the fidelity self-tests assert; fchmod/fchown on a non-file fd (pipe/console) return EINVAL. Fidelity gaps (minor, known-issues B-CHOWN1): lchown / fchownat(AT_SYMLINK_NOFOLLOW) still follow the final symlink (set_owner always follows), and chmod/chown are gated on the generic File-WRITE capability rather than a dedicated CAP_CHOWN/CAP_FOWNER. Self-test: a hand-built raw-syscall ELF (build_linux_chmod_chown_test_elf) calls chmod("/chmod-chown-test", 0o640) then chown(path, 1234, 5678) from ring 3 (sentinels 0xE1/0xE2); the harness stages the file on the memfs root and, after the process exits 0, independently asserts Vfs::metadata reports permissions==0o640, uid==1234, gid==5678. Part 31 — truncate() and ftruncate() now resize files for ring-3 callers (truncate/ftruncate stub fix; known-issues B-TRUNC1). Both syscalls previously ran their full input-shape gate ladders (EINVAL on negative length, EFAULT/ENOENT on bad/empty/missing paths, EISDIR on directories, EINVAL on non-regular inodes and on a read-only fd via the FMODE_WRITE check) and then hard-coded EROFS for a confirmed regular file, even though Vfs::truncate is implemented across memfs/ext4/fat. Now, for ring-3 callers, sys_truncate (after its real Vfs::stat triage confirms a regular file) and sys_ftruncate's File arm enforce RLIMIT_FSIZE (EFBIG on a grow past the soft limit → the check returns to its proper Linux position now that mounts are writable, between the FMODE_WRITE/mnt_want_write gate and do_truncate), require a File-WRITE capability, resolve the target (canonicalize_path for the path variant, handle_path on the open fd for ftruncate), and call Vfs::truncate (grow-with-zeros or shrink). Kernel context keeps the EROFS terminal (gated on caller_pid().is_none()), so the batch-447/448 fidelity self-tests still pass. Self-test (Path Z Part 31, self_test_linux_truncate): a hand-built raw-syscall ELF (build_linux_truncate_test_elf) shrinks /truncate-test to 4 bytes via the path syscall, then open(O_RDWR)+ftruncate(fd, 10) grows it (sentinels 0xF1/0xF2/0xF3); the harness stages a 16-byte file on the memfs root and, after the process exits 0, independently asserts the readback is exactly 10 bytes with the leading 4 preserved ('A') and the grown tail zero-filled. Part 32 — fchmodat2() (syscall #452, the 4-arg flags-aware chmod) now mutates file metadata for ring-3 callers (fchmodat2 stub fix; known-issues B-CHOWN1 follow-up). It was a separate EROFS stub missed by the Part 30 chmod/chown pass; it is now wired in the same idiom as sys_fchownat. AT_EMPTY_PATH resolves dirfd to its backing path (AT_FDCWD → cwd, else an open File fd via handle_path) then chmod_apply; the non-AT_EMPTY_PATH branch keeps the empty-path → ENOENT getname discrimination, then (for ring-3 callers) resolve_at_path + chmod_apply (real Vfs::set_permissions). Kernel context keeps the EROFS terminal, so the batch-485 fidelity self-test stays green. Fidelity gap (minor, known-issues B-CHOWN1): AT_SYMLINK_NOFOLLOW is ignored (set_permissions always follows the final symlink). Self-test (Path Z Part 32, self_test_linux_fchmodat2): a hand-built raw-syscall ELF (build_linux_fchmodat2_emptypath_test_elf) open(O_RDWR)s /fchmodat2-test and calls fchmodat2(fd, "", 0o600, AT_EMPTY_PATH) from ring 3 (sentinels 0xE5/0xE6); the harness stages the file on the memfs root and, after the process exits 0, independently asserts Vfs::metadata reports permissions==0o600. Path Z Part 33 (fallocate real allocate — syscall #285): wired sys_fallocate from the stale EOPNOTSUPP terminal ("Our VFS doesn't expose fallocate") to the real VFS for ring-3 callers, completing the FS-write line. The full Linux gate ladder (fd validation → offset/len bounds → unknown-mode-bits → PUNCH|ZERO mutual exclusion → PUNCH-needs-KEEP_SIZE → COLLAPSE/INSERT/UNSHARE exclusivity → FMODE_WRITE) is unchanged; after it, ring-3 callers now classify the fd's inode kind (Linux's FIFO→ESPIPE / non-regular→ENODEV gates) and dispatch the two well-defined allocate modes: mode==0 (posix_fallocate) grows the file so its logical size is >= offset+len (never shrinking an already-larger file) via handle_path + Vfs::file_size/Vfs::truncate; mode==KEEP_SIZE reserves blocks for [0, offset+len) without changing the logical size via Vfs::fallocate. Both enforce RLIMIT_FSIZE (EFBIG, also on checked_add overflow) and the File-WRITE capability; MemFd fds grow via ipc::memfd::truncate (KEEP_SIZE is a no-op for in-memory backing). Every other surviving mode combination (PUNCH_HOLE, ZERO_RANGE, COLLAPSE_RANGE, INSERT_RANGE, UNSHARE_RANGE and valid combos) keeps the spec-acceptable EOPNOTSUPP fallback (sqlite/PostgreSQL treat it as "write zeros instead"), as does kernel context (caller_pid None — no fd table), so the batch-536 FMODE_WRITE + vfs_fallocate gate-order self-tests stay green. Self-test (Path Z Part 33, self_test_linux_fallocate): a hand-built raw-syscall ELF (build_linux_fallocate_grow_test_elf) open(O_RDWR)s /fallocate-test and calls fallocate(fd, 0, 0, 10) from ring 3 (sentinels 0xD1/0xD2); the harness stages the file at 4 bytes on the memfs root and, after the process exits 0, independently asserts Vfs::read_file reports a 10-byte file with the original 4 'A' bytes preserved and the grown tail zero-filled. Path Z Part 34 (real GNU make runs a recipe via /bin/sh — access()-stub fix + posix_spawn vfork clone support) (2026-06-16): unmodified prebuilt GNU make 4.3 (glibc, dynamically linked) now runs end-to-end in ring 3: ld.so loads make+libc, make parses a Makefile, and dispatches its recipe through /bin/sh, which fork/exec's /bin/emit with a `>` redirect — the first rung of the GCC/CMake/Make toolchain initiative. Two real kernel bugs were fixed. (1) THE access() STUB (root cause): sys_access/sys_faccessat/sys_faccessat2 unconditionally returned ENOENT (stale no-backing-FS skeleton), so make's `access("/bin/sh", X_OK)` — which it issues BEFORE spawning the recipe shell — always failed and make bailed with `"/bin/sh: No such file or directory"` / `Error 127` without ever spawning (confirmed by strace ground truth on real Linux: `access(shell, X_OK) = 0` precedes the clone3). The three syscalls now share a new access_path_common back-end that canonicalises the path against the caller's cwd and looks it up via Vfs::metadata/lmetadata (follow honours AT_SYMLINK_NOFOLLOW). Under our capability-based, no-DAC security model F_OK/R_OK/X_OK succeed for any existing file or dir — reporting X_OK as grantable is *consistent* with execve, which itself ignores on-disk execute bits (design-decisions §27). Kernel context (caller_pid None) preserves the ENOENT no-file contract the fidelity self-tests assert. (2) posix_spawn's clone: glibc posix_spawn issues `clone3({flags=CLONE_VM|CLONE_VFORK|CLONE_CLEAR_SIGHAND, exit_signal=SIGCHLD, stack=..., stack_size=...})`. validate_clone3_args rejected CLONE_CLEAR_SIGHAND with EINVAL (now accepted — honoured by resetting the child's kernel-side signal state, though the imminent execve resets it anyway), and linux_clone_inner had no path for CLONE_VM|CLONE_VFORK (no CLONE_THREAD) with a caller-provided child stack. A new VFORK_SPAWN branch degenerates this to a copy-on-write fork (our processes are address-space isolated, so a shared-VM vfork is impossible) with the child resuming on the caller's child_stack per clone(2); fork.rs grew fork_process_vfork / fork_process_clone_inner(rsp_override) for this. Known degradation (known-issues): on exec FAILURE in the child the errno written to the Linux-shared stack is lost under CoW, so the parent observes a 127 child exit rather than the precise errno. Self-test (self_test_linux_real_glibc_make): stages ld/libc/make/sh/emit from the /mnt ext4 rootfs, writes a Makefile whose recipe is `@/bin/emit > /make-out.txt`, runs `make -f /Makefile all`, and asserts exit 0 with /make-out.txt == the 16-byte emit body. Path Z Part 35 (real prebuilt C compiler — TinyCC/tcc — compiles C to a native ELF that runs in ring 3; bare-static-binary ABI-detection fix) (2026-06-18): an unmodified prebuilt `tcc` (glibc, dynamically linked against libc+libm) now runs in ring 3, compiles a freestanding C source into an x86_64 ELF, and that freshly-built ELF then *also* runs in ring 3 and produces correct output — proving the OS can host a real toolchain, not merely run prebuilt binaries. Flow (self_test_linux_real_glibc_cc): stage ld/libc/libm/tcc from the /mnt ext4 rootfs, write a `-nostdlib` freestanding C program (own `_start`, raw write/exit syscalls, message built on the stack), run `tcc -nostdlib -static -o /cc-prog /cc-prog.c` (ld.so loads tcc+libc+libm, tcc codegens a 1300-byte ELF), then spawn `/cc-prog` directly with its fd 1 redirected to a capture file (the proven linux_fd_take + linux_fd_install_at mechanism) and assert it wrote the 16-byte `SLATE_TCC_CC_OK\n` payload, exit 0. One real kernel gap was fixed: a bare static binary tcc emits for the Linux ABI carries NO marker `elf::detect_linux_abi` recognises (OSABI=SYSV/0, no PT_INTERP, no PT_GNU_PROPERTY — only a PT_GNU_RELRO segment, which is deliberately not a signal), so it was misclassified as a Native-ABI process and its `write`/`exit` syscalls were routed through the wrong dispatch table (the `write(1,…)` produced 0 observable bytes — confirmed via the new exit-code/byte-count diagnostic). Fix: added `spawn::spawn_process_with_abi(elf, options, AbiMode::Linux)` — a thin `spawn_process` variant (zero call-site churn: both wrap a shared `spawn_process_inner` taking an `Option<AbiMode>` override) that lets a caller which *knows* the binary's ABI (because it just produced it with a known toolchain) state it explicitly instead of relying on a heuristic that cannot see the difference. The broader question of how the OS should auto-classify arbitrary *wild* bare static ELFs (Linux vs SlateOS-native) is escalated to the operator as open-questions.md Q9 (recommendation: default unmarked bare ELFs to Linux ABI and stamp native binaries with an explicit SlateOS OSABI/note). Path Z Part 36 (real prebuilt C compiler — tcc — now performs a HOSTED glibc-linked compile: links a C program against real glibc through crt startup + ld.so into a *dynamically-linked* ELF that runs in ring 3; zero-length-read POSIX fix) (2026-06-18): the hosted complement to Part 35's `-nostdlib -static` freestanding compile.
