An unmodified prebuilt `tcc` now runs `tcc -o /hosted-prog /hosted-prog.c` against the real glibc support set (crt1.o/crti.o/crtn.o + libc.so linker-script + libc_nonshared.a + libtcc1.a, all staged from the /mnt ext4 rootfs by scripts/create-ext4-rootfs.sh), producing a 4135-byte ELF with `PT_INTERP=/lib64/ld-linux-x86-64.so.2`. Because the output carries PT_INTERP it is auto-classified Linux-ABI (no explicit override needed, unlike Part 35's bare static binary), so the run step is a plain `spawn_process`; ld.so then loads the freshly-built binary + libc, `main` calls libc `puts`, and the exit-time stdio flush writes the expected 20-byte `SLATE_TCC_HOSTED_OK
`, exit 0. One real kernel bug was fixed (root-caused via strace ground-truth on Linux): tcc's `full_read` reads exactly `count` bytes and then issues a *terminal* `read(fd, buf, 0)`, relying on POSIX's rule that a zero-length read returns 0; SlateOS's `sys_fs_read` instead rejected `buf_cap == 0` with EINVAL, so `full_read` propagated the negative result and `tcc_object_type` saw a short ELF-header read and rejected *every* relocatable object (crt1.o, crti.o, …) as "unrecognized file type" (the `.c` source read fine because it never issues a terminal zero-read). Fix: `sys_fs_read` now returns 0 for a zero-length read without validating/touching the buffer (matching Linux `read(fd, NULL, 0) == 0`), before the null-pointer check — proper for both the native and Linux ABIs. Self-test (self_test_linux_real_glibc_cc_hosted): no-ops cleanly if the glibc support set is absent; otherwise parses tcc's output and asserts it is dynamically linked (interp present) before running it with fd 1 redirected via the linux_fd_take + linux_fd_install_at capture mechanism. Path Z Part 37 (hosted tcc compile exercising more glibc ABI — printf varargs + heap) (2026-06-19): strengthens Part 36 by compiling+running a freshly-tcc-built dynamic binary that does a malloc/free heap round-trip and a printf with variadic format conversions (`%s` consumes a pointer arg, `%d` formats an int) — the program builds a string on the heap (`malloc(8)` → 'SLATE'), prints `printf("%s-%d
", p, 1234)`, frees it, returns 0. Because fd 1 is redirected to a regular file (not a tty) glibc makes stdout fully buffered, so the printf output is emitted by the exit-time flush — the same path Part 36 validates for puts. tcc produced a 4455-byte dynamic ELF (PT_INTERP set), ld.so loaded it + libc, and the captured output was exactly the 11-byte `SLATE-1234
`, exit 0. No kernel changes needed (the Part 36 zero-length-read fix + the existing dynamic-load / glibc-init path already cover it). Refactor: the Part 36/37 harness was factored into a shared run_hosted_cc_case(label, src, expect_out) back-end (stages the glibc support set, compiles, asserts the output is dynamically linked, runs with fd-1 capture, asserts the bytes) so each rung is a thin ~3-line caller. Path Z Part 38 (separate compilation — tcc -c objects + multi-object link) (2026-06-19): strengthens Parts 36/37, which each compiled+linked a single source in one tcc invocation, by exercising tcc's object emission AND tcc-as-linker over multiple relocatable inputs. Flow (self_test_linux_real_glibc_cc_separate): `tcc -c /sep-a.c -o /sep-a.o` (compile-only TU A, defines slate_add) then `tcc -c /sep-b.c -o /sep-b.o` (compile-only TU B, whose main calls slate_add across the TU boundary), each verified to be a real relocatable ELF object via a new assert_relocatable_elf helper (ELF magic + e_type==ET_REL(1) at offset 0x10 — proving `-c` produced an object, not an executable); then `tcc -o /sep-prog /sep-a.o /sep-b.o` links both relocatables + crt + glibc into one dynamic executable, resolving the cross-TU slate_add reference at link time (asserted PT_INTERP-bearing dynamic ELF). tcc emitted a 1179-byte and a 1494-byte ET_REL object and a 4295-byte dynamic ELF; ld.so ran it with fd 1 redirected to a capture file and the exit-time stdio flush wrote exactly the 13-byte `SLATE-SEP-42` line, exit 0. No kernel changes needed (the Part 36 zero-length-read fix + the existing dynamic-load/glibc-init path already cover it). Refactor: the Part 36/37 single-file harness (formerly run_hosted_cc_case inline) was further factored into four shared helpers — stage_hosted_cc_support, spawn_reap_tcc, assert_dynamic_elf, run_dynamic_capture — reused by all three rungs; Part 38 composes them across its three tcc invocations plus assert_relocatable_elf. Path Z Part 39 (the §4.4 toolchain capstone — real GNU make drives tcc to build a multi-file C program) (2026-06-19): composes Part 34 (real make in ring 3) with Part 38 (tcc separate compilation) into the realistic "build a C project with make + a compiler" flow. Flow (self_test_linux_real_glibc_make_cc): stage the hosted-cc support set plus /bin/make and /bin/sh from the /mnt rootfs, write two TUs (/cap-a.c defines slate_add, /cap-b.c's main calls it across the boundary) and a 3-target Makefile (/cap-prog: /cap-a.o /cap-b.o; each .o built by `tcc -c`; the program linked by `tcc -o`), then run `make -f /cap.mk all`. make parsed the prerequisite graph and fork/exec'd /bin/tcc three times — compiling the two TUs to relocatable objects and linking them + crt + glibc into a 4295-byte dynamic ELF — which then ran in ring 3 with fd 1 redirected to a capture file and the exit-time stdio flush wrote exactly the 13-byte `SLATE-SEP-42` line, exit 0. This is make *as the build driver* spawning the compiler across a real dependency graph (make + tcc×3 is the heaviest multi-process glibc workload in the suite, budget 33,554,432 yields). No kernel changes needed (Part 34's posix_spawn/access fixes + the Part 36 zero-length-read fix already cover it). With this rung the hosted-toolchain line is functionally complete; the next step (compiling sources that `#include <stdio.h>`) is BLOCKED on staging the glibc header tree into the rootfs, which neither the image nor the build host currently carries (documented in todo.txt). Path Z Part 40 (project-local `#include "..."` across multiple TUs) (2026-06-19): self_test_linux_real_glibc_cc_project_header writes a shared include-guarded header (a macro SLATE_BASE + a cross-TU prototype) and two TUs that each `#include "caphdr-hdr.h"`, then `tcc -o prog a.c b.c` resolves the quote-include, expands the macro, honors the prototype across the TU boundary, and the linked dynamic ELF prints SLATE-HDR-42 in ring 3 — filling the header-include gap left by Parts 36-39 (which used bare `extern`s) for the project-relative quote form (the `<system_header.h>` glibc-tree form stays blocked per TD22). Path Z Part 41 (C-runtime constructor/destructor lifecycle) (2026-07-15): self_test_linux_real_glibc_cc_ctor_dtor is the first rung to exercise `.init_array`/`.fini_array` — a program with `__attribute__((constructor))` and `__attribute__((destructor))` (tcc emits them into those sections) prints three raw `write(2)` markers; glibc's csu init (`__libc_csu_init`, called by `__libc_start_main` before `main`) walks `.init_array` and the dynamic linker's `_dl_fini` walks `.fini_array` at exit, so the captured file is exactly `CTOR\nMAIN\nDTOR\n` (15 bytes, exit 0) — proving the full ctor→main→dtor lifecycle for a real dynamically-linked glibc program in ring 3. Unbuffered write(2) (not stdio) makes the byte order the exact temporal order, immune to exit-time-flush-vs-.fini_array ordering ambiguity. No kernel changes needed (reuses the Part 36 run_hosted_cc_case harness). Path Z Part 42 (ELF thread-local storage in a compiled binary) (2026-07-15): self_test_linux_real_glibc_cc_tls is the first rung to exercise the TLS ABI from *tcc output* (the pre-existing pthread self-test runs a pre-built /bin/pthread, not compiled-on-target code). tcc emits a `.tdata`/PT_TLS segment + local-exec TLS relocations for an initialised `__thread int` (42); glibc's `__libc_setup_tls` copies the PT_TLS init image (found via AT_PHDR/AT_PHNUM) into the main thread's TLS block, and `%fs`-relative access reads it — the program prints `slate_tls % 10` (=2), reassigns it to 7, and prints again (=7) so the captured file is exactly `27\n` (3 bytes, exit 0), proving the init image was copied AND the block is writable. Also the first end-to-end validation of the per-task `%fs`-base save/restore (bugs F13/F14) against a real `__thread` consumer rather than a hand-written ELF. No kernel changes needed. Path Z Part 43 (POSIX signal delivery in a compiled binary) (2026-07-15): self_test_linux_real_glibc_cc_signal is the first rung to drive the kernel's Linux signal machinery (`rt_sigaction`, asynchronous signal-frame setup, `rt_sigreturn`) from *tcc output* — the pre-existing signal self-tests (self_test_linux_real_glibc_signal / _sigqueue / _fault) run pre-built ELFs, so no prior rung proved the full "tcc emits a `.text` handler → glibc's `signal()` installs it via `rt_sigaction` (with glibc's SA_RESTORER trampoline) → `raise()` issues `tgkill` → the kernel posts the signal and, on the syscall-return path, builds the Linux signal frame the handler `ret`s into to reach `rt_sigreturn`" round-trip for a binary compiled on-target. The program installs a `SIGUSR1` (10) handler, writes `A`, raise(10)s to itself (delivered synchronously — the pending signal is taken on return from the tgkill syscall before raise() returns), and writes `B`; the handler writes `SIG` in between, so the captured file is exactly `A\nSIG\nB\n` (8 bytes, exit 0). Unbuffered write(2) makes the byte order the exact temporal order. No kernel changes needed (reuses the Part 36 run_hosted_cc_case harness); it is the signal-delivery sibling of Part 41 (ctor/dtor) and Part 42 (TLS). Path Z Part 44 (non-local control flow — setjmp/longjmp) (2026-07-15): self_test_linux_real_glibc_cc_setjmp is the first rung to exercise C's non-local jump (the substrate for error-recovery / exception-like unwinding). It compiles a program that snapshots the register set via glibc's exported `_setjmp` (the POSIX no-signal-mask symbol — the plain `setjmp` macro needs `<setjmp.h>`, blocked per TD22), writes `A`, `_setjmp`s (returns 0 → writes `S`), then calls a deeper function that `_longjmp(env, 7)`s back so `_setjmp` "returns" a second time with 7 → writes `7`; `env` is a static buffer surviving the unwind, so the captured file is exactly `A\nS\n7\n` (6 bytes, exit 0). Proves tcc emits the correct `_setjmp`/`_longjmp` call sequence and glibc's callee-saved-register + `%rsp`/`%rip` save/restore works in ring 3. No kernel changes needed. Path Z Part 45 (user-defined variadic function — SysV varargs ABI codegen) (2026-07-15): self_test_linux_real_glibc_cc_vararg is the first rung to exercise tcc's *own* lowering of the x86_64 variadic ABI (register save area, `%al` vector-register count on the call side, `va_start`/`va_arg`/`va_end` bookkeeping) for a *user-authored* variadic function — a path printf never covers (its `va_arg` walk lives inside glibc). The program defines `isum(int count, ...)` summing `count` int varargs via tcc's builtins (`__builtin_va_list`/`__builtin_va_start`/`__builtin_va_arg`/`__builtin_va_end`, so no `<stdarg.h>` header tree is needed — stays inside TD22); `isum(4,10,20,5,7)` = 42 printed as two digits, captured file exactly `42\n` (3 bytes, exit 0). Pure userspace/codegen (no kernel path); value is proving tcc's variadic ABI lowering produces a correct binary here. No kernel changes needed. Path Z Part 46 (floating-point / SSE codegen + SysV FP ABI) (2026-07-15): self_test_linux_real_glibc_cc_float is the first rung to use floating point — Parts 34-45 never touched an XMM register, so tcc's `double` codegen (`mulsd`/`addsd`), the SysV FP calling convention (args/return in `%xmm0`/`%xmm1`), and the truncating `double`→`int` cast (`cvttsd2si`) were untested from compiled code. The program passes two doubles to `scale(x,f)=x*f+0.5` (`scale(8.0,5.0)`=40.5, `(int)`→40 printed as two digits, captured `40\n`, 3 bytes, exit 0); a `volatile` input defeats constant folding so real SSE + the FP-ABI call sequence run. Pure userspace/codegen; value is proving tcc's FP codegen + SysV FP ABI produce a correct ring-3 binary (and XMM state is sane across the glibc call path). With this rung the compiled-language-feature coverage (control flow, ctor/dtor, TLS, signals, setjmp/longjmp, varargs, floating point) is comprehensive; the remaining gaps are compiled-pthread (deferred while B-PTHREAD-TEARDOWN-PF is open) and the `<system_header.h>` glibc-tree include form (blocked per TD22). No kernel changes needed. REMAINING (TD22 Phase 2) is won't-fix per design-decisions §22; ongoing per-syscall behavioural fidelity tuning.
- [x] epoll, eventfd, signalfd, timerfd emulation — **DONE** (kernel-level Linux-ABI epoll/eventfd/signalfd/timerfd, distinct from the userspace posix-layer at §1222). **epoll**: new kernel/src/ipc/epoll.rs instance object (EpollHandle + interest set BTreeMap<fd, {events:u32, data:u64}>, refcounted create/dup/close mirroring ipc/eventfd.rs, shared across fork/dup holders, 7-check boot self_test). Full HandleKind::Epoll + ResourceType::Epoll(=18) wiring across linux_fd.rs/cap/fork(dup_one+close_one)/procfs(anon_inode:[eventpoll])/ipc cleanup_handles, plus all ~50 exhaustive HandleKind match sites in syscall/linux.rs (read/write→EINVAL, lseek ESPIPE, fstat/statx→S_IFREG|0600 sz 4096, fsync/ftruncate→EINVAL, flock→EBADF, cachestat→EOPNOTSUPP, pidfd_getfd dup/resource/release, handle_kind_ord). Syscalls: epoll_create/create1 (EPOLL_CLOEXEC) via epoll_install (register_ipc_handle→linux_fd_install with rollback), epoll_ctl with the full Linux fs/eventpoll.c 6-gate order (event-read EFAULT → fdget(epfd) EBADF → fdget(fd) EBADF → file_can_poll EPERM → self-loop/non-epoll EINVAL → op switch ADD/MOD/DEL with EEXIST/ENOENT), epoll_wait/pwait/pwait2 on the shared poll_revents_from_entry readiness engine (10ms-slice blocking, 12-byte packed records, EP_MAX_EVENTS=INT_MAX/12 gating, sigsetsize-iff-umask, pwait2 timespec parsing). **signalfd** (2026-06-12): new kernel/src/ipc/signalfd.rs instance object (SignalFdHandle + shared u64 signal mask, refcounted create/dup/close, mask shared across fork/dup holders, SIGKILL/SIGSTOP stripped via sanitize_mask, boot self_test). Full HandleKind::SignalFd + ResourceType::SignalFd(=19) wiring across linux_fd.rs/cap/fork/procfs(anon_inode:[signalfd])/ipc cleanup_handles + all the same ~50 exhaustive HandleKind match sites. Syscalls: signalfd/signalfd4 (create when fd==-1 via register_ipc_handle→linux_fd_install with rollback; update existing mask when fd>=0; SFD_CLOEXEC/SFD_NONBLOCK), read path drains masked-pending signals into 128-byte signalfd_siginfo records (ssi_signo filled, rest zero) gated by the fd mask intersected with the owning process's pending set (proc::signal::take_pending_in_mask). poll_revents_from_entry threaded with owner_pid so a signalfd reports POLLIN when has_pending_in_mask(pid, fd_mask) — i.e. signalfd is pollable inside poll/select/epoll. **timerfd** (2026-06-12): new kernel/src/ipc/timerfd.rs instance object (TimerFdHandle + per-instance {clockid, expiry_ns, interval_ns}, refcounted create/dup/close with armed state shared across fork/dup holders, boot self_test covering pure expiry math + lifecycle + shared-state + stale-handle). **Lazy-expiry model** — no background hrtimer per timerfd: each instance stores only its next absolute expiry and interval, and the expiration count is computed on demand from the current clock at read/poll/gettime (advance/remaining pure fns). Clock domains: CLOCK_MONOTONIC/BOOTTIME via hrtimer::now_ns, CLOCK_REALTIME via timekeeping::clock_realtime; alarm clocks (REALTIME_ALARM/BOOTTIME_ALARM) rejected EPERM at the syscall layer (no CAP_WAKE_ALARM). Full HandleKind::Timerfd + ResourceType::Timerfd(=20) wiring across linux_fd.rs/cap/fork/procfs(anon_inode:[timerfd])/ipc cleanup_handles + all the same exhaustive HandleKind match sites (read→8-byte count or EAGAIN, write→EINVAL, lseek ESPIPE, fstat/statx→S_IFREG|0600 sz4096, fsync/ftruncate/fdatasync→EINVAL, flock→EBADF, cachestat→EOPNOTSUPP, pidfd_getfd dup/resource/release, epoll_ctl allowed, poll_revents_from_entry via is_readable, handle_kind_ord→8). Syscalls now real (were ENOSYS/EINVAL stubs): timerfd_create (create→register_ipc_handle→linux_fd_install with rollback; TFD_CLOEXEC/TFD_NONBLOCK), timerfd_settime (itimerspec64 parse, abstime via TFD_TIMER_ABSTIME, writes old value back through otmr), timerfd_gettime (non-consuming remaining/interval). read() returns the 8-byte expiration count and resets it; pollable inside poll/select/epoll (readability is purely time-based, no owner_pid needed). **Update (2026-06-14): the earlier blocking-read/clock-step/nesting limitations are now resolved.** A blocking signalfd read parks on a per-process signalfd wait-queue woken by signal delivery (proc::signal::set_pending), a blocking timerfd read parks on a one-shot hrtimer armed at the next expiry (and is woken by settime when a disarmed timer is re-armed), and a blocking inotify read parks on an fs::notify owner-token wait-queue woken by notify::emit — so none of the three returns EAGAIN on the blocking path anymore. TFD_TIMER_CANCEL_ON_SET now cancels on a discontinuous realtime-clock step (read→ECANCELED once per step, poll→POLLIN; known-issues.md TD15). Nested epoll/signalfd/timerfd fds now report readiness inside poll/select/epoll via epoll_instance_ready (depth-bounded by EP_MAX_NESTS=4; known-issues.md TD16). All exercised by boot self-tests.
- [x] inotify emulation (kernel-level Linux-ABI, 2026-06-12) — **DONE** (distinct from the userspace polling shim at §1224; this is a real kernel fd backed by the native fs::notify subsystem). New kernel/src/ipc/inotify.rs instance object: each inotify fd owns a watch table (BTreeMap<wd:i32, {native_id:u64, in_mask:u32, path_norm:String}>), a pending VecDeque<InotifyEventOut>, and a refcount; create/dup/close mirror the rest of the fd family, with all native watches released on the final close. **inotify-over-fs::notify adapter:** add_watch translates the Linux IN_* interest mask → native FsEventMask (to_native_mask; as of 2026-06-14 IN_ACCESS/IN_OPEN/IN_CLOSE_WRITE/IN_CLOSE_NOWRITE all map to native bits via the VFS-read and file-handle open/close hooks; IN_ISDIR is output-only — it maps to no interest bit and is OR'd into the reported mask at read time from FsEvent.is_dir) and registers one non-recursive native watch per path; read drains every native watch (notify::read_events) and translates each FsEvent into inotify_event records — native Renamed (old+new path) becomes an IN_MOVED_FROM/IN_MOVED_TO pair sharing one nonzero cookie (respecting each watch's interest direction), Overflow becomes wd=-1 IN_Q_OVERFLOW, others a single record filtered by the watch's mask, with IN_ISDIR OR'd in for directory subjects (mkdir/rmdir, dir-handle close, renamed subdir); rm_watch synthesizes IN_IGNORED into the pending queue and tears down the native watch. **Watch identity is by normalized path string** (re-add returns the same wd and updates the mask, OR-combining under IN_MASK_ADD), not inode. Full HandleKind::Inotify + ResourceType::Inotify(=21) wiring across linux_fd.rs (FdEntry::inotify, needs_kernel_close)/cap/fork(dup_one+close_one)/procfs(anon_inode:inotify — no brackets, matching real Linux)/ipc cleanup_handles + all 26 exhaustive HandleKind match sites in syscall/linux.rs (read→dispatch_inotify_read serializing 16-byte-header + NUL-padded 16-aligned name records, EAGAIN when empty, EINVAL when the buffer can't hold the first event; write→EINVAL, lseek ESPIPE, fstat/statx→S_IFREG|0600 sz4096, fsync/ftruncate→EINVAL, flock→EBADF, cachestat→EOPNOTSUPP, pidfd_getfd dup/resource/release, epoll_ctl allowed, poll_revents via is_readable, handle_kind_ord→9). Syscalls now real (were ENOSYS stubs): inotify_init/inotify_init1 (IN_CLOEXEC/IN_NONBLOCK via inotify_init_common→register_ipc_handle→linux_fd_install with rollback), inotify_add_watch (mask-bit validation against ALL_INOTIFY_BITS, IN_MASK_ADD/IN_MASK_CREATE conflict→EINVAL, path canonicalized against cwd + Vfs::stat existence check, IN_ONLYDIR→ENOTDIR for non-dirs, EEXIST under IN_MASK_CREATE, ENOSPC on watch exhaustion), inotify_rm_watch (EINVAL for unknown wd). 9-step boot self_test (mask translation, record sizing, add_watch + create/modify event emission and read, move-pair cookie pairing, buffer-too-small EINVAL keeping the event, rm_watch IN_IGNORED + double-rm EINVAL, dup/close refcount, stale-handle safety). **Limitations** (todo.txt): a blocking read now parks on an fs::notify owner-token wait-queue woken by notify::emit (the earlier EAGAIN-on-blocking shortcut is fixed, matching signalfd/timerfd); IN_ACCESS/IN_OPEN/IN_CLOSE_WRITE/IN_CLOSE_NOWRITE are now observable (via the VFS-read hook and the fs::handle open/close hooks), and IN_ISDIR is OR'd into directory-subject events via a new FsEvent.is_dir flag threaded through both the kernel adapter and the native fs_watch ABI (byte 524) into the posix shim; watches are non-recursive and keyed by path not inode; IN_ONESHOT/IN_DONT_FOLLOW/IN_EXCL_UNLINK are accepted-but-ignored; and Linux FS-mutation syscalls remain stubs, so events flow only from native-VFS activity.
- [-] /proc emulation (enough for WINE and common Linux apps) — broad procfs implemented; added per-PID comm/statm/limits (2026-06-10); /proc/<pid>/stat now emits full Linux 52-field layout for positional parsers (ps/top/htop/glibc/WINE) (2026-06-10); /proc/<pid>/status rewritten to Linux key:value format, /proc/self symlink, /proc/<pid>/maps from the VMA list (committed + lazy mmap both register a VMA), and /proc/<pid>/mountinfo in Linux 11-field show_mountinfo format for findmnt/glibc/systemd (2026-06-10); /proc/<pid>/cgroup + cpuset (cgroup v2 unified hierarchy, shared membership lookup), oom_score (read) and oom_score_adj (read+write, validates -1000..=1000 and routes to fs::oomkiller::adjust_score via a ProcFs::write_file override; every other procfs path stays read-only), schedstat (real per-task TSC cpu_ns / run-queue wait / dispatch count), and loginuid/sessionid (audit "unset" = u32::MAX) (2026-06-10); /proc/<pid>/task/<tid>/ thread dirs implemented (nested-dir routing in classify_path + per-thread comm/schedstat/stat/status, thread fields keyed by tid and process-wide fields by owning pid) (2026-06-11); /proc/<pid>/status extended with genuinely-backed NoNewPrivs, Seccomp, Cpus_allowed/Cpus_allowed_list (per-thread affinity) and Mems_allowed/Mems_allowed_list (all online NUMA nodes), Name/comm truncated to 15 bytes, with stat<->status State-char consistency self-tested (2026-06-11); system-wide /proc/stat converted from a custom native format to the real Linux fs/proc/stat.c layout (cpu/cpuN jiffy lines from real per-CPU TSC accounting in cputime, intr/ctxt/btime/processes/procs_running/procs_blocked/softirq), with a new monotonic fork counter (pcb::processes_created) and zeros for genuinely-untracked columns — never fabricated (2026-06-11); /proc/uptime converted to the Linux fs/proc/uptime.c two-field "<uptime> <idle>" centisecond format, idle summed across all CPUs from cputime's real per-CPU TSC idle accounting (2026-06-11); /proc/loadavg converted from instantaneous-runnable-in-all-three-slots to real Linux 1/5/15-minute EWMAs — scheduler's update_load_average now maintains three fixed-point averages with Linux's exact FSHIFT/EXP_1/EXP_5/EXP_15 constants, sampled every 5s (LOAD_FREQ) from O(1) per-CPU queue lengths, formatted <int>.<frac> like Linux LOAD_INT/LOAD_FRAC (2026-06-11); /proc/buddyinfo cleaned to the pure Linux mm/vmstat.c frag_show layout (real per-order buddy free-block counts; dropped the non-Linux trailing "# Order sizes"/"# Total free frames" comment lines that broke strict parsers) (2026-06-11); /proc/<pid>/io implemented with honest per-process counters — four new PCB u64 counters (rchar/wchar/syscr/syscw) incremented at the Linux-ABI read/write syscall boundary (dispatch_linux → account_io_syscall classifying the read/write/pread/pwrite/readv/writev/preadv/pwritev(+2) family exactly as Linux folds into task io accounting), served via gen_pid_io in the Linux 7-line key:value layout with the three storage-layer fields (read_bytes/write_bytes/cancelled_write_bytes) reported as 0 (genuinely untracked, never fabricated); increment logic self-tested in kernel context (pcb::test_io_accounting) plus formatter+path self-test (2026-06-11); native-ABI io accounting now also wired — syscall::dispatch::dispatch folds completed native read/write syscalls (FS_READ/FS_READ_FILE, PIPE_READ/_TRY_READ/_READ_TIMEOUT, CONSOLE_READ_CHAR/_TRY_READ_CHAR; FS_WRITE, PIPE_WRITE/_TRY_WRITE/_WRITE_TIMEOUT, CONSOLE_WRITE) into the same account_io_{read,write} via a pure unit-tested io_dir_for_syscall classifier, reusing the task_id already resolved for the syscall filter (FS_WRITE_FILE deliberately excluded — returns 0 not a byte count), so native processes get real io counters instead of all-zero; native and Linux-ABI dispatch are separate entry paths so no double-counting (2026-06-11); /proc/<pid>/fd/ directory + per-fd magic symlinks added — backed by the real per-process Linux KernelFdTable (new list_open enumerator + pcb::linux_fd_list accessor), each fd/<n> resolving to its backing object's target (File→VFS path via fs::handle::handle_path, Pipe→pipe:[id], Console→/dev/console, eventfd/pidfd/memfd→anon_inode:[type]); the directory is honestly empty for native processes whose fd table lives in userspace and is not kernel-visible (2026-06-11); /proc/<pid>/fdinfo/<n> added alongside fd/ — regular files rendering Linux's pos:/flags: lines (pos = the open-file description's real f_pos via fs::handle::current_offset for File fds, 0 for non-seekable objects as on Linux; flags reproduces fs/proc/fd.c by folding the descriptor's FD_CLOEXEC into O_CLOEXEC), deliberately omitting mnt_id/ino rather than fabricating them since key-based readers like lsof/CRIU look up pos:/flags: by name; same honestly-empty-for-native behaviour (2026-06-12); /proc/<pid>/auxv now served by gen_pid_auxv from the per-process saved auxv that the Linux SysV initial-stack builder persists into pcb::linux_saved_auxv at spawn/exec — the raw Elf64_auxv_t byte stream for Linux-ABI pids, an honestly-empty file for native pids (which have no auxv by design), added to PID_FILES so it lists and resolves (2026-06-12). **/proc/sys sysctl tree added (2026-06-13)** — the first nested-directory subtree besides per-PID `task/`/`fd/`. New `SYS_FILES`/`SYS_DIRS` flat tables + two `ProcPath` variants (`SysDir`/`SysFile`) routed in `classify_path` (intercepted before the numeric-PID parse since "sys" isn't a number); `sys_immediate_child`/`sys_basename`/`sys_children` enumerate interior dirs from the flat tables. Files served by `gen_sys`, all real-backed (never fabricated): `kernel/{ostype,osrelease,version,hostname,domainname}` are the exact `uname(2)` surface (byte-consistent with `sys_uname` — "Linux"/"6.6.0-slateos"/"#1 SMP"/nameservice hostname+domain), `kernel/pid_max`=`pidns::MAX_PIDS_PER_NS`, `fs/nr_open`=`linux_fd::MAX_FDS`, and `kernel/random/{uuid,boot_id}` generated from the kernel CSPRNG per Linux semantics (uuid fresh per read; boot_id stable per boot via a cached `spin::Once`, RFC 4122 v4 with forced version/variant bits). `/proc` root readdir now lists the `sys` directory; tree is read-only (only `oom_score_adj` honours writes). 10-case classify test + listing/value/kind/UUID self-tests ("[procfs]   /proc/sys: ... OK"). This is what systemd/D-Bus/glibc/WINE read for kernel identity, machine session id, and fd/pid ceilings. Extended with `kernel/random/{poolsize,entropy_avail}` (2026-06-13): poolsize is the fixed 256-bit ceiling matching our ChaCha20 CSPRNG seed width (= Linux POOL_BITS since ~5.18), entropy_avail reports 256 once `rng::is_initialized()` (0 before init) so userspace can tell the random source is ready; both parsed + bounds-checked (0|256, ≤poolsize) in the self-test. **/proc/cpuinfo converted to the real Linux per-processor format (2026-06-13)** — `gen_cpuinfo` previously emitted a custom layout (a `processors:`/`flags:`/`tsc_freq:` header block followed by per-CPU blocks keyed on `acpi_id`/`apic_id`/`enabled`/`online_cap`), which broke every standard consumer: `grep -c ^processor`/nproc/locale counted the `processors:` header line as an extra CPU (off-by-one overcount), and lscpu/hwinfo (which split blocks on blank lines) parsed the header block as a phantom CPU#0 with empty vendor/model, while glibc/toolchains found none of the keys they look for. Rewritten to one Linux-style block per online logical CPU, each beginning `processor\t: N` and carrying vendor_id/cpu family/model/model name/stepping/cpu MHz/cache size/physical id/siblings/core id/cpu cores/apicid/initial apicid/fpu/flags/bogomips/clflush size/cache_alignment — sourced from `cpu::vendor_string`/`brand_string`/`cpu_family_model_stepping`/`features`/`cache_topology` + `bench::tsc_freq` (a shared `push_cpu_flags` emits the Linux baseline + CPUID-detected flag tokens per block). Dropping the header block makes block-counting parsers count exactly the online-CPU count, fixing the off-by-one in native lscpu/nproc/locale/hwinfo and making Linux-binary cpuinfo parsing work. New procfs self-test asserts block count == `acpi::processor_count()`, first line `processor\t: 0`, per-block keys (vendor_id/cpu family/model name/flags/cpu cores) each appear once per CPU, and no legacy header keys remain ("[procfs]   cpuinfo: N Linux-format processor block(s) OK").
- [x] Linux threading model (clone, futex) — **DONE** (verified complete 2026-06-13). **clone/clone3**: linux_clone/linux_clone3 (raw register entry from the syscall trampoline) and sys_clone/sys_clone3 (args-form) in syscall/linux.rs build a new thread or process from the Linux flag set — CLONE_VM/FS/FILES/SIGHAND/THREAD share the parent's address space + fd table + signal state; CLONE_SETTLS installs the TLS base (validated user pointer); CLONE_PARENT_SETTID / CLONE_CHILD_SETTID write the child tid to user memory; CLONE_CHILD_CLEARTID registers a clear-child-tid futex (proc/thread_clone.rs register_clear_child_tid) that is zeroed-and-woken on thread exit (set_tid_address(2) semantics), with the fork path handled separately. **futex**: ipc/futex.rs implements the full Linux futex op set — WAIT/WAIT_BITSET (+timeout), WAKE/WAKE_BITSET, REQUEUE/CMP_REQUEUE, WAKE_OP, the PI family (LOCK_PI/LOCK_PI2/TRYLOCK_PI/UNLOCK_PI with priority inheritance and a PI-owner table), and WAIT_REQUEUE_PI/CMP_REQUEUE_PI; FUTEX_WAITV (Linux 5.16 multi-futex wait) dispatches through the same handlers. Robust lists: set_robust_list/get_robust_list plus on-exit robust-list + PI-owned-futex cleanup (handle_futex_death, exit_pi_owned_futexes) so a crashing thread's held locks are released and waiters woken. gettid returns the per-thread id. Backed by futex stats (/proc/futexstat) and an IPC benchmark (bench_ipc_futex).
- [x] Linux DRM/KMS compatibility (for NVIDIA proprietary driver userspace) — kernel-level DRM (`/dev/dri/*`) device emulation so unmodified Linux graphics clients (Mesa, libdrm, X.Org modesetting, Wayland compositors, SDL/KMSDRM) drive the native SlateOS `drm` subsystem (kernel/src/drm/: Limine + virtio-gpu backends, GEM, atomic KMS, connectors/CRTCs/planes/encoders), mirroring the ALSA shim's structure. **Commit 1 (2026-06-13):** pure Linux-uAPI ABI layer kernel/src/drm/uapi.rs — 'd'-magic ioctl request-number encoding, byte-exact `#[repr(C)]` mirrors of the core `include/uapi/drm/drm.h` structs (drm_version 64B, drm_unique 16B, drm_auth 4B, drm_get_cap 16B, drm_set_client_cap 16B, drm_set_version 16B), core ioctl numbers derived from those layouts (VERSION 0xC0406400 / GET_UNIQUE / GET_MAGIC / SET_VERSION / GET_CAP 0xC010640C / SET_CLIENT_CAP / SET_UNIQUE / AUTH_MAGIC), DRM_CAP_*/DRM_CLIENT_CAP_* tag constants, driver identity strings, and the pure client-cap acceptance policy (atomic + universal-planes + aspect-ratio accepted; stereo-3d/writeback rejected). No device nodes / per-fd state / unsafe yet. Exhaustive boot self-test (fatal in main.rs) asserts every struct size vs drm.h, every ioctl number vs its known hex, and the cap policy — prints "[drm-uapi] DRM uAPI ABI self-test PASSED". **Commit 2 (2026-06-13):** KMS mode structs added to uapi.rs — byte-exact `#[repr(C)]` mirrors of `include/uapi/drm/drm_mode.h` (drm_mode_card_res, drm_mode_get_connector, drm_mode_get_encoder, drm_mode_crtc, drm_mode_modeinfo 68B, drm_mode_get_plane/get_plane_res, drm_mode_fb_cmd2, drm_mode_create/map/destroy_dumb, atomic) plus their ioctl numbers (MODE_GETRESOURCES/GETCONNECTOR/GETENCODER/GETCRTC/SETCRTC/GETPLANE/GETPLANERESOURCES/ADDFB2/RMFB/PAGE_FLIP/CREATE_DUMB/MAP_DUMB/DESTROY_DUMB/ATOMIC) and the DRM_MODE_* connection/connector-type/page-flip constants; self-test extended to assert each new struct size + ioctl hex. **Commit 3 (2026-06-13):** `/dev/dri/card0` (primary) + `/dev/dri/renderD128` (render node) device nodes + the stateful refcounted `HandleKind::DrmCard` fd family. New kernel/src/drm/card_fd.rs instance object — refcounted DRM_CARD_TABLE keyed by DrmCardId, each DrmClient holding {device index, render_node flag, DRM_CLIENT_CAP_* opt-in bits, refcount}; create/dup/close/exists/device/is_render_node/set_client_cap/client_cap API mirroring the AlsaPcm model (per-fd mutable client state shared across dup/fork, matching Linux struct drm_file). ResourceType::Drm(=23) + full wiring across linux_fd.rs (FdEntry::drm_card, needs_kernel_close)/cap/fork(dup_one+close_one)/procfs(fd symlink → /dev/dri/card0 or renderD128)/ipc cleanup_handles + every exhaustive HandleKind match site in syscall/linux.rs. try_open_drm intercepts the two device paths before VFS (in both open_common and the resolved-relative open_kernel_path_install), ENODEV when drm::device_count()==0, registers ResourceType::Drm with install-failure rollback. fd attributes: char device S_IFCHR|0660, lseek→ESPIPE, read/write→EINVAL, poll never-ready, epoll_ctl allowed, kcmp ord 12. drm_card_ioctl currently validates the fd + 'd' ioctl-type and returns ENOTTY (real request handlers land in commit 4). Boot self_test (fatal in main.rs) covers create/dup/close refcounting, cap set/get, render-node flag — prints "[drm_card] DRM card client lifecycle self-test PASSED". **Commit 4 (2026-06-13):** core (non-KMS) ioctl dispatch — drm_card_ioctl replaces its ENOTTY stub with real handlers for the open-time ioctl sequence every libdrm client issues. DRM_IOCTL_VERSION fills the three version ints + copies name/date/desc via drm_copy_field (Linux drm_copy_field semantics: copies min(*len, srclen) bytes, writes the full source length back so a len=0 probe learns the size, no kernel-added NUL); GET_CAP serves a new pure-policy uapi::cap_value table (TIMESTAMP_MONOTONIC/VBLANK_HIGH_CRTC/CRTC_IN_VBLANK_EVENT=1, CURSOR_WIDTH/HEIGHT=64, dumb-buffer/PRIME/async-flip/modifiers/syncobj=0 until their handlers land, unknown tag→EINVAL); SET_CLIENT_CAP routes through card_fd::set_client_cap (atomic/universal-planes/aspect-ratio accepted, else EINVAL); GET_MAGIC hands out a nominal nonzero per-client token and AUTH_MAGIC accepts any (single-user model, no separate DRM master); GET_UNIQUE reports the bus-id string; SET_VERSION negotiates (reports DRM interface 1.4 + driver version); SET_UNIQUE→EINVAL (legacy). Render-node restriction enforced: a renderD128 fd gets EACCES on the primary-node-only ioctls (auth pair, GET_UNIQUE, SET_UNIQUE, SET_VERSION), matching Linux's DRM_RENDER_ALLOW gating; VERSION/GET_CAP/SET_CLIENT_CAP allowed on both. uapi self-test extended to cover the cap_value policy. **Commit 5 (2026-06-13):** KMS resource enumeration — drm_card_ioctl gains MODE_GETRESOURCES/GETCONNECTOR/GETENCODER/GETCRTC/GETPLANERESOURCES/GETPLANE, each render-node gated (EACCES on renderD128, matching Linux DRM_MODE_* primary-node gating). Maps the native SlateOS drm model (connectors/CRTCs/encoders/planes/modes) onto the Linux KMS read ABI, honoring the two-pass array contract: array-bearing ioctls copy min(capacity, actual) entries when ptr+capacity are non-zero and always write the full actual count back, so a count=0 probe learns the size to allocate. Owned id/struct Vecs are gathered inside the drm::with_device lock then copy_to_user'd after the lock is released (copy_to_user may demand-page). GETRESOURCES enumerates crtc/connector/encoder ids (fbs reported empty, min/max dims 0..16384); GETCONNECTOR reports type/status/encoder + modes array (drm_mode_to_uapi narrows timing to u16, sets PREFERRED|DRIVER type bits, formats the mode name) + encoders array (props empty); GETENCODER reports encoder type/crtc; GETCRTC reports the bound mode (mode_valid + drm_mode_modeinfo) and primary-plane fb id; GETPLANERESOURCES enumerates plane ids; GETPLANE reports crtc/fb/possible-crtcs + the plane's fourcc format array (gamma_size 0). New helpers: drm_card_device, drm_kernel_err (KernelError→errno), drm_copy_array<T> (generic two-pass copy via checked_mul/try_from), drm_connector_type_to_uapi/drm_connector_status_to_uapi/drm_encoder_type_to_uapi/drm_mode_to_uapi conversion tables (also added DVID/LVDS/EDP connector + DAC/LVDS/DPMST encoder uapi consts). Boot self_test extended with a DRM-conversion block (all type/status mappings + drm_mode_to_uapi for preferred 1920x1080@60 and non-preferred 800x600@60) — prints "[syscall/linux]   DRM KMS enumeration conversions: OK". **Commit 6 (2026-06-13):** dumb-buffer + framebuffer *allocation lifecycle* — drm_card_ioctl gains MODE_CREATE_DUMB/DESTROY_DUMB + MODE_ADDFB2/RMFB, all render-node gated (EACCES on renderD128, matching Linux's primary-node-only gating of dumb/scanout + KMS framebuffer ioctls). CREATE_DUMB maps the requested bpp to a native PixelFormat (32→XRGB8888, 16→RGB565, else EINVAL; flags must be 0) and drives crate::drm::DrmDevice::gem_create, reporting the allocated GEM handle + actual 64-byte-aligned pitch + total byte size; DESTROY_DUMB → gem_destroy; ADDFB2 validates the FourCC via PixelFormat::from_raw and rejects multi-plane requests (any handles[1..]/pitches[1..]/offsets[..] set) then calls fb_create with handles[0]/pitches[0], writing the new fb object id back; RMFB (bare unsigned-int fb id payload) → fb_destroy. New helper drm_dumb_format(bpp); drm_kernel_err extended to map OutOfMemory→ENOMEM. Boot self_test gains a dumb-buffer block (bpp→format incl. rejection of 24/8 bpp, ADDFB2 FourCC round-trip + unknown-FourCC rejection) — prints "[syscall/linux]   DRM dumb-buffer format mapping: OK". DRM_CAP_DUMB_BUFFER stays 0 until MAP_DUMB lands (a client gates CREATE_DUMB on the cap; advertising it before the buffer is CPU-mappable would break the client). **Commit 7 (2026-06-13):** MAP_DUMB + the mmap-on-/dev/dri-fd integration — the dumb buffer is now CPU-mappable, so DRM_CAP_DUMB_BUFFER flips to 1. New kernel/src/drm/dumb_mmap.rs: the SlateOS analogue of Linux's drm_vma_offset_manager — a global table mapping a 16 KiB-aligned *fake mmap offset* token to the (device index, GEM handle) it stands for. offset_for(device,handle,size) is idempotent (a buffer already mapped gets the same offset back, matching drm_vma_offset_add) and bumps the token space by the frame-rounded size; lookup(offset)→(device,handle); forget(device,handle) drops the token on DESTROY_DUMB. drm_card_ioctl gains MODE_MAP_DUMB (render-node gated): validates the GEM handle is live on this device (DrmDevice::gem_size), allocates the fake offset, writes it back into drm_mode_map_dumb.offset. New DrmDevice accessors gem_phys_addrs(handle)→Vec<u64> (raw *physical* frame bases, vs the existing gem_frame_addrs which returns HHDM virtuals) + gem_size(handle). sys_mmap (linux) intercepts an mmap on a HandleKind::DrmCard fd *before* the file-backed ENOSYS gate: resolves the fake offset → (device,handle), confirms it belongs to this fd's device, gathers the buffer's physical frames under the drm lock (released before touching page tables), rounds the requested length up to whole 16 KiB frames (bounded by the buffer's frame count, else EINVAL), derives PageFlags from prot (USER|PRESENT always; PROT_WRITE→WRITABLE; no PROT_EXEC→NO_EXECUTE), charges RLIMIT_AS, picks a base vaddr (aligned MAP_FIXED hint honored, else handlers::mmap_alloc_vaddr), then ref_inc's + map_frame's each frame with full rollback (drm_mmap_dumb_rollback unmaps + ref_dec's, and the RLIMIT_AS charge is refunded) on any failure. **Frame-lifetime crux:** each mapped frame is frame::ref_inc'd before mapping, so the GEM object keeps its own reference (until DESTROY_DUMB) and the process address space holds the extra one; process-exit teardown's refcounted free_frame (clear_user_address_space) merely decrements, and whichever side drops the last reference truly frees — so neither destroying a still-mapped buffer nor exiting with one allocated double-frees. DESTROY_DUMB now also dumb_mmap::forget's the offset (existing user mappings stay valid until unmap/exit, kept alive by the per-mapping refcount — documented). uapi::cap_value(DRM_CAP_DUMB_BUFFER)=1 + its self-test updated. New boot self-test [drm_dumb_mmap] (run from drm::self_test) covers alloc/alignment/idempotency/distinctness/resolution/forget/fresh-offset-after-forget — prints "[drm_dumb_mmap] fake-offset allocator self-test PASSED". **Fork caveat (Judgment Call, todo.txt; known-issues TD11):** a dumb mmap that survives fork is not yet ref-tracked on the child side; documented as a known limitation. **Commit 8 (2026-06-13):** PAGE_FLIP + vblank-event delivery — the last piece of the basic KMS flip loop. uapi.rs gains the page-flip flags (DRM_MODE_PAGE_FLIP_EVENT=0x01 / _ASYNC=0x02 + the DRM_MODE_PAGE_FLIP_FLAGS validation mask), the KMS event-type tags (DRM_EVENT_VBLANK=0x01 / DRM_EVENT_FLIP_COMPLETE=0x02), and a byte-exact `#[repr(C)]` drm_event_vblank (32B: type@0/length@4/user_data@8/tv_sec@16/tv_usec@20/sequence@24/crtc_id@28) with DrmEventVblank::flip_complete(crtc_id,user_data,seq,now_ns) (CLOCK_MONOTONIC-derived tv_sec/tv_usec) + to_bytes() little-endian serializer; self-test asserts the 32B size and round-trips every field offset. card_fd.rs gains a per-client FIFO event queue (VecDeque<Vec<u8>>, shared across dup like Linux's struct drm_file, capped at MAX_PENDING_EVENTS=128 dropping oldest) with queue_event/has_events/next_event_len/pop_event/drain_into_kernel (the drain is single-lock-atomic so a concurrent reader on a dup'd fd never double-delivers); self-test covers empty/FIFO-order/length-probe/dup-sharing/drain/stale-handle. drm_card_ioctl gains MODE_PAGE_FLIP (render-node gated EACCES): validates flags (unknown bits or non-zero reserved → EINVAL), drives DrmDevice::page_flip (which validates crtc+fb+gem), and if DRM_MODE_PAGE_FLIP_EVENT is set queues a flip-complete drm_event_vblank carrying the client's user_data + a monotonic vblank sequence. read(2) on a DrmCard fd now drains whole queued events into the user buffer (dispatch_drm_card_read: validates the whole buffer up front like Linux drm_read, EINVAL if too small for the first whole record, EAGAIN when empty); poll(2) reports POLLIN whenever an event is queued. Because our backends retire flips synchronously, the event is queued before PAGE_FLIP returns, so a poll→read after submitting a flip always succeeds. **Blocking-read caveat (known-issues TD12):** an empty DRM-event read returns EAGAIN rather than blocking; harmless under synchronous flip retirement (a true wait queue is deferred until an async-flip backend exists). Boot self-tests pass: [drm-uapi] (event size + field offsets), [drm_card] (event queue lifecycle). **Task 5094 complete** — the kernel DRM/KMS Linux-ABI shim now supports the full unmodified-client flow: open → VERSION/GET_CAP/SET_CLIENT_CAP → KMS enumeration → CREATE_DUMB → MAP_DUMB+mmap → ADDFB2 → PAGE_FLIP(+EVENT) → poll/read flip-complete → DESTROY_DUMB/RMFB.
- [-] ALSA/PulseAudio compatibility shim — kernel-level ALSA (`/dev/snd/*`) device emulation so unmodified Linux audio clients (ALSA-lib, and PA/PipeWire/JACK/SDL/WINE which all layer on ALSA) drive the SlateOS software mixer. **PCM side (`/dev/snd/pcmC0D0p`|`c`):** pure ABI layer kernel/src/audio_alsa.rs (ioctl request-number encoding, byte-exact `#[repr(C)]` mirrors of every `asound.h` payload struct, format/rate/access constants, exhaustive boot self-test); per-open substream instance object kernel/src/ipc/alsa_pcm.rs (refcounted create/dup/close, OPEN→SETUP→PREPARED→RUNNING→… state machine reserving an audio_mixer slot, frame write path to the mixer ring, capture-silence read path, position tracking); HandleKind::AlsaPcm fd family wired through linux.rs/linux_fd/cap/fork/procfs/cleanup + every exhaustive match site; ioctl dispatch covering PVERSION/INFO/HW_REFINE/HW_PARAMS/SW_PARAMS/HW_FREE/PREPARE/START/DROP/DRAIN/RESET/PAUSE/WRITEI_FRAMES/READI_FRAMES/SYNC_PTR/STATUS/STATUS_EXT (+HWSYNC/RESUME/XRUN/UNLINK/TTSTAMP no-ops); SYNC_PTR (the timestamp-ABI-independent per-period pointer exchange ALSA-lib's kernel plugin relies on) reports appl_ptr/hw_ptr from the mixer's buffered-frame count; STATUS/STATUS_EXT (2026-07-15) return a byte-exact `snd_pcm_status` (time64 ABI, `size_of==152`, `STATUS=0x8098_4120`/`STATUS_EXT=0xC098_4124` — see design-decisions.md §67) filling state/appl_ptr/hw_ptr/**delay** (queued frames, what `snd_pcm_delay(3)` needs for A/V sync)/**avail** (playback: free buffer space from the HW_PARAMS-negotiated BUFFER_SIZE; capture: full buffer) from the same snapshot as SYNC_PTR, plus monotonic reference timestamps and the trigger_tstamp stamped at START. **Control side (`/dev/snd/controlC0`):** pure ABI layer kernel/src/audio_alsa_ctl.rs ('U'-magic ioctls, snd_ctl_card_info/elem_id/elem_list/elem_info/elem_value byte-exact structs, element type/iface/access constants, card-element model + resolve_numid/elem_id_for/fill_elem_info helpers, exhaustive self-test); stateless HandleKind::AlsaControl fd (no per-open resource — a pure window onto the global mixer, mirroring Console/PidFd — wired through every match site); ioctl dispatch covering PVERSION, CARD_INFO (SlateOS card identity), and ELEM_LIST/ELEM_INFO/ELEM_READ/ELEM_WRITE mapping the two master controls (Master Playback Volume INTEGER 0..100, Master Playback Switch BOOLEAN) to audio_mixer master_volume/mute. This makes the card *visible* to `snd_ctl_open()` (alsamixer/amixer/PulseAudio's ALSA backend) and lets it read/set master volume + mute. **REMAINING:** real hardware-backend audio output (currently the software mixer with no physical sink when no virtio-snd/ac97 device is present); and a userspace PulseAudio-protocol daemon is an *alternative* shape (not needed — providing ALSA covers PA/PipeWire/JACK/SDL/WINE with one interface, see todo.txt design note).
- [ ] Result: WINE runs unmodified (or with minimal patches) → Windows app support

### 5.2 Additional filesystems
- [ ] Port Btrfs (CoW, snapshots, checksums)
- [ ] Port F2FS (SSD optimization)
- [ ] NTFS read/write support
- [x] Queryable file metadata / indexed attributes (fs::queryable): BeOS BFS-inspired typed attribute store per design.txt lines 35-37 and 249; AttrValue (Text/Int/Bool/Bytes) with per-file attribute maps; relational query engine with CompareOp (Equal/NotEqual/LessThan/LessEqual/GreaterThan/GreaterEqual/Contains/StartsWith/EndsWith); QueryMode (All=AND/Any=OR); indexed queries via reverse index (attr_name → BTreeMap<value_key, Set<path>>); attribute schemas with category:name convention (Audio:*/Image:*/Document:*/Email:*/App:*); 27 built-in schemas; register_builtins(); create_index/drop_index; rename_path support; unique_values discovery; 65536 max files, 64 attrs/file, 1024 indexed attrs; `queryable`/`qattr` kshell command (set/get/rm/list/clear/query/index/schema/test/stats/reset); /proc/queryable; 7 self-tests
- [x] Application-level atomic write transactions (Vfs::atomic_write, write-temp-sync-rename pattern, atomic_write_preserve for metadata, VFS self-test)

### 5.3 Additional schedulers (if needed)
- [x] EEVDF-style scheduler (for users wanting sophisticated fairness)
  - [x] EevdfScheduler struct: BTreeMap run queue keyed by (deadline, task_id), reverse index for O(log n) dequeue; split eligible/ineligible partition indexes (eligible keyed by deadline, ineligible keyed by vruntime) give amortised O(log n) pick_next with a true-minimum min_vruntime (2026-07-15 rewrite — see known-issues EEVDF-PICK-ON RESOLVED)
  - [x] 32-entry geometric weight table (ratio ~1.25× per level, modeled on Linux sched_prio_to_weight)
  - [x] Virtual runtime tracking: advances as VRUNTIME_UNIT / weight per tick
  - [x] Virtual deadline computation: vruntime + time_slice * VRUNTIME_UNIT / weight
  - [x] Eligibility check: task.vruntime <= min_vruntime
  - [x] New/waking task placement at min_vruntime (anti-starvation)
  - [x] Work stealing (least-urgent tasks from back of BTreeMap)
  - [x] Scheduler trait implementation, WorkloadProfile integration, has_real_work
  - [x] Preemption-on-wake: should_preempt() checks front-of-queue deadline vs current task; tick() triggers early reschedule when woken task has significantly earlier deadline (MIN_GRANULARITY threshold prevents oscillation)
  - [x] 15 self-tests: pick_next ordering, tick vruntime advance, dequeue, equal-priority fairness, weighted fairness (CPU-time), steal, has_ready/has_real_work, workload profiles, anti-starvation, preemption-on-wake (high-prio preempts, equal-prio doesn't, empty queue safe), partition invariant across ops, deadline-correctness under adversarial vruntime mix, true-minimum min_vruntime
- [x] Deadline scheduler (for real-time/audio workloads)
  - [x] DeadlineScheduler struct: BTreeMap run queue keyed by (abs_deadline, task_id), reverse index for O(log n) dequeue
  - [x] DeadlineParams: budget_ticks, deadline_ticks, period_ticks per task
  - [x] Admission control: utilization check (Σ budget/period ≤ 95%), reject overload
  - [x] Budget throttling: exhausted tasks removed until next period
  - [x] Period replenishment: automatic re-enqueue when period elapses
  - [x] Non-deadline task fallback with priority-based pseudo-deadlines
  - [x] Work stealing: skips registered deadline tasks (CPU affinity)
  - [x] Scheduler trait implementation, WorkloadProfile integration
  - [x] 9 self-tests: admission control, EDF ordering, throttling, replenishment, fallback, dequeue, utilization accounting, has_ready/has_real_work, steal protection
- [x] Selectable in settings, requires reboot to switch
  - [x] SchedulerBackend enum: PriorityRR (0), EEVDF (1), Deadline (2) — match dispatch, no dyn Trait
  - [x] PerCpuScheduler refactored to use SchedulerBackend (was hardcoded PriorityRoundRobin)
  - [x] sched.backend sysctl parameter (read/write via sysctl command, takes effect on reboot)
  - [x] Desired vs active backend tracking (AtomicU8, set_desired/active_backend API)
  - [x] Boot log shows active backend name
  - [x] 11 self-tests: backend creation, dispatch for all 3 backends, time slices, profiles, deadline-specific ops

### 5.4 Advanced security
- [x] Per-process filesystem namespaces for sandboxing (fs::mount_ns)
- [x] Interceptor hooks (synchronous, capability-gated) (fs::intercept)
- [x] Async notification hooks / tracing subsystem (ktrace: 25 tracepoints across 6 categories)
- [x] Profiling mode for high-frequency events (alloc/dealloc tracing)
  - [x] alloc_trace ring buffer wired to alloc_order/free_order (frame-level tracing)
  - [x] Zero-cost disabled path (single atomic load ~1ns), default disabled
  - [x] mm.alloc_trace sysctl parameter for runtime enable/disable
  - [x] Frame allocator OOM path tries memory compaction before OOM kill
  - [x] Reverse mapping (rmap) wired into page lifecycle (cow, swap-out, swap-in, compaction)
  - [x] Memory compaction migration loop uses rmap iteration to find/migrate private pages
  - [x] Self-tests: memtype accounting, compaction subsystem, VMA management

### 5.5 Container support
- [x] Namespace primitives (PID, network, mount, user)
  - [x] PID namespace: hierarchical PID isolation (max 64 namespaces)
    - [x] Per-namespace PID number space (local PIDs from 1, monotonic)
    - [x] Bidirectional PID translation (global ↔ local)
    - [x] Visibility hierarchy: parent sees children, not vice versa
    - [x] Init process tracking (PID 1, exit triggers cleanup signal)
    - [x] 18 self-tests: lifecycle, alloc/free, translation, visibility, init, separate spaces
  - [x] Network namespace: per-container network isolation
    - [x] Independent interface config (IP, subnet, gateway, DNS) per namespace
    - [x] Per-namespace routing table with longest-prefix-match + metric tie-breaking
    - [x] Process attach/detach tracking
    - [x] kshell `netns` command: list/create/delete/ifconfig/route/stats/up/down/test
    - [x] 18 self-tests: lifecycle, routing, isolation, metric, table full
    - [x] Integration with net/ module (namespace-aware interface accessors + routing)
      - [x] interface.rs: ns_ip(), ns_info(), ns_is_up() query netns for non-root NS
      - [x] interface.rs: configure() syncs DHCP config to netns root namespace
      - [x] ipv4.rs: send_ns() with per-namespace source IP + route_lookup()
      - [x] netns.rs: is_initialized() for boot-order safety
      - [x] ARP/firewall doc notes (global/shared, per-namespace ARP is future)
      - [x] Per-namespace ARP cache (16 entries per namespace, independent of global cache)
        - [x] ns_init/ns_destroy lifecycle management per namespace
        - [x] ns_lookup/ns_insert/ns_flush with root→global delegation
        - [x] ns_cache_entries/ns_entry_count diagnostics
        - [x] 3 self-tests: namespace isolation, root delegation, lifecycle
      - [x] Virtual Ethernet (veth) pairs: connected virtual links between namespaces
        - [x] VethPair with two VethEnd endpoints, per-end MAC/ns/queue/stats
        - [x] Frame loopback: TX on end A → RX on end B (and vice versa)
        - [x] Bounded RX queue (256 frames) with drop counting
        - [x] Endpoint move between namespaces (requires down state)
        - [x] poll_all() integration with net::poll() for protocol stack injection
        - [x] interface.rs ns_info() returns veth MAC for namespace endpoints
        - [x] find_endpoint_for_ns() lookup for namespace → veth mapping
        - [x] 10 self-tests: create/destroy, MAC generation, loopback, down drop, queue full, move, move-requires-down, stats, multiple pairs, bidirectional
      - [x] Per-namespace firewall rules (16 rules, 32 conntrack entries per namespace; ns_init/ns_enable/ns_add_rule/ns_check_outbound_ns/ns_check_inbound_ns API; 3 self-tests for isolation, conntrack, lifecycle)
      - [x] IPv6 firewall (Rule6/ConntrackEntry6 with independent enable/policy; check_inbound_v6/check_outbound_v6 wired into IPv6 processing; ip6_matches u128 prefix comparison; Protocol::Icmp maps to ICMPv6 for v6 rules; fw on6/off6/policy6/allow6/deny6/remove6/clear6 commands; 5 self-tests)
      - [x] Wire process→container→net_ns into socket layer callers
  - [x] Mount namespace: separate mount point trees (implemented as fs::mount_ns)
  - [x] User namespace: UID/GID remapping for rootless containers
    - [x] IdMapping ranges (up to 16 per namespace) translate inner ↔ outer IDs
    - [x] Hierarchical namespace tree with parent/child tracking
    - [x] uid_to_host() walks full hierarchy for permission checks
    - [x] Process attach/detach tracking per namespace
    - [x] Overflow ID (65534) for unmapped UIDs (Linux convention)
    - [x] kshell `userns` command: list/create/delete/uidmap/gidmap/stats/test
    - [x] 15 self-tests including nested two-level UID translation
- [x] Resource control groups (CPU, memory, I/O limits per group)
  - [x] cgroup.rs: hierarchical group tree (max 256 groups, root always exists)
  - [x] CPU controller: per-group quota/period (quota_ticks per period_ticks), cpu_charge() hot-path check, cpu_period_reset() for BSP timer
  - [x] Memory controller: per-group frame limit, CAS-based mem_charge() with atomic limit enforcement, mem_uncharge() with underflow saturation
  - [x] Hierarchical limits: effective_cpu_quota/effective_mem_limit walk parent chain, return tightest constraint
  - [x] Task integration: cgroup_id field in Task struct (default ROOT_CGROUP), attach_task/detach_task API
  - [x] 18 self-tests: root exists, create/delete, hierarchy, attach/detach, CPU charge/throttle/reset/unlimited, memory charge/limit/uncharge/underflow, effective hierarchical limits, stats queries
  - [x] Scheduler timer_tick integration: charges task's cgroup on each tick, throttles when group quota exceeded, BSP period reset drives cgroup::cpu_period_reset()
  - [x] Frame allocator integration (check cgroup memory limit on alloc)
    - [x] Per-frame cgroup owner array (65536-entry u8, records which cgroup was charged)
    - [x] CGROUP_MEM_ACTIVE AtomicBool fast-exit (zero overhead when no limits configured)
    - [x] charge_cgroup_alloc in alloc_frame (per-CPU cache path) and alloc_order/alloc_order_constrained
    - [x] uncharge_cgroup_free in free_frame and free_order (uses stored cgroup, correct even when different task frees)
    - [x] alloc_order/alloc_order_constrained refactored to charge after releasing allocator lock (clean lock ordering)
    - [x] Rollback on cgroup OOM: frame freed back via free_order_inner (no double-uncharge)
    - [x] 4 self-tests: fast-exit disabled path, per-frame tracking round-trip, charge/uncharge, limit enforcement
    - [x] Demand paging integration (try_charge_current_mem before frame alloc in try_resolve_fault)
    - [x] Reverse mapping integration (rmap::add after demand-page map_frame in try_resolve_fault)
  - [x] I/O controller (bandwidth limits per group)
    - [x] IoLimit struct: ops_max + bytes_max per period (0 = unlimited)
    - [x] set_io_limit(), io_charge(), io_period_reset() API
    - [x] Dual-limit enforcement: whichever dimension hit first triggers throttle
    - [x] io_would_throttle() pre-check for I/O scheduler
    - [x] effective_io_ops_limit/effective_io_bytes_limit hierarchy queries
    - [x] try_charge_current_io() convenience wrapper for drivers
    - [x] BSP timer integration: io_period_reset alongside cpu_period_reset
    - [x] Sysctl parameters: cgroup.cpu_period, cgroup.io_ops_max_default, cgroup.io_bytes_max_default
    - [x] Kshell `cgroup io` command for interactive limit management
    - [x] 7 new self-tests (25 total): ops throttle, period reset, bytes throttle, unlimited, effective limits, would_throttle, cpu_period tunable
- [-] Container runtime support
  - [x] Container lifecycle manager (kernel/src/container.rs)
    - [x] ContainerConfig builder: name, UID/GID mappings, CPU/mem/IO limits, network
    - [x] Atomic create with rollback (pidns + userns + netns + cgroup as unit)
    - [x] State machine: Created → Running → Stopped/Failed → deleted
    - [x] Process tracking across all sub-resources
    - [x] container::run(id, elf, opts): spawn a real init process into a container, bind it (cgroup billing via Q14 + pidns/userns/netns), record init PID, Created→Running; rolls back the spawn on bind failure
    - [x] PID-vs-task-id binding split: add_process_task/remove_process_task key scheduler resources (cgroup, net_ns) on the initial-thread task id, pidns mapping + tracking on the global PID (a spawned process's PID != its task id); add_process/remove_process are pid==task wrappers (design-decisions §41)
    - [x] Per-container filesystem root (chroot): ipc::namespace PROCESS_ROOT map (set_root/clear_root/get_root) re-anchors a process's absolute paths under its rootfs and clamps `..` so the jail can't be escaped (apply_root/normalize_jailed); resolve_path_for applies it after Bind/Hide rules, keyed on the global PID so child threads inherit it; Container gains root_path + set_root_path (Created-only), wired through add_process_task/remove_process_task (design-decisions §42)
    - [x] oci run launches the image entrypoint as the container init, jailed to the extracted rootfs (sets root_path, reads command[0] from the host path inside the rootfs, runs with image argv+env); falls back to start()+`container exec` when there's no entrypoint/unreadable binary. Limitation: jail points at the extracted lower dir, no overlay CoW write-isolation yet; relative paths not jailed (known-issues TD32)
    - [x] kshell `container`/`ct` command: list/create/delete/rootfs/run/start/stop/exec/info/test (`rootfs ID <host-path>` sets the chroot; `run ID <elf-path> [args]` loads an ELF from the VFS and launches it as the jailed container init; `info` shows init PID + Rootfs)
    - [x] 18 self-tests (veth auto-setup, net_ns task propagation, run init process + end-to-end cgroup billing, rootfs jail/chroot for init process)
    - [x] Automatic veth pair creation for networked containers
      - [x] setup_container_veth(): create pair, move end B to container NS, bring up both
      - [x] Veth pair ID stored in Container and ContainerInfo for lifecycle tracking
      - [x] delete() destroys veth pair before cleaning up namespaces
  - [x] Namespace-aware TCP/UDP stacks
    - [x] ns_id field on TcpConnection, TcpListener, UdpSocket, TcpConnectionInfo
    - [x] All public APIs (connect, connect_start, bind) take ns_id parameter
    - [x] 5-tuple connection lookup (ns_id + local_port + remote_ip + remote_port)
    - [x] Same port bindable in different namespaces
    - [x] 30+ callers updated; self-tests for namespace isolation
  - [x] Cross-namespace TCP correctness (physical NIC reachability)
    - [x] alloc_port_for() global uniqueness (prevents wire 4-tuple collisions)
    - [x] Connection lookup: ROOT_NS packets search all namespaces
    - [x] Listener lookup: accepted connections inherit listener's ns_id
  - [x] Process→container→net_ns wiring into syscall layer
    - [x] net_ns field on Task struct (sched/task.rs), default ROOT_NS
    - [x] current_task_net_ns() / set_task_net_ns() scheduler helpers
    - [x] container::add_process() sets task's net_ns, remove_process() resets it
    - [x] SYS_TCP_CONNECT, SYS_TCP_BIND, SYS_UDP_BIND use current_task_net_ns()
    - [x] Self-test: net_ns propagation verified on add/remove
  - [x] NAT/masquerade for container outbound traffic (kernel/src/net/nat.rs)
    - [x] Source NAT: containers with private IPs communicate through host's public IP
    - [x] Port mapping table (256 entries, round-robin allocation in 32768-60999)
    - [x] TCP (300s) and UDP (30s) timeout with automatic entry expiry
    - [x] translate_outgoing() / translate_incoming() for forward/reverse path
    - [x] flush_namespace() wired into container delete for cleanup
    - [x] tick() driven from net::poll() 5-second periodic maintenance
    - [x] DNAT port forwarding: add_port_forward/remove_port_forward/lookup, 32 rules
    - [x] flush_port_forwards(ns_id) wired into container delete
    - [x] kshell `nat` command: enable/disable, status, list, flush, forward add/del/list
    - [x] 12 self-tests (SNAT: enable/disable, root bypass, outgoing/incoming, flush, UDP, stats; DNAT: add/lookup/remove/flush)
  - [x] Syscall filter (seccomp equivalent, kernel/src/scfilter.rs)
    - [x] Bitmap-based O(1) per-syscall check (1000-bit bitmap)
    - [x] Allow-all and deny-all modes, per-process filters
    - [x] Fork inheritance (copy_filter), tighten-only invariant
    - [x] Per-process deny count audit tracking
    - [x] kshell `scfilter`/`seccomp` command
    - [x] 14 self-tests
    - [x] Wire into syscall/dispatch.rs (kernel-ipc zone)
      - [x] scfilter::check(task_id, nr) called after bounds check, before handler lookup
      - [x] Denied syscalls return PermissionDenied without invoking handler
      - [x] current_task_id() used for caller identification
  - [x] OCI-compatible container image format parsing
    - [x] json.rs: minimal recursive-descent JSON parser (no_std, no floats, 8 self-tests)
    - [x] oci.rs: OCI Image Spec v1.0 parser (index, manifest, config, digest verification)
    - [x] Layer extraction via tar + gunzip + overlayfs infrastructure
    - [x] kshell `oci` command: inspect, layers, run, test
    - [x] `oci run`: full container creation from OCI image (layer extraction → overlay rootfs → container with namespace isolation)
  - [x] Per-namespace DNS resolution: containers use their own configured DNS server (fallback to host)
  - [x] `container exec <id> <cmd>`: run kshell commands inside a container's network namespace
  - [-] Port Docker (or equivalent container runtime) — in progress. Native
    `container`/`ct` runtime + `oci` image tooling + a `docker`/`dk` compat
    shim. Shipped: OCI image load/inspect/layers/extract, overlay rootfs,
    volumes (host bind, named, read-only `:ro`, and **tmpfs** `--tmpfs`),
    user-defined networks + IPAM + **shared L2 bridge** (one
    `net::bridge` per network, veth host-ends switched at L2 so same-network
    peers reach each other directly) + **embedded DNS** (container
    name/hostname/`--network-alias` → peer IP, network-scoped and
    case-insensitive, consulted by the in-container resolver before any
    upstream query — 127.0.0.11 semantics), port publishing, resource limits
    (mem/cpu via cgroups), restart/`--rm` policies, `run`/`create`/`start`/
    `stop`/`kill`/`pause`/`ps`/`rm`/`inspect`/`logs`/`events`/`stats`/`top`/
    `port`/`wait`/`diff`/`rename`/`update`/`prune`/`cp`/`commit`/`export`/
    `import`, `system df`/`prune`, image `save`/`load`/`history`, and
    **`build`** (Dockerfile → OCI image via `oci::build_image`: FROM
    scratch|local-image with layer+config inheritance, COPY/ADD with
    `.dockerignore` filtering + `--chmod`/`--chown` (numeric) + wildcard
    source globbing (`filepath.Match`) + relative-dest resolution against
    WORKDIR + `ADD` local-tar auto-extraction (plain/gzip),
    ENV/CMD/ENTRYPOINT/`WORKDIR` (records config *and* materialises the
    directory as a filesystem layer)/USER/EXPOSE/LABEL/
    VOLUME/STOPSIGNAL/SHELL/ONBUILD, ARG `${VAR}` expansion + `--build-arg`
    overrides, **multi-stage builds** (`FROM … AS <name>`, `FROM <stage>`
    inheritance, `COPY --from=<stage|index|image>`, `--target <stage>`),
    and OCI config
    `history[]` recording surfaced via `oci`/`docker history`), plus a
    **named image store** at `/var/lib/images` (single shared OCI layout keyed
    by `ref.name` annotations: `oci`/`docker` `tag`/`images`/`rmi` with
    content-addressed blob dedup + reference-counted blob GC on removal).
    Store references are usable everywhere an image is named: `FROM name:tag`
    (base inheritance from the store), `oci`/`docker run name:tag`,
    `oci inspect|layers|history name:tag`, `oci build -t name:tag`
    (auto-tag the built image into the store), and `save`/`load`
    (`save name:tag` exports a single-image tar via `store_export_ref`;
    `load` imports annotated manifests back into the store by `ref.name`) —
    all via `oci::resolve_image_source` (dir-or-reference). **`commit`**
    (`oci commit <ctr> <dest-dir> [name:tag]` / `docker commit <ctr> name:tag`):
    authors a *new image* from a running container's filesystem changes —
    captures the container's overlay upper layer (added/changed files) plus
    whiteouts (deletions) as one new layer on top of the base image the
    container was created from (tracked via `ContainerConfig::image_source`,
    stamped at `oci run` time), carrying the base config (Env/Cmd/Entrypoint/…)
    and layers forward verbatim and appending a COMMIT `history[]` entry
    (`oci::commit_image` → `container::commit_image`). Distinct from the native
    `container commit`, which clones a container; `docker commit` stages a
    standalone layout in a temp dir then imports it into the store under the
    given `name:tag`.
    Real in-container `container exec` (spawns a genuine process in the
    container's namespaces + cgroup and, foreground, blocks on its exit via
    `wait_process`) and image `HEALTHCHECK` (parsed from OCI config, driven by
    a non-blocking hrtimer→workqueue supervisor, surfaced in `inspect`/`ps`)
    both shipped. Per operator decision Q17 (§58, option B): the netns-debug
    `container exec` facade is kept AND real rootfs-binary exec is added under a
    distinct verb (`container run-in` / `container exec --rootfs`); the `docker
    exec` delegate routes to the real path. Dockerfile `RUN` now executes via
    the real in-container exec pipeline (materialize lower rootfs → overlay
    create+mount → ephemeral container → `exec_path_env` → `wait_process` →
    capture the overlay upper as the new layer; failures map to
    `RunLaunch`/`RunFailed`), and Dockerfile `HEALTHCHECK` is parsed and
    serialized into the image config (`ImageSpec.healthcheck`, Go-duration flags,
    NONE/CMD/CMD-SHELL forms, FROM inheritance). Runtime `network
    connect/disconnect` shipped (Q19/§60, option B): the container network model
    is generalised to N-interface multi-network membership — a `Container` keeps
    its create-time primary veth plus a `memberships[]` list of named-network
    attachments (each with its own veth pair, IP, and connected route), exposed
    via `container network connect/disconnect <net> <ctr>` (+ `docker network
    connect/disconnect` delegate), surfaced in `container info`/`inspect`
    (`networks[]`), and covered by the `Multi-network membership (attach/detach)`
    boot self-test. Disconnecting the primary network is refused (its veth is
    lifecycle-owned). Honest limitation: the netns L3 config still tracks only the
    primary interface; additional networks provide L2 bridge reachability + IPAM
    lease + embedded DNS + a connected route.

### 5.6 Additional software
- [x] Archive support (zip, 7z, tar.gz/bz2/xz/zst/lz4, rar, cpio, ar, deb)
- [ ] Speech input / speech output
- [ ] Cellphone camera/microphone integration
- [x] Scripting language registration (Lua and/or WASM runtime for app extensibility) — implemented as fs::scriptlang with 5 built-in engines (Lua/Wasmtime/Shell/Fastpy/QuickJS), sandbox levels, resource limits, eval API
- [x] Keyboard layout customizer (arbitrary remap, save named layouts) — implemented as fs::keylayout with per-key remap, disable keys, 64 max layouts
- [x] Let's Encrypt SSL certificate helper — implemented as fs::certmgr with ACME request/complete workflow, auto-renewal, 5 built-in root CAs
- [x] Optimized keyboard layouts (Dvorak, Colemak, others) — built-in US QWERTY, Dvorak, Colemak, US-NoCaps layouts in fs::keylayout init_defaults()

### 5.7 Installation wizard — Python/fastpy candidate
- [x] Easy install (automatic partitioning) and manual install (partition manager) — fs::installer with Easy/Manual/Unattended modes, PartitionPlan struct
- [x] Keyboard/layout selection — set_keyboard() in InstallSession, integrated with fs::keylayout
- [x] Auto-detect monitor DPI, let user adjust scaling — detect_and_set_scaling() with recommended_scale() from fs::display
- [x] Workload type selection (populates tuning presets, changeable later) — WorkloadType enum (Desktop/Server/Development/Gaming) with fs::fspolicy integration
- [x] Swap file sizing — swap_mib field in PartitionPlan (None = file-based via fs::swapcfg)
- [x] Post-reboot setup: audio device, timezone, user/password, WiFi, theme, browser choice — FirstBoot phase in InstallSession with all fields
- [x] Unattended install via YAML configuration file (apps/installer: InstallConfig, YAML parser, validation, InstallPlan, CLI)
- [x] GRUB integration for dual-boot (grub.rs: GrubDetector, entry generation, /etc/grub.d/40_slateos lifecycle, UUID validation)

## Dependency Graph (critical path)

```
Phase 0 (setup)
    │
Phase 1.1 (boot) ──→ 1.2 (memory) ──→ 1.3 (scheduler) ──→ 1.4 (IPC/syscalls)
                                                                    │
                                            1.5 (capabilities) ←───┤
                                                                    │
                                            1.6 (processes) ←──────┘
                                                    │
                    ┌───────────────────────────────┤
                    │                               │
            2.1-2.2 (drivers)              2.5 (POSIX layer)
                    │                               │
            2.3 (filesystem)               2.7 (shell, tools)
                    │                               │
            2.4 (networking)               2.6 (service manager)
                    │                               │
                    └───────────┬───────────────────┘
                                │
                    3.1 (GPU drivers) ──→ 3.2 (graphics stack)
                                                    │
                                        3.3 (compositor) ──→ 3.4 (desktop shell)
                                                                    │
                                                            3.5 (GUI toolkit)
                                                                    │
                                                    ┌───────────────┤
                                                    │               │
                                            4.1 (core apps)  4.2 (package mgr)
                                                    │
                                            4.3 (Chromium)
                                                    │
                                        5.1 (Linux compat) ──→ WINE ──→ Windows apps
```

---

## Notes

- **Large-initiative ordering (operator-fixed 2026-07-18 — do NOT re-ask).** Now
  that the self-hosting C toolchain + POSIX layer are comprehensive, the remaining
  giant initiatives are executed in this fixed order (Q25 → design-decisions.md §69):
  1. **Oils (OSH) + coreutils** — the interactive-shell userland. Oils is a
     bash-*superset* shell (roadmap-detailed.md §2.7), **not** bash itself.
  2. **fastpy build-system integration** — unlocks the Python-via-fastpy userspace lane.
  3. **Mesa / GPU userspace (3D)** — gated by Q18 until a virgl test environment exists.
  4. **Chromium** — browser + system-web-app / Electron framework.
  5. **WINE** — Windows app compatibility.
  6. **Additional filesystems** — Btrfs / F2FS / NTFS.
  Pick the next one whenever the current initiative lands; the operator has already
  set the order, so there's no need to ask which comes next.
- **Don't write custom filesystems early.** Port ext4. Data loss bugs are unforgivable.
- **Don't write a custom browser.** Port Chromium. It's huge but unlocks three things at once.
- **GPU drivers are the hardest part.** Start with AMD (open source). Intel second. NVIDIA last (via Linux compat layer).
- **Benchmark everything.** Write benchmarks before optimizing. AI is good at optimization with a concrete target.
- **One scheduler is enough initially.** Define the trait interface, implement priority round-robin, add alternatives only if users need them.
- **Security model from day one.** Capabilities, IOMMU, CFI — bake these in early. Retrofitting security is much harder.
